Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

Definition of Fard: Fard 'Ayn and Fard Kifayah
Defines fard and its two types in Hanafi fiqh.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define fard in Hanafi usul and distinguish between fard 'ayn and fard kifayah with examples.

Core Idea
Fard is an obligation proven by definitive evidence; denial constitutes disbelief.

This passage establishes the foundational definition of fard in the Hanafi school, emphasizing its epistemological basis. It then introduces the critical distinction between individual and collective obligations. Understanding this classification is essential for a mufti when determining the scope of duties in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the source of definition
The passage defines fard based on the evidence type (Quran, mutawatir hadith). Note that it requires no doubt.
2
Understand the legal consequences
Recognize the consequences: denial = kufr, neglect without excuse = fisq.
3
Distinguish the two types
Fard 'ayn vs fard kifayah: focus on the criterion of individual vs collective obligation.
4
Memorize the examples
Five daily prayers for fard 'ayn, funeral prayer for fard kifayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقہ کی چند اصطلاحات
 فرض کی تعریف
 جو بات قرآن کریم اور حدیث دونوں یا صرف قرآن سے یا بے شمار حدیثوں سے ثابت ہو اور اس میں کوئی شبہ نہ ہو وہ فرض ہے اس کا منکر کافر اور بغیر عذر چھوڑ نے والا فاسق ہوتا ہے۔
 فرض کی دوقسمیں ہے
 (۱) فرض عین (۲) فرض کفایہ۔
 فرض عین: وہ فرض ہے جس کا ادا کرنا ہر شخص کے لیے ضروری ہو جیسے پنجوقتہ نماز وغیرہ۔
 فرض کفایہ وہ ہے جس کا ادا کرنا ہر شخص کے لیے ضروری ہو لیکن اگر کچھ لوگ ادا کر لیں تو عام لوگ گناہ سے بچ جائیں جیسے نماز جنازہ ۔ (رد المختار بن راص (۷۰)
Some terms of fiqh. Definition of fard: Whatever is proven by the Quran and Hadith both, or by the Quran alone, or by numerous hadith, and in which there is no doubt, is fard. Its denier becomes a disbeliever, and one who leaves it without excuse becomes a sinner. Fard has two types: (1) Fard 'ayn, (2) Fard kifayah. Fard 'ayn: it is fard whose performance is necessary for every person, like the five daily prayers, etc. Fard kifayah: it is fard whose performance is necessary for every person, but if some people perform it, the general people are absolved of sin, like the funeral prayer. (Radd al-Muhtar 1:70)
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage provides a foundational definition of 'fard' in Hanafi fiqh. It is an obligation proven by definitive evidence (qat'i) from the Quran or mutawatir hadith. Denying such an obligation removes one from Islam, while neglecting it without valid reason makes one a sinner (fasiq). The passage then distinguishes two types: fard 'ayn (individual obligation) which every Muslim must perform personally, such as the five daily prayers; and fard kifayah (collective obligation) which is required from the community as a whole, but if enough Muslims fulfill it, the rest are relieved of responsibility, like the funeral prayer. This classification is essential for understanding the scope of religious duties.

Key Terms
فرض عین (Fard 'ayn): An individual obligation that every Muslim must perform personally.
فرض کفایہ (Fard kifayah): A collective obligation; if some Muslims perform it, the rest are absolved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, a person who denies the obligation of a fard becomes:
A) a fasiq
B) a kafir
C) excused if ignorant
D) none of the above

Key Takeaway
Fard is a definitive obligation; its ignorance leads to kufr, and it is divided into individual (fard 'ayn) and collective (fard kifayah) duties.

Definition of Sunnah: The Prophet's Practice
Defines sunnah as Prophet's action or command

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of sunnah and distinguish it from fard and wajib.

Core Idea
Sunnah is the Prophet's action or command, rewardable but not obligatory.

This lesson anchors the core definition of sunnah as a legal category. In Hanafi fiqh, sunnah sits below fard and wajib in the hierarchy of obligations. Understanding this distinction is crucial for accurately deriving rulings and issuing fatwas. The definition here is concise but foundational for all subsequent discussions of Prophetic practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its source
Locate the act being defined and the authority source. Here, the act is sunnah and the source is the Prophet's action or command.
The definition explicitly limits sunnah to the Prophet's own conduct or explicit command.
2
Classify the hukm level
Determine where sunnah sits in the Hanafi hierarchy. Sunnah is recommended but not obligatory; performance earns reward, omission is not sinful but may be disliked if habitual.
Hanafi: sunnah mu'akkada is closer to wajib in emphasis, but still not fard/wajib.
3
Define the legal effect (athar)
State the consequence of performing or leaving the sunnah. Performance is rewarded; leaving without excuse is makruh tanzihi.
The athar distinguishes sunnah from fard (sin for omission) and wajib (sin for omission but proof is zanni).
4
Apply in fatwa context
As a mufti, use this definition to categorize a practice: if the Prophet did it or commanded it, it is sunnah; then decide if it is mu'akkada or ghayr mu'akkada based on other evidence.
This definition is the starting point for all sunnah-related fatwas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سنت کی تعریف
 سنت وہ فعل ہے جس کو رسول اکرم اللہ نے خود کیا ہو یا کرنے کا حکم دیا ہو۔ (رد اختاران داره ۷ )
Definition of Sunnah: Sunnah is an act that the Messenger of Allah himself performed or commanded to be done. (Radd al-Mukhtar 1:?)
Source pages p. 25

Commentary
This passage gives a basic Hanafi definition of 'sunnah'. It refers to actions that the Prophet Muhammad either performed himself or explicitly commanded others to perform. This definition is narrower than the broader concept of 'sunnah' as a source of law (which includes his sayings, actions, and tacit approvals). Here it is specifically defined as the Prophet's practice that believers are encouraged to follow. In Hanafi fiqh, sunnah is a level below fard and wajib; leaving it without excuse is blameworthy but not sinful unless done habitually. The passage is cut off; the author likely went on to discuss differences among scholars on the definition.

Key Terms
سنت (Sunnah): An act performed or commanded by the Prophet; non-obligatory but meritorious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the source of sunnah?
A) The consensus of scholars
B) The Quran
C) The Prophet's action or command
D) Analogical reasoning

Key Takeaway
Sunnah in Hanafi fiqh is specifically the Prophet's action or command, distinguishing it from fard and wajib.

Understanding Qawa'id Fiqhiyyah: Definition, History, and Benefits
Definition, history, and benefits of legal maxims

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define qawa'id fiqhiyyah, trace their historical development in the Hanafi school, and identify their practical benefits for ifta.

Core Idea
A qa'idah is a universal fiqhi rule that encapsulates many particulars, revealing the spirit of Shariah.

This passage introduces legal maxims as foundational tools in Hanafi jurisprudence. It explains their definition, traces their historical codification, and enumerates five key benefits. Mastering maxims enables the mufti to derive rulings systematically, reduce contradictions, and understand the higher objectives of Shariah.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Definitions
First, learn the linguistic and terminological meanings of 'qa'idah' and 'qawa'id fiqhiyyah'. The passage defines it as a universal ruling applying to many particulars across fiqh chapters.
Note that the fiqhi definition requires the rule to apply directly (bila wasitah) to multiple cases.
2
Trace the Historical Development
Identify the key Hanafi scholars: Abu Tahir al-Dabbas (first 17 maxims), Imam al-Karkhi (Risalah fi al-Usul). Then note contributions from Shafi'i (al-Zanjani) and Hanbali (Ibn Rajab) schools.
This shows that codification of maxims was a cross-madhhab endeavour.
3
List the Five Benefits
From the passage, enumerate: (1) reduces memorization, (2) reveals secrets and sources of rulings, (3) prevents contradictions in teaching, (4) facilitates understanding of maqasid, (5) helps derive rulings for new incidents.
Each benefit addresses a practical need in fiqh education and ifta.
4
Analyse the Example Maxim
The passage gives the maxim 'al-darurat tubih al-mahdhurat' (necessities make prohibitions permissible). See how this maxim ties to the maqsad of removing hardship.
This example illustrates how a single maxim can guide rulings across chapters.
5
Apply to Contemporary Ifta
Consider how a mufti would use maxims like this to address novel issues (e.g., organ donation in necessity). The maxim helps to derive a ruling consistent with Shariah objectives.
Maxims are not sources but tools; they must be applied with proper conditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قواعد فقہیہ کی تعریف
قاعد ولغت میں بنیا دو اساس کو کہتے ہیں اسکی جمع قواعد آتی ہے۔
قاعدہ کی عام اصطلاحی تعریف:
دو کی جو اپنی تمام جزئیات پر محیط ہو۔ قاعدہ کی فقہی اصطلاحی تعریف: فقہی حکم کلی جو متعدد ابواب قلب کی کثیر جزئیات پر بلا واسطہ صادق آئے جس سے متعددا بجواب کے احکام سمجھ میں آجا ئیں۔ قواعد فقہ سے شریعت کی دو علامتیں اور مصلحتیں مراد ہیں جو شریعت اسلامی کی اصل روح ہیں چنا نچہ کہا جاتا ہے کہ سے پہلے ابو طاھر دباس نے سترہ قاعدے مقرر کئے اور فقہ حنفی کے تمام احکام کیلئے انہیں کو مدار قراردیا اسکے بعد پھر ایک اور فقہ حنفی فقیہ امام کرخی (۳۴۹۳ھ) کے قوائد میں رسالۃ الاصول مرتب کیا اسکے بعد شوافع فقہاء میں زنجانی (۶۵۲۴ ھ ) تخریج الفروع علی الاصول اور ابن رجب حنبلی (۷۹۵۴ھ) کی قواعد کا نمبر آتا ہے۔ الاشباہ والنظائر قواعد فقہیہ کی کتابوں میں سے ایک کتاب ہے جس میں قواعد فقہیہ کو ذکر کیا گیا ہے قواعد فقہیہ کے بہت سے فوائد ہیں جن میں سے چند مندرجہ ذیل ہیں۔ (1) قوالدہ کو جاننے کے بعد اکثر جزئیات کے یاد کرنے سے مستعفی ہو جاتا ہے اکثر جزئیات کے کلیات میں داخل ہونیکی وجہ ہے۔ (۲) قواعد فقہیہ کی معرفت سے پڑھنے پڑھانے والا اسرار شریعت مدارک احکام اور مسائل فقہیہ کے ماخذ سے مطلع ہو جاتا ہے۔ (۳) فقہی فروعات کی درس و تدریس بدون قواعد طالب علم کے ذہن میں تناقض کا باعث ہوتی ہے جبکہ قواعد کے ساتھ تناقض کے دور کرنے کا باعث بنتی ہے۔ (۴) قواعد کی معرفت سے مقاصد شریعت کو سمجھنا آسان ہوتا ہے مثلا ایک قاعدہ ہے کہ ضرورات ممنوعات کو جائز کردیتی ہیں جس سے یہ بات کبھی جاسکتی ہے کہ حرج کا دور کرنا اور بندوں کیلئے آسانی پیدا کرنا مقاصد شریعت میں سے ایک مقصد ہے۔ (۵) قواعد فقہ کے جاننے سے فقیہ کو ان حوادث و واقعات کے احکام کے جانے میں مد ملتی ہے جن کا کوئی حکم نصوص
Definition of Qawa'id Fiqhiyyah:
Linguistically, 'qa'id' means foundation and base; its plural is 'qawa'id'.
General terminological definition of 'qa'idah': A principle that encompasses all of its particulars.
Fiqhi terminological definition: A universal fiqhi ruling that applies directly to many particulars across multiple chapters of fiqh, by which the rulings of many issues can be understood.
By 'qawa'id fiqhi', the intended meanings are the wisdoms (hikam) and interests (masalih) of the Shariah, which are the essential spirit of Islamic law.
Thus it is said that first Abu Tahir al-Dabbas established seventeen principles and made them the basis for all Hanafi rulings. Then after him, another Hanafi jurist, Imam al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH?), arranged the principles in his 'Risalah fi al-Usul'. After that, among the Shafi'i jurists, al-Zanjani (d. 652 AH) composed 'Takhrij al-Furu' ala al-Usul', and then comes the 'Qawa'id' of Ibn Rajab al-Hanbali (d. 795 AH).
Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair is one of the books on legal maxims in which qawa'id fiqhiyyah are discussed.
Qawa'id fiqhiyyah have many benefits, among which are the following:
(1) After knowing the maxim, one is dispensed from memorizing most of the particulars, because most particulars fall under the universal.
(2) Through knowledge of legal maxims, the reader and teacher become aware of the secrets of Shariah, the bases of rulings, and the sources of fiqhi issues.
(3) Teaching and learning fiqhi branches without maxims causes contradiction in the student's mind, while with maxims it becomes a means of removing contradiction.
(4) With knowledge of maxims, understanding the objectives (maqasid) of Shariah becomes easier. For example, there is a maxim: 'Necessities make prohibitions permissible' (al-darurat tubih al-mahdhurat), from which it can be understood that removing hardship and creating ease for people is one of the objectives of Shariah.
(5) By knowing legal maxims, the jurist is helped in knowing the rulings of new incidents and events for which there is no ruling in the texts.
Source pages p. 30

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive definition of the concept of 'qawa'id fiqhiyyah' (legal maxims) along with a brief historical overview and enumeration of their benefits. The term 'qa'idah' linguistically means foundation; technically, a qa'idah is a general rule that covers its particulars. In fiqh, it is a universal ruling that applies to many cases across different chapters without mediation, thus enabling the jurist to understand the rulings of multiple issues at once.
The text then traces the development of maxim literature in the Hanafi school: Abu Tahir al-Dabbas is credited with first formulating 17 maxims; Imam al-Karkhi wrote a risalah on the principles; among the Shafi'is, al-Zanjani wrote Takhrij al-Furu' ala al-Usul; and the Hanbali scholar Ibn Rajab compiled his own Qawa'id. This shows that the codification of legal maxims was a shared concern across schools.
The passage lists five benefits of studying legal maxims: (1) they reduce the need to memorize individual cases; (2) they reveal the underlying wisdom and sources of rulings; (3) they prevent contradictions in teaching; (4) they facilitate understanding of the higher objectives of Shariah (maqasid), as illustrated by the maxim that necessity allows prohibitions; (5) they assist the mufti in deriving rulings for novel issues not explicitly covered by primary texts.
The text concludes by noting that Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair is one such work on legal maxims.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'idah): A foundational principle that encompasses many subsidiary rulings.
قواعد فقهية (qawa'id fiqhiyyah): Legal maxims that are universal statements summarizing the rulings of many cases across fiqh chapters.
الضرورات تبيح المحظورات (al-darurat tubih al-mahdhurat): Necessities make prohibitions permissible. A major legal maxim.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which Hanafi jurist is credited with first establishing seventeen legal maxims?
A) Imam al-Karkhi
B) Abu Tahir al-Dabbas
C) Zain al-Din Ibn Nujaym
D) Ibn Rajab al-Hanbali

Key Takeaway
Qawa'id fiqhiyyah are universal rules derived from primary sources that systematize fiqh, reveal maqasid, and aid in deriving rulings for novel cases.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate

First Benefit: Qawa'id as the Path to Ijtihad in Fatwa
Stating that knowledge of qawa'id is the first benefit and key to ijtihad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the relationship between qawa'id and ijtihad in the Hanafi madhhab and explain why mastery of qawa'id enables a mufti to perform ijtihad within fatwa.

Core Idea
Mastery of qawa’id elevates the faqih to ijtihad, even in fatwa.

This passage from Sharah al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair lays the foundation for the entire work: the first benefit is knowledge of the qawa'id (legal maxims). These qawa'id are described as the true usul al-fiqh, and by them a faqih ascends to the level of ijtihad—even within the context of fatwa. The author also assures the reader that he transmits only sound, relied-upon positions and flags weak ones. The commentary further clarifies the epistemological distinction between 'ilm (knowledge of universals) and ma'rifah (knowledge of particulars), underlining the precision required in understanding qawa'id.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first benefit
Locate the phrase 'الأَوَّلُ مَعْرِفَةُ الْقَوَاعِدِ' (the first: knowledge of the qawa'id). Recognize that this is the primary purpose of the book.
The author prioritizes qawa'id over furu'.
2
Note the function of qawa'id
Understand that furu' (branches) are referred to these qawa'id and rulings are built upon them. They are not mere summaries but active principles of derivation.
3
Recognize their status as usul al-fiqh
The text explicitly states: 'وَهِيَ أَصُوْلُ الْفِقْهِ فِي الْحَقِيْقَةِ' (they are in reality the principles of fiqh). This elevates qawa'id to a foundational level.
In Hanafi thought, qawa'id are intermediate principles between usul al-fiqh and furu'.
4
Understand the outcome: ijtihad
The text says 'بِهَا يَرْتَقِى الْفَقِيهُ إِلى دَرَجَةِ الإِجْتِهَادِ وَلَوْ فِي الْفَتْوَىٰ' (by them the faqih rises to the level of ijtihad, even in fatwa). This shows that ijtihad is not limited to absolute mujtahids; a mufti can attain it through mastery of qawa'id.
Ijtihad here means takhrij and tarjih within the madhhab.
5
Analyze the author's methodology
Note the author's commitment to reliability: he transmits only what is 'الصَّحِيحَ الْمُعْتَمَدَ' (sound and relied-upon) and when a branch is based on a weak opinion or narration, he points it out.
This underscores the importance of authority levels in Hanafi fatwa (zahir riwayah, nawadir, etc.).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الأَوَّلُ مَعْرِفَةُ الْقَوَاعِدِ الَّتِى تُرَدُّ إِلَيْهَا وَ فَرَّعُوا الأحكام عَلَيْهَا وَهِيَ أَصُوْلُ الْفِقْهِ فِي الْحَقِيْقَةِ وَبِهَا يَرْتَقِى الْفَقِيهُ إِلى دَرَجَةِ الإِجْتِهَادِ وَلَوْ فِي الْفَتْوَىٰ وَ أَكْثَرُ فُرُوْعِهَا طَفِرَتْ به فِي كُتُبِ غَرِيْبَةٍ أَوْ عَثَرْتُ بِهِ فِي غَيْرِ مَظَنّةِ إلَّا أنّى بحَوْلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى وَ قُوَّتِهِ لَا أَنْقُلْ إِلَّا الصَّحِيحَ الْمُعْتَمَدَ فِي الْمَذْهَبِ وَ إِنْ كَانَ مُفَرَّعاً عَلَى قَوْلِ ضَعِيْفٍ أَوْ رِوَايَةٍ ضَعِيفَةٍ نَبِّهْتُ عَلَى ذَلِكَ غَالِباً. ترجمه: پہلا ان قواعد کو پہچانے میں جن کی طرف ان کولو نادیا جاتا ہے اور احکام کو اس پر متفرع کرتے ہیں اور وہ حقیقت میں فقہ کے اصول ہیں اور ان ہی کے ذریعہ فقیہ اجتہاد کے درجہ تک پہنچتا ہے اگر چہ فتوی میں ہو۔ اور اگر فروعات کی تحصیل میں نادر کتابوں میں کامیاب ہو ایا ایسی جگہ پر مطلع ہوا جو گمان میں نہیں تھی مگر یہ اللہ کی طاق اورانہ کی قدرت سے میں صرف وہی نقل کرتا ہوں جو سیح ہو اور مذہب میں معتمد علیہ ہو اوراگر کسی کمزور قول یا کمزور روایت تفریح ہو گئی تو میں نے اکثر اس پر منتخب کر دیا۔ تشریح: المعرفة: بمعنی پہچانا، جانا اکثر لوگوں نے علم اور معرفت کے درمیان فرق بیان کیا ہے )) کا اطلاق اور اک کلی اور مرکب پر جبکہ معرفت کا اطلاق اور اک جزئی اور بسیط پر ہوتا ہے۔ اسی وجہ سے کہا جاتا ؟ | عرفت الله نه كه علمته (۲) علم جہل سابق کا تقاضہ نہیں کرتا بخلاف معرفت کے اسی وجہ سے اللہ کے لئے عارف نہیں کہا جا سکتا اور عالم کہا جا سکتا ہے نیز اصولیین کی ایک جماعت نے تصریح کی ہے انہیں میں سے آمدی ہیں ہم
The first: Knowledge of the rules (qawa'id) to which [branches] are referred and upon which rulings are branched; they are in reality the principles (usul) of fiqh, and by them the faqih rises to the level of ijtihad, even in fatwa. And many of their branches (furu') have escaped me in rare books or I have come across them in unexpected places; but by the power and might of Allah, I only transmit what is sound and relied upon in the madhhab. And if a branch is based on a weak opinion or weak narration, I mostly point that out. Translation: The first is to recognize those rules to which rulings are referred and upon which they are branched; they are in reality the principles of fiqh, and by them the faqih reaches the level of ijtihad, even if in fatwa. And if in acquiring branches I succeeded in rare books or was informed in an unexpected place, yet by Allah's power and might I only transmit what is sound and relied upon in the madhhab. If a branch is based on a weak opinion or weak narration, I mostly draw attention to it. Commentary: Al-Ma'rifah: meaning to recognize, to know. Most people have distinguished between 'ilm and ma'rifah: 'ilm applies to universal and compound matters, while ma'rifah applies to particular and simple matters. For this reason, it is said 'I recognized Allah' not 'I knew Allah' (with knowledge of preceding ignorance). 'Ilm does not require preceding ignorance, unlike ma'rifah; hence one cannot say 'arif for Allah but can say 'alim. Also a group of usuliyyun have specified this; among them is al-Aamidi.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage sets out the first benefit of the book: knowledge of the qawa'id (legal maxims) to which furu' (branches) are referred and upon which rulings are based. These qawa'id are described as the true usul al-fiqh. Mastery of them elevates the faqih to the level of ijtihad, even if only within the context of fatwa (i.e., tarjih and application). The author then assures the reader that he only transmits sound and relied-upon positions of the madhhab, noting when a branch is based on a weak opinion. The Urdu commentary further distinguishes 'ilm (knowledge of universals) from ma'rifah (knowledge of particulars), noting that 'ilm does not presuppose ignorance while ma'rifah does, which is why Allah is known as 'Alim but not 'Arif. This distinction underscores the precision required in understanding the qawa'id.

Key Terms
القواعد (al-qawa'id): Legal maxims that are the principles (usul) of fiqh, to which furu' are referred
المعرفة (al-ma'rifah): Knowledge of particular, simple matters that requires preceding ignorance
الاجتهاد (al-ijtihad): The level of independent reasoning reached through mastery of qawa'id, even in fatwa

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what does knowledge of qawa'id enable the faqih to achieve?
A) The ability to issue fatwas without consulting any sources.
B) The level of ijtihad, even in fatwa.
C) Memorization of all furu'.
D) The title of 'alim.

Key Takeaway
The qawa'id are the true usul al-fiqh; mastering them enables a faqih to achieve ijtihad in fatwa.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
15 min
The First Rule: Ma'rifah al-Qawa'id and Distinction from 'Ilm
Author explains first rule and defines ma'rifah in contrast to 'ilm

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Hanafi conceptual distinction between ma'rifah and 'ilm and apply it to understanding the nature of qawa'id in fatwa methodology.

Core Idea
Ma'rifah recognizes particulars with prior ignorance; 'ilm knows universals without prior ignorance.

This lesson unpacks the opening rule of the book: the necessity of knowing the qawa'id (principles) to which furu' (branches) are traced. The author emphasizes that these qawa'id are the true usul al-fiqh and that mastery of them elevates the faqih to ijtihad, even in fatwa. He then clarifies his scholarly method—transmitting only sahih, mu'tamad rulings and flagging weak opinions. Finally, he dives into a conceptual analysis distinguishing ma'rifah (recognition) from 'ilm (knowledge), a distinction critical for understanding how qawa'id function as universal principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first rule's purpose
Recognize that the first rule (al-awwal) is about 'ma'rifah al-qawa'id'—knowing the foundational principles to which all furu' are referred. The author says these qawa'id are in reality the principles of fiqh and elevate the faqih to ijtihad.
This is not a substantive legal maxim but a meta-rule about the necessity of mastering qawa'id.
2
Note the author's methodological commitment
The author states he only transmits what is sahih and mu'tamad within the madhhab, and if he ever includes a weak opinion, he alerts to it. This establishes the reliability hierarchy for the work.
This is a typical 'rasm al-mufti' safeguard.
3
Grasp the core distinction between ma'rifah and 'ilm
The commentary explains that ma'rifah applies to particular/simple things and requires prior ignorance, while 'ilm applies to universal/composite things and does not require prior ignorance. For example, we say 'arifta Allah (I recognized Allah) but not 'alimtu Allah in that sense.
This distinction is debated; focus on the Hanafi position.
4
Examine the evidence for the distinction
The author cites hadith (e.g., 'Recognize Allah in prosperity...'), the verse 'la ta'lamunahum Allahu ya'lamuhum', and the story from Sahih al-Bukhari to support that ma'rifah requires prior knowledge of the essence.
The evidence is used to argue that ma'rifah presupposes some prior acquaintance.
5
Apply the distinction to the concept of qawa'id
Understanding that ma'rifah is recognition of particulars helps clarify that qawa'id are universal principles ('ilm) that are known and then applied to particular cases through 'rad al-furu' ilayha' (reverting branches to roots).
The mufti must have 'ilm of the qawa'id to practice ma'rifah of particular cases.

اگر ان کو پہلے سے علم نہ ہوتا تو یہ لوگ اپنے رب کو نہ پہچانتے ان لوگوں کا قول ہوا میں ار کیا جو یہ کہتے ہیں ۔ کہ معرفت جہل سابق کا تقاضہ کرتی ہے، بخلاف علم کے بلکہ معاملہ برعکس ہے فلی حفظ۔ نرد الفروع The first is the recognition of the rules to which [furu'] are referred and upon which rulings are branched, and they are in reality the foundations of fiqh, and by them the faqih rises to the level of ijtihad, even if in fatwa. And most of its furu' have jumped into rare books, or I have come across them in unexpected places, except that by the might and power of Allah, I only transmit what is sound and relied upon in the madhhab, and if it is branched on a weak opinion or weak narration, I have generally alerted to that. Translation: The first is in recognizing those rules to which they are referred and rulings are branched upon them, and they are in reality the principles of fiqh, and by them the faqih reaches the degree of ijtihad, even in fatwa. And if in acquiring furu' I succeed in rare books or come across a place I did not suspect, but by Allah's power I only transmit what is sound and relied upon in the madhhab, and if a weak saying or weak narration is branched, I have generally indicated that. Commentary: al-Ma'rifah: meaning to recognize, to know. Most people have explained the difference between 'ilm and ma'rifah. [The former] applies to universal and composite, while ma'rifah applies to particular and simple. For that reason it is said: 'I recognized Allah, not that I knew Him.' (2) 'Ilm does not require prior ignorance, unlike ma'rifah. For that reason, Allah cannot be called 'arif but can be called 'alim. Also, a group of usuliyyun, among them al-Amidi, have stated that ma'rifah does not apply to pre-eternal knowledge. Allamah Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn 'Imad al-Afqahi clarified in the supercommentary on Sharh Minhaj al-'Ibadi by Allamah 'Abd al-Rahim al-Asnawi that there is a problem in the speech of both parties. First, because they divided knowledge into simple and composite, which is why Allamah Ibn al-Hajib said in his Mukhtasar: 'Knowledge is two types: knowledge of the simple, then he said: and knowledge of the composite.' Second, because in the names of Allah, the application of what is not permitted to Allah is not correct, although in hadith it is reported: 'Recognize Allah in prosperity, He will recognize you in adversity.' Allamah Turqi interpreted 'wa laqad 'alimtum alladhina i'tadayu minkum fi al-sabt' as 'ariftum', meaning you recognized their persons, and it was said you knew their rulings. The difference between 'ilm and ma'rifah is that ma'rifah is directed to the essence of a thing, while 'ilm is directed to the states of a thing. So when you say 'ariftu Zaydan', you mean his personality; when you say 'alimtu Zaydan', you mean knowledge of his states, i.e., his virtue and deficiency. In the first case, the verb is transitive to one object according to Sibawayh, but according to another opinion it is transitive to two objects. Al-Akhfash al-Nahwi mentioned: 'And I knew Zayd and I did not recognize him' and in the verse 'You do not recognize them, Allah recognizes them'. In both, 'ilm is in the meaning of ma'rifah. Allamah Ibn al-'Imad said that this shows that ma'rifah also requires prior knowledge. In Sahih al-Bukhari: An angel comes to people while they are standing, and the angel says: 'I am your Lord.' People say: 'We seek refuge in Allah from you. You are not our Lord, and we are in our place until our Lord comes. When our Lord comes, we will recognize Him.' Then Allah will come to them in the form they recognize, and Allah will say: 'I am your Lord.' They will say: 'You are our Lord' and they will fall in prostration. If they did not have prior knowledge of the Lord, the Messenger (s.a.w.) would not say: 'He will come to them in the form they recognize.' Then it is possible that how they recognized the Lord. It will be said that they saw Allah either in the barzakh or at the time of death, as in the hadith: 'You will not see your Lord until you die.' And Allah said: 'And We made you nations and tribes that you may recognize one another.' If they had no prior knowledge, they would not recognize their Lord. This becomes the statement of those who say that ma'rifah requires prior ignorance, unlike 'ilm; rather the matter is the opposite, so memorize. 'Rad al-furu' ilayha' means turning the particulars back to those rules by which those particulars were derived, and the method of deriving particulars from universals is to combine the minor premise with the major premise to facilitate extraction, as it is said.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is the explanation of the first rule of the book. The author states the importance of knowing the qawa'id to which furu' are traced, as they are the usul al-fiqh. He also outlines his methodology of only transmitting sahih and mu'tamad rulings. The commentary then delves into a detailed discussion of the term 'ma'rifah' (recognition) versus 'ilm' (knowledge), citing various scholars and hadith to clarify the difference. This is a key conceptual analysis for understanding the nature of qawa'id as universal principles.

Key Terms
المعرفة (al-ma'rifah): recognition of particular/simple things, often contrasted with 'ilm which is knowledge of universals/composites and does not require prior ignorance.
العلم (al-'ilm): knowledge that applies to universal and composite concepts, does not require prior ignorance, and can be applied to Allah (as 'alim).
قواعد (qawa'id): the universal principles of fiqh to which particular cases are referred.
رد الفروع إلى القواعد (rad al-furu' ila al-qawa'id): the method of reverting particular cases to the universal principles from which they are derived.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentary, why can Allah be called 'alim but not 'arif?
A) Because 'arif requires a physical encounter, which is impossible for Allah.
B) Because 'ilm does not require prior ignorance, while ma'rifah does, and Allah's knowledge is eternal, devoid of prior ignorance.
C) Because the word 'arif is linguistically forbidden to use for Allah in any context.
D) Because ma'rifah applies only to created beings.

Key Takeaway
The first rule of the book emphasizes that mastery of qawa'id (universal principles) is the foundation of ijtihad and fatwa, and the precise distinction between ma'rifah (particular recognition) and 'ilm (universal knowledge) is essential for applying these principles to cases.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
beginner
6 min
The First Major Maxim: Certainty Not Removed by Doubt
Introduces the first qawida kubra with its historical compilation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first major Hanafi qawida kubra, describe its historical origin, and apply it to a simple fiqh scenario.

Core Idea
Certainty holds until a stronger proof overcomes it; mere doubt never overturns what is established.

This lesson introduces the foundational principle that governs vast areas of Hanafi law: certainty prevails over doubt. We will trace the story of its compilation by Imam Abu Tahir al-Dabbas and understand the maxim's binding force.

Guided Path
1
Understand the historical context
Learn that the maxim was compiled by Imam Abu Tahir al-Dabbas as part of 17 qawaid. The story of al-Harawi illustrates the guarded nature of these principles.
The secrecy highlights the value of qawaid in preserving the methodology of the madhhab.
2
Identify the maxim's wording and translation
Memorize the Arabic: اليقين لا يزول بالشك and its English: Certainty is not removed by doubt.
3
Define key terms
Yaqin (certainty) is a firm conviction that leaves no room for doubt. Shakk (doubt) is uncertainty between two possibilities, neither outweighing the other.
In Hanafi usul, yaqin can only be overturned by another yaqin or a preponderant probability (zann ghalib) in certain contexts.
4
Apply the maxim to a case
Consider a person certain of wudu but later doubting nullification. The maxim rules that the original state of purity remains intact.
This applies across all fiqh chapters: taharah, contracts, evidence, etc.
5
Note exceptions
If doubt becomes frequent (kathrat al-shakk), the ruling may shift under the maxim 'hardship brings ease' (المشقة تجلب التيسير).
The exception does not contradict the main maxim but limits its scope in chronic cases.

ہے اور میں نے ان جزئیات کو ایسی ایسی کتابوں میں تلاش کیا۔ جن کتابوں تک ہر ایک کی رسائی نہیں تھی چونکہ کتا ہیں دستیاب نہیں تھیں ۔ اور ایسی ایسی جگہوں سے ان جزئیات و فروعات پر میں مطلع ہوا، جہاں وہم و گمان بھی نہیں تھا۔ لیکن یہ سب کچھ بفضل خدا وندی ہے اور حتی الامکان میں نے اس کتاب میں اقوال صحیح کو نقل کرنے کی کوشش کی ہے اور جن پر مذہب میں اعتماد کیا ہے وہی روایات فقہ کی میں نے ذکر کی ہے اور اگر کسی جگہ قول ضعیف یا ضعیف روایت پر تفریع کر دی گئی ہے تو اکثر و بیشتر میں نے اس پر متنبہ کر دیا ہے فى كتـب عـزيبـة يـا عثرت في غير مظنة سے یہ شک و شبہ نہیں ہوں چاہئے کہ غیر صحیح اقوال یا ظاہر الروایہ مذہب کے خلاف روایات کو میں نے کتاب میں بھر مارا ہے۔
وَحُكِيَ أَنَّ الإِمَامَ أَبَا طَاهِرٍ الدَّبَّاسُ جَمَعَ قَوَاعِدَ مَذْهَبِ أَبِي حَنِيْفَةَ رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ سَبْعَةَ عَشَرَ قَاعِدَةً وَرَدَّهُ إِلَيْهَا وَلَهُ حِكَايَةٌ مَعَ أَبِي سَعِيدِ الْهَرَوِيِّ الشَّافِعِي رَحِمَهُ اللَّهُ فَأَنَّهُ لَمَّا بَلَغَهُ ذَلِكَ سَافَرَ إِلَيْهِ وَكَانَ أَبُو طَاهِرٍ ضَرِيْرًا يُكَرِّرُ كُلُّ لَيْلَةٍ تِلْكَ الْقَوَاعِدَ بِمَسْجِدِهِ بَعْدَ أَنْ يَخْرُجَ النَّاسَ مِنْهُ فَالْتَفَّ الْهَرَوِيُّ بِحَصِيرَةٍ وَخَرَجَ النَّاسَ وَأَغْلَقَ أَبُو طَاهِرٍ بَابَ الْمَسْجِدِ وَسَرَدَ مِنْهَا سَبْعَةً فَحَصَلَتْ لِلْهَرَوِيِّ سُعْلَةٌ فَأَحَسَّ بِهِ أَبُو طَاهِرٍ فَضَرَبَهُ وَأَخْرَجَهُ مِنَ الْمَسْجِدِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يُكَرِّرْهَا فِيْهِ بَعْدَ ذَلِكَ فَرَجَعَ الْهَرَوِيُّ إِلَى أَصْحَابِهِ وَتَلَاهَا عَلَيْهِمْ. وہ سات قواعد جو انہوں نے سنے تھے ان میں سے کچھ یہ تھے۔ (1) اليقين لا يزول بالشک: یقین سے ثابت شدہ بات محض شک سے ختم نہیں ہوتی۔
And it is narrated that Imam Abu Tahir al-Dabbas collected the maxims of the madhhab of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, seventeen maxims, and referred them back to him. And there is a story with Abu Sa'id al-Harawi al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him: when that reached him, he traveled to him. And Abu Tahir was blind, and he used to repeat those maxims every night in his mosque after the people had left it. So al-Harawi wrapped himself in a mat, and the people left, and Abu Tahir closed the door of the mosque and recited seven of them in sequence. Then al-Harawi had a cough, so Abu Tahir sensed him, struck him, and expelled him from the mosque. Then he did not repeat them there after that. So al-Harawi returned to his companions and recited them to them. The seven maxims that he heard, among them were these: (1) Certainty is not removed by doubt: A matter established by certainty is not nullified by mere doubt.
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage is from the commentary (sharh) of Al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir by Ibn Nujaym. It serves two purposes: first, the author explains his own methodology of relying on authentic narrations and rare books, warning against weak reports. Second, it presents a famous historical anecdote about Imam Abu Tahir al-Dabbas, who compiled the principles of the Hanafi madhhab into seventeen maxims. The story of al-Harawi al-Shafi'i secretly listening and memorizing seven maxims underscores the great value and secrecy of these qawaid. The passage then introduces the first and greatest of these maxims: 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك). This maxim is the first of the five major qawaid kubra and applies across all chapters of fiqh. Its meaning is that once a matter is established with certainty (yaqin), mere doubt (shakk) does not overturn it. For example, if one is certain of having performed wudu, doubt about its nullification does not remove that state; the original certainty prevails.

Key Terms
اليقين (al-yaqin): Certainty – a state of knowledge or conviction that leaves no room for doubt; in legal terms, it is the basis for upholding a ruling until a definitive contrary is established.
الشك (al-shakk): Doubt – uncertainty between two possibilities, neither outweighing the other; insufficient to invalidate a prior certainty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the first qawida kubra, if a person is certain he performed wudu but later doubts whether it was nullified, what is the ruling?
A) He must repeat wudu because doubt cannot be ignored.
B) His wudu is considered intact because certainty is not removed by doubt.
C) He must repeat wudu if the doubt arises frequently.
D) He should do istinja and then repeat wudu.

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' safeguards legal continuity and is the foundation of the Hanafi qawaid system.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
beginner
6 min
The Origin and Significance of the Five Major Hanafi Legal Maxims
Historical anecdote introducing the five major qawaid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five major Hanafi legal maxims and explain their role in ifta and fiqh derivation.

Core Idea
The five major maxims are foundational principles that organize and simplify Hanafi jurisprudence.

This lesson recounts the famed story of Abu Tahir al-Dabbas, a Hanafi jurist who collected and expanded a set of legal maxims from the school of Imam Abu Hanifa. The Shafi'i scholar Abu Sa'id al-Harawi's arduous journey to learn these maxims underscores their immense value. The five maxims listed here are the pillars of Hanafi qawa'id, used by muftis to derive rulings consistently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical context
Recognize that Abu Tahir al-Dabbas initially collected 17 qawaid from the Hanafi madhhab and later expanded them to over 200.
The story shows the early systematization of Hanafi legal theory.
2
Trace the transmission narrative
Understand how Abu Sa'id al-Harawi travelled to learn these maxims and managed to hear seven of them, of which five are recorded.
The incident emphasizes the high value placed on these maxims.
3
List the five major maxims
Write down the five maxims exactly as given: اليقين لا يزول بالشك, المشقة تجلب التيسير, الضرر يزال, العادة محكمة, الأمور بمقاصدها.
These are known as al-qawa'id al-kubra.
4
Understand each maxim's meaning
Translate and explain each maxim in simple terms: Certainty is not removed by doubt; Hardship brings ease; Harm must be removed; Custom is authoritative; Matters are judged by intentions.
Each maxim has specific applications in fiqh.
5
Appreciate the significance
Reflect on why these maxims are essential for a mufti: they provide consistent principles for issuing fatwas across various chapters of fiqh.
They are not sources but organizing tools derived from the sources.

علامہ ابن نجیم المصری ایک حکایت نقل کر رہے ہیں جس کو علامہ جلال الدین سیوطی نے اور صاحب فتح القدیر نے بھی نقل کیا ہے اور اس حکایت کا مقصد صرف ان قواعد کی اہمیت کو بیان کرنا ہے کہ جن کے لئے اتنے بڑے عالم سعید الہروی الشافعی نے بھی سفر کیا اور کس طریقہ پر ان قواعد میں سے کچھ کو حاصل کرنے کے بعد اپنے اصحاب کو جا کر سنایا۔ واقعہ یہ ہے کہ ابو طاہر ( محمد بن سفیان) دباس حنفی نے امام ابی حنیفہ کے مذہب کے مطابق سترہ قواعد کو جمع کیا اور وضاحت کے طور پر ان کو بار بار پڑھتے اور مشق کرتے تھے تا کہ ان قواعد میں اضافہ ہو جائے لہذا وہ قواعد پچاس سے زائد ہو گئے بلکہ دو سو تک ان کی تعداد پہنچ گئی ابوسعید البروی الشافعی کو ان قواعد کے بارے میں معلوم ہوا تو ان کے لئے انہوں نے باقاعدہ سفر کی صعوبتیں اور مشکلات اٹھا کر ابو طاہر الدباس کے پاس پہنچ گئے ابوطاہر نا بینا تھے اور لوگوں کے مسجد سے چلے جانے کے بعد مسجد کا دروازہ بند کر کے ان قواعد کو ترتیب سے ہر رات کو دوہرایا کرتے تھے اور مشق کرتے تھے لوگوں کے چلے جانے کے بعد یہ خیال کر کے کہ سب نمازی چلے گئے مسجد کا دروازہ بند کر کے ان قواعد کو تسلسل کے ساتھ ترتیب سے پڑھنا شروع کر دیا اور ابوسعید الہروی الشافعی صف میں لپٹ گئے انہوں نے سات ہی قواعد کو ترتیب سے پڑھا تھا کہ ابوسعید الہر دی الشافعی کو کھانسی اٹھ گئی تو ابوطاہر کو معلوم ہو گیا کہ مسجد میں کوئی ہے لہذا انہوں نے ابو سعید الہروی الشافعی کو مار کر مسجد سے نکال دیا پھر اس کے بعد انہوں نے اس معمول کو یعنی ہر رات کو مسجد سے لوگوں کے چلے جانے کے بعد جو ان قواعد کو پڑھنے کا تھا ترک کر دیا اور ابوسعید نے جو سات قواعد ان سے سنے تھے وہ جا کر اپنے اصحاب کو سنا دئیے وہ سات قواعد جو انہوں نے سنے تھے ان میں سے کچھ یہ تھے۔
(1) اليقين لا يزول بالشک: یقین سے ثابت شدہ بات محض شک سے ختم نہیں ہوتی۔
(۲) المشقة تجلب التيسير : مشقت سہولت کا باعث بنتی ہے۔ (۳) الضرر يزال : ضرر دور کیا جائے گا۔ (۴) العادة محكمة: عرف و عادت کی حیثیت حکم کی ہوگی۔
(۵) الامور بمقاصدها امور میں مقاصد کا اعتبار ہوگا۔
Allama Ibn Nujaym al-Misri is narrating a story that Allama Jalal al-Din al-Suyuti and the author of Fath al-Qadir also narrated, and the purpose of this story is only to explain the importance of those qawaid for which such a great scholar as Sa'id al-Harawi al-Shafi'i traveled, and in what manner after acquiring some of those qawaid he went and taught them to his companions. The incident is that Abu Tahir (Muhammad ibn Sufyan) al-Dabbas al-Hanafi collected seventeen qawaid according to the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa, and he would repeatedly read and practice them for clarity so that these qawaid would increase. Therefore those qawaid became more than fifty, in fact their number reached two hundred. Abu Sa'id al-Barwi al-Shafi'i learned about these qawaid, so he undertook the hardships and difficulties of travel to reach Abu Tahir al-Dabbas. Abu Tahir was blind, and after people left the mosque, he would lock the door and repeatedly recite these qawaid in order every night and practice them. After the people left, thinking that all the worshippers had gone, he locked the door and began to read these qawaid in sequence. And Abu Sa'id al-Harawi al-Shafi'i rolled up in the row. He had read only seven qawaid in order when Abu Sa'id al-Harwi al-Shafi'i coughed, so Abu Tahir realized that someone was in the mosque. Therefore he beat Abu Sa'id al-Harawi al-Shafi'i and expelled him from the mosque. Then after that, he abandoned that routine, i.e., reciting these qawaid every night after people left the mosque. And Abu Sa'id, having heard seven qawaid from him, went and taught them to his companions. Some of those seven qawaid that he heard were these: (1) Certainty is not removed by doubt: A matter established by certainty does not end by mere doubt. (2) Hardship brings ease: Hardship becomes a cause of ease. (3) Harm must be removed: Harm will be removed. (4) Custom is authoritative: Custom and habit have the status of a ruling. (5) Matters are judged by intentions: In matters, intentions are considered.
Source pages p. 52

Commentary
This passage is a historical anecdote from the author's front matter. It recounts how Abu Tahir al-Dabbas, a Hanafi jurist, collected seventeen qawaid (legal maxims) from the madhhab of Abu Hanifa and later expanded them to over two hundred. The Shafi'i scholar Abu Sa'id al-Harawi traveled to learn these maxims and managed to overhear seven of them before being discovered. The author lists five of those seven: 1) Certainty is not removed by doubt, 2) Hardship brings ease, 3) Harm must be removed, 4) Custom is authoritative, 5) Matters are judged by intentions. These are the five major maxims (al-qawa'id al-kubra) of Hanafi fiqh, which form the foundation for deriving many rulings. The story emphasizes the high value placed on these maxims and the lengths scholars went to preserve and transmit them.

Key Terms
قواعد (qawa'id): Legal maxims or foundational principles of fiqh that encompass many individual rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) اليقين لا يزول بالشک
B) المشقة تجلب التيسير
C) الضرر يزال
D) الأمر إذا ضاق اتسع

Key Takeaway
The five major Hanafi legal maxims encapsulate the spirit of the madhhab and serve as essential tools for deriving and applying rulings.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate

Definition of Qa'idah and the First Maxim
Defines qa'idah and presents the first major maxim.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define 'qa'idah' according to Hanafi fuqaha and state the first major qa'idah (لا ثواب الا بالنية) with its scope as a universal principle in iftaa.

Core Idea
A qa'idah is a universal ruling covering all its particulars; the first maxim: no reward without intention.

This lesson unpacks the foundational term 'qa'idah' as used by Hanafi jurists and introduces the first of the major legal maxims. Understanding what qualifies as a qa'idah is essential before applying it to derive rulings. The author also addresses why the book assumes prior knowledge of such definitions.

Guided Path
1
Locate the definition of qa'idah
Find the sentence where the author explains the technical meaning of qa'idah according to the fuqaha. Note how it differs from the lexicographical meaning and the broader usage by other scholars.
The fuqaha definition requires application to all particulars, unlike the nahw definition which only requires most.
2
Identify the scope of 'universal rules' in this work
The author specifies that by 'qawa'id kulliyyah' he means rules that are not subordinate to another rule. Understand why this matters: these are the top-level maxims used for derivation.
Even if some particulars fall outside the rule, it is still considered a kulli rule if it governs most.
3
Analyze the objection and its response
Read the objection that the author should have defined qa'idah first. Understand the author's response: this book is for advanced scholars. This highlights the intended audience and the pedagogical approach.
The response affirms that the reader is expected to already know basic usul definitions.
4
State the first qa'idah and its literal meaning
The first qa'idah is 'لا ثواب الا بالنية' (There is no reward except with intention). Repeat it in Arabic and English. Recognize it as a parallel to the well-known maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
The translation given in the passage is 'Without intention, no reward is obtained.'
5
Connect the qa'idah to its application in iftaa
Consider how this maxim is used by a mufti: when evaluating an act of worship, if the intention is absent, the act may be valid but carries no reward. Also, it applies in cases like oaths and contracts where intention can alter the ruling.
This maxim is a kubra (major) rule and is foundational in Hanafi fatwa methodology.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمنِ الرَّحِيمِ القاعدة الأولى الْفَنُ الْاَوَّلُ قَوْل فِي القَوَاعِدِ الكُلِّيَّةِ . :ترجمه : فن اول قواعد کلیہ کے بیان میں۔ تشریح : علامہ ابن نجیم مصری المتوفی ۷۹۰ ھ صاحب الاشباہ والنظائر نے اپنی کتاب الاشباہ والنظائر کوسات فنون پر مرتب فرمایا جن میں فن اول قواعد کلیہ کے بیان میں ہے۔ قواعد، قاعدہ کی جمع ہے جس کے لغوی معنی جڑا اور بنیاد کے ہیں اور اصطلاح نحات میں اس حکم اکثٹری کو کہتے ہیں جو اپنی اکثر جزئیات پر منطبق ہوتا کہ اکثر جزئیات کے احکام اس حکم اکثری کے ذریعہ معلوم ہو سکیں۔ فقہاء کے نزدیک اس حکم کلی کو کہتے ہیں جو اپنی تمام جزئیات پر صادق آئے اور اس حکم کلی کے تحت آنے والی تمام جزئیات کے احکام معلوم ہو سکیں۔ یہاں پر قواعد کلیہ سے مراد وہ قواعد ہیں جو کسی دوسرے قاعدہ کے تحت نہ ہوں بلکہ اس قاعدہ کے تحت کچھ جزئیات و فروعات ہوں اگر چہ بعض افراد قاعدہ سے خارج ہو جائیں۔ اعتراض : مصنف کو اولا قاعدہ کی تعریف کرنی چاہئے تھی اس کے بعد اس سے متعلق امور ذ کر کرتے ۔ جواب: یہ کتاب ابتدائی طلبہ کے لیے نہیں لکھی گئی ہے جن کو قاعدہ کے معنی اور اس کی تعریف اور فروع کی ضرورت پیش آتی ہے بلکہ یہ کتاب منتہی طلبہ کے لیے لکھی گئی ہے جو اس طرح کے امور سے پہلے ہی سے واقف ہوتے ہیں جیسے فضلاء مدرسین ، قضاۃ اور مفتیان کرام وغیرہ جیسا کہ مقدمہ میں مصنف اشارہ کر چکے ہیں۔ الأولى لا ثَواب الا بالنية. ترجمه: پیار قاعدہ، بدون ارادہ ثواب نہیں ملتا ہے۔
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The first rule: The first art is a statement in universal rules. Translation: The first art is concerning the statement of universal rules. Explanation: 'Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri (d. 970 AH?), author of al-Ashbah wa al-Naza'ir, arranged his book into seven arts, among which the first art is concerning universal rules. 'Qawa'id' is the plural of 'qa'idah', which in lexical meaning is 'root' or 'foundation'. In the terminology of schoolars, it is a predominant ruling that applies to most of its particulars, such that the rulings of most particulars can be known through this predominant ruling. In the view of jurists, it is a universal ruling that applies to all its particulars, and the rulings of all particulars under it can be known. Here, 'universal rules' refer to those rules that are not under another rule, but rather have particulars and branches under them, even if some individuals fall outside the rule. Objection: The author should have first defined a rule, then discussed its related matters. Answer: This book was not written for beginners who need the meaning and definition of a rule and its branches. Rather, it is written for advanced students who are already familiar with such matters, such as eminent teachers, judges, and muftis, as the author indicated in the introduction. The first: There is no reward except with intention. Translation: The first rule: Without intention, no reward is obtained.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage defines the key term 'qa'idah' (rule/principle) as understood in Hanafi usul. The author distinguishes between the lexicographical meaning (foundation, root) and the technical usage. The 'fuqaha' definition is more precise: a universal ruling that applies to all its particulars. The author then clarifies that 'universal rules' in this work are those that are not subordinates of another rule; they are themselves the basis for deriving rulings. He anticipates an objection: why not start with a definition? He answers that the book is for advanced scholars who already know these definitions. Then he presents the first qa'idah: 'لا ثواب الا بالنية' (There is no reward except with intention). This is the principle that actions are judged by intentions, specifically regarding reward. In Hanafi fiqh, this maxim is fundamental for acts of worship and also relevant in other areas like oaths and transactions.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'idah): A universal ruling that applies to all its particulars, from which the rulings of those particulars can be known.
نية (niyyah): Intention; a prerequisite for reward in acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the definition of 'qa'idah' according to the fuqaha?
A) A ruling that applies to most of its particulars.
B) A universal ruling that applies to all its particulars.
C) A root or foundation in the Arabic language.
D) A ruling that is always mentioned with its exceptions.

Key Takeaway
A qa'idah in Hanafi usul is a universal ruling covering all its particulars, and the first major maxim is 'لا ثواب الا بالنية' (no reward without intention), which governs reward in acts of worship.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
beginner
8 min
The First Major Maxim: No Reward Without Intention
Defining the first major maxim and the concept of intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the first major maxim, explain the definition of intention according to the Hanafi mutakallimun, and classify acts of worship as maqsoodah or ghair maqsoodah with regard to the role of intention.

Core Idea
Intention is essential for reward, but not always for validity of worship.

This lesson introduces the foundational maxim of Islamic jurisprudence: 'There is no reward except with intention.' We will unpack the definition of intention (niyyah) as a legal concept, clarify its scope, and apply it to different types of worship. Understanding this maxim is critical for every mufti, as it underpins the analysis of sincerity and legal effect across all chapters of fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its source
State the maxim in Arabic: 'لا ثواب إلا بالنية'. Note that it is derived from the hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنيات' and is the first of the major universal principles in al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair.
The maxim is a qa'ida kubra (major principle) that applies to all acts, especially worship.
2
Define niyyah terminologically
Understand the definition given: 'directing the heart to perform an action, for attaining benefit or repelling harm, in the present or future.' Recognize that this definition covers both commanded and prohibited acts, and both commission and omission.
The author broadens the definition to include acts that incur punishment, not just reward.
3
Differentiate between ibadat maqsoodah and ghair maqsoodah
Identify that maqsoodah acts (e.g., salah, zakat, sawm, hajj) are intended in themselves and require intention for validity, while ghair maqsoodah acts (e.g., wudu', ghusl) are means and do not require intention for validity, but intention is still needed for reward.
This distinction is unique to Hanafi fiqh and has practical consequences for fatwa.
4
Apply the maxim to specific cases
For wudu' and ghusl: intention is not a condition of validity (sihha) but is required for reward (thawab). For salah, zakah, etc., intention is a condition of both validity and reward.
This is stated explicitly by the mashā'ikh in many places of fiqh.
5
Evaluate the role of intention in fatwa
As a mufti, when issuing a fatwa, you must determine whether intention affects the validity or merely the reward of an act. This maxim guides the distinction and helps resolve issues like repeating wudu' without intention.
Always refer to the mufta bihi position: intention is not required for validity of wudu' in the Hanafi school.

الأولى لا ثَواب الا بالنية.
ترجمه: پیار قاعدہ، بدون ارادہ ثواب نہیں ملتا ہے۔
تشریح : نیت اکثر بتشدید الیاء اور کبھی کبھی بدون تشدید بحالت تخفیف مستعمل ہوتی ہے ، نیت کے لغوی معنی دل کو کسی چیز پر جما لینے کے ہیں اور اصطلاح میں کسی فعل کے کرنے سے اللہ کی اطاعت اور اس کا تقرب مقصود ہو۔ سوال: نیت کی یہ تعریف ما مورات پر صادق آتی ہے اور منہیات پر صادق نہیں آتی ہے جس پر عقاب مرتب ہوتا ہے۔
جواب: بہتر یہ ہے کہ یوں تعریف کی جائے کسی فعل کو کرنے کے لئے دل کو متوجہ کرنا جلب منفعت یا دفع مضرت کے لئے زمانہ حال یا مستقبل میں یہ تعریف ایجاد فعل اور ترک فعل دونوں کو شامل ہو جا ئیگی اور مامورات جن پر ثواب مرتب ہوتا ہے اور منہیات جن پر عقاب کا ترتب ہو سکتا ہے دونوں کو نیت کی تعریف شامل ہوگی۔ اس قاعدہ کا مفہوم یہ ہے کہ ثواب کے حصول کا دارومدار نیت پر ہے اگر عمل سے مقصود رضاء الہی ہے تو ثواب ملیگا اور اگر محض ریا کاری اور شہرت مقصود ہے تو ثواب تو در کنار بلکہ وہ عمل کرنے والے کے لئے الٹا وبال جان بھی بن سکتا ہے اگر چہ فی نفسہ وہ عمل عبادت اور ثواب کا باعث ہو لیکن نیست نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اسے ثواب نہیں ملے گا اور نیت فاسدہ ہو نیکی وجہ سے اس کے لئے راحت کے بجائے زحمت کا باعث ہوسکتا ہے۔
صَرَّحَ بِهِ الْمَشَائِحُ فِى مَوَاضِعَ مِنَ الْفِقْهِ أَوَّلُهَا فِي الْوُضُوْءِ سَواءٌ قُلْنَا إِنَّهَا شَرْطُ الصِّحَّةِ
كَمَا فِي الصَّلوة والزَّكرةِ وَالصَّوْمِ وَالْحَجِّ أَوْلَا كَمَا فِي الوُضُوْءِ وَالْعُسل.
ترجمه : فقہ کے بہت سے مقامات پر مشائخ عظام نے اس کی تصریح کی ہے ان میں پہلے وضو ہے برابر ہے ہم نے کہا کہ نیت صحیح ہونے کے لئے شرط ہے جیسے نماز، زکوۃ، روزہ اور حج میں یا صحیح ہونے کے لئے شرط نہ ہو جیسے وضو اور غسل میں ۔
تشریح : الوضوء بضم الواو فعل وضو کو کہتے ہیں اور بفتح الواو آلہ وضو کو کہتے ہیں ۔ و في الشريعة هو نظافة مخصوصة والأحسن ماقالة العيني أنه في الشرع غسل الأعضاء الثلثة و مسح الرأس (عمدة الايضاح شرح اردو نور الايضاح ، ج ۱، ص: ۱۱۱) مذکورہ قاعدہ سے یہ معلوم ہو ہی گیا ہے کہ ثواب کے حصول کا دار ومدار نیت پر ہے تو اب سمجھئے کہ عبادات کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) مقصودہ (۲) غیر مقصودہ ۔
عبادات مقصودہ: وہ عبادات میں جنگلی تحصیل اور حصول دونوں ضروری ہوں یعنی مقصود بالذات ہوں جیسے نماز ، روزہ ، زکوۃ، حج وغیرہ۔
عبادات غير مقصودہ : وہ عبادات ہیں جنکا حصول تو ضروری ہولیکن ان کی تحصیل نہ ضروری ہے اور نہ مطلوب یعنی مقصود بالذات نہ ہو بلکہ دوسری عبادات کے لئے ذریعہ اور وسیلہ ہو جیسے وضو اور غسل ۔
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The First Principle. The first art is a statement regarding the universal principles. Translation: The first art is about the statement of universal principles. Explanation: Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri (d. 790 AH), author of al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair, arranged his book into seven arts, among which the first art is about universal principles. Qawaid is the plural of qaida, which literally means root and foundation. According to the terminologists (nuhāt), it refers to a majority ruling that applies to most of its particulars, such that the rulings of most particulars can be known through this majority ruling. According to the jurists (fuqaha'), it refers to a universal ruling that applies to all its particulars, and under this universal ruling the rulings of all its particulars can be known. Here, by 'universal principles' are meant those principles that are not under another principle, but rather have under them some particulars and branches, even if some individuals are excluded from the principle. Objection: The author should have first defined a principle (qaida), then dealt with related matters. Answer: This book was not written for beginners who need the meaning of qaida, its definition, and its branches; rather, it was written for advanced students who are already familiar with such matters, such as learned teachers, judges, and muftis, as the author indicated in the introduction. The first [maxim]: No reward except with intention. Translation: Dear principle, without intention no reward is obtained. Explanation: Niyah (intention) is mostly used with tashdid on the ya', and sometimes without tashdid with takhfif. Its literal meaning is to fix the heart upon something, and terminologically it means that the purpose of doing an act is obedience to Allah and seeking nearness to Him. Question: This definition of niyah applies to commanded acts (ma'murat) but not to prohibited acts (manhiyat) which incur punishment. Answer: It is better to define it as: directing the heart to perform an action, for attaining benefit or repelling harm, in the present or future. This definition will include both initiating an act and refraining from it, and will encompass both commanded acts (which incur reward) and prohibited acts (which incur punishment). The meaning of this principle is that the attainment of reward depends on intention. If the purpose of the act is the pleasure of Allah, then reward will be obtained; if the purpose is mere ostentation and fame, then not only is there no reward, but rather the act may become a burden for the doer. Even if the act in itself is worship and a cause of reward, but due to lack of sincerity, he will not get reward, and due to corrupt intention it may become a source of hardship instead of ease. The mashā'ikh (scholars) have explicitly stated this in many places of fiqh, the first of which is in wudu': whether we say that intention is a condition of validity as in salah, zakah, sawm, and hajj, or not a condition of validity as in wudu' and ghusl. Translation: The great scholars have explicitly stated this in many places of fiqh. The first is wudu': it is equal whether we say that intention is a condition for validity as in prayer, zakah, fasting, and hajj, or not a condition for validity as in wudu' and ghusl. Explanation: Al-wudu' with damm on waw refers to the act of wudu, and with fatha on waw refers to the water of wudu. In sharia, it is a specific purification. The best definition is what al-Ayni said: in sharia it is washing three limbs and wiping the head (Umdat al-Idah Sharh Urdu Nur al-Idah, vol. 1, p. 111). From the aforementioned principle it has been understood that reward depends on intention. Now understand that acts of worship ('ibadat) are of two types: (1) maqsoodah (intended) and (2) ghair maqsoodah (non-intended). Maqsoodah acts of worship: those acts where both the pursuit and attainment are necessary, i.e., they are intended in themselves, like prayer, fasting, zakah, hajj, etc. Ghair maqsoodah acts of worship: those acts whose attainment is necessary but their pursuit is neither necessary nor desired, i.e., they are not intended in themselves but are means and instruments for other acts of worship, like wudu' and ghusl.
Source pages p. 63

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the first universal legal maxim (qaida kulliya) in al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair. The author, Ibn Nujaym, first explains what a 'qaida' means according to terminologists and jurists, and clarifies that his book is for advanced scholars. Then he presents the first maxim: 'There is no reward except with intention.' This is a foundational principle in Islamic law, derived from the hadith 'Actions are but by intentions.' The commentary discusses the definition of niyah (intention), addressing a potential objection that its standard terminology definition (seeking Allah's obedience and nearness) does not cover prohibited acts. The author offers a broader definition that includes both commission and omission. The key point is that reward depends solely on the sincerity of intention. The passage then applies this maxim to various acts of worship, noting that intention is a condition of validity in prayers, zakat, fasting, and hajj, but not in wudu' and ghusl (according to Abu Hanifa). Finally, it distinguishes between 'intended acts of worship' (like salah) which are objectives in themselves, and 'non-intended acts of worship' (like wudu') which are means to other acts. This distinction is critical for understanding when intention is required for validity or just for reward.

Key Terms
قاعدة (qa'ida): A universal legal principle that applies to all or most of its particulars (according to the jurists) or a majority ruling (according to terminologists).
نية (niyya): Directing the heart to perform an action for a purpose (benefit or avoidance of harm), whether it is an act or omission, present or future.
عبادات مقصودہ (ibadat maqsoodah): Acts of worship that are intended for their own sake (maqsud bi al-dhat), meaning their attainment is desired in itself.
عبادات غير مقصودہ (ibadat ghair maqsoodah): Acts of worship that are not intended for their own sake but are means to other acts of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the difference between 'ibadat maqsoodah' and 'ibadat ghair maqsoodah' regarding intention?
A) Maqsoodah requires intention for validity; ghair maqsoodah does not require intention at all.
B) Maqsoodah are intended for their own sake; ghair maqsoodah are means to other acts, and reward for both depends on intention.
C) Maqsoodah are supererogatory; ghair maqsoodah are obligatory.
D) Ghair maqsoodah require intention for validity; maqsoodah do not.

Key Takeaway
The first major maxim establishes that the attainment of reward in any act depends on the sincerity of intention, though intention is not always a condition for the legal validity of an act.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate

Actions by Intentions: Application to Worship Types
Explaining the maxim's application to maqsuda and ghayr maqsuda ibadat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to distinguish between Maqsuda and Ghayr Maqsuda acts of worship, state the ruling on intention for each, and explain the Hanafi muqtada interpretation of the hadith.

Core Idea
Intention determines ruling: in some acts it validates, in others it only brings reward.

The maxim 'Actions are judged by intentions' is foundational in Islamic law. This lesson examines its application to acts of worship through the Hanafi distinction between Maqsuda (intended in themselves) and Ghayr Maqsuda (preparatory) acts. You will also explore the Hanafi usul method of interpreting the key hadith via muqtada, ensuring consistency with observable reality.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its sub-maxim
Identify the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' and its sub-maxim 'la thawaba illa bi al-niyyah'. Recognize that reward depends on intention, but validity may not.
The sub-maxim is a dabt (restriction) specifying that reward is conditional on intention.
2
Classify the act as Maqsuda or Ghayr Maqsuda
Determine whether the act is intended in itself (e.g., salah, sawm) or is a means to another act (e.g., wudu, ghusl). This classification dictates the role of intention.
Maqsuda acts require both seeking (tahsīl) and attainment; Ghayr Maqsuda only require attainment.
3
Apply the rule for intention
For Maqsuda acts, intention is a condition for validity (shart al-sihha). For Ghayr Maqsuda acts, intention is not required for validity but is necessary for reward.
This distinction is explicitly stated by the Mashayikh in many fiqh works.
4
Resolve the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat'
The hadith cannot mean actions literally require intention to exist, since actions occur without intention. Hanafi scholars assume an omitted word 'hukm' (ruling) via muqtada: the ruling of actions depends on intention.
Muqtada is an addition demanded by the text for correctness; here it is a legal demand.
5
Derive the fiqh outcome
Apply the above to a specific case: wudu without intention is valid (act exists) but carries no reward. This contrasts with the Shafi'i position.
The practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) is that a Hanafi may pray with such wudu; a Shafi'i may not.

كَمَا فِي الوُضُوْءِ وَالْعُسل. ترجمه : فقہ کے بہت سے مقامات پر مشائخ عظام نے اس کی تصریح کی ہے ان میں پہلے وضو ہے برابر ہے ہم نے کہا کہ نیت صحیح ہونے کے لئے شرط ہے جیسے نماز، زکوۃ، روزہ اور حج میں یا صحیح ہونے کے لئے شرط نہ ہو جیسے وضو اور غسل میں ۔ تشریح : الوضوء بضم الواو فعل وضو کو کہتے ہیں اور بفتح الواو آلہ وضو کو کہتے ہیں ۔ و في الشريعة هو نظافة مخصوصة والأحسن ماقالة العيني أنه في الشرع غسل الأعضاء الثلثة و مسح الرأس (عمدة الايضاح شرح اردو نور الايضاح ، ج ۱، ص: ۱۱۱) مذکورہ قاعدہ سے یہ معلوم ہو ہی گیا ہے کہ ثواب کے حصول کا دار ومدار نیت پر ہے تو اب سمجھئے کہ عبادات کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) مقصودہ (۲) غیر مقصودہ ۔ عبادات مقصودہ: وہ عبادات میں جنگلی تحصیل اور حصول دونوں ضروری ہوں یعنی مقصود بالذات ہوں جیسے نماز ، روزہ ، زکوۃ، حج وغیرہ۔ عبادات غير مقصودہ : وہ عبادات ہیں جنکا حصول تو ضروری ہولیکن ان کی تحصیل نہ ضروری ہے اور نہ مطلوب یعنی مقصود بالذات نہ ہو بلکہ دوسری عبادات کے لئے ذریعہ اور وسیلہ ہو جیسے وضو اور غسل ۔ عبادات حصول ثواب کے لئے نیت تو دونوں میں ضروری ہے خواہ عبادات مقصودہ ہوں یا عبادات غیر مقصودہ البتہ مقصودہ میں تحصیل بھی ضروری ہے اس لئے عبادات مقصودہ بدون نیت صحیح اور درست نہ ہونگی اسی کو صاحب کتاب نے انہا شرط الصحیہ سے تعبیر کیا ہے اور عبادات غیر مقصودہ میں صرف حصول ضروری ہے تحصیل نہیں اس لئے عبادات غیر مقصودہ بدون نیست وجود میں تو آجائینگی لیکن ثواب بدون نیت حاصل نہ ہوگا اس کو مصنف نے فی الوضوء والغسل سے تعبیر فرمایا ہے۔ صرح به المشائخ میں پغمبر کا مرجع لا ثواب الا بالدنیہ جملہ ہے جو مونث ہے لیکن یہ قول کی تاویل میں ہے تاکہ ضمیر اور اسکے مرجع کے مابین تذکیر و تانیث کے مطابقت اور عدم مطابقت کا اعتراض نہ ہو ۔ وَعَلَى هَذَا قَرَّرُوْا حَدِيْتَ إِنَّمَا الْأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ بَابِ الْمُقْتَضَى إِذْلَا يَصِحُ بِدُوْنِ التَّقْدِيرِ لِكَثْرَةِ وُجُوْدِ الْأَعْمَالِ بِدُوْنِهَا فَقَدَّرُوْا مُضَافَاً أَي حُكْمُ الْأَعْمَالِ. ترجمہ: اور اس پر انہوں نے حدیث إنما الاعمال بالنیات کو معمول کیا ہے کہ یہ باب مقتضی سے ہے اس لئے کہ بغیر مقدر مانے ہوئے حدیث صحیح نہیں ہوگی بدون نیت زیادہ اعمال کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے تو انہوں نے مضاف کو مقدر مانا یعنی حکم الاعمال ۔ تشریح : اس حدیث میں اعمال کی اضافت غیر کل یعنی نیت کی طرف کی گئی جس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ کوئی بھی عمل بدون نیت وجود میں نہیں آئیگا حالانکہ یہ بات مشاہدہ اور تجربہ کے خلاف ہے ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ کتنے ہی اعمال بدون نیت وجود میں آتے ہیں اور ان کا تحقق ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے فقہاء کو ضرورت پیش آئی کہ حدیث کے معنی کو سیح کرنے کے لئے کوئی لفظ مقدر جانا جائے تا کہ حدیث کا مفہوم صحیح ہو جائے تو فقہاء نے اس کے پیش نظر اعمال سے پہلے حکم کومقدر مانا ہے اور تقدیری عبارت ہوگی انما حكم الاعمال بالنیات یعنی اعمال کے حکم کا دارو مدار صرف نیتوں پر ہے اور یہ صحیح ہے اور یہ لفظ حکم جو مقدر مانا گیا ہے شرعی تقاضہ سے مقدر نہیں مانا گیا بلکہ متکلم کا صادق ہونا ہی اس مقدر مانے پر موقوف ہے۔ مقتضی کی تعریف: مقتضی عند المتقد میں اس زیادتی کو کہتے ہیں جس کا تقاضہ کلام منطوق نے کیا ہو اور کلام منطوق اس زیادتی کے بغیر صحیح نہ ہو سکے اور وہ زیادتی اس کلام منطوق کے لئے شرط ہو خواہ کلام منصوص نے اس زیادتی کا تقاضہ شرعاً کیا ہو یا عقلاً يا لغةً. جبکہ متاثرین کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کلام منصوص نے اس زیادتی کا تقاضہ شرعاً کیا ہو تو اسکو مقتضی کہتے ہیں اور اگر افتہ کیا ے تو اسکو حذوف اور اگر کام منطوق نے اس زیادتی کا تقاضہ عقل کیا ہے تو اس کو مضمر کہتے ہیں جسکی تفصیل نورالانوار اور حسامی وغیرہ میں دیکھی جاسکتی ہے۔
Explanation: Niyyah is mostly used with tashdid on the ya, and sometimes without tashdid in a lightened form. Linguistically, niyyah means to fix the heart upon something. In terminology, it is that from performing an act, obedience to Allah and seeking nearness to Him is intended. Question: This definition of niyyah applies to commanded acts but not to prohibited acts which incur punishment. Answer: It is better to define it as directing the heart to perform an act for the purpose of attaining benefit or repelling harm, in the present or future. This definition will include both the commission of an act and its omission, and it will cover both commanded acts that carry reward and prohibited acts that may incur punishment. The meaning of this maxim is that the attainment of reward depends on intention. If the purpose of an act is the pleasure of Allah, then reward will be given. If mere hypocrisy and fame are intended, not only will there be no reward, but the act may even become a burden for the doer. Even if the act in itself is worship and a cause for reward, due to the lack of sincerity, he will not get reward, and due to the corrupt intention, it may cause him hardship instead of comfort. The Mashayikh have explicitly stated this in many places of fiqh. The first of them is in wudu. It is the same whether we say that intention is a condition for validity, as in salah, zakat, sawm, and hajj, or that it is not a condition for validity, as in wudu and ghusl. Translation: The great Mashayikh have explicitly stated this in many places of fiqh. The first of them is wudu. It is the same whether we say that intention is a condition for validity, as in salah, zakat, sawm, and hajj, or that it is not a condition for validity, as in wudu and ghusl. Explanation: Al-wudu with damm on the waw refers to the act of wudu, and with fatha on the waw refers to the water of wudu. In Shariah, it is a specific purification. The best definition is what al-Ayni said: in Shariah, it is the washing of three limbs and wiping the head (Umdat al-Idah Sharh Urdu Nur al-Idah, vol. 1, p. 111). From the mentioned maxim, it has become clear that the attainment of reward depends on intention. Now understand that worship is of two types: (1) Maqsuda (intended) and (2) Ghayr Maqsuda (not intended). Maqsuda worship: those acts of worship in which both the seeking (tahsīl) and attainment (husūl) are necessary, i.e., they are intended in themselves, like salah, sawm, zakat, hajj, etc. Ghayr Maqsuda worship: those acts of worship whose attainment is necessary, but their seeking is neither necessary nor desired, i.e., they are not intended in themselves, but are a means and instrument for other acts of worship, like wudu and ghusl. In worship, intention is necessary for both types for the attainment of reward, whether they are Maqsuda or Ghayr Maqsuda. However, in Maqsuda, seeking is also necessary, so Maqsuda worship without intention will not be valid and correct. This is what the author expressed as 'it is a condition for validity'. In Ghayr Maqsuda worship, only attainment is necessary, not seeking. Therefore, Ghayr Maqsuda worship without intention will come into existence, but reward will not be attained without intention. This is what the author expressed as 'in wudu and ghusl'. In 'sarraha bihi al-mashayikh', the pronoun refers to the sentence 'la thawaba illa bi al-niyyah' which is feminine, but this is in interpretation of the saying so that there is no objection regarding agreement or disagreement of gender between the pronoun and its antecedent. And upon this, they have applied the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' that it is from the category of muqtada, because without assuming an omitted word, the hadith would not be correct, due to the frequent occurrence of actions without intention. So they assumed an omitted possessive construction, i.e., 'hukmu al-a'mal' (the ruling of actions). Translation: And upon this, they have applied the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' that it is from the category of muqtada, because without assuming an omitted word, the hadith would not be correct, due to the frequent occurrence of actions without intention. So they assumed an omitted possessive construction, i.e., 'hukmu al-a'mal'. Explanation: In this hadith, actions are added to other than the whole, i.e., to intention, which would mean that no action comes into existence without intention, but this contradicts observation and experience. We see many actions coming into existence without intention. Therefore, the jurists needed to assume some word to correct the meaning of the hadith. With this in view, the jurists assumed 'hukm' before 'a'mal', and the assumed phrase would be 'innama hukmu al-a'mali bi al-niyyat', i.e., the ruling of actions depends only on intentions, and this is correct. This assumed word 'hukm' was not assumed due to a legal requirement, but the truthfulness of the speaker depends on this assumption. Definition of Muqtada: According to the early scholars, muqtada is that addition which the explicit speech demands, and without which the explicit speech cannot be correct, and that addition is a condition for that explicit speech, whether the explicit text demands that addition legally, rationally, or linguistically. According to the later scholars, if the explicit text demands that addition legally, it is called muqtada; if logically, it is called mahzuf (omitted); and if rationally, it is called mudmar (implicit). Details can be seen in Nur al-Anwar and Hisami etc.
Source pages p. 64

Commentary
This passage is a discussion of the Qa'ida al-Kubra 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' (Actions are judged by intentions) as it applies to acts of worship. The author begins by defining niyyah (intention) both linguistically and terminologically. Linguistically, it means to fix the heart upon something. In Hanafi terminology, it is the intent to perform an act for the sake of Allah's obedience and nearness. A question is raised: this definition applies only to commanded acts (ma'murat) and not to prohibited acts (manhiyat) which incur punishment. The answer provides a broader definition: directing the heart to perform an act for the purpose of gaining benefit or repelling harm, covering both commission and omission, and both commanded and prohibited acts. This is a typical Hanafi approach to ensure comprehensiveness.

The core maxim is then stated: the attainment of reward depends on intention. If an act is done for Allah's pleasure, reward follows. If done for show, not only is there no reward, but it may become a burden. The author then cites the Mashayikh's explicit statement in fiqh works, especially regarding wudu, noting that the fuqaha differ on whether intention is a condition for validity in wudu and ghusl. For salah, zakat, sawm, and hajj, intention is a condition for validity (shart al-sihha). For wudu and ghusl, it is not a condition for validity, but it is still necessary for reward.

The passage then divides worship into two categories: Maqsuda (intended in themselves, e.g., salah, sawm, zakat, hajj) and Ghayr Maqsuda (not intended in themselves but means to an end, e.g., wudu, ghusl). For Maqsuda acts, intention is required for both the act's validity and reward. For Ghayr Maqsuda acts, intention is required only for reward; the act is valid without it. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh.

Finally, the author discusses the hadith 'Innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat'. Since actions are observed to exist without intention (e.g., involuntary movements), the hadith cannot mean that actions literally do not exist without intention. Therefore, the Hanafi jurists interpret it as a case of muqtada: an implied addition is necessary for the speech to be correct. They assume the word 'hukm' (ruling) so that the meaning becomes 'The ruling of actions is according to intentions'. This reconciles the hadith with observable reality. The passage concludes with a definition of muqtada according to early and later Hanafi scholars, noting that it refers to an implied addition demanded by the text, and distinguishing it from mahzuf and mudmar. This is a standard Hanafi usul al-fiqh analysis.

Key Terms
النية (an-niyyah): Directing the heart to perform an act for the purpose of gaining benefit or repelling harm, in the present or future, encompassing both commanded and prohibited acts.
مقصودة (maqsūdah): Acts of worship that are intended in themselves, where both the seeking (tahsīl) and attainment (husūl) are necessary; e.g., salah, sawm, zakat, hajj.
غير مقصودة (ghayr maqsūdah): Acts of worship that are not intended in themselves but are means to other acts; their attainment is necessary but their seeking is not; e.g., wudu, ghusl.
مقتضى (muqtaḍā): An addition (ziyādah) demanded by the explicit speech (kalam mantūq) without which the speech cannot be correct; the demand may be legal, logical, or linguistic.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the difference between Maqsuda and Ghayr Maqsuda acts of worship regarding intention?
A) Intention is required for validity in both types.
B) Intention is required for validity only in Maqsuda acts; for Ghayr Maqsuda acts, it is only required for reward.
C) Intention is not required in any act of worship.
D) Intention is required for reward in Maqsuda acts but not in Ghayr Maqsuda acts.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school distinguishes between acts where intention validates (Maqsuda) and acts where intention only brings reward (Ghayr Maqsuda), and interprets the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' as referring to rulings, not physical existence.
