Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
advanced
12 min
The Hadith of Intention: Muqtada vs Mudmar in Hanafi Usul
Analyzing hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' and its usuli implications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' to classify an act of worship as requiring intention for validity or only for reward.

Core Idea
The hadith means the ruling, not the existence, of actions depends on intention.

This lesson unpacks the classic Hanafi resolution of a jarring issue: the hadith 'Actions are by intentions' seems to claim that no action exists without intention, yet we perform countless acts (eating, walking) with no intention. How do Hanafi jurists resolve this? They taught that the hadith requires an implied word—'hukm'—so that it becomes 'The ruling of actions depends on intentions.' This opens a deep usuli distinction between muqtada and mudmar, and between worldly and otherworldly rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the apparent contradiction
The hadith's literal meaning contradicts observable reality. What is the contradiction?
Literal reading: no action exists without intention. Reality: many actions occur without intention.
2
Locate the Hanafi solution: taqdir (estimation)
The scholars estimated an implied word, 'hukm'. What does this achieve?
The meaning becomes 'The ruling of actions depends on intentions.'
3
Distinguish muqtada vs. mudmar
According to early and later Hanafi scholars, what is the difference? How does this affect generality?
Early: muqtada (no generality). Later: mudmar (normally has generality, but here context restricts).
4
Analyze the homonymy of 'hukm'
'Hukm' can mean ukhurawi or dunyawi. Which did they intend by consensus? Why?
Ukhurawi (reward/punishment) by consensus; dunyawi (validity/corruption) debated.
5
Apply to fiqh: intended vs. unintended worship
For ibadat maqsuda (salat), intention is a condition of validity; for ibadat ghayr maqsuda (wudu), intention is needed only for reward.
Use the examples from the text: salat without intention invalid; wudu without intention valid but no reward.

صرح به المشائخ میں پغمبر کا مرجع لا ثواب الا بالدنیہ جملہ ہے جو مونث ہے لیکن یہ قول کی تاویل میں ہے تاکہ ضمیر اور اسکے مرجع کے مابین تذکیر و تانیث کے مطابقت اور عدم مطابقت کا اعتراض نہ ہو ۔
وَعَلَى هَذَا قَرَّرُوْا حَدِيْتَ إِنَّمَا الْأَعْمَالُ بِالنِّيَّاتِ أَنَّهُ مِنْ بَابِ الْمُقْتَضَى إِذْلَا يَصِحُ بِدُوْنِ التَّقْدِيرِ لِكَثْرَةِ وُجُوْدِ الْأَعْمَالِ بِدُوْنِهَا فَقَدَّرُوْا مُضَافَاً أَي حُكْمُ الْأَعْمَالِ.
ترجمہ: اور اس پر انہوں نے حدیث إنما الاعمال بالنیات کو معمول کیا ہے کہ یہ باب مقتضی سے ہے اس لئے کہ بغیر مقدر مانے ہوئے حدیث صحیح نہیں ہوگی بدون نیت زیادہ اعمال کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے تو انہوں نے مضاف کو مقدر مانا یعنی حکم الاعمال ۔ تشریح : اس حدیث میں اعمال کی اضافت غیر کل یعنی نیت کی طرف کی گئی جس کا مطلب یہ ہوگا کہ کوئی بھی عمل بدون نیت وجود میں نہیں آئیگا حالانکہ یہ بات مشاہدہ اور تجربہ کے خلاف ہے ہم دیکھتے ہیں کہ کتنے ہی اعمال بدون نیت وجود میں آتے ہیں اور ان کا تحقق ہوتا ہے۔ اس لئے فقہاء کو ضرورت پیش آئی کہ حدیث کے معنی کو سیح کرنے کے لئے کوئی لفظ مقدر جانا جائے تا کہ حدیث کا مفہوم صحیح ہو جائے تو فقہاء نے اس کے پیش نظر اعمال سے پہلے حکم کومقدر مانا ہے اور تقدیری عبارت ہوگی انما حكم الاعمال بالنیات یعنی اعمال کے حکم کا دارو مدار صرف نیتوں پر ہے اور یہ صحیح ہے اور یہ لفظ حکم جو مقدر مانا گیا ہے شرعی تقاضہ سے مقدر نہیں مانا گیا بلکہ متکلم کا صادق ہونا ہی اس مقدر مانے پر موقوف ہے۔ مقتضی کی تعریف: مقتضی عند المتقد میں اس زیادتی کو کہتے ہیں جس کا تقاضہ کلام منطوق نے کیا ہو اور کلام منطوق اس زیادتی کے بغیر صحیح نہ ہو سکے اور وہ زیادتی اس کلام منطوق کے لئے شرط ہو خواہ کلام منصوص نے اس زیادتی کا تقاضہ شرعاً کیا ہو یا عقلاً يا لغةً. جبکہ متاثرین کہتے ہیں کہ اگر کلام منصوص نے اس زیادتی کا تقاضہ شرعاً کیا ہو تو اسکو مقتضی کہتے ہیں اور اگر افتہ کیا ے تو اسکو حذوف اور اگر کام منطوق نے اس زیادتی کا تقاضہ عقل کیا ہے تو اس کو مضمر کہتے ہیں جسکی تفصیل نورالانوار اور حسامی وغیرہ میں دیکھی جاسکتی ہے۔
بقول مصنف یہ حدیث جس میں لفظ مضاف یعنی حکم مقدر مانا گیا ہے عند المتقد میں مقتضی کے قبیل سے ہے جبکہ متاخرین کے نزدیک باب مضمر کے قبیل سے ہے کیونکہ یہاں پر زیادتی کا تقاضہ کلام منصوص نے شرعا نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ عقلاً کیا ہے۔ صاحب کتاب علامہ ابن نجیم مصری نے یہاں پر متقدمین کے مسلک کو اختیار فرمایا ہے۔ مقتضی اور مضمر میں کئی اعتبار سے فرق ہے ان میں سے ایک یہ ہے کہ مقتضی میں عموم نہیں ہوتا جبکہ مضمر میں عموم ہوتا ہے۔ متاخرین کے مسلک کے اعتبار سے یہاں ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ جب یہ حدیث بقول ان کے باب مضر سے ہے اور مضمر میں عموم ہوتا ہے تو حکیم الاعمال میں بھی عموم ہونا چاہئے جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث میں عدم محموم اس وجہ سے نہیں ہے کہ یہ مقتضی کے قبیل سے ہے بلکہ اس لئے ہے کہ اگر چہ مضمر میں عموم ہوتا ہے لیکن یہاں پر عدم عموم اس لئے ہے کہ جب اعمال کی اضافت غیر محل یعنی نیت کی طرف کی گئی ہے حالانکہ بدون نیت بھی بہت سے اعمال کا محقق ہوتا ہے تو ضرورت پیش آئی ایک ایسے محل کے مقدر ماننے کی جو نیت کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور یہاں کے مناسب حال حکم ہے اس لئے ہم نے حکم کو مقدر مانا ہے۔
وَهُوَ نَوْغان أُخْرَوى وَهُوَ الثَّوَابُ وَإِسْتِحْفَاق الْعِقَابِ وَدُنْيَوِيٌّ وَهُوَ الصَّحْةُ وَالْفَسَادُ وَقَدْ أُريدُ الأخْرَوِيٌّ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ لِلْإِجْمَاع عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَاثَوَابَ وَلَا عِقَابَ إِلَّا بِالنِّيَّةِ فَالْتَقَى الآخر أن يكون مُراداً وَإِمَّا لأنَّهُ مُشْتَرَكَ وَلَا عُمُوْمَ لَهُ أَوْلِانْدِفاع الضَّرُورَةِ بِهِ مِنْ صِحْةِ الكلام به فَلاحَاجَةَ إلى الآخرِ وَالثَّانِي أوْجَهُ لأن الأوَّلَ لَا يُسَلِّمُهُ الْخَصْمَ لأَنَّهُ قَائِل بعموم المُشْتَرَى.
ترجمه : اور وہ (حکم) دو قسم پر ہے (۱) اخروی اور وہ ثواب اور استحقاق عقاب ہے (۲) دنیوی اور وہ صحت اور فساد ہے اور اجماع کی وجہ سے اخروی مراد لیا گیا ہے اس پر اتفاق علماء کی وجہ سے کہ بدون نیت ثواب اور عقاب نہیں ہوتا نپس دوسرے ( دنیوی) کی نفی ہوگئی مراد ہونے سے اور یا اس وجہ سے کہ وہ مشترک ہے اور اس میں عموم نہیں ہوتا یا کلام کے صحیح ہونے پر ضرورت کے ختم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور دوسرا افضل ہے اسلئے کہ اول کو فریق مخالف تسلیم نہیں کرتا کیوں کہ وہ عموم مشترک کا قائل ہے۔
تشریح : حدیث مذکورہ کی صحت کے لئے لفظ حکم محذوف مانا تھا اور محذوف حکم کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) اخروی اور وہ اچھے کام کے کرنے پر ثواب اور برے فعل کے ارتکاب پر سزا کا ملنا ہے (۲) دنیوی اور قم دنیوی سے مراد کسی عمل کا درست ہونا صحیح ہونا یا غیر صحیح اور فاسد ہوتا۔
Worship: Intention is necessary for obtaining reward in both (types of worship), whether they are intended acts of worship or unintended acts of worship. However, in intended acts, actualization is also necessary; therefore, intended acts of worship without intention will not be valid. The author (of the matn) expressed this as 'shart al-sihhah'. In unintended acts of worship, only acquisition (of reward) is necessary, not actualization; hence, unintended acts of worship will come into existence without intention, but reward will not be obtained without intention. The author expressed this as 'fi al-wudu' wa al-ghusl'. The phrase 'saraha bihi al-masha'ikh' contains a pronoun whose referent is the sentence 'la thawaba illa bi al-niyyah', which is feminine, but this is in the interpretation of the saying, so that there would be no objection regarding agreement or disagreement in gender between the pronoun and its antecedent. And upon this they applied the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' that it is from the category of muqtada, because it is not valid without estimation (taqdir) due to the frequent occurrence of actions without it. So they estimated an added element, i.e., hukm al-a'mal. Translation: And upon this they have made the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' operative, that it is from the category of muqtada, because without assuming an estimation the hadith would not be valid due to the many actions that occur without intention. So they estimated an added element, i.e., hukm al-a'mal. Explanation: In this hadith, the idafah of actions is directed towards intention, which would mean that no action exists without intention, even though this contradicts observation and experience; we see many actions occur without intention and come into existence. Therefore, the jurists needed to assume some intended word to correct the meaning of the hadith. So they assumed the word 'hukm' before 'a'mal', and the estimation would be: innama hukmu al-a'mali bi al-niyyat, meaning the ruling of actions depends only on intentions, and this is correct. This estimated word 'hukm' is not estimated due to a shar'i requirement but because the speaker's truthfulness depends on this estimation. Definition of muqtada: Muqtada according to the early scholars (mutaqaddimin) is that addition which the spoken statement requires and the statement cannot be valid without it; that addition is a condition for the statement, whether the requirement is shar'i, rationally, or linguistically. While the later scholars (muta'akhkhirin) say: if the requirement is shar'i, it is called muqtada; if it is linguistic, it is called hadhf; and if the requirement is rational, it is called mudmar. Details can be seen in Nur al-Anwar and Husami etc. According to the author, this hadith, in which an added word (hukm) is estimated, is from the muqtada category according to the early scholars, while according to the later scholars it is from the mudmar category because here the requirement of the statement is not shar'i but rational. The author, 'Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri, adopted the view of the early scholars. There are several differences between muqtada and mudmar; one of them is that muqtada does not have generality (umum), while mudmar does. According to the later school, there is an objection: when this hadith is from mudmar, and mudmar has generality, then in 'hukm al-a'mal' there should also be generality. The answer is that in this hadith, absence of generality is not because it is from muqtada, but because although mudmar has generality, here the generality is absent because when the idafah of actions is directed to intention, yet many actions occur without intention, so the need arose to estimate a word that can accommodate intention. And the word consistent with the context is 'hukm'; therefore we estimated 'hukm'. And it (hukm) is of two types: ukhurawi (otherworldly), which is reward and deserving of punishment, and dunyawi (worldly), which is validity (sihhah) and corruption (fasad). And the ukhurawi is intended by consensus because there is consensus that there is no reward or punishment except with intention. So the other becomes negated from being intended. Or because it (hukm) is a homonym and has no generality, or because the necessity is removed by one of them for the validity of the speech, so there is no need for the other. And the second is more appropriate because the opponent does not accept the first, as he believes in the generality of homonyms. Translation: And it (hukm) is of two types: (1) ukhurawi: reward and deserving punishment; (2) dunyawi: validity and corruption. And by consensus the ukhurawi is intended, because there is consensus that there is no reward or punishment without intention. So the other is negated from being intended. Or because it is a homonym and has no generality, or because the necessity of making the speech correct is fulfilled by [the ukhurawi meaning], so there is no need for the other. The second opinion is more appropriate because the opponent does not accept the first, since he believes in the generality of homonyms. Explanation: For the correctness of the aforementioned hadith, the word 'hukm' was considered deleted. And the deleted hukm is of two types: (1) ukhurawi: obtaining reward for good deeds and punishment for bad deeds; (2) dunyawi: the validity or invalidity of an action.
Source pages p. 65

Commentary
This passage discusses a foundational usul al-fiqh issue: how to interpret the hadith 'Innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' (Actions are by intentions). The author explains that the hadith, taken literally, would claim that actions cannot exist without intention, which contradicts observable reality (actions like sleeping or eating happen without explicit intention). Therefore, Hanafi jurists (and others) agree that a word must be implied (muqtada or mudmar) to make the hadith consistent. The implied word is 'hukm' (ruling), so the meaning becomes 'The ruling of actions depends on intentions.' The passage then distinguishes between two types of rulings: ukhurawi (reward/punishment) and dunyawi (validity/corruption). By consensus, the ukhurawi meaning is intended because it is established that reward and punishment require intention. The dunyawi meaning (sihha/fasad) is debated: some say it is also included, but the author (Ibn Nujaym) follows the early scholars (mutaqaddimin) who consider the hadith to be from the category of muqtada (not mudmar), thus it lacks generality. The late scholars (muta'akhkhirin) consider it mudmar, which normally implies generality, but the author argues that even in that view, generality is not present because the context necessitates that the implied word be 'hukm', which is a homonym and therefore not general. The practical fiqh implication: For intended acts of worship (ibadat maqsuda, e.g., salat), intention is a condition of validity; without it, the act is invalid and yields no reward. For unintended acts of worship (ibadat ghair maqsuda, e.g., wudu as a cleansing act that becomes worship with intention), the act can exist without intention (as a valid physical act) but yields no reward. Thus, the maxim 'Actions are by intentions' is true in the sense of legal effect (hukm), not existence.

Key Terms
مقتضى (muqtada): An implied word required for the speech to be valid, required by the spoken text itself (shar'an or 'aqlan or lughatan according to early scholars; only shar'an according to later scholars).
مضمر (mudmar): An implied word required by rational necessity, not by the text itself; according to later scholars, it has generality.
حكم الاعمال (hukm al-a'mal): The legal ruling of actions, which can be ukhurawi (reward/punishment) or dunyawi (validity/corruption).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Hanafi usul, which word is estimated (muqaddar) in the hadith 'innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat' to resolve the apparent contradiction?
A) الثواب (reward)
B) الحكم (the ruling)
C) الصحة (validity)
D) العمل (the action)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school reconciles the hadith with reality by interpreting it as 'The ruling of actions depends on intentions,' requiring an implied word and distinguishing between the existence and legal effect of actions.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
12 min
The Rule of Generality for Implicit Elements (Muqtada and Mudmar) in the Hadith of Intentions
Analyzing implicit elements and generality in the hadith of intentions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that muqtada lacks generality and mudmar has generality to determine the intended meaning in texts, and evaluate the role of consensus (ijma) in resolving disputes over homonyms.

Core Idea
The implicit element's type determines generality; in the hadith of intentions, context restricts meaning to otherworldly hukm.

This passage examines a key methodological distinction in Hanafi usul: the difference between muqtada (implicit element required by reason) and mudmar (implicit element understood from context). The author, Ibn Nujaym, applies this distinction to the famous hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنيات' to show that the intended 'hukm' (ruling) is otherworldly (reward/punishment), not worldly (validity/invalidity). Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper istinbat and fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of implicit elements
Muqtada (مقتضى) is an element required by reason, not explicit in the text, and it does not carry generality. Mudmar (مضمر) is an element understood from context and normally carries generality unless context restricts it.
The early Hanafis (متقدمين) classify the implicit 'hukm' as muqtada; later Hanafis (متأخرين) classify it as mudmar.
2
Apply the rule to the hadith of intentions
In the hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنيات', the implicit word is 'حكم' (hukm). According to the early scholars (followed by Ibn Nujaym), since it is muqtada, it lacks generality, so only one meaning is intended. According to later scholars (mudmar), generality would normally apply but is restricted by context.
The context of deeds requiring intention necessitates a specific locus (hukm ukhrawi).
3
Analyze the three proofs for otherworldly hukm
Three proofs are given: (1) Consensus (ijma) that reward and punishment depend on intention, while worldly validity does not; (2) The word 'hukm' is a homonym (مشترک) and Hanafis hold homonyms have no general meaning; (3) Necessity: the otherworldly meaning suffices for the correctness of speech.
The author prefers the first proof because the opponent (Shafi'i) believes in generality of homonyms, so the second proof would not convince them.
4
Compare the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on homonym generality
Hanafis deny that a homonym can carry all its meanings simultaneously (عموم المشترك). Shafi'is affirm that a homonym can have general meaning if context allows. This difference leads to different interpretations of the hadith.
The thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis restrict to otherworldly hukm; Shafi'is could intend both.
5
Evaluate the strength of each proof
The consensus proof is strongest because it is accepted by both schools. The homonym proof is weak against Shafi'is. The necessity proof is sufficient but less powerful. Ultimately, the Hanafi position relies on the consensus of later scholars.
Note: The consensus is specifically of later Hanafis, as early scholars held that actions without intention could still be rewarded.

بقول مصنف یہ حدیث جس میں لفظ مضاف یعنی حکم مقدر مانا گیا ہے عند المتقدمین میں مقتضی کے قبیل سے ہے جبکہ متاخرین کے نزدیک باب مضمر کے قبیل سے ہے کیونکہ یہاں پر زیادتی کا تقاضہ کلام منصوص نے شرعا نہیں کیا ہے بلکہ عقلاً کیا ہے۔ صاحب کتاب علامہ ابن نجیم مصری نے یہاں پر متقدمین کے مسلک کو اختیار فرمایا ہے۔ مقتضی اور مضمر میں کئی اعتبار سے فرق ہے ان میں سے ایک یہ ہے کہ مقتضی میں عموم نہیں ہوتا جبکہ مضمر میں عموم ہوتا ہے۔ متاخرین کے مسلک کے اعتبار سے یہاں ایک اعتراض ہے وہ یہ ہے کہ جب یہ حدیث بقول ان کے باب مضر سے ہے اور مضمر میں عموم ہوتا ہے تو حکیم الاعمال میں بھی عموم ہونا چاہئے جواب اس کا یہ ہے کہ اس حدیث میں عدم محموم اس وجہ سے نہیں ہے کہ یہ مقتضی کے قبیل سے ہے بلکہ اس لئے ہے کہ اگر چہ مضمر میں عموم ہوتا ہے لیکن یہاں پر عدم عموم اس لئے ہے کہ جب اعمال کی اضافت غیر محل یعنی نیت کی طرف کی گئی ہے حالانکہ بدون نیت بھی بہت سے اعمال کا محقق ہوتا ہے تو ضرورت پیش آئی ایک ایسے محل کے مقدر ماننے کی جو نیت کا احتمال رکھتا ہے اور یہاں کے مناسب حال حکم ہے اس لئے ہم نے حکم کو مقدر مانا ہے۔
وَهُوَ نَوْعان أُخْرَوى وَهُوَ الثَّوَابُ وَإِسْتِحْقاق الْعِقَابِ وَدُنْيَوِيٌّ وَهُوَ الصَّحَّةُ وَالْفَسَادُ وَقَدْ أُرِيدَ الأخْرَوِيُّ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ لِلْإِجْمَاعِ عَلَى أَنَّهُ لَا ثَوَابَ وَلَا عِقَابَ إِلَّا بِالنِّيَّةِ فَالْتَقَى الآخَرُ أن يكون مُراداً وَإِمَّا لأنَّهُ مُشْتَرَكَ وَلَا عُمُوْمَ لَهُ أَوْلِانْدِفاع الضَّرُورَةِ بِهِ مِنْ صِحَّةِ الكلام به فَلاحَاجَةَ إلى الآخَرِ وَالثَّانِي أوْجَهُ لأن الأوَّلَ لَا يُسَلِّمُهُ الْخَصْمَ لأَنَّهُ قَائِل بعموم المُشْتَرَك.
ترجمه : اور وہ (حکم) دو قسم پر ہے (۱) اخروی اور وہ ثواب اور استحقاق عقاب ہے (۲) دنیوی اور وہ صحت اور فساد ہے اور اجماع کی وجہ سے اخروی مراد لیا گیا ہے اس پر اتفاق علماء کی وجہ سے کہ بدون نیت ثواب اور عقاب نہیں ہوتا پس دوسرے (دنیوی) کی نفی ہوگئی مراد ہونے سے اور یا اس وجہ سے کہ لفظ مشترک ہے اور اس میں عموم نہیں ہوتا یا کلام کے صحیح ہونے پر ضرورت کے ختم ہونے کی وجہ سے اور دوسرا افضل ہے اسلئے کہ اول کو فریق مخالف تسلیم نہیں کرتا کیوں کہ وہ عموم مشترک کا قائل ہے۔
تشریح : حدیث مذکورہ کی صحت کے لئے لفظ حکم محذوف مانا تھا اور محذوف حکم کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ (۱) اخروی اور وہ اچھے کام کے کرنے پر ثواب اور برے فعل کے ارتکاب پر سزا کا ملنا ہے (۲) دنیوی اور دنیوی سے مراد کسی عمل کا درست ہونا صحیح ہونا یا غیر صحیح اور فاسد ہونا۔
جب تم دونوں کو عام ہے اخروی اور دنیوی تو یہاں پر کون سا حکم مراد ہے صاحب کتاب کہتے ہیں جب ہم نے دلائل میں غور وفکر کیا تو ہمیں معلوم ہوا کہ یہاں پر حکم سے اخروی حکم مراد ہے نہ کہ دنیوی ۔ اخروی مراد ہونے پر صاحب کتاب نے تین دلیلیں بیان کی ہیں (۱) اجماع ، اس لئے کہ ثواب و عقاب کا مدار بالاجماع نیت پر ہے جب کہ صحت و فساد کا مدار دنیوی اعتبار سے نیت پر نہیں پس جب اجماع کی وجہ سے حکم اخروی مراد لے لیا تو دوسرے معنی یعنی حکم دنیوی مراد نہیں لے سکتے۔ (۲) لانہ مشترک دوسری دلیل کا خلاصہ یہ ہے کہ جب لفظ حکم دو معانی میں مشترک ہے اور عند الاحناف مشترک میں عموم نہیں ہوتا لہذا جب باجماع علماء حکم اخروی مراد ہے تو دوسرا حکم یعنی دنیوی مراد نہیں لے سکتے۔ (۳) دنیوی حکم مراد لینے کی بظاہر کوئی وجہ نہیں کیونکہ حکم اخروی مراد لینے سے ہمارا جو مقصود تھا صدق متکلم وہ پورا ہو گیا تو دنیوی حکم مراد لینے کی ضرورت باقی نہیں رہی۔ حدیث شریف میں حکم اخروی مراد لینے پر جو دلیلیں ذکر کی گئی ہیں ان میں پہلی دلیل (اجماع) زیادہ قابل توجہ ہے کیونکہ اگر دوسری دلیل عموم مشترک مراد لیجائے تو مد مقابل اس دلیل کو تسلیم نہیں کریگا کیونکہ وہ عموم مشترک کا قائل ہے ان کے نزدیک بیک وقت حکم اخروی اور حکم دنیوی دونوں مراد لے سکتے ہیں اسلئے دلیل اجتماع کو اختیار کرنا اولی ہے لیکن یہ بات یاد ہے کہ عبارت میں اجماع سے اجماع متأخرین مراد ہے کیونکہ وہ وضو جس میں نیت نہ کی گئی ہو متقدمین علماء کے نزدیک ثواب دیا جائیگا جبکہ متاخرین کے نزدیک وضو بدون نیت پر ثواب نہ ملے گا صاحب البحر الرائق نے قول متآخرین کو صحیح قرار دیا ہے۔
According to the author, this hadith in which the added word, i.e., 'hukm', is considered implicit is of the category of 'muqtada' according to the early scholars, while according to the later scholars it is from the category of 'mudmar' because the requirement of addition is not made by the explicit text legally, but rationally. The author, Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri, has adopted the way of the early scholars here. There are several differences between muqtada and mudmar, one of which is that muqtada does not have generality, while mudmar has generality. According to the way of the later scholars, there is an objection here: since this hadith according to them is of the category of mudmar, and mudmar has generality, then 'hukm of deeds' should also have generality. The answer to this is that the lack of generality in this hadith is not because it is of the category of muqtada, but because although mudmar has generality, here the lack of generality is because when deeds are attributed to something other than their locus, i.e., intention, while many deeds are realized without intention, necessity arises for assuming a locus that can accommodate intention, and appropriate to the context here is 'hukm', so we have assumed 'hukm' as the implicit word. And it (hukm) is of two types: otherworldly, which is reward and deserving of punishment, and worldly, which is validity and invalidity. And the otherworldly is intended by consensus, because of the consensus that there is no reward or punishment except with intention; thus the other (worldly) is excluded from being intended. Or because it (the word hukm) is a homonym and has no general meaning, or because necessity for the correctness of speech is fulfilled by it, so there is no need for the other. And the second (reason) is more appropriate because the opponent does not accept the first, since he is a proponent of the generality of homonyms. Translation: And that (hukm) is of two types: (1) otherworldly, which is reward and deserving of punishment, (2) worldly, which is validity and invalidity. And the otherworldly is intended by consensus, due to the agreement of scholars that without intention there is no reward and punishment, so the other (worldly) is negated from being intended. Or because it is a homonym and has no generality, or because necessity for correctness of speech is fulfilled by it, so there is no need for the other. And the second is more appropriate because the opponent does not accept the first, since he is a proponent of the generality of homonyms. Explanation: For the correctness of the aforementioned hadith, the word 'hukm' was considered deleted. And the deleted 'hukm' has two types: (1) otherworldly, which is reward for good deeds and punishment for bad deeds; (2) worldly, which means the correctness or incorrectness of an action. When both are general, otherworldly and worldly, then which hukm is intended here? The author says: when we pondered the evidences, we came to know that here by 'hukm' the otherworldly hukm is intended, not the worldly. For the otherworldly being intended, the author gives three proofs: (1) Consensus, because reward and punishment depend by consensus on intention, while validity and invalidity from a worldly perspective do not depend on intention. So when by consensus the otherworldly hukm is intended, the other meaning, i.e., worldly hukm, cannot be intended. (2) Because it is a homonym: the gist of the second proof is that when the word hukm is a homonym between two meanings, and according to the Hanafis a homonym does not have generality, therefore when by consensus of scholars the otherworldly hukm is intended, the second, i.e., worldly, cannot be intended. (3) There is no apparent reason for intending the worldly hukm because our purpose, the truthfulness of the speaker, is fulfilled by intending the otherworldly hukm, so there is no need to intend the worldly hukm. Among the proofs mentioned for intending the otherworldly hukm in the noble hadith, the first proof (consensus) is more worthy of attention because if the second proof, the generality of the homonym, is taken, the opponent will not accept it, because he is a proponent of the generality of homonyms; according to him both the otherworldly and worldly hukm can be intended simultaneously. Therefore, adopting the proof of consensus is preferable. But it should be noted that by 'consensus' in the text is meant the consensus of the later scholars, because a wudu without intention was considered rewardable by the early scholars, while the later scholars hold that no reward is given for wudu without intention. The author of al-Bahr al-Rai'q declared the statement of the later scholars as correct.
Source pages p. 66

Commentary
This passage discusses a methodological rule in usul al-fiqh regarding the implicit element in a text (مقتضى and مضمر). The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains that in the hadith 'إنما الأعمال بالنيات', the word 'حكم' (hukm) is implicit. The early scholars (متقدمين) classify this as مقتضى (muqtada) meaning something required by reason, not explicit text. The later scholars (متأخرين) classify it as مضمر (mudmar) meaning something implicitly understood. The key difference is that مقتضى does not allow generality (عموم), while مضمر does. However, in this specific hadith, even if it were مضمر, generality is not allowed because the context necessitates a specific meaning: the intended hukm is otherworldly (اخروي) not worldly (دنيوي). Three proofs are given: (1) consensus (اجماع) that reward and punishment depend on intention, whereas worldly validity does not necessarily require intention; (2) the word حكم is a homonym (مشترک) and according to Hanafis homonyms do not carry general meaning; (3) necessity: intending the otherworldly meaning suffices for the correctness of speech. The author prefers the first proof (consensus) because the opponent (Shafi'i) believes homonyms can have general meaning, so the second proof would not convince them. The consensus referred to is that of the later scholars, as early scholars held that an action without intention could still be rewarded. This is an application of the qawida that the implicit element's type (muqtada vs mudmar) affects the ruling of generality.

Key Terms
مقتضى (muqtada): An implicit element required by reason, not explicitly mentioned in the text, and it does not have generality.
مضمر (mudmar): An implicit element that is understood from the context and normally has generality.
عموم المشترك (umum al-mushtarak): The idea that a homonymous word can be used to mean all its meanings simultaneously.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the qawida discussed in this lesson, which type of implicit element carries generality by default?
A) Muqtada has generality.
B) Mudmar has generality.
C) Both have generality.
D) Neither has generality.

Key Takeaway
The implicit 'hukm' in the hadith of intentions is restricted to otherworldly meaning by consensus and contextual necessity, illustrating the Hanafi rule that muqtada lacks generality and mudmar's generality can be overridden by context.

The Rule of Niyyah in Purifications: Means vs. Ends
Establishes a qawida with its exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that niyyah is not required for the validity of acts of purification (wudu, ghusl, masah al-khuffayn, removal of najasah) and identify the exception of tayammum, applying the distinction between ibadat maqsurah and wasila.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, niyyah is required for primary worship ends, not for preparatory means—except when the means itself linguistically implies intention.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between acts that are ends in themselves (ibadat maqsurah) and acts that are merely means (wasila) to those ends. This lesson examines a key qawida from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair: niyyah is not a condition for the validity of purification acts, which are means to prayer. The source passage also highlights the exception of tayammum, where niyyah is required due to its linguistic meaning. By understanding this rule, you will be able to correctly apply conditions for worship in daily practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Core Rule
The rule states that niyyah is not required for the validity (sihhah) of wudu, ghusl, wiping over khuffayn, and removal of actual najasah from clothing, body, place, or vessels. Write down the rule in Arabic: 'لا تشترط النية في الوضوء والغسل ومسح الخفين وإزالة النجاسة'.
This is a dabt (sub-maxim) under the major qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
2
Trace the Proof
The text gives two proofs: consensus (ijma) and the Quranic verse (98:5). The author favors consensus because the verse's word 'ibadah' is interpreted broadly as tawhid, as indicated by the conjunction of prayer and zakat. Thus, niyyah is required only in primary acts of worship.
The Hanafi position is that these purification acts are not ibadat maqsurah.
3
Distinguish the Exception
Tayammum requires niyyah because the word 'tayammum' linguistically means 'intention' and the Quranic verse (5:6) indicates purpose and intent. This exception is based on the wording of the text, not on the general rule.
This shows that linguistic analysis (dalalah lughawiyyah) plays a role in deriving exceptions.
4
Apply to New Cases
Consider other actions: washing a najis dish, removing a drop of najasah from a garment, or performing ghusl without niyyah (e.g., for Friday). Each is valid without niyyah.
However, niyyah is recommended (sunnah) for reward, but not required for validity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنَّمَا اشْتَرِطَتِ النِّيَّةُ فِي الْعِبَادَاتِ بِالْإِجْمَاعِ أَوْ بِايَةٍ وَمَا أُمِرُوا إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُو اللَّهَ مُخْلِصِيْنَ لَهُ الدِّينَ حُنَفَاءَ وَالْاَوَّلُ أَوْجَة لأنَّ الْعِبَادَةَ بِمَعْنَى التَّوْحِيْدِ بِقَرِيْنَةِ عَطْفِ الصَّلَوةِ وَالزَّكَوةِ فَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ فِى الْوُضُوْءِ وَالْغُسْلِ وَمَسْحِ الْحُفَّيْنِ وَإِزَالَةِ النِّجَاسَةِ الْحَقِيقِيَّةِ عَنِ الثَّوْبِ وَالْبَدَنِ وَالْمَكَانِ وَالْأَوَانِي لِلصَّحَةِ.
وَأَمَّا اِشْتِرَاطُهَا فِي التَّيَمُّم فَلِدَلَالَةِ ايَتِهِ عَلَيْهَا لأَنَّهُ الْقَصْدُ.
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال تیم میں نیت کا شرط ہوتا آیت تیم کے نیت پر دلالت کرنے کی وجہ سے ہے کیونکہ تم کے معنی قصد وارادہ کے ہیں۔
And indeed niyyah is stipulated in the acts of worship by consensus or by the verse 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion, inclining to truth.' And the first [consensus] is more appropriate because 'worship' here means tawhid, as indicated by the conjunction of prayer and zakat. So niyyah is not stipulated for the validity of wudu, ghusl, wiping over khuffayn, and removal of actual najasah from clothing, body, place, and vessels. And as for its stipulation in tayammum, it is due to the indication of its verse [implying] it, because 'tayammum' means 'intention'.
Source pages p. 71

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the requirement of niyyah in acts of worship. The text establishes that niyyah is required in primary acts of worship (ibadat maqsurah) like prayer and zakat, based either on ijma (consensus) or the Quranic verse. The author favors the consensus argument because the verse's word 'liya'budu' is interpreted broadly as tawhid, and the conjunction of specific acts like prayer and zakat shows that 'ibadah here is general. The rule then states that niyyah is NOT required for the validity of wudu, ghusl, wiping over khuffayn, and removing actual najasah from clothing, body, place, or vessels. These are means (wasila) to other acts, not ends in themselves. An exception is tayammum, where niyyah is required because the word 'tayammum' itself linguistically means 'intention' and the Quranic verse (5:6) indicates purpose.

Key Terms
نِيَّة (niyyah): Intention; the conscious purpose to perform an act of worship.
عِبَادَات مَقْصُورَة (ibadat maqsurah): Primary acts of worship that are ends in themselves (e.g., salah, sawm, zakat).
تَيَمُّم (tayammum): Dry ablution with clean earth as a substitute for wudu or ghusl when water is unavailable or harmful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, is niyyah required for the validity of wudu?
A) Yes, because it is an act of worship.
B) No, because it is a means to another act, not an end in itself.
C) Yes, but only if one intends to pray.
D) No, unless one is in a state of janabah.

Key Takeaway
Niyyah is not a condition for the validity of purification acts in Hanafi fiqh, except for tayammum due to its linguistic meaning.

Evidence for Intention in Intended Acts of Worship
Defends condition of intention using ijma and Quranic verse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two proofs (ijma and Quran) establishing intention as a condition for intended acts of worship, and explain the Hanafi response to the objection on the Quranic verse.

Core Idea
Intention is required for intended acts by ijma and Quran; the Quranic verse's conjunction is explained via Tawhid or general worship.

In this passage, the author defends the condition of intention (niyyah) for intended acts of worship (ibādāt maqṣūrah) such as prayer and fasting. He cites two proofs: consensus (ijma) and a Quranic verse. While ijma is straightforward, the verse requires careful interpretation because its grammatical structure might suggest identity rather than difference between the commanded worship and the specific acts. The author provides two elegant solutions, demonstrating how classical Hanafi usul handles potential objections.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two proofs
Locate where the author states the two evidences: ijma and the Quranic verse (98:5). Understand that ijma is presented as stronger because it faces no objection.
The verse is 'wa ma umiru illa liya'budu Allah mukhliṣīna lahu al-dīn ḥunafā'.'
2
Analyze the objection to the verse
The objection is that the conjoined elements (prayer, zakat) are the same type as the conjoined-to ('liya'budu'), but conjunction requires difference. The author acknowledges this challenge.
This is a standard grammatical objection in usul al-fiqh.
3
Study the first response: 'ibadah as Tawhid'
The author suggests that 'liya'budu' here means Tawhid (monotheism), which is distinct from specific acts like prayer. Thus, difference is achieved.
This interpretation relies on the context of the verse (Surah al-Bayyinah).
4
Study the second response: general vs. specific
Alternatively, 'liya'budu' means general worship (al-ibadah al-ammah), while prayer and zakat are specific acts (ibadah khassah). Conjunction of specific to general is valid because difference exists 'min wajh' (in some respect).
This is a more flexible grammatical approach.
5
Apply the conclusion to non-intended acts
The passage ends by stating that intention is not required for non-intended acts (ghayr maqṣūrah), such as wudu. This is an important exception to the qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'.
This distinction is unique to the Hanafi school; Shafi'is require intention in wudu.

صاحب کتاب علیہ الرحمہ کی یہ عبارت ایک سوال مقدر کا جواب ہے: سوال: یہ ہے کہ حدیث مذکورہ انما الاعمال بالنيات، مقاصد میں نیت کے شرط صحت ہونے پر دلالت نہیں کرتی پھر مقاصد میں نیت کے شرط ہونے کو کس دلیل سے ثابت کیا ہے۔ جواب : اس عبارت سے دیا ہے کہ مقاصد یعنی عبادات مقصودہ میں نیت کے شرط پر دو دلیلیں قائم کی میں (1) اجماع (۲) آیت قرآنیه و ما امروا إلا ليعبدوا الله مخلصين له الدین حنفاء ۔ ان میں پہلی دلیل یعنی اجماع زیاد مناسبے کیونکہ پہلی دلیل پر کوئی اعتراض نہیں ہے جبکہ دوسری دلیل پر اعتراض ہو سکتا ہے اور وہ اعتراض یہ ہے کہ آیت میں لیعبدوا الله معطوف علیہ ہے جس سے مراد عبادات مقصورہ ہیں اور نماز وروزہ جن کا عطف لیعبدوا اللہ پر کیا گیا ہے وہ بھی عبادات مقصودہ ہیں اس صورت میں معطوف علیہ اور معطوف میں مغایرت نہیں بلکہ اتحاد ثابت ہورہا ہے جبکہ معطوف علیہ اور معطوف میں مغامرت ہوتی ہے۔ اس کا جواب مصنف نے یہ دیا ہے کہ یہاں لیعبد وا میں عبادت توحید کے معنی میں ہے اور قرینہ اس کا کہ عبادة بمعنی تو حید ہے یہ ہے کہ صلوۃ اور زکوۃ کا عطف ليعبدوا پر ہے معطوف علیہ اور معطوف میں مغایرت ہوتی ہے اور مغایرت اس وقت ثابت ہوگی جب یہاں لیعبدو ا میں عبادت سے تو حید مراد لیجائے اس لئے یہاں عبادت توحید کے معنی میں ہے صلوۃ اور زکوۃ عبادات مخصوصہ ہیں اور تو حید و عبادت میں من وجہ مغایرت ہے۔ دوسرا جواب یہ ہے کہ معطوف علیہ اور معطوف میں من کل الوجود مغایرت ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ من وجہ مغامرت کافی ہے اور یہاں من وجہ مغایرت موجود ہے اس طور پر کہ لیعبد وا میں عبادت سے عام عبادت مراد لی جائے اور ا قامت صلوۃ اور ایتاء زکوۃ سے خاص عبادت مراد لیجائے اور خاص کا عطف عام پر درست ہے۔ فلا تشترط الخ : یہ تفریح ہے "لا يدل على اشتراطها پرکہ عبادات غیر مقصودہ کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے نیت شرم نہیں ہے۔
The author’s statement is an answer to an implied question: The question is that the mentioned hadith 'Actions are by intentions' does not indicate that intention is a condition for the validity of intended acts. So with what evidence is the condition of intention in intended acts established? The answer given in this passage is that for the condition of intention in intended acts, two proofs are established: (1) Ijma (consensus) and (2) the Quranic verse 'And they were not commanded except to worship Allah, being sincere to Him in religion, inclining to truth.' Among these, the first proof, ijma, is more appropriate because there is no objection to the first proof, while an objection can be raised to the second proof. And that objection is that in the verse, 'liya'budu Allah' is the object of the verb, from which intended acts are meant, and prayer and fasting, which are conjoined to 'liya'budu Allah', are also intended acts. In that case, there is no difference between the conjoined and the conjoined-to; rather, identity is established, whereas difference is required between them. The author answers this by saying that here 'liya'budu' means worship of Tawhid, and the evidence for this is that 'ibadah' is in the meaning of Tawhid. This is that prayer and zakat are conjoined to 'liya'budu'; there must be difference between the conjoined and the conjoined-to, and difference is established only if here in 'liya'budu' worship is taken to mean Tawhid. Therefore, here worship is in the meaning of Tawhid, while prayer and zakat are specific acts of worship, and between Tawhid and worship there is difference in some respects. The second answer is that difference in every respect is not necessary between the conjoined and the conjoined-to; rather, difference in some respects is sufficient, and here difference in some respects exists in this manner: that in 'liya'budu' worship is taken in a general sense, and in 'establishing prayer' and 'giving zakat' specific worship is taken, and the conjunction of the specific to the general is valid. 'So it is not a condition' etc.: This is a branching statement: 'does not indicate its condition' — meaning that for the validity of non-intended acts, intention is not a condition.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage is a commentary defending the condition of intention (niyyah) in intended acts of worship (ibādāt maqṣūrah). The author addresses a hypothetical objection: the famous hadith 'Actions are by intentions' does not explicitly prove that intention is a condition for validity of acts like prayer and fasting. To prove it, two evidences are cited: first, ijma (consensus) of the scholars, which is irrefutable; second, the Qur'anic verse (Quran 98:5) commanding sincere worship. The objection raised is that the verse's structure ('liya'budu' and then specific acts) seems to imply identity rather than difference, but the author resolves this through two interpretations: either 'liya'budu' means Tawhid (monotheism) which is distinct from specific acts, or it means general worship while the specific acts are a subset, and conjunction of specific to general is valid. The passage concludes by stating that intention is not required for non-intended acts (ghayr maqṣūrah), setting the stage for exceptions.

Key Terms
عبادات مقصودہ (ibādāt maqṣūrah): Acts of worship that are intended for their own sake, like prayer, fasting, zakat, hajj.
عبادات غیر مقصودہ (ibādāt ghayr maqṣūrah): Acts of worship that are not intended for themselves but as means, like wudu, ghusl, removal of impurity.
اجماع (ijmā'): Consensus of the mujtahidun of the ummah on a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is the condition of intention in intended acts of worship primarily established by ijma rather than the Quranic verse?
A) Because the Quranic verse is ambiguous and can be interpreted differently
B) Because ijma is beyond objection while the verse may be subject to interpretation
C) Because the verse only applies to non-intended acts
D) Because ijma overrides the Quran in this matter

Key Takeaway
Intention is a condition for intended acts (ibādāt maqṣūrah) based on ijma and Quran; for non-intended acts, it is not required.

Intention in Tayammum: Exception to the Rule
Explains why intention is a condition in tayammum despite it being a non-intended act.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that intention is required in tayammum due to its linguistic meaning, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
Tayammum requires intention because its name means 'to intend'—an exception to the rule for non-intended acts.

In the Hanafi school, intention is generally not a condition in acts of purification that are not inherently intended (ghayr maqṣūrah). Wudu and ghusl are prime examples. However, tayammum breaks this pattern. Why? The answer lies in the very word 'tayammum', which linguistically means to intend. This lesson unpacks that reasoning and addresses the Shafi'i objection that tayammum's requirement should apply to wudu by analogy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Rule
Recall the Hanafi principle: intention is not required in non-intended acts (e.g., wudu, ghusl). This is the baseline from which tayammum is an exception.
This rule is a qāʿida fiqhiyya: 'لا تشترط النية في العبادات غير المقصودة'.
2
Locate the Exception and its Proof
The exception is tayammum. The proof is the Qur'anic verse 'fa tayammamū' because the word itself denotes intention. Lexical meanings are carried into legal definitions.
The author argues that since the linguistic meaning includes qaṣd, intention is inherent.
3
Examine the Shafi'i Objection
Imam al-Shafi'i uses qiyas: tayammum is a deputy (nāʾib) of wudu; if the deputy requires intention, the original (wudu) should a fortiori require it.
This is a classic case of qiyas al-awlawī (a fortiori analogy).
4
Analyze the Hanafi Response
The Hanafi response is that wudu and tayammum are fundamentally different. Wudu's acts (washing, wiping) do not linguistically imply intention, while tayammum's name does. Also, water is inherently purifying; earth is not.
Qiyas fails because the ʿilla (effective cause) is absent: the linguistic link that makes intention necessary in tayammum is not shared by wudu.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
The thamarah al-khilāf: Hanafis hold wudu valid without intention; Shafi'is require intention for wudu. For tayammum, both schools agree intention is required, but the reasoning differs.
This affects fatwa: a mufti must know when intention is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا اِشْتِرَاطُهَا فِي التَّيَمُّم فَلِدَلَالَةِ ايَتِهِ عَلَيْهَا لأَنَّهُ الْقَصْدُ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال تیم میں نیت کا شرط ہوتا آیت تیم کے نیت پر دلالت کرنے کی وجہ سے ہے کیونکہ تم کے معنی قصد وارادہ کے ہیں۔ تشریح تیم کے لغوی معنی ارادہ کرنا اور شرعی معنی ہیں پاکی کے ارادہ سے دونوں ہاتھ پاک مٹی پر مار کر پورے چہرے اور دونوں ہاتھوں پر پھیرنا ۔ (م 1 ایضان شرح او را اینا ح ص ۲۱۰) ماقبل میں یہ بات واضح طور پر معلوم ہو چکی ہے کہ عبادات غیر مقصودہ میں نیت شرما نہیں ہے اور تمیم بھی عبادات غیر مقصودہ میں شامل ہے پھر اس میں نیت کو کیوں شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے اس کا جواب مصنف دے رہے ہیں کہ تیم کے اندر نیت کے شرط ہونیکی دلیل خود آیت تیم "فلم تجدوا ماء فتيممو صعیداً طبیبا“ ہے کیونکہ تمیم کے معنی ہی قصد وارادہ کے ہیں لغوی معنی کا لحاظ شرعی معنی میں بھی رکھا جاتا ہے اس لئے تمیم کے اندر نیت کو شرط قرار دیا ہے۔ اگر چہ امام شافعی بھی تیم میں نیت کو شرط قرار دیتے ہیں لیکن انہوں نے ایک بات اور فرمائی کہ تیم وضو کا نائب اور خلیفہ ہے اور جب نائب وخلیفہ کی صحت کے لئے نیت کو ضروری قرار دیا گیا ہے تو اصل یعنی وضو میں بدرجہ اولی نیت کو شرط قرار دیا جائے گا لیکن ہم یہ کہتے ہیں کہ وضو غسل اور مسح کا مجموعہ ہے اس میں نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے جبکہ تمیم کے معنی ہی قصد وارادہ کے ہیں لہذا وضو کو تیم پر قیاس نہیں کر سکتے ۔ بعض علماء نے ایک جواب اور بھی دیا ہے کہ طہارت کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) طہارت حقیقیہ (۲) طہارت غیر حقیقیہ ، اللہ نے پانی کو مظہر بنا کر ہی اتارا ہے اس لئے اس سے ازالہ نجاست کے لئے نیت شرط نہیں بخلاف مٹی کے اس کا وصف خاص تلویث ہے بوقت حاجت مٹی کو طہارت کے لئے استعمال کیا جاتا ہے اور حاجت کا پتہ نیت سے چلتا ہے اس لئے اس میں نیت کو شرط قرار دیا گیا ہے۔
And as for making intention a condition in tayammum, it is because its verse indicates it, for it means intention. Translation: And indeed the condition of intention in tayammum is because the verse of tayammum indicates it, for tayammum means intention and will. Explanation: The lexical meaning of tayammum is to intend, and the legal meaning is to strike pure earth with the hands with the intention of purification and wipe the face and hands. (Reference) In the previous discussion, it became clear that in non-intended acts, intention is not a condition, and tayammum is included among non-intended acts. Then why is intention made a condition in it? The author answers that the evidence for the condition of intention in tayammum is the verse itself: '...and if you find no water, then perform tayammum with pure earth' because tayammum means intention and will; the lexical meaning is also considered in the legal meaning. Therefore intention is made a condition in tayammum. Although Imam Shafi'i also makes intention a condition in tayammum, he further says that tayammum is a deputy and successor of wudu, and when intention is required for the validity of the deputy, then in the original (wudu) a fortiori intention should be a condition. But we say that wudu is a combination of washing and wiping; intention is not required in it, whereas tayammum means intention and will, so we cannot make an analogy of wudu to tayammum. Some scholars have given another answer: that purification is of two types: (1) real purification and (2) non-real purification. Allah sent down water as a manifest agent, so for removing impurity with it intention is not a condition. In contrast, earth's inherent property is to make impure; at the time of need, earth is used for purification, and the need is known through intention, so intention is made a condition in it.
Source pages p. 72

Commentary
This passage addresses an exception: tayammum is a non-intended act (ghayr maqṣūrah) like wudu, yet intention is required for it. The author explains that the requirement stems from the Qur'anic verse 'fa tayammamu' because the word tayammum itself linguistically means 'to intend' (qasd). This lexical meaning is incorporated into the legal definition, making intention inherent. The Hanafi school compares this with wudu and ghusl, where intention is not required because water is inherently purifying and does not need qasd. The passage also refutes Imam Shafi's qiyas (analogy) that since tayammum (deputy) requires intention, wudu (original) should also require it. The Hanafi response is that wudu is composed of washing and wiping, which do not inherently require intention, whereas tayammum's very name implies intention. Additionally, another justification is given: water is a natural purifier, so no intention is needed; earth is not naturally purifying, so intention identifies the need.

Key Terms
التيمم (al-tayammum): Striking pure earth with hands and wiping face and hands with the intention of purification.
القياس (al-qiyas): Analogical reasoning extending a ruling from an original (asl) to a branch (far') based on a common effective cause (illah).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does the Hanafi school require intention in tayammum but not in wudu?
A) Because tayammum is a substitute for wudu
B) Because the word tayammum linguistically means intention
C) Because water is scarce and intention is needed to conserve it
D) Because all acts of worship require intention

Key Takeaway
Intention is a condition in tayammum because its name implies intention, making it an exception to the rule that non-intended acts do not require intention.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

Intention Required for All Acts of Worship Except Islam
Stating a universal maxim with its single exception and proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi maxim on intention in worship, identify its sole exception, and apply the maxim to new cases (furuat) using the evidence of Islam al-mukrah.

Core Idea
Intention is the key to worship, but entering Islam itself requires only the tongue, not the heart.

In the Hanafi school, intention (niyyah) is a fundamental condition for the validity of most acts of worship. However, there is one striking exception: the act of entering Islam. This lesson presents the maxim that intention is required for all acts of worship except Islam, and explains the evidence from the ruling on a coerced convert. Understanding this maxim is crucial for the mufti, as it governs the distinction between worldly and otherworldly recognition of one's faith.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
Locate the textual statement: intention is a condition for the validity of all acts of worship (al-ibadat al-maqsudah). Recognize that this includes salah, sawm, hajj, zakat, etc., but excludes mere means like wudu.
The maxim is a kulliya (universal) with a single exception.
2
Examine the exception: Islam
Notice that the text explicitly exempts Islam. The proof given is the validity of a coerced person's conversion (Islam al-mukrah). Even without internal intention, the outward utterance of the shahadah makes one a Muslim for worldly legal purposes.
This does not address religious acceptance in the Hereafter, which requires true belief.
3
Understand the proof
The evidence is a practical ruling: the jurists (Hanafi) hold that a person forced to say the shahadah becomes a Muslim in terms of inheritance, marriage, and other worldly matters. This shows that intention is not a condition for the validity of Islam itself.
This is a dalil naqli (transmitted evidence) from the practice of the Companions.
4
Distinguish worldly vs otherworldly Islam
The text clarifies that Islam has two aspects: worldly (dunyawi) and otherworldly (ukhrawi). The rule about intention only applies to worldly rulings; the Hereafter depends on true belief. Thus, a coerced convert is treated as a Muslim in society but is not guaranteed salvation.
This distinction prevents misunderstanding: the maxim only governs legal status, not ultimate salvation.
5
Apply to furuat
Work through the furuat (applications) provided: a coerced person's Islam is valid, and a person who only intends Islam without uttering the shahadah does not become a Muslim. Test these cases using the maxim and its exception.
This step solidifies the ability to apply the maxim to real scenarios.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا فِي الْعِبَادَاتِ كُلَّهَا فَهِيَ شَرْطُ صِحْتِهَا إِلَّا الْإِسْلَامُ فَإِنَّهُ يَصِحُ بِدُونِهَا بِدَلِيْلٍ قَوْلِهِمْ إِنَّ إسْلَامَ الْمُكْرَهِ صَحِيْحٌ وَلَا يَكُونُ مُسْلِماً بِمُجَرَّدِ نِيَّةِ الْإِسْلَامِ بِخِلَافِ الْكُفْرِ كَمَا سنبيلة فِي بَحْث التروي.
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال تمام عبادات میں سوائے اسلام کے نیت عبادات کی صحت کی شرط ہے کیونکہ اسلام بدون نیت صحیح ہو جاتا ہے دلیل فقہاء کا یہ ارشاد ہے کہ مرہ کا اسلام درست ہے اور محض اسلام کی نیت سے مسلمان نہیں ہوگا بخلاف کفر کے اس کو ہم تروک کی بحث میں بیان کریں گے۔ تشریح: مصنف فرماتے ہیں کہ جملہ عبادات مقصودہ کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے نیت کا پایا جانا ضروری ہے عبادات مقصودہ کی تعریف ماقبل میں کی جاچکی ہے، البتہ صحت اسلام کے لئے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے بلکہ اسلام کے معتبر ہونے کے لئے صرف اظہار اسلام کافی ہے لیکن یہ بات ذہن میں رہے کہ اسلام کی دو حیثیتیں ہیں (۱) دنیوی (۲) اخروی۔
As for all acts of worship, intention is a condition for their validity, except Islam, for it is valid without it, by the evidence of their statement: the Islam of a coerced person is valid, and one does not become Muslim merely by the intention of Islam, contrary to disbelief, as we will mention in the discussion of tark (relinquishing). Translation: In all acts of worship, intention is a condition for their validity, except Islam, because Islam becomes valid without intention. The proof is the jurists' statement that the Islam of a coerced person is valid, and one does not become Muslim merely by the intention of Islam, contrary to disbelief. We will mention this in the discussion of tark. Explanation: The author says that for all intended acts of worship (al-ibadat al-maqsudah), intention is necessary for their validity. The definition of intended acts of worship was given previously. However, for the validity of Islam, intention is not necessary; rather, for Islam to be considered, mere verbal pronouncement is sufficient. But keep in mind that Islam has two aspects: (1) worldly and (2) otherworldly.
Source pages p. 74

Commentary
This passage presents a key legal maxim: intention is a condition for the validity of all acts of worship except for the act of embracing Islam. The author explains the exception with a proof: even a person coerced into uttering the shahadah becomes a Muslim in the worldly sense, and conversely, a person who merely intends Islam in the heart without uttering it does not become a Muslim. This is contrary to disbelief (kufr), where internal conviction alone can make one a disbeliever. The author also distinguishes between the worldly and otherworldly aspects of Islam: worldly rulings (such as inheritance, marriage) follow the external pronouncement, while the otherworldly acceptance (in the Hereafter) depends on true belief. The passage underscores that intention is needed for acts like prayer, fasting, etc., but for entering the fold of Islam, the outward declaration suffices, regardless of inner state.

Key Terms
نیة (niyyah): Intention in the heart distinguishing an act of worship from a mere habit
عبادات مقصودة (al-ibadat al-maqsudah): Acts of worship that are ends in themselves (e.g., salah, sawm, hajj), not merely means (like wudu)
اسلام المكره (islam al-mukrah): The conversion of a person under coercion by uttering the shahadah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is an exception to the rule that intention is a condition for the validity of acts of worship?
A) Tayammum
B) Ghusl al-mayyit
C) Entering Islam
D) Salah

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that intention is a condition for the validity of all acts of worship, except for the act of entering Islam itself, which is valid with mere outward declaration.

Intention for Imam and Muqtadi: Rules and Exceptions
Legal ruling on necessity of intention for imam and follower

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'No reward except with intention' to the cases of imam and muqtadi, state the exceptions for women and substitute imam, and evaluate the opposing view of al-Karkhi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir.

Core Idea
Imam's prayer is valid without intention of imamah; follower's intention is essential; exceptions arise for women and substitutes.

This passage unpacks one of the key distinctions in Hanafi fiqh: the role of intention (niyyah) in congregational prayer for the imam and the follower. While the follower cannot connect to the imam without a clear intent, the imam’s leadership is valid even without an explicit intention to lead. However, this rule has important exceptions when women or a substitute imam are involved. Understanding these nuances is essential for issuing correct fatwas on congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the Main Rule
Identify the core ruling: the follower (muqtadi) must intend to follow the imam for the prayer to be valid, but the imam does not need to intend imamah for his own prayer or the congregation's prayer to be valid.
The rule is based on the principle that intention is needed to establish connection (iqtida'), not to lead.
2
Recognize the Opposing View
Note that al-Karkhi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir dissent: they analogize the imam to the follower and argue the imam must also intend. Understand their proof and the Hanafi response that the imam’s role is primary and does not require connection.
The Hanafi view relies on the fact that the imam's action of leading itself establishes the role.
3
Understand the Exception for Women
When women are behind the imam, the imam must intend imamah for their following to be valid. This exception is to prevent the imam's prayer from becoming invalid if a woman stands parallel to him, a harm he did not consent to.
This exception is derived from the qawida 'al-darar yuzal' (harm must be removed).
4
Analyze the Further Exception for Jumu'ah and 'Eid
Some scholars (supported by al-Khulasah) exclude Jumu'ah and the two 'Eid prayers from the women exception, meaning the imam's intention is not required even with women present. The reason is that the harm (women standing parallel) is rare in such prayers, and the rare is considered non-existent (al-nadir ka'l-ma'dum).
The author endorses this view as correct.
5
Apply the Qawida 'No Reward Without Intention'
Note that even when the imam's prayer is valid without intention, he loses the reward of imamah because reward is conditional on intention. This illustrates the qawida 'la thawaba illa bi al-niyyah'.
This qawida complements the main rule: validity does not require intention, but reward does.

کی اقتداء کے بیچ ہونے کے لیے امام کا ان کی امامت کی نیت کرنے کو ضروری قرار دیا گیا ہے تا کہ اس کے التزام کئے بغیر امام کی نماز کا فساد لازم ندا ہے۔ لیکن یہ حکم نماز جنازہ کو شامل نہیں ہے یہ حکم تو صرف تصحیح کی ہے اور اس کو قول مخترقراردیا گیا ہے۔
Following an imam is not valid except with intention, and imamah is valid without intention of it, contrary to al-Karkhi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir, as in al-Binayah. Except when women pray behind him, then their following him without the imam's intention for imamah is not valid. And some excepted Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids, and that is correct as in al-Khulasah. Translation: Following the imam is not valid without intention, and imamah is valid without intention of imamah; al-Karkhi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir differ, as in al-Binayah. But when women pray behind the imam, their following is not valid without the imam's intention for imamah. And some excepted Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids, and that is correct as in al-Khulasah. Explanation: al-Iqtida' is the connection of the follower's prayer to his imam's prayer. A person who prays following and accompanying another person must intend to follow his imam; otherwise his prayer is not valid. However, it is not necessary for the imam to intend imamah; rather, his imamah is valid without intention of imamah. But in that case, due to the absence of intention, he is not deserving of the reward of imamah, because the well-known fiqh principle: no reward except with intention. Imam al-Karkhi and Imam Abu Hafs al-Kabir say that just as it is necessary for the follower to intend to follow the imam, so too it is necessary for the imam to intend imamah. Yes, in one case: if an imam becomes imam by way of deputyship, then it is necessary for him to intend imamah; otherwise his imamah is not valid. "But an exception is made for one whose imamah is by way of deputyship, for he does not become an imam unless he intends imamah, by agreement" (Shami Karachi, vol. 1, p. 423). Except when women pray behind him: if women also pray behind the imam, then just as it is necessary for the follower to intend to follow, so too it is necessary for the imam to intend for the women. The reason is that if a woman comes in line with the imam, the imam's prayer would become invalid, and the imam would incur a harm that he did not undertake; this is contrary to Shariah. Therefore, for the women's following to be valid, the imam's intention for their imamah is made necessary, so that the invalidation of the imam's prayer is not entailed without his undertaking. But this ruling does not include the funeral prayer; this ruling is only for prayers that are a complete individual of prayer, and the funeral prayer is not a complete individual, so that no objection occurs. And some excepted Jumu'ah and the two 'Eids: according to the majority of scholars, for the validity of women's following, it is necessary for the imam to intend their imamah, and this includes Jumu'ah and 'Eid. While according to some jurists, for Jumu'ah and 'Eid, it is not necessary for the imam to intend their imamah. The reason is that the harm due to which a distinction was made in the following of men and women is rare in Jumu'ah and 'Eid, and the rare is considered non-existent. The author of the book has corrected the statement of some jurists from al-Khulasah, and it is considered the preferred view.
Source pages p. 77

Commentary
This passage is a detailed legal discussion on the necessity of intention for the follower (muqtadi) and the imam. It opens by stating the rule: following an imam is not valid without intention (the follower must intend to follow), but the imam's leading is valid without him intending to be imam. This is the Hanafi position, opposed by al-Karkhi and Abu Hafs al-Kabir who say the imam must also intend. The passage then provides exceptions: when women are behind the imam, the imam must intend imamah for the prayer to be valid (exception to the rule that imam does not need intention). However, some scholars exclude Jumu'ah and 'Eid from this exception (so intention not required for them). The reason given for the women exception is that if a woman stands parallel to the imam, it would invalidate his prayer; thus, requiring intention ensures he accepts this risk. Funeral prayer is excluded because it is not a complete prayer (not a full fardh). The passage also mentions that a substitute imam must intend. Finally, it cites the well-known fiqh principle 'no reward without intention' to explain that the imam loses reward if he does not intend, but the prayer is valid. The author endorses the view of al-Khulasah that Jumu'ah and 'Eid are exceptions.

Key Terms
اقتداء (iqtida'): Following the imam in prayer by connecting one's prayer to his
إمامة (imamah): The act of leading prayer
الثواب (al-thawab): Reward from Allah

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling when women pray behind an imam who did not intend imamah?
A) The women's prayer is valid because the imam's intention is not required.
B) The women's prayer is invalid because the imam must intend for their following to be valid.
C) The prayer is valid only if it is Jumu'ah or 'Eid.
D) The prayer is valid if the imam is a substitute imam.

Key Takeaway
The follower's intention is required for valid iqtida'; the imam's intention is not required except when women follow, for substitute imam, and by the majority view also for Jumu'ah/'Eid (though the preferred view exempts them).

Intention for Facing Qiblah: The Mufta Bihi Position
Explaining the need for intention when facing the qiblah in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the mufta bihi position on whether intention is required for facing the qiblah, evaluate the opposing arguments, and apply the relevant Hanafi legal maxim to a fatwa scenario.

Core Idea
Intention is not required for facing the qiblah in prayer — ease prevails over strictness.

This passage addresses a subtle issue: is intention (niyyah) needed when facing the qiblah? The answer is not obvious because it depends on whether facing the exact Kaaba is obligatory. Different Hanafi scholars argued, but the relied-upon fatwa is clear. Let's walk through the reasoning and see how the principle of ease (taysir) governs the matter.

Guided Path
1
Identify the khilaf
Recognize the disagreement on whether intention is required for facing qiblah. The majority (jumhur) say no; Abdullah al-Jurjani and others say yes.
2
Analyze the opposing position
Al-Jurjani argued that since distant persons cannot face the exact Kaaba, intention substitutes for exactness. This is the core of the opposing dalil.
3
Apply the Hanafi tarjih methodology
The jumhur view is preferred because it avoids unnecessary hardship. The principle of ease (al-mashaqqah tajlibu al-taysir) overrides the stricter view.
4
Extract the governing qawida
The maxim 'hardship brings ease' is the operative legal principle. It governs situations where exact specification is difficult.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The fatwa is that intention is not required at all, whether in a mihrab (built area) or wilderness, known or unknown qiblah.
This is the final ruling for issuing fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تشریح : استقبال قبلہ کے لئے نیت شرط ہے یا نہیں در اصل یہ مسئلہ ایک دوسرے مسئلہ پر موقوف ہے کہ منی کعبہ کو سامنے کرنا صحت صلاۃ کے لئے شرط ہے یا نہیں ۔ جمہور علماء کے نزدیک کی مشاہد کے لئے عین قبلہ کی طرف رخ کرنا ضروری ہے اور مکی غیر مشاہد کے لئے جت قبلہ سمت قبلہ ہی کافی ہے میں قبلہ کی طرف رخ کرنا ضروری نہیں ہے۔
عبدالله جرجانی کے نزدیک عین قبلہ کا رخ کرنا ہر ایک کے لئے ضروری ہے مشاہد ہو یا غیر مشاہد یعنی قریب ہو یا بعید چونکہ بعید کو اس کا مکلف بنانے میں پریشانی ہے اس لئے انہوں نے نیت کو ضروری قرار دیکر عین قبلہ کا درجہ دیدیا پھر اس کے بعد دو قول ہو گئے ۔
(1) شیخ ابو بکرمحمد بن الفضل کے نزدیک کعبہ کا رخ کرنے کے بعد بھی نیت کعبہ کرنا شرط ہے۔ (۲) شیخ محمد بن حامد کے نزدیک شرط نہیں ہے اور جمہور کا مسلک بھی یہی ہے جیسا کہ صاحب ہدایہ تجنیس کے حوالہ سے نقل کرتے ہیں کہ صحیح قول کے مطابق نیت کعبہ مطلقا شرط نہیں ہے۔
بعض حضرات نے اول صورت کو اس پر محمول کیا ہے کہ جب جنگل وغیرہ میں نماز پڑھے اور دوسری صورت کو اس پر محمول کیا ہے جب محراب کی طرف یعنی آبادی میں نماز پڑھے۔ بہر حال فتقومی اس پر ہے کہ نیت نہ استقبال کے لئے شرط صحت ہے اور نہ استقبال کے بعد تعیین کعبہ کے لئے خواہ محراب میں نماز پڑھی جائے یا جنگل میں قبلہ متعارف ہو و متعین ہو یا غیر متعارف و غیر متعین ہو۔
Explanation: Whether intention is a condition for facing the qiblah. In reality, this issue depends on another issue: whether facing the Kaaba is a condition for the validity of prayer. According to the majority of scholars, for one who sees the Kaaba, it is necessary to face the exact direction of the qiblah, while for one who does not see it, facing the direction of the qiblah is sufficient; it is not necessary to face the exact direction of the qiblah. According to Abdullah al-Jurjani, facing the exact qiblah is necessary for everyone, whether they see it or not, i.e., whether near or far. Because making the distant person obligated to do so involves difficulty, they made intention necessary and gave it the status of facing the exact qiblah. Then there are two opinions: (1) According to Sheikh Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl, intending the Kaaba is a condition even after facing it. (2) According to Sheikh Muhammad ibn Hamid, it is not a condition, and this is the position of the majority, as the author of al-Hidayah narrates from al-Tajnish that according to the correct statement, intention of the Kaaba is absolutely not a condition. Some scholars have interpreted the first case as when one prays in the wilderness, and the second case as when one prays towards the mihrab, i.e., in a populated area. In any case, the fatwa is based on the view that intention is neither a condition for the validity of facing the qiblah nor for specifying the Kaaba after facing it, whether prayer is performed in the mihrab or the wilderness, whether the qiblah is known and specified or unknown and unspecified.
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage discusses the role of intention (niyyah) in facing the qiblah for prayer. It first frames the issue within the broader question of whether facing the exact Kaaba is a condition for prayer validity. The majority view is that only those who see the Kaaba must face it exactly; others may face its general direction. Abdullah al-Jurjani held a stricter view, but to alleviate difficulty, he made intention a substitute for exactness. Two subsequent opinions emerged among Hanafi scholars: Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn al-Fadl required intention even after facing the Kaaba, while Muhammad ibn Hamid and the majority did not require it at all. The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is the latter: intention is not required, neither for the act of facing nor for specifying the Kaaba, regardless of location or clarity. This ruling is based on ease and is the standard for fatwa.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention; a mental resolve to perform an act of worship for the sake of Allah.
قبلہ (qiblah): The direction of the Kaaba in Mecca, which Muslims face during prayer.
مشاہد (mushāhid): One who sees the Kaaba directly, i.e., a person present in Mecca near the Kaaba.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi), is intention (niyyah) required for facing the qiblah in prayer?
A) Yes, always required
B) Required only for those who see the Kaaba
C) Not required at all
D) Required only in the wilderness

Key Takeaway
Intention is not a condition for facing the qiblah; the majority Hanafi view, based on ease, is the mufta bihi.

Intention and Reward: Al-Umūr bi Maqāṣidihā Applied
Two legal applications of the maxim 'al-umūr bi maqāṣidihā'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qā‘ida 'al-umūr bi maqāṣidihā' to determine when intention is required for validity and when it suffices for reward.

Core Idea
Intention not required for covering awrah but is the basis for reward, even if the act is unintentionally invalid.

This lesson explores the boundaries of the maxim 'al-umūr bi maqāṣidihā'. While many acts of worship require intention for validity, covering the awrah is an exception. Moreover, even an invalid act can yield reward if the intention was sincere and the invalidity was unintentional. We will examine the two applications given by Ibn Nujaym and supported by a hadith qudsi.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two distinct rulings
The passage presents two independent points: covering awrah does not require intention for validity; reward for worship is based on intention even if the act is invalid due to unintentional error.
Both are applications of the same qā‘ida.
2
Analyze the ruling on covering awrah
The text states that intention is not a condition for the validity of covering awrah and that there is no scholarly disagreement on this. This is an exception to the general rule that acts of worship require intention.
Ibn Nujaym affirms consensus.
3
Analyze the ruling on reward for invalid worship
The text explains that reward depends on intention, not outward validity. If an act is invalid due to an unintentional mistake (e.g., praying without wudu under false assumption of purity), the person still receives reward for his intention. But if the invalidity is deliberate, no reward is given.
The hadith qudsi supports this: Allah records a good intention as a full good deed.
4
Connect both rulings to the qā‘ida
The first ruling shows that sometimes the act itself fulfills the obligation regardless of intention (exception). The second ruling shows that intention is the primary basis for divine reward (direct application). Both illustrate the scope of 'al-umūr bi maqāṣidihā'.

وَأَمَّاسَتْرُ الْعَوْرَةِ فَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ لِصِحْتِهِ النِّيَّةُ وَلَمْ أرَفِيْهِ خِلَافًا وَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ لِلتَّوَابِ صِحَّةُ الْعِبَادَةِ بَلْ يُقَابُ عَلَى نِيَّتِهِ وَإِنْ كَانَتْ فَاسِدَةً بِغَيْرِ تَعَمُّدِهِ كَمَا لَوْصَلَّى مُحْدِثًا عَلَى ظَنِّ طَهَارَتِهِ وَسَيَاتِي تَحْقِیقه
ترجمہ: اور بہر حال ستر عورت تو اس کی صحت کے لئے نیت شرم نہیں اور میں نے اس میں کسی کا اختلاف نہیں دیکھا اور ثواب کے لئے عبادت کا صحیح ہونا شرط نہیں بلکہ اسے اس کی نیت پر تو اب دیا جائے گا اگر چہ وہ فاسد ہی ہو بغیر اس کے کہ اس کی طرف سے عمد ا ہو جیسا کہ کوئی محدث ہونے کی حالت میں اس گمان کے ساتھ نماز پڑھ لے کہ وہ ظاہر ہے اور اس کی تحقیق عنقریب آئے گی۔ تشریح: ستر عورت کے لئے کسی کپڑے کا استعمال کرے تو اسے استعمال کرتے وقت ستر عورت کی نیت نہ کرے تو بھی ستر عورت کا فریضہ ہو جائیگا اس کے لئے نبیت کی کوئی ضرورت نہیں ہے، علامہ ابن نجیم مصری فرماتے ہیں اس مسئلہ میں کسی کا اختلاف میری نظر سے نہیں گذرا۔ ولا تشترط للنواب صحة العبادة : اخروی ثواب کے لئے عبادت کا صحیح ہونا شرط نہیں ہے بلکہ ثواب کا مدار فعل کے مقابلہ میں نیت پر زیادہ ہے اگر کسی آدمی نے عبادت شروع کی عبادت کی نیت سے تو اخروی ثواب اس سے متعلق ہو گا اگر اس کے قصد و ارادہ کے بغیر بھی وہ عبادت فاسد ہوگئی تب بھی ثواب ملے گا اور اگر اس نے جان بوجھ کر عبادت فاسد کی تو پھر تو اب نہ ملے گا مثلا کسی کا غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ وہ با وضو ہے اور اس حال میں اس نے نماز ادا کی حالانکہ وہ محدث یعنی بے وضو تھا تو اس کو اس صورت میں بھی ثواب ملے گا کیونکہ ثواب کا تعلق نیست سے ہے اور اس نے اس صفت پر نماز پڑھی جس صفت پر نماز کی ادائیگی کا مکلف بنایا گیا ہے اس لئے اس پر ثواب کا ترتب ہو گا ہاں اگر بعد میں اسے یقین ہو جائے کہ نماز بغیر وضو پڑھی گئی تو دوبارہ نماز پڑھے جس کی تائید مسلم شریف کی ایک حدیث سے ہوتی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فيما يرويه عن ربه عز وجل قال إن الله كتب الحسنات والسيئات ثم بين ذلك فمن هم بحسنة فلم يعملها كتبها الله عنده حسنة كاملة فان هم بها فعملها كتبها الله عنده عشر حسنات الى سبع مائة ضعف الى اضعاف كثيره وان هم بسيئة فلم يعملها كتبها الله عنده حسنة كاملة وان هم بها فعملها كتبها الله سيئة واحدة ( مسلم شریف ج راص / ۷۸ )
And as for covering the private parts (awrah), intention is not required for its validity, and I have not seen any disagreement in this. And for reward, the validity of the worship is not a condition; rather, he will be rewarded according to his intention, even if it is invalid without deliberate intent, such as when one prays in a state of ritual impurity while thinking he is pure, and its verification will come later. Translation: And in any case, for covering the private parts, intention is not a condition for its validity, and I have not seen any disagreement in this. And for reward, the correctness of worship is not a condition; rather, reward will be given based on his intention, even if it is invalid without his deliberate act, such as when someone prays in a state of impurity under the assumption that he is pure, and its verification will come soon. Explanation: If one uses a cloth to cover his private parts without intending to cover them, the obligation of covering is still fulfilled; intention is not required. Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says: I have not seen any disagreement in this issue. 'And for reward, the validity of worship is not a condition': For the reward of the Hereafter, the correctness of worship is not a condition; rather, reward is more dependent on intention than on the act itself. If someone starts an act of worship with the intention of worship, he will receive reward for it; even if the worship becomes invalid without his intent, he will still be rewarded. But if he deliberately invalidates the worship, he will not receive reward. For example, if someone has a dominant assumption that he is in a state of ablution and prays in that state while actually he was in impurity, he will still be rewarded because reward is connected to intention, and he performed the prayer in the state that he was commanded to. Yes, if he later becomes certain that the prayer was performed without ablution, he should repeat the prayer. This is supported by a hadith in Sahih Muslim: From Ibn Abbas, from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him), from his Lord, He said: 'Indeed, Allah has written down the good deeds and the evil deeds, and then clarified that. Whoever intends a good deed but does not do it, Allah writes it for him as a complete good deed. If he intends it and does it, Allah writes it for him as ten good deeds up to seven hundred times, up to many multiples. And if he intends an evil deed but does not do it, Allah writes it for him as a complete good deed. And if he intends it and does it, Allah writes it for him as a single evil deed.' (Muslim, Vol. 1, p. 78)
Source pages p. 83

Commentary
This passage presents two distinct rulings. First, covering the awrah (private parts) does not require intention for its validity. This is a settled matter without disagreement. Second, even if an act of worship is invalid due to an unintentional error, the doer may still receive reward if he had a sincere intention. The text uses the example of someone praying without wudu while unaware of his impurity; he obtains reward because his intention was genuine, though he must repeat the prayer. A hadith qudsi from Sahih Muslim supports the principle that Allah rewards a good intention even if the act is not completed. This principle is crucial for understanding that reward (thawab) in the Hereafter is primarily based on intention, not merely the outward validity of the act. The commentary by Allamah Ibn Nujaym affirms the consensus on the first point.

Key Terms
ستر العورة (satr al-‘awrah): Covering the private parts which must be covered during prayer; also in daily life.
ثواب (thawāb): Divine reward in the Hereafter for sincere acts of obedience.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for an act of worship to yield reward in the Hereafter?
A) The act must be perfectly valid and all conditions met.
B) The intention must be sincere, even if the act is unintentionally invalid.
C) Both intention and outward validity are required.
D) Only outward validity matters, intention is irrelevant.

Key Takeaway
Covering awrah is valid without intention; for reward, intention is primary, and unintentional invalidity does not negate it.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
