Reward Depends on Intention: The Qawida and Its Application
Explains the rule that reward depends on intention, with a hadith proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida that reward is based on niyyah, apply it to cases of unintentional invalidity, and identify the exception for intentional invalidity.

Core Idea
Reward depends on intention, not external validity — even an unintentionally invalid act earns reward.

This passage introduces a fundamental qawida in Hanafi fiqh: reward is related to intention (niyyah). It clarifies that even if an act of worship becomes invalid without intention, the worshipper still receives reward. The key is sincerity of intention, not whether the act meets all conditions externally. This is rooted in a hadith qudsi from Sahih Muslim that emphasizes how Allah records intentions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida
Read the passage and find the exact statement that expresses the rule. The text says 'ثواب کا تعلق نیست سے ہے' (reward is related to intention). This is the legal maxim being taught.
The qawida is a concise rule derived from multiple evidences.
2
Parse the scope of the qawida
Determine whether the rule applies to all acts or specifically to acts of worship. The passage discusses 'عبادت' (acts of worship) and the example is prayer (salah). The scope is acts of worship, but the principle of intention applies broadly.
Later Hanafi scholars often extend this qawida to all acts of obedience.
3
Apply to the given example
Work through the example of a person who prays without wudu due to a predominant assumption (ghalabat al-zann) of having wudu. According to the rule, he still receives reward because his intention was sincere, even though the prayer was invalid.
The note about repeating the prayer if certainty of invalidity arises is a separate ruling.
4
Note the exception
Identify when the rule does not apply: if the invalidity was intentional (e.g., deliberately invalidating salah), then no reward is given. The intention is corrupted.
This exception is crucial for the mufti to apply correctly.
5
Connect to the hadith proof
Read the hadith qudsi cited. It shows that even intending a good deed without acting on it earns a full reward, supporting the principle that intention is the basis for reward. The hadith directly reinforces the qawida.
The hadith is from Sahih Muslim and is a key textual evidence for this principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
سے متعلق ہو گا اگر اس کے قصد و ارادہ کے بغیر بھی وہ عبادت فاسد ہوگئی تب بھی ثواب ملے گا اور اگر اس نے جان بوجھ کر عبادت فاسد کی تو پھر تو اب نہ ملے گا مثلا کسی کا غالب گمان یہ ہے کہ وہ با وضو ہے اور اس حال میں اس نے نماز ادا کی حالانکہ وہ محدث یعنی بے وضو تھا تو اس کو اس صورت میں بھی ثواب ملے گا کیونکہ ثواب کا تعلق نیست سے ہے اور اس نے اس صفت پر نماز پڑھی جس صفت پر نماز کی ادائیگی کا مکلف بنایا گیا ہے اس لئے اس پر ثواب کا ترتب ہو گا ہاں اگر بعد میں اسے یقین ہو جائے کہ نماز بغیر وضو پڑھی گئی تو دوبارہ نماز پڑھے جس کی تائید مسلم شریف کی ایک حدیث سے ہوتی ہے۔ عن ابن عباس عن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فيما يرويه عن ربه عز وجل قال إن الله كتب الحسنات والسيئات ثم بين ذلك فمن هم بحسنة فلم يعملها كتبها الله عنده حسنة كاملة فان هم بها فعملها كتبها الله عنده عشر حسنات الى سبع مائة ضعف الى اضعاف كثيره وان هم بسيئة فلم يعملها كتبها الله عنده حسنة كاملة وان هم بها فعملها كتبها الله سيئة واحدة ( مسلم شریف ج راص / ۷۸ )
Will be related: even if an act of worship becomes invalid without his intention and will, reward will still be given. But if he intentionally invalidated the worship, then reward will not be given. For example, someone's predominant assumption is that he has wudu, and in that state he performed prayer while he was actually impure (without wudu). In that case he will still get reward because reward is related to intention (niyyah). He performed the prayer while he was charged to do so. Therefore, reward will be given. However, if later he becomes certain that the prayer was performed without wudu, he should repeat the prayer, as supported by a hadith in Sahih Muslim. From Ibn Abbas from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) in what he narrates from his Lord, Almighty: 'Indeed Allah wrote the good deeds and the evil deeds, then clarified that. So whoever intends a good deed but does not do it, Allah writes it for Him as a complete good deed. But if he intends it and does it, Allah writes it for Him as ten good deeds up to seven hundred times, up to many multiples. And if he intends an evil deed but does not do it, Allah writes it for Him as a complete good deed. And if he intends it and does it, Allah writes it as one evil deed.' (Muslim, volume [1], page 78)
Source pages p. 84

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a legal maxim. It explains that reward for acts of worship depends on intention (niyyah). The text presents a rule: if an act of worship becomes invalid unintentionally, the worshipper still receives reward because reward is connected to the intention, not to the outward validity. The example given is salah performed without wudu due to a predominant assumption that one has wudu. In Hanafi fiqh, this is known as 'ghalabat al-zann'. The ruling is that reward is still given, but if certainty of invalidity arises later, the prayer must be repeated. The text then cites a hadith qudsi from Sahih Muslim that underscores the principle that rewards are based on intention. This hadith is often used to support the general maxim 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions).

Key Terms
نیست (niyyat): قصد و ارادہ (intention), the mental resolve to perform an act of worship.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the basis for receiving reward in acts of worship?
A) The external validity of the act
B) The intention (niyyah)
C) The physical effort exerted
D) The presence of wudu

Key Takeaway
Reward for acts of worship depends on intention (niyyah), not external validity; unintentional invalidity does not deprive reward, but the act must be repeated if certainty of invalidity arises.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

The Maxim 'Al-Manthuru Kal-Fard' and Nadhr Conditions
Maxim definition with intra-madhhab dispute and furuat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maxim 'al-manthuru kal-fard', identify its conditions (including that the vowed act must not already be obligatory and must be from a wajib genre), and apply it to determine the validity of a nadhr in cases like Umrah, Hajj, and Udhiyah.

Core Idea
A nadhr is only valid if the vowed act is a non-obligatory act of obedience from a wajib genre; pre-existing obligations nullify the vow.

In this passage, the author explores the Hanafi maxim 'al-manthuru kal-fard' (the vowed act is like a fard). He first presents an intra-madhhab dispute on the status of Umrah—is it wajib or sunnah? The answer determines whether a nadhr to perform Umrah can create an obligation. He then elaborates the maxim, explaining that a valid nadhr requires the act to be non-obligatory, an act of obedience, and from the category of intended obligations (wajibat maqsuda). Two illustrative furuat are given: a vow to perform Hajj while already obligated, and a vow to sacrifice while already obligated. In both, the nadhr is invalid. This lesson unpacks the maxim and its application in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Understand the Umrah dispute
Why does the author start with Umrah? What is the practical consequence for nadhr? The dispute on whether Umrah is wajib or sunnah directly affects the effectiveness of a nadhr to perform it.
If Umrah were wajib, a nadhr would be invalid (pre-existing obligation); if sunnah, the nadhr still does not make it wajib because Umrah's genre is sunnah.
2
State the maxim and its meaning
What does 'al-manthuru kal-fard' mean? It equates the vowed act to a fard in terms of binding force and need for intention. But this is conditional.
The maxim is a dabt (restrictive sub-maxim) limited by the conditions of nadhr.
3
Identify the conditions for a valid nadhr
List the conditions from the text: the vowed act must not already be obligatory, must be an act of obedience, not a sin, and must belong to a genre that is wajib (wajibat maqsuda).
The condition 'genre wajib' is critical: a nadhr for a nafl act that is not from a wajib genre (e.g., Umrah) does not make it wajib.
4
Apply the condition of non-obligation to the examples
For Hajj and Udhiyah, why is the nadhr invalid? Because the vowed act is already obligatory at the instance level; the condition of non-obligation is missing.
The istithna (exception) to the maxim: if the act is already wajib, the maxim does not apply; the original obligation stands.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
What is the relied-upon view on Umrah and how does it affect fatwa? The mufta bihi is that Umrah is sunnah, so a nadhr does not make it wajib.
This follows the tarjih of later scholars like Ibn Abidin and Ibn Qayyim.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
طواف اور صفا و مروہ کی سعی کرنے کے ہیں عمرہ کو حج اصغر بھی کہتے ہیں۔
علماء احناف میں سے بعض وجوب عمرہ کے قائل ہیں صاحب بحر بھی وجوب عمرہ کے قائل ہیں اور صاحب بدائع الہ نائع علامہ کا سائی نے بھی اس کو اختیار کیا ہے۔
علامہ شامی فرماتے ہیں کہ ظاہر روایت سنیت عمرہ کی ہے امام محمد نے نفل ہونے کی تصریح کی ہے صاحب فتح القدیر کار بستان بھی اسی طرف ہے۔
علامہ ابن قیم مصرفی نے بھی عمرہ کے سلیٹ ہونے کی تصریح کی ہے۔ نیز اس جگہ یہ بات بھی یا دور رہے کہ جب عمرہ اپنی اصل کے اعتبار ہے سنت ٹھہرا تو اگر اس میں کوئی نذر بھی مانے گا تو وہ سنت ہی رہے گا واجب نہیں ہوگا کیونکہ اسی چیز کی نذروا جب ہوتی ہے جو اپنی جنس کے اعتبار سے واجب ہو اور جو اپنی جنس کے اعتبار سے واجب ہی نہ ہو تو اس کی نذر مان لینے سے بھی وہ واجب نہ ہوگا بلکہ محض کرنے یا نہ کرنے کا اختیار ہوگا کیونکہ یہاں نذر ہی کا اعتبار ہی نہیں ۔
والمنذور كالفرض : منذور فرض کے مانند ہے جس طرح فرض کی صحت اور تعیین کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے اس طرح نذر کی صحت اور تعیین کے لئے بھی نیت ضروری ہے۔ یہ تشبیہ دراصل اس بات پر مبنی ہے کہ نذر فرض ہے یا واجب ہے۔ بعض وجوب کے قائل ہیں اور بعض فرضیت کے قائل ہیں علامہ ابن نجیم مصری بھی نذر کے وجوب کے قائل ہیں۔ نذر کہتے ہیں کہ بندہ کسی غیر لازم چیز کو اپنے اوپر لازم کر لے حکم اس کا یہ ہے کہ یہ فرض کے قائم مقام ہے اس کو پورا کرنا ضروری ہے بشرطیکہ وہ کسی معصیت کی نذر نہ ہو یا کسی ایسی عبادت کی نذر نہ ہو جو بذاتہ مقصود نہ ہو اور وہ ایسی طاعت پر مشتمل ہو جس کی جنس از قبیل واجبات مقصودہ ہو ۔
ولونذ رحجة الاسلام: اگر کسی شخص نے نذر مانی کہ اگر میرا افلاں کام ہو گیا تو میں حج فرض ادا کروں گا تو اس پر حج فرض ہی فرض ہوگا اس پر نذر کی وجہ سے حج فرض نہ ہو گا اس لئے کہ شرائط نذر میں سے یہ بھی ہے کہ منذور واجب نہ ہو چونکہ یہاں منذور پہلے ہی سے واجب ہے اس لئے شرط مفقود ہونے کی وجہ سے نذرتیح نہیں ہوئی جس کی وجہ سے صرف اصل فرض اس پر رہ گیا۔ ی ایسا ہی ہے جیسے کسی نے ایام نحر میں قربانی کی نذر مانی حال یہ ہے کہ اس پر قربانی پہلے سے واجب ہے تو اس کی نذر کی وجہ سے اس پر قربانی واجب نہ ہوگی صرف پہلے سے واجب شدہ قربانی واجب ہوگی۔
The actions of Tawaf and Sa'i between Safa and Marwah are [part of Umrah]; Umrah is also called the Lesser Hajj. Some Hanafi scholars hold the obligation (wujub) of Umrah; the author of al-Bahr also holds it obligatory, and the author of Bada'i' al-Sana'i' and Allamah Kasani have also chosen this. Allamah Shami says that the apparent transmission (zahir al-riwayah) is that Umrah is Sunnah; Imam Muhammad specified it as Nafl; the author of Fath al-Qadir also leans this way. Allamah Ibn Qayyim Misri also specified Umrah as Sunnah. Also, note here: when Umrah by its origin is Sunnah, then if one makes a nadhr (vow) therein, it remains Sunnah and does not become obligatory, because a nadhr is only valid for something that is obligatory by its own type; if the act is not obligatory by its own type, then making a nadhr does not make it obligatory; rather, one has the option to do it or not, because the nadhr is not effective. 'Al-manthuru kal-fard': The vowed act is like a fard. Just as intention is necessary for the validity and specification of fard, similarly intention is necessary for the validity and specification of nadhr. This analogy is based on whether nadhr is fard or wajib. Some hold wujub, some hold fardiyyah. Allamah Ibn Nujaym Misri also holds wujub of nadhr. Nadhr means a person makes a non-obligatory thing obligatory upon himself; its ruling is that it stands in place of fard; it is necessary to fulfill it, provided it is not a vow of disobedience, nor a vow of an act of worship that is not inherently intended, and it must consist of an obedience whose category is among intended obligations. 'Wa law nadhra hajjat al-islam': If a person vows, 'If my such-and-such work is accomplished, I will perform the obligatory Hajj,' then the Hajj remains obligatory (fard) upon him, and it does not become [a separate] obligation due to the vow, because among the conditions of nadhr is that the vowed act is not already obligatory. Since the vowed act here is already obligatory, the condition is missing, so the nadhr is not valid; only the original obligation remains. This is similar to a person who vows to sacrifice during the days of Nahr while sacrifice is already obligatory upon him; then the sacrifice does not become obligatory due to his vow; only the previously obligatory sacrifice remains obligatory.
Source pages p. 91

Commentary
This passage is a legal discussion combining two issues: the status of Umrah and the rule of nadhr (vow) when the vowed act is already legally obligatory. The author first presents the ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars on whether Umrah is wajib or sunnah/nafl, noting that the dominant position in the madhhab is that it is sunnah based on the explicit statement of Imam Muhammad. He then draws a practical consequence: if one makes a nadhr to perform Umrah, since Umrah by its nature is sunnah (not wajib), the nadhr does not elevate it to wajib; it remains sunnah with the option to perform or not. This is because a valid nadhr requires that the act be non-obligatory at the time of the vow. The author then explains the maxim 'al-manthuru kal-fard' (the vowed act is like a fard), emphasizing that intention is required for both fard and nadhr. Finally, he applies the rule: if one vows to perform Hajj while already obliged to do so (e.g., before fulfilling one's obligatory Hajj), the vow is ineffective; only the original obligation stands. Similarly, if one vows to sacrifice during the days of Nahr while already obliged to sacrifice (e.g., due to a prior cause), the vow does not add an extra obligation.

Key Terms
نذر (nadhr): A vow by which a person makes a non-obligatory act obligatory upon themselves, provided it is an act of obedience and not already obligatory.
منذور (manthur): The act vowed (the subject of the nadhr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if someone vows to perform an act that is already obligatory upon them, what happens to the nadhr?
A) The nadhr becomes valid and adds a separate obligation.
B) The nadhr is invalid and the original obligation remains.
C) The nadhr is valid but the original obligation is removed.
D) The nadhr is considered a supererogatory act.

Key Takeaway
A valid nadhr requires the vowed act to be non-obligatory and from a genre that is wajib; pre-existing obligations nullify the vow.

Intention in Udhiyah: Purchase vs. Slaughter, and Unauthorized Slaughter
Rules that intention for udhiyah must be at purchase, and consequences if another slaughters without permission

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that intention for udhiyah is required at the time of purchase, and evaluate the validity of udhiyah when an unauthorized person slaughters the animal, depending on whether the owner demands compensation.

Core Idea
Intention for udhiyah must be at purchase; unauthorized slaughter may not invalidate if the owner accepts without compensation.

In this lesson, we explore a specific legal maxim (qa'ida) concerning the sacrificial animal (udhiyah) for Eid al-Adha. The Hanafi school emphasizes that the intention (niyyah) must be made when purchasing the animal, not when slaughtering it. This distinction leads to nuanced rulings when someone else slaughters the animal without the owner's permission. By understanding this qawida and its derived cases (furu'), you will be able to determine when the udhiyah remains valid and when compensation affects its validity.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida
Paraphrase the ruling: Intention for udhiyah is necessary, but at the time of purchase, not at the time of slaughter.
This is the core principle from which furu' derive.
2
Identify the key element (dabt)
Note that the controlling factor is the purchase with intention. The animal becomes designated (mu'ayyan) as udhiyah at purchase.
The dabt is 'نية الأضحية عند الشراء' (intention at purchase).
3
Analyze the furu' cases
Walk through each scenario: (1) Unauthorized slaughter without compensation → valid. (2) Unauthorized slaughter with compensation → invalid. (3) Unauthorized slaughter on behalf of owner → valid, no liability.
The distinction hinges on whether the owner accepts the animal as his udhiyah or treats it as a loss.
4
Extract the underlying principle
The owner's acceptance without compensation indicates that the animal remains designated as udhiyah. Demanding compensation shows the owner considers the animal as his property, not udhiyah.
This aligns with the qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions).
5
Apply to similar cases
Think of other scenarios where the timing of intention matters, e.g., the designation of a sacrificial animal before hajj or the setting aside of sadaqah.
The mufti must be careful to apply the rule only to udhiyah, not to other sacrifices generally.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَأَمَّا الضَّحَايَا فَلَابُدَّ فِيهَا مِنَ النِّيَّةِ لَكِنْ عِندَ الشَّرَاءِ لَا عِنْدَ الذَّبْحِ وَتَفَرَّعَ عَلَيْهِ أَنَّهُ لَوْ إشْتَرَاهَا بِنِيَّةِ الأضْحِيَّةِ فَذَبَحَهَا غَيْرُهُ بِلا إذن فَإِنْ أَخَذَهَا مَذْبُو حَقَّوَلَمْ يُضْمِنهُ أجْزَانه و إنْ ضَمَّنَهُ لَا تَجْزِيْهِ كَمَا فِي أَضْحِيَّةِ النَّخِيْرَةِ وَهَذَا إِذَا ذَبَحَهَا عَنْ نَفْسِهِ وَأَمَّا إِذَا ذَبَحَهَا
عَنْ مَالِكِهَا فَلَاضِمَانَ عَلَيْهِ.
ترجمه اور میں قربانیاں تو ان میں نیت ضروری ہے لیکن خریدنے کے وقت نہ کہ ذبح کے وقت اور اسی پر متفرع ہے کہ اگر اسکو قربانی کی نیت سے خریدا پھر کسی دوسرے نے بغیر اجازت کے ذبح کر دیا پس اگر اس نے زنا شده لے لیا اور اسکو ضامن قرار نہیں دیا تو اسکو کافی ہے۔ اور اگر اسکو ضامن قرار دیا تو اس کو کافی نہیں ہے۔ جیسا کہ ذخیرہ کے کتاب الاضحیۃ میں ایسا ہی ہے۔ اور یہ اس صورت میں ہے کہ جب اسکو اپنی طرف سے ذبح کیا اور بہر حال جب اسکو اسکے مالک کی طرف سے ذبح کیا تو اسپر ضمان نہیں۔
And as for udhiyah (sacrificial animals), intention is necessary in them, but at the time of purchase, not at the time of slaughter. And derived from this is that if one purchased it with the intention of udhiyah, then another person slaughtered it without permission: if he took it slaughtered and did not make him liable (did not claim compensation), it suffices him; if he made him liable (claimed compensation), it does not suffice him, as in al-Dhakhirah in the chapter of Udhiyah. This is when he slaughtered it for himself; but if he slaughtered it on behalf of its owner, then there is no liability upon him.
Source pages p. 92

Commentary
This passage states a specific fiqhi rule regarding the intention (niyyah) for udhiyah (the sacrificial animal for Eid al-Adha). The key point is that the intention must be made at the time of purchasing the animal, not at the time of slaughter. This is because the purchase with the intention of sacrifice designates the animal as an udhiyah. The author then presents a furu' (branch) derived from this rule: if someone buys an animal with the intention of udhiyah, and then another person slaughters it without the owner's permission, the ruling depends on whether the owner holds the slaughterer liable (i.e., demands compensation). If the owner accepts the slaughtered animal without requiring compensation, the sacrifice is valid (the owner's obligation is fulfilled). If the owner demands compensation (i.e., the price of the animal) from the slaughterer, then the sacrifice is not valid because the owner's action effectively shows that he did not accept the animal as his udhiyah. This distinction is taken from the book al-Dhakhirah. Additionally, if the unauthorized person slaughters it on behalf of the owner (intending the reward for the owner), then there is no liability (i.e., no compensation), presumably because the sacrifice is considered valid.

Key Terms
أضحية (udhiyah): The sacrificial animal slaughtered on the days of Eid al-Adha with the intention of worship.
ضمان (daman): Liability or compensation for loss or damage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if someone slaughters another's udhiyah animal without permission, but the owner accepts the meat without demanding compensation?
A) The udhiyah is invalid and the owner must slaughter another.
B) The udhiyah is valid and suffices for the owner.
C) The udhiyah is valid only if the slaughterer pays the price.
D) The udhiyah is invalid and the owner must not eat the meat.

Key Takeaway
Intention for udhiyah is valid only at purchase; unauthorized slaughter may be salvaged if the owner accepts without compensation.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

All Qurbat Require Intention for Reward: The Maxim and Its Applications
Explaining the maxim that all qurbat require intention for reward with applications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi qawida that all qurbat require intention for reward, identify its scope, and apply it to multiple furuat including teaching, judging, testimony, and permissible acts.

Core Idea
Reward for any good deed depends on intending to draw near to Allah — intention transforms even permissible acts into worship.

In this lesson, we explore a foundational legal maxim from the Hanafi school: every act of drawing near to Allah (qurbah) requires intention (niyyah) for reward. This maxim is not limited to ritual worship but extends to teaching, judging, testimony, and even mundane acts like eating and sleeping. The source text from Al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair by Ibn Nujaym explains this rule and illustrates it with numerous applications, along with careful definitions of related terms.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim
Read the opening statement of the passage: 'وَعَلى هَذَا سَائِرُ الْقُرَبِ لَا بُدَّ فِيْهَا مِنَ النِّيَّةِ'. Paraphrase the maxim in your own words, noting that reward depends on intending to draw near to Allah.
The maxim is a sughra (minor) kulliya (universal) qawida.
2
Classify the terms: 'ibadah, ta'at, qurbat
The passage defines three categories. Distinguish them: 'ibadah requires intention for validity and reward; qurbat requires intention only for reward; ta'at brings reward without requiring intention for validity. Understand where each applies.
This classification is key to applying the maxim correctly.
3
Apply the maxim to the furuat
Work through the examples given: teaching (talim), fatwa, authorship, judging, hudud, testimony, and mubahat. For each, state the ruling: reward depends on intention, but the act itself is valid even without intention (except for 'ibadat).
Note the hadith warning against corrupt intentions in seeking knowledge.
4
Connect to the complementary maxim
The maxim complements 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). Explain how the two maxims work together: the general principle that intentions determine the value of actions is specified for qurbat in this lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَعَلى هَذَا سَائِرُ الْقُرَبِ لَا بُدَّ فِيْهَا مِنَ النِّيَّةِ بِمَعْنَى تَوَقُّفِ حُصُوْلِ الثَّوَابِ عَلَى قَصْدِ التَّقَرُّب بِهَا إِلى اللهِ تَعَالَى مِنْ نَشْرِ الْعِلْمِ تَعْلِيماً وَإِفْتَاءً وَتَصْنِيْفاً.
:ترجمه اور اس پر جملہ قرجمین محمول ہیں کہ ان میں نیت ضروری ہے اس اعتبار سے کہ ثواب کا حصول موقوف بے ان کے ذریعہ اللہ کے تقرب کا ارادہ کرنے پر ان میں سے ) اشاعت علم ہے تعلیم کے ذریعہ ہو یا افتاء کے ذریعہ یا تصنیف کے ذریعہ۔ تشریح: علامہ ابن نجیم مصری فرماتے ہیں کہ جملہ قربات نکاح کی طرح ہیں کہ اگر ان میں اللہ کے تقرب کا ارادہ کر لیا جائے تو ثواب حاصل ہوگا اور اگر تقرب کی نیت نہ کی تو اگر چہ وہ صحیح اور درست ہو جائیں گے لیکن ثواب نہ ملے گا۔ ان ہی تقریبات میں سے اشاعت علم ہے۔ ار علم سیکھنے سے نیت دوسروں کو سکھانے اور اس پر عمل کرنے کی ہو تو ثواب ملے گا اسی طرح فتویٰ دینے سے نیت وں کو کی راہ دکھلانے کی ہوتب ہی عمل آخرت میں ثواب کا سبب ہوگا اور اگر نیت جاہلوں پر بڑائی جتلانے اور تکبر کی جوب پھر یہی علم وبال جان ہو جائے گا۔ حدثنی ابن کعب بن مالک عن ابيه قال سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول من طلب العلم ليجارى به العلماء او ليمارى به السفهاء او يصرف به وجوه الناس إليه ادخله الله الغفار . ( ترندی شریف ج راص ۹۴۶)
(۱) عبادت ایسے فعل کو کہتے ہیں جس پر ثواب کا ترتب ہو سکتا ہو اور وہ اپنی صحت کے لئے نیت کا محتاج ہو اور اس میں مجود کی معرفت بھی حاصل ہو جیسے نماز ، روزہ وغیرہ۔
(۲) طاعت ایسے فعل کو کہتے ہیں جس پر ثواب کا ترتب ہو سکتا ہو خواہ وہ فعل اپنی صحت کے لئے نیت کا نشان ہوا نہ ہو اور جس کی طاعت کی جارہی ہو اور جس وجہ سے کی جارہی ہو وہ معلوم ہو یا نہ ہو جیسے معرفت خداوندی میں غور دیگر کرنا یہ عبادت ہے نہ قربت بلکہ صرف طاعت ۔
(۳) قربت ایسے فعل کو کہتے ہیں جس پر ثواب کا ترتب ہو سکتا ہو اور اس کی صحت نیت پر موقوف نہ ہو لیکن اس فعل کو انجام دیتے وقت منتقرب الیہ ضرور معلوم ہو جیسے قراءت قرآن، حق اور وقف و غیرہ لیکن ان میں سے ہرایک کا دوسرے کی جگہ استعمال کیا جا سکتا ہے۔
وَأَمَّا الْقَضَاءُ فَقَالُوْا إِنَّهُ مِنْ أَشْرَفِ الْعِبَادَاتِ فَالثَّوَابُ عَلَيْهِ مُتَوَفَّفٌ عَلَيْهَا وَكَذَلِكَ إِقَامَةٌ الْحُدُودِ وَالتَّعَازِيرِ وَكُلُّ مَا يَتَعَاطَاهُ الْحُكَامُ وَالْعُلَاةُ وَكَذَا تَحَمُّلُ الشَّهَادَاتِ وَأَدَاؤُهَا. جمه : اور بہر حال قضا تو فقہا ء فرماتے ہیں کہ وہ افضل ترین عبادات میں سے ہے اس پر نواب نیست پر موقوف ہے اور یہی حکم حدود و تعزیرات قائم کرنے کا اور ان تمام امور کا ہے جنہیں حکام اور ذمے داران اختیار کرنے ہیں اور یہی محکم تحمل شہادت اور اداء شہادت کا ہے۔
تشريح : القضاء لغة الحكم وشرعاً فصل الخصومات وقطع المنازعات. (شامی ج (۲۷۸) تعلیم و تعلم کی طرح قضاء بھی ضروری ہے پس جس طرح تعلیم و تعلم میں نیت پر ثواب مرتب ہوتا ہے اسی طربنا اگر قضاء میں بھی نیت کی جائے گی تو ثواب ملے گا اور نہ نہیں یہی حکم حدود کو قائم کرنے اور تعزیرات کے نفاذ کا ہےاگر ثواب کی نیت کی تو ثواب حاصل ہو گا ورنہ نہیں۔ وكذا تحمل الشهادة : گواہ بنے اور گواہی دینے کا ثواب نیت پر موقوف ہے، شہادت کا عمل امر مبانا ہے فی نفسہ عبادت نہیں ہے اور اگر کوئی امر مباح کو عبادت بنانا چا ہے تو اس کے لئے ثواب کی نیت کرنا ضروری ہے تا لئے گواہ بننے اور گواہی دینے کا ثواب نیت پر موقوف ہے۔
وَأَمَّا الْمُبَاحَاتُ فَإِنَّهَا تَخْتَلِفُ صِفَتُهَا بِإِعْتِبَارِ مَا قُصِدَتْ لِأجْلِهِ فَإِذَا قَصَدَ بِهَا التَّقَوِّى عَلَى الطَّاعَاتِ أَوْ الْتَوَكَّلَ إِلَيْهَا كَانَتْ عِبَادَةَ كَالا كُل وَالنَّوْمِ وَاكْتِسَابِ الْمَالَ وَالْوَطي. ترجمه اور بہر حال مباحات تو ان کی صفت اس کے اعتبار سے مختلف ہے جس کی وجہ سے ان کا ارادہ کیا گیا ہو۔ پس جب ان کے ذریعہ طاعات پر طاقت حاصل کرنے یا ان تک پہنچنے کا ارادہ کیا جائے تو وہ عبادت ہوئے
And upon this are all acts of drawing near to Allah (qurbat): intention is necessarily required in them, meaning the attainment of reward is dependent on intending to draw near to Allah thereby, such as spreading knowledge through teaching, issuing fatwas, and authoring books. Translation: And all qurbat are included in this: intention is necessary in them, in that reward depends on intending to draw near to Allah through them. Among them is spreading knowledge, whether through teaching, fatwa, or authorship. Commentary: Allama Ibn Nujaym al-Misri says that all qurbat are like marriage: if one intends to draw near to Allah, reward is obtained; if not, though they are valid, no reward is given. Among these qurbat is spreading knowledge. When learning knowledge, if one intends to teach others and act upon it, reward is given; similarly, when giving fatwa, if one intends to guide people, it becomes a cause of reward in the hereafter; but if the intention is to show off before the ignorant or to gain pride, then this knowledge becomes a burden. Ibn Ka'b ibn Malik narrated from his father that he heard the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) say: 'Whoever seeks knowledge to contend with the scholars, or to argue with the foolish, or to turn people's faces towards him, Allah will enter him into the Fire.' (Tirmidhi, Vol. 1, p. 946)
(1) 'Ibadah is an act upon which reward can be based and which requires intention for its validity, and knowledge of the object of worship is also obtained, like prayer and fasting.
(2) Ta'at is an act upon which reward can be based, whether or not it requires intention for its validity, and whether or not the one being obeyed and the reason for obedience are known, like contemplating the knowledge of God; this is not 'ibadah nor qurbat but merely ta'at.
(3) Qurbat is an act upon which reward can be based and whose validity does not depend on intention, but at the time of performing the act, the one to whom one draws near must be known, like recitation of Quran, Hajj, and waqf; however, each of these terms can be used interchangeably.
As for qada (judging), the jurists said that it is among the noblest acts of worship, so reward for it is dependent on intention, and similarly establishing hudud and ta'zirat, and everything undertaken by rulers and authorities, and likewise bearing and giving testimony. Translation: As for qada, the jurists say it is among the noblest acts of worship, so reward for it is dependent on intention. Similarly, establishing hudud and ta'zirat, and all matters that rulers and authorities undertake, and likewise bearing and giving testimony. Commentary: Qada linguistically means judgment; in Shariah, it is resolving disputes and ending conflicts. (Shami vol. 278) Just like teaching and learning, qada also requires intention for reward. So if in qada one intends reward, reward will be given; if not, not. This same ruling applies to establishing hudud and implementing ta'zirat: if one intends reward, reward is obtained; otherwise not. Similarly, bearing and giving testimony: reward is dependent on intention. The act of testimony is a permissible thing in itself, not inherently worship. If one wants to make a permissible act into worship, intention for reward is necessary. Therefore, bearing and giving testimony relies on intention for reward.
As for permissible acts (mubahat), their nature changes according to what they are intended for. So if one intends through them to strengthen oneself for acts of obedience (ta'at) or to rely on them, they become worship, such as eating, sleeping, earning money, and sexual intercourse. Translation: As for permissible acts, their nature varies according to what they are intended for. If one intends through them to gain strength for acts of obedience or to rely on them, they become worship, such as eating, sleeping, earning money, and sexual intercourse.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage expounds a key legal maxim: all acts of drawing near to Allah (qurbat) require intention (niyyah) for reward. The author begins by stating the maxim, then provides a detailed commentary. First, it is explained that even if an act is valid in itself, reward is contingent on intending nearness to Allah. Examples include teaching, giving fatwa, and writing books. A hadith warns against corrupt intentions in seeking knowledge. The passage then defines three related terms: 'ibadah, ta'at, and qurbat. 'Ibadah (e.g., prayer, fasting) requires intention for both validity and reward. Ta'at (e.g., contemplating God's signs) brings reward but does not require intention for validity. Qurbat (e.g., reciting Quran, Hajj) brings reward without requiring intention for validity, but the actor must be aware they are drawing near to Allah. The discussion then extends the maxim to qada (judging), hudud, ta'zirat, and bearing testimony: all require intention for reward. Finally, permissible acts (mubahat) like eating and sleeping become worship if intended to support obedience to Allah. This illustrates the principle that intention transforms ordinary acts into acts of worship.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention; the mental resolve to perform an act for the sake of Allah, which determines whether the act yields reward.
قربت (qurbat): An act upon which reward can be based but whose validity does not depend on intention, though the actor must be aware of drawing near to Allah; examples include recitation of Quran, Hajj, and waqf.
عبادت (ibadah): An act that requires intention for both validity and reward, and in which knowledge of the object of worship is obtained; examples are prayer and fasting.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following acts is classified as 'ibadah (requires intention for validity)?
A) Recitation of Quran
B) Judging (qada)
C) Fasting
D) Teaching

Key Takeaway
All acts of qurbat require intention for reward; intention transforms even permissible acts into worship.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

Mubah Acts Becoming Worship Through Intention
Explaining how permissible acts become worship with proper intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to mubah acts, determining when they become worship, sin, or remain neutral.

Core Idea
A permissible act becomes worship if intended as a means for obedience.

The maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions' permeates all fiqh. In this lesson, we examine a key furu: how mubah (permissible) acts like eating, earning, or sleeping transform into acts of worship when the intention is to gain strength for obedience. This illustrates the power of niyyah to elevate neutral actions to rewardable deeds. We also contrast with mandub and sunnah acts, which require intention for reward.

Guided Path
1
Define mubah and its default ruling
Identify the Hanafi definition of mubah: an act whose doing and leaving are equally permissible without preference. Understand that without intention, it carries no reward or sin.
Refer to Umdat al-Izah: mubah is neutral.
2
Apply the maxim to mubah acts
State the ruling: if the intention behind the mubah act is to facilitate obedience (e.g., eat to have strength for prayer), the act becomes worship and earns reward. If the intention is sinful, it becomes sin.
Intention changes the legal description of the act.
3
Distinguish between mubah and mandub/sunnah
Masnun and mandub acts require intention to be considered obedience and receive reward. Without intention, they are not rewarded. Mubah acts require intention to transform them at all.
Mandub definition: doing preferable, leaving less preferable.
4
Analyze the example of earning money
Work through the text's example: earning with no intention → no reward/sin; earning to spend on good deeds → reward; earning to spend on sin → sin. Generalize to all mubah acts.
This shows niyyah creates three possible outcomes.
5
Relate to obligatory acts
Note that obligatory acts that are intended as worship (e.g., prayer) require intention for validity. Obligatory acts that are not intended as worship (e.g., repaying debts) do not require intention for validity but require it for reward.
The purpose of mu'amalat is benefiting people, not worship per se.

As for permissible acts, their description varies according to the purpose for which they are intended. So if one intends thereby to gain strength for acts of obedience or to achieve reliance, they become worship, like eating, sleeping, earning money, and intercourse. Translation: And in any case, permissible acts: their description varies according to what they are intended for. So when through them one intends to gain strength for acts of obedience or to reach them, they become worship, like eating, earning money, and intercourse. Commentary: Mubah is every act whose doing and not doing are permissible, without preference for one over the other (from Umdat al-Izah, p. 37). The description of permissible acts varies according to intention. For example, if one earns money with no intention, there is no reward or sin. If one intends to spend on disobedience, it is sin. If one intends to spend on good deeds, it is reward. Analogy applies to eating. Since permissible acts are not among intended acts of worship, they do not require intention for validity. However, if one intends to gain strength for good deeds or to reach good deeds through these permissible acts, they become worship and reward will be given. For example, eating is permissible; if the purpose is to gain strength for good deeds, reward; if for mischief, sin; if no intention, no reward or sin. Similarly, masnunat and mandubat require intention to be acts of obedience and receive reward; otherwise intention is not necessary. Hence, any permissible matter becomes worship through intention. Example of masnun and mandub: visiting the sick and offering condolences. The definition of sunnah has passed. Mandub is an act whose doing and leaving are both permissible, but doing it is preferable and leaving it is less preferable. As for obligatory acts: those which are intended acts of worship require intention for validity, like prayer and fasting. But those which are not intended acts of worship do not require intention for validity, though intention is necessary for reward, like repaying debts and returning entrusted items, because the purpose of these and all transactions is to benefit people. As for transactions, they are many types: sale does not depend on intention, similarly iqala and ijarah. But they said: if one contracts using a mudari' that is not preceded by sawfa or sin, it depends on intention. If he intends thereby the present obligation, it is a sale, otherwise not. Unlike the past tense, for sale with it does not depend on intention. As for the mudari' that is purely future, it is like a command: sale is not valid with it, not even with intention. We have explained this in Sharh al-Kanz. Translation: And in any case, transactions are many types: sale does not depend on it, and similarly iqala and ijarah. But the jurists say: if one contracts with a mudari' that is not preceded by sawfa and sin, it depends on intention.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage applies the maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions' to permissible acts and contracts. Mubah acts like eating or earning become worship when intended as a means for obedience. This is a key furu of the maxim. The text then discusses mu'amalat: sales contracts in past tense require no intention, but if expressed in future tense (without sawfa/sin), intention determines whether it is a binding sale. If the mudari' is purely future, it cannot form a valid sale. This shows the Hanafi position on the role of niyyah in contracts.

Key Terms
مباح (mubah): Every act whose doing and not doing are permissible, without preference.
مندوب (mandub): An act whose doing and leaving are both permissible, but doing is preferable and leaving is less preferable.
مضارع (mudari'): The imperfect tense verb in Arabic; used here for expressing future or present action in contracts.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) It becomes worship if the money is later spent on good.

Key Takeaway
Mubah acts become worship with good intention and sin with bad intention; without intention, they remain neutral.

Intention in Contracts: Mudari' Verb in Sale
Explaining the effect of intention on contracts using future tense

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on intention in sale contracts using mudari' verbs and apply it to determine the validity of a sale.

Core Idea
A mudari' sale contract is valid only if intention indicates present obligation; purely future mudari' cannot form a contract.

Intention plays a crucial role not only in worship but also in contracts. The Hanafi school distinguishes between sale expressed in past tense (no intention needed) and future tense (mudari'). A mudari' verb without sawfa or sin can become a valid sale if the intention is for immediate obligation. But if the mudari' is purely future, no contract can be formed even with intention. This lesson explores this nuanced application of the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.

Guided Path
1
Recall the default rule for sale contracts
Sales expressed in past tense (madi) are valid without intention because past tense clearly indicates immediate obligation.
Past tense is explicit and unambiguous.
2
Introduce the mudari' exception
When a contract is made using a mudari' verb that is not preceded by sawfa (will) or sin (future marker), intention becomes decisive. If the intention is for present obligation, the sale is valid; otherwise, it is not.
Mudari' without future markers is ambiguous between present and future.
3
Distinguish purely future mudari'
If the mudari' is clearly future (with sawfa/sin or context), it cannot form a valid sale, even with intention. Future tense cannot create immediate obligation.
This is unlike command verbs (amr) which also cannot form sale.
4
Apply to iqala and ijarah
The same rule applies to iqala (rescission) and ijarah (lease) as to sale—they do not depend on intention in past tense, but mudari' requires intention.
The text specifically mentions these as examples.
5
Connect to the governing qawida
This ruling is a furu of 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha': intention determines the nature of the mudari' utterance. However, it is limited by linguistic rules: purely future expressions cannot be overridden by intention.
Istithna' from the maxim: past tense does not require intention; purely future cannot be saved by intention.

As for permissible acts, their description varies according to the purpose for which they are intended. So if one intends thereby to gain strength for acts of obedience or to achieve reliance, they become worship, like eating, sleeping, earning money, and intercourse. If one intends to spend on good deeds, it is reward. Analogy applies to eating. Since permissible acts are not among intended acts of worship, they do not require intention for validity. However, if one intends to gain strength for good deeds or to reach good deeds through these permissible acts, they become worship and reward will be given. For example, eating is permissible; if the purpose is to gain strength for good deeds, reward; if for mischief, sin; if no intention, no reward or sin. Similarly, masnunat and mandubat require intention to be acts of obedience and receive reward; otherwise intention is not necessary. Hence, any permissible matter becomes worship through intention. Example of masnun and mandub: visiting the sick and offering condolences. The definition of sunnah has passed. Mandub is an act whose doing and leaving are both permissible, but doing it is preferable and leaving it is less preferable. But those which are not intended acts of worship do not require intention for validity, though intention is necessary for reward, like repaying debts and returning entrusted items, because the purpose of these and all transactions is to benefit people. As for transactions, they are many types: sale does not depend on intention, similarly iqala and ijarah. But they said: if one contracts using a mudari' that is not preceded by sawfa or sin, it depends on intention. If he intends thereby the present obligation, it is a sale, otherwise not. Unlike the past tense, for sale with it does not depend on intention. As for the mudari' that is purely future, it is like a command: sale is not valid with it, not even with intention. We have explained this in Sharh al-Kanz. Translation: And in any case, transactions are many types: sale does not depend on it, and similarly iqala and ijarah. But the jurists say: if one contracts with a mudari' that is not preceded by sawfa and sin, it depends on intention.
Source pages p. 103

Commentary
This passage applies the maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions' to permissible acts and contracts. Mubah acts like eating or earning become worship when intended as a means for obedience. This is a key furu of the maxim. The text then discusses mu'amalat: sales contracts in past tense require no intention, but if expressed in future tense (without sawfa/sin), intention determines whether it is a binding sale. If the mudari' is purely future, it cannot form a valid sale. This shows the Hanafi position on the role of niyyah in contracts.

Key Terms
مضارع (mudari'): The imperfect tense verb in Arabic; used here for expressing future or present action in contracts.
ماض (madi): Past tense verb; in contract law, it creates immediate obligation without need for intention.
سين (sin): A future marker in Arabic (like sawfa) that makes mudari' purely future.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on a sale contract made using a mudari' verb that is not preceded by sawfa or sin?
A) It is always valid regardless of intention.
B) It is valid only if the intention is for present obligation.
C) It is invalid regardless of intention.
D) It is valid only if the intention is for future obligation.

Key Takeaway
Mudari' sale contracts without future markers are valid only with intention for present obligation; purely future mudari' cannot form a valid contract even with intention.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate

Explicit Talaq (Sarih) Does Not Require Intention in Qada
Rule that explicit talaq does not require intention for judicial occurrence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that explicit talaq occurs in qada without intention, and distinguish between qada and diyanah.

Core Idea
Explicit talaq words effect divorce in court (qada) regardless of intent; only inner conscience (diyanah) considers intention.

A crucial distinction in Hanafi fiqh is between qada (judicial enforcement) and diyanah (religious judgment). This rule governs explicit talaq: once the words are uttered, the law presumes intent unless a clear counter-indication exists. In this lesson, we unpack the reasoning, the governing maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt,' and the mufti's application of this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of talaq words
Talaq words are divided into explicit (sarih) and implicit (kinayah). Sarih words are exclusively used for divorce (e.g., 'I divorce you'). Kinayah words can mean divorce but need intention or context.
This classification is essential because the rule differs for each.
2
State the rule for sarih: intention not required for qada
The passage states that if a person utters sarih words while heedless, forgetful, or mistaken, talaq occurs in qada (judicial ruling). No inner intent is needed for legal effect.
The rule is strict: outward expression suffices.
3
Understand the epistemological reasoning: outward is taken as certain
Intention is an inner state impossible to verify. Therefore, the law relies on the outward (zahir). The person is assumed to be sane and capable; without a counter-indication, the words are taken at face value.
This follows the maxim 'Certainty is not removed by doubt' (اليقين لا يزول بالشك).
4
Apply the maxim: اليقين لا يزول بالشك
The outward is certain; any doubt about inner intent does not override it. So talaq is effective in qada. However, in diyanah (the individual's conscience), if the person truly had no intention, the divorce is not valid before Allah.
This distinction is key for muftis: they rule on apparent evidence but advise on inner responsibility.
5
Distinguish qada and diyanah
Qada is the enforceable legal ruling by a judge; diyanah is the personal religious obligation. In sarih talaq, qada does not require intention; diyanah does. A mufti must explain both aspects.
Ignoring this distinction leads to confusion in fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما الطلاق فَصَرِيحٌ وَكِتَايَةٌ وَالْأَوَّلُ لَا يَحْتَاجُ فِي وَقَوْعِهِ إِلَيْهَا فَلَوْ طَلَّقَ غَافِلًا أَوْ سَاهِياً أَوْ مُخْطِي وَقَعَ قَالُوا إِنَّ الطَّلَاقَ يَقَعُ بِالْأَلْفَاظِ الْمُصْحَفَةِ قَضَاءً وَلكِنْ لَا بُدَّ أنْ يَقْصِدَهَا بِاللَّفْظِ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال طلاق تو وہ صریح اور کنایہ ہے پس اول اپنے وقوع میں اس کی محتاج نہیں ہے پس اگر غفلت میں یا بھول کر یا غلطی سے طلاق دیدی تو واقع ہو جائے گی اور فقہاء کہتے ہیں کہ طلاق الفاظ مصحفہ سے قضاء واقع ہو جاتی ہے لیکن لفظ سے اس کا ارادہ کرنا ضروری ہے۔ تشريح الطلاق وهو لغة رفع القيد سواء كان حسنا كقيد الفرس وقيد الاسير او معنوياً كقيد النكاح وهو الارتباط الحاصل بين الزوجين ( فتاوى النوازل ص (۱۹۶) وشرعاً رفع قيد النكاح في الحال او المآل بلفظ مخصوص . (شای ج ۳۳۰۴۱) جن الفاظ سے طلاق دی جاتی ہے ان کی دو قسمیں ہیں (۱) صریح (۲) کنایہ۔ الفاظ صریح سے طلاق دیتے وقت نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور طلاق بدون نیت بھی قضاء واقع ہو جائیگی البتہ ولكن لابد ان يقصد ها باللفظ سے ذکر فرمایا ہے۔ فلو طلق غافلاً : الفاظ صریح میں ان کے وقوع کے لئے نیت کی ضرورت نہیں ہے بشرطیکہ کوئی قرین صارف ہوا دیانہ ان کے حکم کا وقوع نہ ہو گا اس پر تفریح پیش کرتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے غفلت یا بھول میں یا غلطی سے طلاق دیدی تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ رہی یہ بات کہ ان صورتوں میں طلاق واقع نہ ہونی چاہئے کیونکہ غافل یا نسیان میں بہتا لشخص یا خطی کا ارادہ طلاق کا نہیں تھا تو اس کا جواب یہ ہے کہ قصد وارادہ ایک امر باطنی ہے جس پر مطلع ہونا مشکل امر ہے۔ الہذا حکم ظاہر پر لگے گا اور ظاہر یہ ہے کہ ان الفاظ صریحہ کا استعمال کرنے والا عاقل بالغ ہے اور اس کے اندر قصد و ارادہ کی اہلیت ہے لہذا بغیر قرینہ صارفہ کے الفاظ صریحہ کو ان کے ظاہر سے نہیں پھیرا جائے گا۔ دیانہ طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی جب تک کہ الفاظ طلاق سے اپنی بیوی کا ارادہ نہ کیا ہو۔ اس قید کو صاحب کتاب نے یہاں پر غفلت سے مراد یہ ہے کہ ذہن سے کون چیز نکل جائے اور زور ڈالنے پر یاد آ جائے اور سہو میں زور ڈالئے سے بھی وہ بات نہیں آتی مصنف کی عبارت میں سہو کا عطف غفلت پر کیا ہے جو مغایرت کا تقاضہ کرتا ہے اس لئے بھی معنی مراد لینا بہتر ہے جبکہ بعض حضرات نے دونوں کو مترادف قرار دیا ہے اور تعریف محفلہ کی گئی ہے هو سهو بعثری الانسان من قله التحفظ والتيقظ .
And as for divorce, it is explicit (sarih) and implicit (kinayah). The first does not need [intention] for its occurrence. So if a person divorces while heedless, forgetful, or mistaken, it occurs. They said: divorce occurs through mispronounced words (musahhafah) in qada, but one must intend them by the word. Translation: And anyway, divorce is explicit and implicit. The first does not need [intention] for its occurrence. So if he divorces in heedlessness, forgetfulness, or error, it occurs. And the jurists say that divorce occurs through mispronounced words in qada, but intending them by the word is necessary. Definition of talaq: linguistically, it is the removal of a restriction, whether physical like the fetter of a horse or the shackle of a prisoner, or metaphorical like the restriction of marriage, which is the bond between spouses (Fatawa al-Nawazil, p. 196). Legally: removal of the restriction of marriage immediately or eventually by a specific word (Shami, vol. 3, p. 3041). The words by which divorce is given are of two types: (1) explicit (sarih), (2) implicit (kinayah). With explicit words, intention is not necessary when giving divorce, and divorce without intention occurs in qada. However, from 'but one must intend them by the word' it is mentioned. So if he divorces heedlessly: in explicit words, intention is not necessary for their occurrence, provided there is no counter-indication; diyanah the ruling of occurrence will not be. On this they elaborate: if someone gave divorce in heedlessness, forgetfulness, or error, divorce will occur. As for the objection that divorce should not occur in these cases because the heedless or forgetful person or the mistaken person did not intend divorce, the answer is that intention is an inner matter that is difficult to ascertain. Therefore, the ruling will be based on the outward, and the outward is that the person using these explicit words is a sane adult and possesses the capacity for intention. So without a counter-indication, explicit words will not be diverted from their apparent meaning. Diyanah, divorce will not occur unless he intended his wife by the words of divorce. The author mentioned this restriction here. By heedlessness (ghaflah) is meant something slipping from the mind and being recalled upon effort; while forgetfulness (sahw) is something that does not come even with effort. In the author's text, sahw is conjoined with ghaflah, which requires them to be different, so it is better to take the distinct meaning, though some have considered them synonymous. And a formal definition is given: sahw is a state of the person due to lack of caution and vigilance.
Source pages p. 107

Commentary
This lengthy passage is a comprehensive treatment of explicit (sarih) talaq and the role of intention. It opens with a classification: talaq words are either sarih or kinayah. For sarih, intention is not required for the legal occurrence (qada); even if pronounced heedlessly, forgetfully, or by mistake, talaq takes effect. The proof is that intention is an inner state that cannot be known with certainty, so the law looks to outward expression. However, for diyanah (religious conscience), talaq does not occur unless the person actually intended to divorce his wife. This distinction is fundamental: a judge enforces the apparent, but in private religious assessment, missing intention matters. The passage also defines talaq linguistically and legally, and distinguishes between ghaflah (heedlessness, where something slips the mind but can be recalled) and sahw (forgetfulness that persists even with effort). The author notes that some treat them as synonyms, but the conjunctive structure suggests a difference. This passage is a model of Hanafi juridical reasoning: combining textual definitions with pragmatic epistemology (outward vs. inner).

Key Terms
صریح (sarih): Words exclusively used for talaq, without needing intention.
کنایہ (kinayah): Words that can imply talaq but require intention.
قرینہ صارفہ (qarinah sarifah): A counter-indication that diverts the literal meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the effect of a counter-indication (qarinah sarifah) on explicit talaq?
A) Talaq occurs regardless
B) Talaq does not occur in qada
C) Talaq occurs in qada but not in diyanah
D) The ruling remains the same

Key Takeaway
Explicit talaq words are effective in qada without regard to inner intent; diyanah remains a matter of personal conscience.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

The Quran Exits from Being Quran by Intention: Applications and Disputes
Explains a qawida and its furuat with a dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'The Quran exits from being Quran by intention' to cases involving junub, ha'id, and janazah prayer, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on reciting less than a verse, identifying the mufta bihi in normal and hardship circumstances.

Core Idea
Intentions transform Quranic recitation into dhikr, allowing junub and ha'id to recite verses—but the ruling changes in its proper place.

This lesson explores a subtle yet powerful qawida: the legal nature of Quranic recitation can be altered by the reciter's intention. This principle has direct implications for junub (ritually impure) and ha'id (menstruating) individuals, who are normally prohibited from reciting Quran. By intending dhikr or du'a, they may recite verses containing those elements. We will examine the qawida, its scope, applications, and an important intra-Hanafi dispute regarding reciting less than a verse, concluding with the relied-upon position for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its basis
Express the qawida in Arabic and English. Understand that it derives from the jurists' permission for junub/ha'id to recite verses with intention of dhikr/du'a, implying the recitation loses its Quranic status.
The qawida is a minor (sughra) maxim governing specific chapters.
2
Identify the scope and furuat
List the fiqh chapters where this qawida applies: taharah and salat. Review the examples given: junub/ha'id reciting dhikr, reciting with intention during salah (does not invalidate), muqtadi in janazah, and teaching children during hayd/nifas.
Each furu' shows how intention changes the ruling.
3
Analyze the objection and response
Consider the objection: if intention changes the nature, why does reciting with dhikr intention during salah not invalidate prayer? The response from Sharh al-Kanz: 'it is in its place'—recitation in salah retains its Quranic status because the act itself is defined as Quran recitation in that context.
The qawida has an implicit restriction: it operates outside the formal context of salah.
4
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on maddun al-ayah
Understand the disagreement: Imam Karkhi holds prohibition of reciting less than a verse, citing the generality of the hadith 'La yaqra' al-junub...'. Imam Mahawati permits it. The preferred view (mufta bihi) in normal circumstances is Karkhi's, but hardship cases allow Tahawi's permissive view.
The dispute is methodological: generality of text vs. reasoning (talil).
5
Apply the fatwa hierarchy
Identify the mufta bihi: for normal circumstances, prohibition; for hardship (e.g., long hayd/nifas teaching), permissibility. Understand the tarjih mechanism: the text is preferred over talil, except when necessity (darura) shifts the balance.
This is a classic example of 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' applying to the original prohibition.

Source Text

ترجمه : اور بہر حال قرآت قرآن تو فقہاء کہتے ہیں کہ وہ قصد کے ذریعہ قرآن ہونے سے خارج ہو جاتا ہے چنانچہ انہوں نے جنبی اور حائضہ کے لئے ذکر کے ارادے سے ان آیات کے پڑھنے کو جائز کہا ہے جن میں اذکار ہوں اور دعاء کے قصد سے ان کے پڑھنے کو جن میں دعائیں ہوں لیکن اس پر فقہاء کے قول سے اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ اگر کوئی ذکر کے قصد سے قرآت کرے تو اس کی نماز نہیں ہوتی اور ہم نے شرح کنز میں اس کا جواب یہ دیا ہے کہ وہ اپنے محل میں ہے اس لئے اس کے ارادہ سے وہ متغیر نہ ہوگی نیز فقہاء کہتے ہیں کہ نماز جنازہ میں اگر مقتدی ذکر کی نیت سے سورہ فاتحہ کی قرآت کرے تو وہ اسپر حرام نہیں حالانکہ نماز جنازہ میں اسے پڑھنا اسپر عا با ذکر پر مشتمل ہوں اور ذکر یا دعاء کے ارادہ سے پڑھیں تو قرآن ہونے سے خارج ہو جاتی ہیں ) یہ ہے کہ فقہاء نے حائضہ اور جنبی کے لئے ان آیات کو دعاء یاد کر کے ارادہ سے پڑھنے کی اجازت دی ہے اگر یہ آیات قرآنیہ قرآن ہونے سے خارج نہ ہو تیں تو حائضہ اور جنبی کے لئے پڑھنے کی اجازت نہ ہوتی کیونکہ رسول کریم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا: لا يقرأ الجنب ولا الحائض شيئاً من القرآن . باتفاق علماء جنبی اور حائضہ کے لئے قرآت قرآن حرام ہے۔ پھر پوری آیت پڑھی جائے یا مادون الآیتہ امام کرخی کے نزدیک دونوں میں کوئی فرق نہیں صاحب بدائع الصنائع نے عام حالات میں علماء متاخرین کا فتویٰ امام کرخی کے قول پر نقل کیا لہذا جنسی اور حائضہ کے لئے آیت و مادون الایت دونوں پڑھنا حرام ہوں گے۔ جبکہ امام محاوتی نے مادون الآیۃ پڑھنے کو حائضہ اور جنبی کے لئے جائز قرار دیا ہے۔ اور خلاصہ میں اس کو رائج قرار دیا گیا ہے۔ حاصل کلام یہ ہے کہ صحیح مادون الآیۃ میں اختلاف ہے امام کرخی کے قول کو راجح قرار دینا اولی ہے اس لئے کہ احادیث میں آیت و مادون الآیتہ کی کوئی تفصیل نہیں ہے بلکہ مطلقاً آیت و مادون الآینہ کی قرآت حائضہ اور نبی کے لئے حرام ہے اور تعلیل نص کے مقابلہ میں قابل رد ہے اور اگر حائضہ ونفساء بچوں کو تعلیم دیتی ہے اور چونکہ ان کا زمنہ حیض و نفاس کا طویل ہوتا ہے اور ترک تعلیم میں چونکہ حرج عظیم ہے اس لئے اس صورت میں امام طحاوی کے قول پر عمل کرنے کی گنجائش ہوگی ۔ اور اگر ترک تعلیم کی وجہ سے حرج نہ ہوتو امام کرخی کے قول پر عمل کیا جائے گا۔ لكن اشكل عليه قولهم. اس جگہ ایک اشکال ہوتا ہے کہ جب قرآت دعا ء یا ذ کر کے ارادہ سے ذکر یا دعا کے درجہ میں ہو جاتی ہے اور قرآت قرآن ۔ قرآن ہونے سے خارج ہو جاتی ہے ۔ تو اگر کوئی دوران نماز قرآن کرتے ہوئے ذکر کی یا دعاء کی نیت کرلے تو اس کی نماز فاسد ہو جانی چاہئے اس لئے کہ نماز میں قرآت کر نا فرش ہے اور وہ پایا نہیں گیا۔
As for recitation of the Quran, they said: The Quran exits from being Quran by intention, so they permitted for the junub and the ha'id to recite what is in it of remembrances with the intention of remembrance, and supplications with the intention of supplication. But it is problematic against it their statement: If one recites with the intention of remembrance, his prayer is not invalidated. And we answered about it in Sharh al-Kanz that it is in its place, so it does not change by his determination. And they said: When the muqtadi recites al-Fatihah in the janazah prayer with the intention of remembrance, it is not forbidden upon him, although reciting it in the prayer is forbidden upon him. Translation: As for recitation of the Quran, the jurists say that it exits from being Quran by intention. Thus they permitted for the junub and ha'id to recite verses that contain remembrances with the intention of remembrance, and those containing supplications with the intention of supplication. But it is problematic against their statement that if someone recites with the intention of remembrance, his prayer is not nullified. And we answered in Sharh al-Kanz that it is in its place, so it does not change by his intention. Also, the jurists say that in the janazah prayer, if the muqtadi recites Surah al-Fatihah with the intention of remembrance, it is not haram upon him, while reciting it in janazah prayer is normally haram. Explanation: Allamah Ibn Qayyim al-Misri says that verses which contain remembrance or supplication, when recited with the intention of remembrance or supplication, exit from being Quran. The evidence for that is that the jurists permitted the ha'id and junub to recite those verses with the intention of supplication or remembrance. If these Quranic verses did not exit from being Quran, they would not permit their recitation for the ha'id and junub because the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'The junub and the ha'id should not recite anything of the Quran.' By consensus of the scholars, recitation of the Quran is forbidden for the junub and ha'id. Then whether a complete verse is recited or less than a verse, according to Imam Karkhi, there is no difference. The author of Badai' al-Sanai' transmitted the fatwa of the later scholars in general cases according to Imam Karkhi's statement. Imam Turandi graded the hadith 'La yaqra' al-junub wa la al-ha'id shay'an min al-Quran' as hasan. The deduction from this hadith is that 'shay'an min al-Quran' falls under negation, and whatever indefinite falls under negation yields generality. Therefore, for the junub and ha'id, both reciting a verse and less than a verse are forbidden. While Imam Mahawati declared reciting less than a verse permissible for the ha'id and junub. And in al-Khulasah, it was considered widespread. The conclusion is that there is disagreement about less than a verse. Preferring Imam Karkhi's statement is preferable because the hadith does not detail between verse and less than a verse, rather it absolutely forbids recitation of verse and less than a verse for the ha'id and junub. And reasoning (talil) is rebuttable in the face of the text. If a ha'id or nufasa' is teaching children, and because their period of hayd and nifas is long, and abandoning teaching involves great hardship, then in that case acting upon Imam Tahawi's statement is permissible. And if there is no hardship due to abandoning teaching, then Imam Karkhi's statement will be acted upon. But it is problematic against their statement. Here an objection arises: When recitation with the intention of supplication or remembrance becomes at the level of supplication or remembrance, and recitation of the Quran exits from being Quran, then if someone during prayer recites the Quran and then intends remembrance or supplication, his prayer should become invalid because recitation in prayer is obligatory, and it has not been fulfilled.
Source pages p. 119

Commentary
This passage discusses a key Hanafi qawida: 'The Quran exits from being Quran by intention.' It addresses the permissibility of junub and ha'id (those in a state of major impurity) reciting Quranic verses that contain dhikr or du'a, provided they intend them as such. The author clarifies that the intention changes the legal classification of the recitation, so it is no longer considered Quranic recitation, which is forbidden for them. The passage then addresses an objection: if intention changes the nature, then reciting with dhikr intention during prayer should invalidate the prayer because it would not count as Quran recitation. The answer from Sharh al-Kanz is that in its proper place (i.e., during prayer), the recitation retains its Quranic status despite the intention. Another application: in janazah prayer, the muqtadi normally may not recite Fatihah, but if he intends dhikr, it becomes permissible. The evidence from Ibn Qayyim is the practice of the jurists. Then the passage delves into a dispute regarding reciting less than a verse: Imam Karkhi and most scholars hold it is forbidden, citing the generality of the hadith 'la yaqra' al-junub wa la al-ha'id shay'an min al-Quran', while Imam Mahawati permits it. The preferred view is that of Karkhi, except in cases of hardship like teaching children during prolonged hayd/nifas, when Imam Tahawi's permissive view may be followed. The passage ends with a lingering objection about intention during prayer, which is left unresolved.

Key Terms
جنب (junub): A person in a state of major ritual impurity requiring ghusl
حائض (ha'id): A woman in her menstrual period
مادون الآية (maddun al-ayah): Less than a complete verse of the Quran
قصد (qasd): Intention that changes the legal classification of an act

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi qawida discussed, why is a junub or ha'id permitted to recite a verse like 'Alhamdu lillahi Rabbil 'alameen' if they intend it as dhikr?
A) Because the verse is short and does not count as Quran.
B) Because the intention changes the recitation from Quran to dhikr, removing the prohibition.
C) Because junub and ha'id are always allowed to recite Quran.
D) Because the verse is a du'a, not Quran.

Key Takeaway
Intention can transform Quranic recitation into dhikr, permitting junub and ha'id to recite verses, but this principle is context-sensitive: it does not apply during prayer, and the dispute on less than a verse is resolved by preferring the text-based prohibition in normal circumstances, with hardship exceptions.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
8 min
The Second Grand Qa'idah: Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha
Defining and illustrating the second grand qa'idah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qa'idah 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' to determine the validity of an action based on the underlying intention, and identify its exception in acts of worship.

Core Idea
The validity of an action hinges on its intention — a mubah becomes haram when the purpose is sinful.

This lesson introduces you to the second grand qa'idah (legal maxim) of Hanafi fiqh: 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by their intentions). Building on the first qa'idah about intention for reward, this qa'idah extends to the legal validity of actions, particularly in transactions (mu'amalat). You will see how the Hanafi fuqaha derived this maxim from three concrete examples and learn to apply it in fatwa scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the Qa'idah and Its Rank
Write down the Arabic 'الأمور بمقاصدها' and its English equivalent. Recognise it as one of the five major (kubra) maxims of Hanafi fiqh.
This qa'idah is also known as 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' and is a kulliya (universal) maxim.
2
Understand the Scope and Dabt
The qa'idah governs all chapters of fiqh, especially transactions and family law. However, note the sub-maxim (dabt): for positive actions, the ruling is not established by intention alone until an action accompanies it.
This prevents the qa'idah from being misapplied to mere thoughts without deeds.
3
Analyse the Three Furuat (Derived Cases)
Work through the three examples from the text: (1) the trade slave intended for service — zakat not obligatory until trade action actualised; (2) mubahat — permissibility changes with intention; (3) selling grape juice to a winemaker — permissible if seller's purpose is trade, impermissible if he intends wine production.
Each example illustrates how intention determines the legal ruling in practical terms.
4
Identify the Istithna' (Exception)
The qa'idah has an exception in acts of worship (ibadat). For ibadat, intention alone is insufficient; the specific actions must also be performed. This is because worship requires both niyyah and amal.
This exception is governed by the supplementary principle that acts of worship require physical performance.
5
Apply to a New Furu'
Given a novel scenario, such as selling halal meat to a restaurant that also serves haram food, determine the ruling based on the seller's intention. If the seller intends merely to profit from halal trade, the sale is permissible; if he intends to support the haram enterprise, it becomes impermissible.
This demonstrates how the qa'idah is used by the mufti to issue consistent fatwas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم القَاعِدَةُ الثانية الأمُورُ بِمَقَاصَدِها دوسرے قاعدہ کو مصنف الامور بمقاصدها" کے نام سے ذکر کر رہے ہیں القاعدۃ الاولی میں ذکر کیا گیا تھا کہ اعمال پر ثواب کا دارو مدار نیت پر ہے بدون نیت ثواب حاصل نہ ہوگا، دوسرے قاعدہ میں یہ بات واضح کی جارہی ہے کہ امور کا جواز اور عدم جواز امور کے انجام دینے والے کی نیت پر موقوف ہے اگر مقصد جائز ہے تو عمل بھی جائز ہوگا اور اگر مقصد نا جائز ہے تو عمل بھی نا جائز ہوگا۔ وَمِنْ هُنَا وَمِمَّا قَدَّمْنَاهُ يَعْنِي فِي الْمُبَاحَاتِ وَمِمَّا سَتَذْكُرُهُ عَنِ الْمَشَائِحَ صَحْ لَنَا وَضْعُ فَاعِدَةِ لِلْفِقْهِ هِيَ الثَّانِيَّةُ : الْأُمُوْرُ بِمَا قَاصِدِهَا ، كَمَا عَلِمْتَهُ فِي التَّرُوْي. ترجمہ: اور یہاں سے اور اس سے جس کو ہم نے مباحات میں بیان کیا اور اس سے جس کو ہم مشائخ کے حوالہ سے ذکر کریں گے ہمارے لئے فقہ کا ایک قاعدہ وضع کرنا صحیح ہو گیا اور وہ دوسرا قاعدہ ہے الامور بمقاصدها (امور کامدار اس کے مقاصد پر ہے ) ہے جیسا کہ تو نے بحث تروک میں جان لیا۔ تشریح صاحب کتاب فرماتے ہیں کہ ناقبیل میں ایک جزئیہ گذرا ہے کہ اگر تجارت کے غلام میں خدمت کی نیت کر لی تو وہ غلام خدمت کے لئے متعین ہو جائے گا اور اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی اور اگر کوئی غلام خدمت کے لئے تھا اور اس میں تجارت کی نیت کر لی تو وہ خدمت ہی کے لئے رہے گا جب تک نیت کے ساتھ عمل تجارت کا محقق نہ ہو اسی طرح مباحات کے سلسلہ میں گذرا ہے کہ مباح کی صفت مقصد کے اعتبار سے بدلتی ہے اگر مقصد جائز ہے تو مباح بھی جائز اور اگر مقصد برا ہے تو مباح بھی برا ہو کر عدم جواز کے زمرہ میں آجائے گا۔ ای طرح مشائخ نے ایک جزئیہ ذکر کیا ہے کہ انگور کا سر کہ اس شخص کو فروخت کرنا جو شراب بناتا ہے اگر مقصد صرف تجارت ہے تو شراب بنانے والے کو بھی بیچنا جائز ہے اور اگر شراب بنانے کی نیت سے فروخت کر رہا ہے تو وہ انگور کا شیرہ اس کے ہاتھ بیچنا نا جائز ہوگا۔ صاحب کتاب علامہ ابن نجیم المصری علیہ الرحمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ان جزئیات کی وجہ سے فقہاء نے ایک اور قاعدہ
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The second qa'idah: Matters are according to their intentions. The author mentions the second qa'idah by the name 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'. In the first qa'idah, it was mentioned that the reward of actions depends on intention; without intention, reward is not obtained. In the second qa'idah, it is being clarified that the validity and invalidity of matters depend on the intention of the doer. If the purpose is valid, the action is valid; if the purpose is invalid, the action is invalid. And from here and from what we have presented, meaning in the permissible actions (mubahat), and from what we will mention from the mashayikh, it became correct for us to formulate a qa'idah for fiqh, which is the second: al-umur bi maqasidiha, as you understood from the discussion of tark. Explanation: The author says: In the previous discussion, a partial example passed that if one intends service in a trade slave, then that slave becomes designated for service and zakat is not obligatory on him. And if a slave was for service and one intends trade for him, then he remains for service until the action of trade is actualized along with the intention. Similarly, in the discussion of mubahat, it passed that the attribute of mubah changes according to the purpose. If the purpose is valid, the mubah is also valid; if the purpose is evil, then the mubah becomes evil and enters the category of impermissibility. Similarly, the mashayikh mentioned a partial example: selling grape juice to a person who makes wine. If the purpose is merely trade, selling to the wine maker is permissible; if one is selling with the intention that he makes wine, then selling the grape juice to him is impermissible. The author, Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri (may Allah have mercy on him) says: Because of these partial examples, the fuqaha established another qa'idah...
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage introduces and explains the second major qa'idah of Hanafi fiqh: 'Matters are according to their intentions.' It builds on the first qa'idah (deeds are by intentions) but extends from reward to the realm of legal validity. The author explains that this qa'idah was derived from three types of examples: (1) The case of a slave intended for trade vs. service — intention alone does not change the ruling without action; zakat is only waived if there is actual trade action. (2) Mubahat (permissible actions) — their permissibility can become impermissible if the intention is sinful. (3) Selling grape juice to a winemaker — if the seller intends for wine production, the sale becomes impermissible. This demonstrates that the qa'idah applies across many fiqh chapters. The passage ends by noting that these examples led the fuqaha to formulate this qa'idah.

Key Terms
مقاصد (maqasid): The purposes or intentions behind an action, which determine its legal validity.
مباح (mubah): A legally permissible action whose ruling can change based on the intention behind it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, selling grape juice to a winemaker is impermissible under which condition?
A) If the seller knows the buyer is a winemaker.
B) If the seller intends for the buyer to make wine from it.
C) If the grape juice is specially packaged for wine production.
D) If the seller does not ascertain the buyer's purpose.

Key Takeaway
The second grand qa'idah 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' establishes that the legal validity of actions in mu'amalat is determined by the intention of the doer, with the exception that for acts of worship, physical performance is also required.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
8 min
The Second Major Qaidah: Matters are According to Their Objectives
Explaining the second qaidah with furuat examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim al-umuru bi maqasidiha to determine the permissibility of transactions based on intention, and distinguish it from the first maxim al-umuru bi niyyatiha.

Core Idea
A lawful act becomes unlawful if done with an unlawful objective; intention defines the worldly ruling.

In this passage, Ibn Nujaym explains the second major legal maxim of the Hanafi school: al-umuru bi maqasidiha. While the first maxim governs reward in the afterlife, this maxim governs the worldly legal ruling (hukm dunyawi) of an act—its permissibility or impermissibility. Through examples like selling grape juice to a winemaker, the author shows that the same objective act can be either lawful or unlawful depending solely on the intention behind it.

Guided Path
1
State the maxim and its scope
Identify the Arabic text of the second maxim and note that it governs worldly rulings (hukm dunyawi) across all fiqh chapters, especially transactions.
Distinguish from the first maxim (al-umuru bi niyyatiha) which concerns reward in the afterlife.
2
Analyze the example of selling grape juice
Examine the ruling: if the seller intends trade, the sale is permissible; if he intends to enable wine-making, it is prohibited. Understand that the same act (selling juice) has opposite rulings based on intention.
This is the primary furu' from the text.
3
Apply the maxim to planting vines and other cases
Similarly, planting vines is permissible if intended for cultivation, but prohibited if intended to supply a winemaker. Also, selling juice for vinegar is permissible, for wine is prohibited.
These demonstrate the maxim's operation in different chapters.
4
Understand the distinction from the first maxim
Note that the first maxim (al-umuru bi niyyatiha) relates to intention for reward, while the second (al-umuru bi maqasidiha) relates to permissibility/impermissibility. They complement but govern different aspects.
Ibn Nujaym and Hamawi clarify this difference.
5
Explore the nuance of selling to Magians vs. libertines
The text states that selling to a Magian is permissible (though preferable to avoid), while selling to a libertine is impermissible. This shows that the buyer's known intent can affect the ruling when the seller's intent is ambiguous.
This illustrates the boundary of the maxim: the seller must be aware of the buyer's likely use.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
القَاعِدَةُ الثانية الأمُورُ بِمَقَاصَدِها
دوسرے قاعدہ کو مصنف الامور بمقاصدها" کے نام سے ذکر کر رہے ہیں القاعدۃ الاولی میں ذکر کیا گیا تھا کہ اعمال پر ثواب کا دارو مدار نیت پر ہے بدون نیت ثواب حاصل نہ ہوگا، دوسرے قاعدہ میں یہ بات واضح کی جارہی ہے کہ امور کا جواز اور عدم جواز امور کے انجام دینے والے کی نیت پر موقوف ہے اگر مقصد جائز ہے تو عمل بھی جائز ہوگا اور اگر مقصد نا جائز ہے تو عمل بھی نا جائز ہوگا۔
وَمِنْ هُنَا وَمِمَّا قَدَّمْنَاهُ يَعْنِي فِي الْمُبَاحَاتِ وَمِمَّا سَتَذْكُرُهُ عَنِ الْمَشَائِحَ صَحْ لَنَا وَضْعُ فَاعِدَةِ لِلْفِقْهِ هِيَ الثَّانِيَّةُ : الْأُمُوْرُ بِمَا قَاصِدِهَا ، كَمَا عَلِمْتَهُ فِي التَّرُوْي.
