(امور کامدار اس کے مقاصد پر ہے ) ہے جیسا کہ تو نے بحث تروک میں جان لیا۔ تشریح صاحب کتاب فرماتے ہیں کہ ناقبیل میں ایک جزئیہ گذرا ہے کہ اگر تجارت کے غلام میں خدمت کی نیت کر لی تو وہ غلام خدمت کے لئے متعین ہو جائے گا اور اس پر زکوۃ واجب نہیں ہوگی اور اگر کوئی غلام خدمت کے لئے تھا اور اس میں تجارت کی نیت کر لی تو وہ خدمت ہی کے لئے رہے گا جب تک نیت کے ساتھ عمل تجارت کا محقق نہ ہو اسی طرح مباحات کے سلسلہ میں گذرا ہے کہ مباح کی صفت مقصد کے اعتبار سے بدلتی ہے اگر مقصد جائز ہے تو مبارح بھی جائز اور اگر مقصد برا ہے تو مباح بھی برا ہو کر عدم جواز کے زمرہ میں آجائے گا۔ ای طرح مشائخ نے ایک جزئیہ ذکر کیا ہے کہ انگور کا سر کہ اس شخص کو فروخت کرنا جو شراب بناتا ہے اگر مقصد صرف تجارت ہے تو شراب بنانے والے کو بھی بیچنا جائز ہے اور اگر شراب بنانے کی نیت سے فروخت کر رہا ہے تو وہ انگور کا شیرہ اس کے ہاتھ بیچنا نا جائز ہوگا۔ صاحب کتاب علامہ ابن نجیم المصری علیہ الرحمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ان جزئیات کی وجہ سے فقہاء نے ایک اور قاعدہ وضع کیا ہے اور وہ دوسرا قاعدہ ہے الامور بمقاصدها " کہ امور کے جواز و عدم جواز کا دارو مدار قصد و نیت پر ہے اگر مقصد و نیت جائز ہے تو عمل بھی جائز اور اگر قصد کی ناجائز کام کا ہوتو پھر وہی عمل نا جائز ہو جائے گا جیسا کہ مجھے تروک میں آپ کو معلوم ہو گیا اگر منہیات اور تروک میں کف یعنی روکنا پایا گیا تو ثواب ملے گا بشرطیکہ اس فعل منہی پر قدرت ہو ورنہ تو اب نہ ملے گا۔ علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ مصنف کے کلام سے بظاہر یہ معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اس دوسرے قاعدہ کی وضع ان جزئیات سے ہوتی ہے اگر چہ فقہا ء نے اس کی تصریح نہیں کی ہے لیکن ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ یہ قاعدہ مصرح ہے قاعدہ اولیٰ اور قاعدہ ثانیہ میں فرق یہ ہے کہ قاعدہ اولی کا تعلق تعلم اخروی سے ہے اور قاعدہ ثانیہ کا تعلق حکم دنیوی یعنی جواز و عدم جواز سے ہے۔ وَذَكَرَ قَاضِي خَانَ فِي فَتَاوَاهُ : أَنَّ بَيْعَ الْعَصِيْرِ مِمَّنْ يَتَّخِذُهُ خَمْرًا إِنْ قَصَدَ بِهِ التِّجَارَةَ فَلَا يَحْرُمُ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ بِهِ لأَجْلِ التَّحْمِيْرِ حَرُمَ وَكَذَا عَرْشُ الْكَرَمِ عَلَى هَذَا، إِنْتَهَى، وَعَلَى هذَا عَصِيْرُ العِنَبِ بِقَصْدِ الْخَلِيَّةِ أَوِ الْخَمْرِيَّةِ.
ترجمہ: اور قاضی خاں نے اپنے فتاوی میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ اس کی بیع اس شخص کو جو شراب بناتا ہے اگر اس نے اس سے تجارت کا ارادہ کیا ہے تو حرام نہیں اور اگر اس شراب بنانے کی وجہ سے بیچا ہے تو حرام ہے اور ایسے ہی انگور کا ہونا لگانا ، قاضی خان کا کلام پورا ہوا اور اسی پر ہے انگور کا رس ہر کہ اور شراب کے ارادہ سے۔ تشریح : اگر کوئی شیرہ کسی شرابی کوفروخت کرتا ہے اور اس کی نیت اپنے کاروبار کی ہے اس سے کوئی مطلب نہیں ہے کہ وہ اس کا کیا کرے گا تو اس کا شرابی کو شیر و بینا بلا کراہت درست ہوگا اور اگر وہ اس نیت سے بیچتا ہے کہ شرابی اس شیرہ کی شراب بنائے تو اس طرح اس کا یہ فروخت کرنا نا جائز ہوگا۔ وكذا غرس الكرم: اگر کوئی انگور کی کاشت کرتا ہے اور اس کی نیت اس سے محض کاشت کی ہے اس سے کوئی مطلب نہیں ہے کہ شراب جنگی یا نہیں اور اس کے لئے انگور کی کاشت کرنے میں کسی طرح کی کراہت نہیں اگر کاشت کار نے یہ نیت کی کہ میں اس کو ایسے آدمی کے ہاتھ فروخت کروں گا جو شراب بنائے گا تو کاشت کر نا جائزنہ ہوگا نگور کی۔ وعلى هذا عصير العنب کسی شخص نے انگور کا شیرہ سرکہ بنانے کی نیت سے فروخت کیا اور اس کی نیت بہ تھی کہ اس شیرہ سے سرکہ بنایا جائے گا تو یہ جائز ہوگا۔ اور اگر نیت یہ ہو کہ شیر و سے شراب بنائی جائے گی تو پھر اس کا بچنا نا جائز ہوگا۔ علامہ حموی نے سراج کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا ہے کہ مجوس کو بیچنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اس لئے معصیت مین عصیر میں نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے تغیر کے بعد ہے ورنہ تو شیرہ حلال ہے۔ البتہ لا باس یہ واضح کر رہا ہے کہ مجوسی کے ہاتھ بھی فروخت نہ کرنا ہی اولی ہے۔ سوال: مجوسی کے ہاتھ شیرہ بیچنے کو جائز قرار دیا ہے البتہ لوطی کو امر د بیچنے کو نا جائز قرار دیا ہے وجہ فرق کیا ہے؟
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. The Second Qaidah: Matters are According to Their Objectives. The author mentions the second rule under the name 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha'. In the first rule it was mentioned that the reward of deeds depends on intention; without intention, no reward is obtained. In the second rule it is clarified that the permissibility or impermissibility of matters depends on the intention of the doer: if the objective is lawful, the act is lawful; if the objective is unlawful, the act is unlawful. And from here [the previous discussion] and from what we have presented concerning permissible acts (mubahat) and from what will be mentioned from the mashayikh, it becomes correct for us to establish a legal maxim, which is the second one: al-umuru bi maqasidiha (matters are according to their objectives), as you already know from the discussion of tark (refraining). Translation: From here and from what we have mentioned in mubahat and from what we will mention from the mashayikh, it becomes correct for us to establish a legal maxim, and that is the second maxim: al-umuru bi maqasidiha (matters depend on their objectives), as you have understood in the discussion of tark. Explanation: The author says that in the previous part, an example was given: if a trade slave is intended for service, he becomes designated for service and zakat is not obligatory on him; if a slave was for service and then trade intention is made, he remains for service until trade is actually carried out with the intention. Similarly in mubahat, it has passed that the attribute of mubah changes based on the objective: if the objective is lawful, the mubah is also lawful; if the objective is evil, the mubah becomes evil and falls into the category of impermissibility. Similarly, the mashayikh mentioned an example: selling grape juice to someone who makes wine—if the intention is merely trade, selling to the winemaker is permissible; if selling with the intention that he makes wine, then selling the grape juice to him is impermissible. The author, Allamah Ibn Nujaym al-Misri (may Allah have mercy on him) says that due to these examples, the jurists established another rule, and it is the second rule: al-umuru bi maqasidiha, that the permissibility and impermissibility of matters depend on intention and purpose: if the intention and purpose are lawful, the act is lawful; if the intention is for an unlawful act, then that same act becomes unlawful, as you have already understood in the discussion of tark (refraining). If refraining from prohibitions is found, then reward is obtained, provided one has the ability to commit the prohibited act; otherwise, no reward is obtained. Allamah Hamawi says that from the author's words, it apparently seems that this second rule is derived from these examples, even though the jurists did not explicitly state it; but it is not so—rather this rule is explicit. The difference between the first rule and the second rule is that the first rule concerns reward in the afterlife, while the second rule concerns worldly legal rulings (hukm dunyawi), i.e., permissibility and impermissibility. And Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa: The sale of grape juice to someone who makes wine—if he intends trade thereby, it is not prohibited; if he intends thereby to enable making wine, it is prohibited. Similarly, planting grapevines is like this. End. And upon this is the grape juice with the intention of vinegar or wine. Translation: And Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa that the sale of grape juice to a winemaker—if the seller intends trade, it is not prohibited; if he sells because of the winemaking, it is prohibited. Similarly, planting vines. His words end. And upon this is grape juice with the intention of vinegar or wine. Explanation: If someone sells grape juice to a wine-drinker and his intention is his own business, not caring what the buyer does, then selling to the wine-drinker is permissible without dislike. If he sells with the intention that the wine-drinker make wine, then such sale is impermissible. Similarly, planting vines: if someone plants grapes merely for cultivation, not caring whether wine is made or not, there is no dislike in planting. If the cultivator intends to sell to someone who will make wine, then planting is impermissible. And upon this: grape juice—if someone sells grape juice with the intention that vinegar be made, it is permissible. If the intention is that wine be made, then its sale is impermissible. Allamah Hamawi narrated from Siraj that there is no harm in selling to a Magian, because disobedience is not in the juice itself but after its transformation; otherwise, juice is lawful. However, 'la ba's' indicates that not selling to a Magian is preferable. Question: Selling juice to a Magian is declared permissible, but selling to a libertine (lutiyy) is declared impermissible. What is the reason for the difference?
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is an expansion and application of the second grand legal maxim of Hanafi jurisprudence: al-umuru bi maqasidiha (matters are according to their objectives). The author, Ibn Nujaym, explains that while the first maxim (al-umuru bi niyyatiha) relates to the reward of deeds in the afterlife, the second maxim governs the worldly legal ruling (hukm dunyawi) of an act—its permissibility or impermissibility—based on the intention or objective behind it. The author derives this maxim from three sources: (1) a previously discussed example of a trade slave where the intention changes the zakat obligation; (2) the discussion on mubahat (permissible acts) where the same act can become blameworthy if done with a bad intention; and (3) the mashayikh's example of selling grape juice to a winemaker. The key ruling is that if one sells grape juice intending merely trade, the sale is permissible even if the buyer is a known winemaker; but if one sells the juice specifically to enable wine-making, the sale becomes haram. This ruling is supported by Qadi Khan's Fatawa. The same principle applies to planting grapevines and selling juice for vinegar vs. wine. Allamah Hamawi clarifies that the maxim is not new but rather an explicit corollary of the first maxim, distinguished by its application to worldly rulings. The passage ends with a question about the difference between selling to a Magian (permissible, though better avoided) and selling to a libertine (impermissible)—the answer lies in the fact that a Magian might use it for lawful purposes, whereas a libertine is assumed to use it for sin; however, the text does not provide the full answer.

Key Terms
الأمور بمقاصدها (al-umuru bi maqasidiha): A legal maxim meaning that the legal ruling (permissibility/impermissibility) of an action depends on the intention or objective behind it.
عصير (asir): Juice, specifically grape juice before fermentation.
غرس الكرم (ghars al-karm): Planting grapevines.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the second qaidah (al-umuru bi maqasidiha), what is the ruling on selling grape juice to a known winemaker if the seller's intention is merely trade?
A) It is absolutely prohibited because the buyer will make wine.
B) It is permissible, but disliked (makruh).
C) It is permissible without dislike, because the seller's intention is trade.
D) It is prohibited only if the seller intends to enable wine-making.

Key Takeaway
The second qaidah, al-umuru bi maqasidiha, establishes that the worldly permissibility of an act depends on the intention behind it, not merely its external form.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
8 min
The Second Maxim (al-Umur bi-Maqasidiha) and Its Application to Grape Juice Sale
Qawida with furuat: expansion of the second maxim with practical cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to determine the permissibility of a transaction based on the seller's intention, and distinguish between inherent and incidental sin in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
The same sale can be permissible or prohibited depending solely on the seller's intention.

This lesson examines the second major legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions) as applied to the sale of grape juice. Using Qadi Khan's Fatawa, we explore how the seller's purpose transforms a neutral transaction into either permissible trade or prohibited facilitation of sin. The discussion also clarifies why selling grape juice to a Magian differs from selling a beardless youth to a pederast, illustrating the Hanafi principle that intention determines worldly rulings (ahkam dunyawiyya).

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing maxim and its scope
Recognize that the second maxim (al-umur bi-maqasidiha) governs worldly rulings of permissibility, distinct from the first maxim which relates to otherworldly reward.
This maxim is a kulliya (universal) qawida kubra applicable across all fiqh chapters.
2
State the core ruling from Qadi Khan
Qadi Khan rules that selling grape juice to a wine-maker is permissible if the seller intends trade, but prohibited if he intends to enable wine-making. The same applies to planting grapes.
The intention (qasd) is the decisive factor, not the eventual use.
3
Apply the maxim to each furu' (case) in the text
For each case (e.g., sale for vinegar, sale to a Magian, planting grapes), identify the seller's intention and derive the ruling using the maxim.
The maxim is applied consistently: permissible intention → permissible act; impermissible intention → prohibited act.
4
Understand the istithna' (exception) for Magians and distinguish it from the amrad case
Selling to a Magian is permissible because sin is not inherent in the juice but in its transformation; the Magian considers wine lawful. In contrast, selling an amrad (beardless youth) to a pederast is prohibited because sin is inherent in the youth himself.
The distinction hinges on where the disobedience (ma'siya) resides: in the object itself (amrad) or in a subsequent transformation (juice).
5
Determine the fatwa hierarchy for these rulings
The rulings from Qadi Khan's Fatawa are from the later authorities (mutakhkhirin) and are relied upon (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school. The amrad ruling is stricter due to inherent sin.
For selling to a Muslim wine-maker, the ruling is makruh (disliked) because it assists in sin.

ترجمہ: اور قاضی خاں نے اپنے فتاوی میں ذکر کیا ہے کہ اس کی بیع اس شخص کو جو شراب بناتا ہے اگر اس نے اس سے تجارت کا ارادہ کیا ہے تو حرام نہیں اور اگر اس شراب بنانے کی وجہ سے بیچا ہے تو حرام ہے اور ایسے ہی انگور کا ہونا لگانا ، قاضی خان کا کلام پورا ہوا اور اسی پر ہے انگور کا رس ہر کہ اور شراب کے ارادہ سے۔ تشریح : اگر کوئی شیرہ کسی شرابی کوفروخت کرتا ہے اور اس کی نیت اپنے کاروبار کی ہے اس سے کوئی مطلب نہیں ہے کہ وہ اس کا کیا کرے گا تو اس کا شرابی کو شیر و بینا بلا کراہت درست ہوگا اور اگر وہ اس نیت سے بیچتا ہے کہ شرابی اس شیرہ کی شراب بنائے تو اس طرح اس کا یہ فروخت کرنا نا جائز ہوگا۔ وكذا غرس الكرم: اگر کوئی انگور کی کاشت کرتا ہے اور اس کی نیت اس سے محض کاشت کی ہے اس سے کوئی مطلب نہیں ہے کہ شراب جنگی یا نہیں اور اس کے لئے انگور کی کاشت کرنے میں کسی طرح کی کراہت نہیں اگر کاشت کار نے یہ نیت کی کہ میں اس کو ایسے آدمی کے ہاتھ فروخت کروں گا جو شراب بنائے گا تو کاشت کر نا جائزنہ ہوگا نگور کی۔ وعلى هذا عصير العنب کسی شخص نے انگور کا شیرہ سرکہ بنانے کی نیت سے فروخت کیا اور اس کی نیت بہ تھی کہ اس شیرہ سے سرکہ بنایا جائے گا تو یہ جائز ہوگا۔ اور اگر نیت یہ ہو کہ شیر و سے شراب بنائی جائے گی تو پھر اس کا بچنا نا جائز ہوگا۔ علامہ حموی نے سراج کے حوالہ سے نقل کیا ہے کہ مجوس کو بیچنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اس لئے معصیت مین عصیر میں نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے تغیر کے بعد ہے ورنہ تو شیرہ حلال ہے۔ البتہ لا باس یہ واضح کر رہا ہے کہ مجوسی کے ہاتھ بھی فروخت نہ کرنا ہی اولی ہے۔ سوال: مجوسی کے ہاتھ شیرہ بیچنے کو جائز قرار دیا ہے البتہ لوطی کو امر د بیچنے کو نا جائز قرار دیا ہے وجہ فرق کیا ہے؟
جواب: علامہ حموی نے وجہ فرق یہ بیان کی ہے کہ معصیت امرد میں ہے جو عین امرد کے ساتھ قائم ہے اس لئے لوطی کے ساتھ امرد کے بیچنے کو نا جائز قرار دیا ہے جبکہ شیرہ حلال ہے کیونکہ معصیت میں حصیر کے ساتھ نہیں ہے بلکہ اس کے تغیر ہو جانے کے بعد ہے ورنہ تو شیرہ حلال ہے۔ یاد پر کی تفصیل مجوسی وغیرہ کے ہاتھ بیچنے میں ہے کیونکہ مجوی شراب کو حلال سمجھتے ہیں اور ہمارے لئے محکم یہ ہے کہ ہم ان سے تعرض نہ کریں کہ وہ شراب بنائیں اور پیئیں۔ ورنہ اگر کوئی مسلمان شراب بنانے کا کام کرتا ہے تو اس کے ہاتھ شیرہ وغیرہ بیچنا جائز نہیں ہے مکروہ ہے کیونکہ اس کو بیچنے میں فسق و معصیت پر مدد کرنا ہے۔
اور فضول العلائی میں ہے کہ شیرہ، انگور اور انگور کی کاشت وغیرہ کو ایسے آدمی کے ہاتھ بیچنے میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے جو شراب بناتا ہے۔
Discussion: The second maxim is 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). That the permissibility or impermissibility of actions depends on intention and purpose. If the purpose and intention are permissible, the action is also permissible; if the intention is for an impermissible act, then that same action becomes impermissible. As you understood in the chapter on prohibitions and abandonments, if abstention from prohibitions is found, reward will be given provided there is ability to avoid the prohibited act; otherwise no reward. Allama Hamawi says that apparently from the author's words it seems that this second maxim is derived from those particulars, although the jurists have not explicitly stated it, but that is not the case; rather this maxim is explicitly mentioned. The difference between the first and second maxim is that the first maxim relates to otherworldly reward, and the second relates to worldly rulings, i.e., permissibility and impermissibility. Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa: 'The sale of grape juice to one who makes it into wine: if he intends by it trade, it is not prohibited; but if he intends it for the purpose of making wine, it is prohibited. Similarly, planting grapevines is upon this.' End. And upon this is the grape juice with the intention of vinegar or wine. Translation: Qadi Khan mentioned in his Fatawa that the sale of grape juice to a wine-maker: if he intends trade, it is not prohibited; if he sold it because of wine-making, it is prohibited. Similarly, growing grapes. Explanation: If someone sells juice to a drinker intending his own business, not caring what the buyer does, the sale is valid without dislike. But if he sells with the intention that the drinker will make wine, then such sale is impermissible. Likewise, planting grapes: if a farmer intends mere cultivation, not caring whether wine is made, there is no dislike. But if he intends to sell to a wine-maker, the cultivation is impermissible. And upon this is grape juice: if someone sells grape juice intending vinegar, it is permissible; if intending wine, it is impermissible. Allama Hamawi narrated from Siraj that there is no harm in selling to Magians because disobedience is not in the juice itself but after its transformation; the juice is lawful. However, it is better not to sell to Magians. Question: Selling to a Magian is deemed permissible, but selling an amrad (beardless youth) to a pederast is deemed impermissible. What is the difference? Answer: Allama Hamawi explained that disobedience lies in the amrad himself, inherent in his being, so selling him to a pederast is impermissible. Whereas juice is lawful because disobedience is not inherent in it but after transformation. This detail applies to selling to Magians etc., because Magians consider wine lawful, and our ruling is that we do not interfere with them making and drinking it. However, if a Muslim is a wine-maker, selling juice etc. to him is not permissible; it is disliked because it assists in sin and disobedience. And in Fadl al-'Ala'i: selling juice, grapes, and their cultivation to a wine-maker is not objectionable.
Source pages p. 128

Commentary
This passage is a detailed application of the second major maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). The author first distinguishes this maxim from the first (which relates to reward in the afterlife) by noting that this maxim governs worldly rulings of permissibility. The core teaching is that the same action can be permissible or impermissible depending on the agent's intention. The passage presents a key ruling from Qadi Khan's Fatawa: selling grape juice (عصير) to a wine-maker. If the seller intends mere trade, the sale is permissible; if he intends to enable wine-making, it is prohibited. This applies also to planting grapes. The discussion extends to a comparative issue: selling to a Magian (who considers wine lawful) is permissible because the disobedience is in the transformation, not the juice itself; however, selling an amrad (beardless youth) to a pederast is impermissible because the sin is inherent in the youth. The passage also notes that selling to a Muslim wine-maker is disliked because it assists in sin. This shows the Hanafi emphasis on intention (niyya) in determining the ruling of transactions.

Key Terms
قصد (qasd): Intention or purpose that determines the legal ruling of an action
عصير (asir): Grape juice or any juice that can be made into wine
معصية (ma'siya): Disobedience or sin, which may inhere in an object or in a subsequent action
أمرد (amrad): Beardless youth; selling him to a pederast is prohibited because sin is inherent in his being
مجوس (majus): Magians or Zoroastrians, who consider wine lawful

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Qadi Khan's Fatawa, what is the ruling on selling grape juice to a wine-maker if the seller intends trade?
A) It is prohibited because the juice will become wine.
B) It is permissible because the seller's intention is trade, not enabling sin.
C) It is disliked because it involves a Muslim buyer.
D) It is permissible only if the buyer is a Magian.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of a transaction depends on the seller's intention, not merely on the eventual use of the item; the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' is the key to resolving such cases.

Praying for Long Life for a Dhimmi: Intention Matters
Application of the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to supplication for a dhimmi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to the case of supplicating for a dhimmi and identify the operative intention that determines permissibility.

Core Idea
Supplication for a dhimmi's long life is permissible if the intention is his guidance or Muslim benefit.

In this lesson, we examine a furu' application of one of the five major maxims: 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (Actions are judged by intentions). The source passage from Fatawa Hindiyya presents a case where the outward act—praying for a dhimmi's long life—can be either permissible or impermissible depending solely on the intention. This illustrates how the same verbal expression carries different legal rulings based on what the heart conceals.

Guided Path
1
State the governing maxim
Recall the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' in Arabic and English. This maxim is the foundation of the case.
One of the five major maxims (al-qawaid al-kubra).
2
Identify the outward action
The action is a Muslim saying to a dhimmi: 'May Allah prolong your life.' This is a verbal supplication.
The same words can have different rulings based on intention.
3
Identify the valid intentions
Two valid intentions are mentioned: (1) hoping the dhimmi will embrace Islam, and (2) hoping he will continue paying jizyah for the benefit of Muslims.
Both intentions are religiously beneficial.
4
Derive the ruling for each valid intention
With either of these intentions, the supplication is permissible (la ba'sa bihi). The maxim transforms the act into a form of da'wah or benefit-seeking.
5
Recognize the condition for impermissibility
If any other intention (e.g., pure worldly affection) is present, the ruling changes accordingly. The maxim applies negatively: impermissible intentions render the act impermissible.
The source says: 'jaisa maqsad hoga waisa hi hukm hoga.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَفِيْهَا أَيْضًا: إِذَاقَالَ الْمُسْلِمُ لِلذَّمّى: أَطَالَ اللهُ بَقَاءَكَ، قَالُوا: إِنْ نَوَى بِقَلْبِهِ أَنْ تُطِيْلَ اللهُ بَقَاءَهُ لَعَلَّهُ أَنْ يُسْلِمَ، أَوْ يُؤدَى الْجِزْيَةَ عَنْ ذُلٍّ وَصَغَارٍ لَا بَأْسَ بِهِ لِأَنَّ هَذَا دُعَاءُ لَهُ إِلَى الْإِسْلَامِ أَوْ لِمَنْفَعَةِ الْمُسْلِمِينَ، إِنْتَهى.
:ترجمہ: اور نیز اسی میں ہے کہ جب مسلمان نے کسی ذمی سے کہا اللہ تیری عمر دراز کرے فقہا ، فرماتے ہیں اگر دل سے نیت کی کہ اللہ اس کی عمر دراز کرے شاید کہ یہ مسلمان ہو جائے یا ذلت ورسوائی کے ساتھ جز یہ دے تو کوئی حرج نہیں اس لئے کہ یہ اس کے لئے اسلام کی دعا کرنا ہے یا مسلمانوں کے فائدہ کی ، کلام پورا ہوا ۔ تشریح کوئی مسلمان کسی کا فر کولمبی عمر کی دعا دیتا ہے اور مقصد یہ ہے کہ اللہ اس کو اسلام کی ہدایت دیدے یا مقصد ہے کہ لمبی عمر ہوگی مسلمانوں کو جزیہ دے گا بیت المال کے خزانہ میں جمع ہو کر مسلمانوں کا فائدہ ہوگا تو اس میں کوئی حرج نہیں ہے اور اگر اس کے علاوہ کوئی اور مقصد ہے جیسا مقصد ہوگا ویسا ہی حکم ہوگا الامور ہم مقاصد با قاعدہ مسلمہ ہے اس پر تفریعات پیش کی جارہی ہیں۔ ولو دعا له بطول العمر قيل يجوز لان فيه نفعاً للمسلمين بالجزية وقيل لايجوز تكملة البحر الرائق ج/٣٧٣/٨)
And also in it: When a Muslim says to a dhimmi, 'May Allah prolong your life,' they (the jurists) said: If he intends in his heart that Allah prolong his life so that perhaps he may become Muslim, or that he may pay the jizyah with humility and subjugation, there is no harm in it, because this is a supplication for him towards Islam or for the benefit of the Muslims. End.
Source pages p. 133

Commentary
This passage is an application of the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions). The author presents a case from Fatawa Hindiyya: a Muslim prays for a dhimmi's long life. The ruling depends on the intention. If the intention is that the dhimmi might embrace Islam through this life, or that he will continue paying jizyah benefiting the Muslim treasury, then it is permissible. Any other intention (e.g., pure worldly affection) would render it impermissible. This illustrates that the same outward action can be lawful or unlawful based on what the heart intends. The author then quotes from Bahr al-Raiq that there are two opinions, but the relied-upon view is that it is permissible if it benefits Muslims.

Key Terms
نية (niyyah): The intention in the heart that determines the legal nature of an action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why is it permissible for a Muslim to pray for a dhimmi's long life according to this passage?
A) Because the dhimmi is a human being deserving of respect.
B) Because the Muslim intends that he might become Muslim or that jizyah benefits Muslims.
C) Because it is always good to pray for others regardless of intention.
D) Because the dhimmi has a contract of protection.

Key Takeaway
The ruling on supplication for a dhimmi's long life depends entirely on the intention behind it, illustrating the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

Eating Beyond Fullness: Intentions Determine Ruling
Applies the grand maxim 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha' to eating beyond satiety.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha' to determine the ruling of eating beyond fullness in scenarios involving personal pleasure, worship, or hospitality.

Core Idea
The ruling of eating beyond fullness changes with intention: haram for pleasure, mustahabb for worship or hospitality.

This lesson explores a classic application of the grand maxim 'Actions are judged by intentions.' The fuqaha use this qawida to differentiate between eating beyond fullness for mere pleasure (haram) and eating for a noble purpose such as gaining strength for fasting or keeping a guest company (mustahabb). Understanding this demonstrates how intention transforms the legal nature of a neutral act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing qawida
Recognize that the passage applies the qawida 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha'. This maxim states that the legal ruling of an act depends on the intention behind it.
This qawida is kubra (major) and covers all fiqh chapters.
2
Determine the default ruling of eating beyond fullness
The fuqaha state that eating beyond satiety is haram when done for pleasure (shahwa). This is the default ruling.
The default is based on avoiding harm and excess.
3
Identify the exceptions where intention changes the ruling
Two exceptions are given: (1) to gain strength for fasting, (2) to keep a guest company so the guest does not feel ashamed. In these cases, the act becomes mustahabb.
The intention of worship or hospitality overrides the default prohibition.
4
Apply the qawida to each scenario
For each exception, explain how the intention (qasd) transforms the act from haram to mustahabb. The qawida directly links intention to ruling.
The same physical act becomes legally distinct based on inner motive.
5
Consider the broader scope of the qawida
Note that the same principle applies to other acts like eating just enough to survive (fard) or eating little that prevents worship (not permissible). The qawida universally determines rulings based on purpose.
The commentary by Allama Hamawi expands the categories.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقالوا الأكل فوق الشَّبْع حَرَامٌ بِقَصْدِ الشَّهْوَةِ، وَإِنْ قَصَدَ بِهِ التَّقَوّى عَلَى الصَّوْمِ أَوْ مُواكَلَةَ الضَّيْفِ فَمُسْتَحَبٌّ.
:ترجمہ: اور فقہا ء فرماتے ہیں پیٹ بھر سے زائد کھانا شہوت کے ارادہ سے حرام ہے اور اگر اس سے روزہ پر تقویت یا مہمان کو کھلانے کا ارادہ ہو تو مستحب ہے۔
تشریح : علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کھانا کھانے کے چند مراتب ہیں اتنا کھانا کہ جس کے ذریعہ ہلاکت سے بچ جائے اور نماز کھڑے ہو کر ادا کر سکے تو فرض ہے اور اس سے زائد پیٹ بھر تک کھانا مباح ہے البتہ پیٹ بھر سے زائد کھانا حرام ہے البتہ دو موقعوں پر (۱) کہ روزے پر تقویت حاصل ہو اس لئے پیٹ بھر سے زائد کھا رہا ہے تو جائز ہے۔ (۲) یا اس نیت سے پیٹ بھر سے زائد کھا رہا ہے کہ اگر وہ کھانے سے رک گیا تو جو مہمان اس کے ساتھ کھا رہا ہے وہ بھی شرم کے مارے رک جائے گا اور وہ بھوکا رہ جائے گا۔ اس صورت میں پیٹ بھر سے زائد کھانا مستحب ہے اس لئے کہ مہمان نوازی نہ کرنا شریعت کی نظر میں برا ہے۔ اور مہمان نوازی نہ کرنے والے کی شکایت کا اظہار کرسکتا ہے جس کی دلیل یہ آیت "لا يحب الله الجهر بالسوء من القول إلا من ظلم" ہے۔ علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ اتنا کم کھانا جس سے کمزوری کے سبب عبادت کی ادائیگی بھی نہ کر سکے جائز نہیں ہے دلیل یہ حدیث ہے "لـقـولـه علیه الصلاة و السلام نفسک مطيئتک فارفق بھا" اور حدیث سے مراد یہ ہے کہ نفس کو نہ تو اذیت دے اور نہ اس کو اتنا بھوکا رکھو کہ وہ ہلاک یا ہلاکت کے قریب پہنچ جائے۔ نبی اکرم صلى الله عليه وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا " المؤمن القوى خير من المؤمن الضعيف، طاقت ورمؤمن کمزور مؤمن
سے افضل ہے۔ اگر کسی نے کھانا پینا ترک کر دیا تو انہوں نے شریعت اسلامیہ کے حکم کی خلافت ورزی کی۔ حالت مخمصہ میں اگر مردار کھا کر جان نہ بچائی اور وہ ہلاک ہو گیا تو عاصی ہو کر مرا تو تمہارا اس کے بارے میں کیا خیال ہے جو حلال کو ترک کر دے اور بھوک کی وجہ سے مرجائے بخلاف اس کے اگر کسی کو دست لگ گئے یا پیچس یا آنکھ دکھنے لگی اور علاج نہ کرایا حتی کہ مر گیا۔
علامہ جموعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس سے ان صوفی جہلاء کا حکم بھی معلوم ہو جاتا ہے جو بغرض ریاضت حلال کھانا چھوڑ دیتے ہیں اور اتنے کمزور اور لاغر ہو جاتے ہیں کہ اللہ کے ذکر اور عبادت کو بھی بچا نہیں لائے اور اس کو قربت وعبادت تصور کر دیتے ہیں۔ اس جزئیہ کو ذہن میں اچھی طرح بٹھالینا بہت کام آئے گا۔
And they (the fuqaha) said: Eating beyond fullness is haram when intended for pleasure; but if one intends by it strength for fasting or feeding a guest, then it is mustahabb. Translation: And the jurists say: Eating beyond fullness with the intention of pleasure is haram, and if with the intention of strength for fasting or feeding a guest, it is mustahabb. Commentary: Allama Hamawi says: There are several levels of eating. Eating just enough to avoid destruction and to be able to stand in prayer is fard. Beyond that until satiety is mubah. However, eating beyond satiety is haram, except in two situations: (1) to gain strength for fasting – then eating beyond satiety is permissible; (2) with the intention that if he stops, the guest who is eating with him will also stop out of shame and remain hungry – then eating beyond satiety is mustahabb, because not being hospitable is bad in the eyes of the Shariah, and the wronged person may complain, as evidenced by the verse 'Allah does not like the public mention of evil except by one who has been wronged'. Allama Hamawi also says: Eating so little that one cannot perform worship due to weakness is not permissible, as evidenced by the hadith 'Your soul is your mount, so be gentle with it'. The meaning is that one should not torment the soul nor let it starve to death or near destruction. The Prophet said: 'A strong believer is better than a weak believer.' If someone abandons food and drink, he has opposed the command of the Shariah. In a state of starvation, if one does not eat carrion to save his life and dies, he dies as a sinner. What do you think of one who abandons halal food and dies of hunger? Similarly, if someone does not treat diarrhea or eye pain until death, it is different. Allama Jamui said: From this, the ruling on ignorant Sufis who abandon halal food for spiritual exercise and become so weak they cannot even remember Allah or worship, thinking it is piety, is known. Keep this rule in mind well.
Source pages p. 135

Commentary
This passage is an application of the qawida 'al-umuru bi maqasidiha' to eating beyond fullness. The source text from the fuqaha states that the ruling depends on intention: if for pleasure, it is haram; if for strength to fast or to keep a guest company, it is mustahabb. Allama Hamawi expands by categorizing eating levels: fard (just enough to survive and pray), mubah (up to fullness), and then the exceptions to haram. The qawida is explicitly referenced in the previous section and applied here. The text also warns against extreme asceticism that harms the body, reinforcing that preservation of health is important for worship.

Key Terms
قصد (qaṣd): Intention; the motive behind an action
مباح (mubāḥ): Permissible; an act about which there is no reward or punishment
مستحب (mustaḥabb): Recommended; an act that is rewarded but not obligatory

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does eating beyond fullness become mustahabb (recommended)?
A) When done for pleasure and enjoyment.
B) When done to gain strength for fasting or to keep a guest company.
C) When done to show off wealth.
D) When done without any intention.

Key Takeaway
The ruling of eating beyond fullness is not fixed; intention (qasd) can transform a normally haram act into a mustahabb one when aimed at worship or noble character.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
10 min
The Maxim 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' and Its Applications
Expanding the maxim of intentions with furu' from luqtah, books, mosque trees, and coins.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' to classify the permissibility of everyday actions based on intention, and identify when the maxim is overridden by the principle of public necessity.

Core Idea
Intention transforms the ruling – picking up lost property with return intent is halal; with possess intent, haram.

This lesson examines the fifth major Hanafi maxim: 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha'. While often thought to apply only to acts of worship, the maxim governs everyday transactions and conduct. Through a series of furu' (applications) from luqtah, books, mosque trees, and coins, the text demonstrates how intention is the decisive factor in determining the legal ruling. The passage also introduces an important exception where public necessity overrides individual intention.

Guided Path
1
Identify the maxim and its scope
The maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' means 'matters are judged by their aims'. It is a kulliya maxim applicable across ibadat, mu'amalat, and jinayat.
This is one of the five major maxims of Hanafi fiqh.
2
Analyze the first furu': luqtah
Picking up a lost item is either halal (if intending return) or haram/ghasb (if intending personal ownership). Intention determines the ruling from the moment of picking up.
The definition of luqtah is key: preservation for others, not for oneself.
3
Examine the second and third furu': using a book as a pillow and planting a tree in a mosque
Both have the same pattern: if the intention is preservation or a valid purpose (e.g., shade), the action is not makruh; otherwise it is makruh.
Disrespect is evaluated with intention.
4
Review the fourth and fifth furu': writing Allah's name on a coin and sitting on a saddlebag with a mus-haf
Again, intention matters: if intended for a valid purpose (marker, preservation), no karaah; otherwise karaah.
These are from al-Muhit al-Burhani and al-Tatarkhaniyyah.
5
Consider the exception: public harm overrides individual intention
The Hidayah example of shooting at an enemy shielding with Muslim prisoners shows that when general harm (al-darar al-'amm) is at stake, individual intention is overridden by the necessity to repel the greater harm.
This exception is governed by the maxim 'al-darar yuzal'.

ا راستہ میں پڑھی ہوئی چیز اس نیت سے اٹھائی ہے کہ اس کو مالک تک پہنچانے کی پوری جد و جہد کروں گا تو اس کے لئے اس لقطہ کا اٹھانا جائز ہے۔ تواس کا اعلان وغیرہ کرنے اور اس کے مالک تک اس کو پہنچانے کی پوری جدوجہد کرے۔ مالک کے نہ ملنے پر صدقہ کر دے اور اگر صدقہ کرنے پر وہ چیز ہلاک ہو جائے یا ختم ہو جائے اور اس کے بعد مالک آجائے تو لاقط اس کا تاوان اپنی جیب سے ادا کرے گا اور اگر لاقط غریب ہے تو خود بھی استعمال کر سکتا ہے یا کوئی معمولی چیز ہے جس کو مالک تلاش نہیں کر سکتا تو اس کو اٹھا لینے والا خود بھی استعمال کر سکتا ہے۔
وَفِي التَّاتَارُ خَانِيَةِ : فِى الْحَظَرِ وَالْإِبَاحَةِ إِذا تَوَسَّدَ الْكِتَابَ، فَإِنْ قَصَدَ الْحِفْظُ لَا يَكْرَهُ، وَإِلَّا يَكْرَهُ.
ترجمہ : اور تار تارخانیہ کے باب الحظر والاباحة “ میں ہے جب کتاب کو تکیہ بنایا پس اگر حفاظت کی ارادہ کیا تو مکروہ نہیں ورنہ مکروہ ہے۔
تشریح بلاضرورت شرعیہ کے کتاب پر ٹیک لگانا بے ادبی اور مکروہ ہے اور اگر چوری کے خوف سے سر کے نیچے رکھ کر ٹیک لگا کر سو گیا تو مکروہ نہیں ہے۔ الأمور بمقاصدها : کی وجہ سے۔
معلــم مـعـه خريطة فيها كتب من اخبار النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم او كتب ابي حنيفة أو غیره فتوسد خريطة ان قصد الحفظ لا يكره . اذ ليس فيه ترك التعظيم وإن لم يقصد الحفظ يكره لان فيه ترك التعظيم (المحيط البرهاني ج ۶ ص / ۴۹)
وَإِنْ غَرَسَ فِى الْمَسْجِدِ، فَإِنْ قَصَدَ الظَّلِ لَا يَكْرَهُ وَإِنْ قَصَدَ مَنْفَعَةً أُخْرَى يَكْرَهُ.
ترجمه: اور اگر مسجد میں درخت لگائے پس اگر سائے کا ارادہ ہے تو مکروہ نہیں ہے اور اگر کوئی دوسری منفعت ہے تو مکروہ ہے۔
تشریح: مسجد سے مراد مسجد شرعی ہے اگر درخت لگانے کا مقصد سایہ ہے تو جائز ہے کراہت نہیں اور اگر کوئی اور مقصد ہے مثلاً پتوں کی بیع یا اور کوئی منفعت مقصود ہے اور اس کی وجہ سے مسجد تنگ ہو جائے یا صفوں میں تفریق نو جائز نہیں ہے اور اگر ملحقات مسجد ہے تو ہر دو صورت جائز ہے کراہت نہیں ۔ وعنه ايضاً فيمن غرس الاستجار في المسجد ان كان يفعل ذلك للظل لا بأس وان كان يفعل ذلك لبيع الاوراق او لمنفعة اخرى يكره اذا كانت تضيق على الناس مسجدهم لصلاتهم او يقع فيه تفريق الصفوف (المحيط البرهانی ج ۲ ص / ۵۳۹)
وَكِتَابَةُ إِسْمِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى عَلَى الدَّرْهَمِ إِنْ كَانَ بِقَصْدِ الْعَلَامَةِ لَا يَكْرَهُ، وَلِلنَّهَاوُنِ يَكْرَهُ وَالْجُلُوْسُ عَلَى جَوْلِقٍ فِيْهِ مُصْحَفٌ إِنْ قَصَدَ الْحِفْظِ لَا يَكْرَهُ، وَإِلَّا يَكْرَهُ.
There is no harm in shooting them even if among them there is a Muslim prisoner and a merchant, because shooting is repelling general harm by defending the core of Islam, and killing the prisoner and the merchant is a specific harm. And because a fortress is never devoid of a Muslim, so if one desisted due to his consideration, the door would be closed. And if they shield themselves with Muslim children or prisoners, they are not refrained from shooting them as we have explained, and they aim at the disbelievers with shooting. (Hidayah vol. 2 p. 561) And if not for fear of length, we would have cited many branches testifying to what we have deduced from the rule, which is: Matters are judged by their aims. Translation: If not for fear of length, we would have cited so many branches upon this rule 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' that would testify to it. Explanation: Many particulars can be deduced from this rule, but due to fear of length we did not mention further branches and particulars. And they said in the chapter of luqtah: If he takes it with the intention of returning it, it is permissible for him to pick it up, and if he takes it with the intention of keeping it for himself, he becomes a usurper and sinner. Translation: The jurists say regarding luqtah: if he picks it up with the intention of returning it, then picking it up is halal for him, and if he picks it up with the intention of keeping it for himself, then he is a usurper and sinner. Explanation: Luqtah (with fath of qaf according to the well-known language said by the majority, and the second language with sukun, and third luqatah with damm of lam, and fourth laqat with fath of lam and qaf) is a name given to lost property, and in Islamic law it is property found lost. In al-Muhit: raising a lost thing for preservation for others, not for ownership. (Shami Yaseen p. 430) ... And in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, in the chapter of prohibition and permission: If he uses a book as a pillow, then if he intended preservation, it is not disliked, otherwise it is disliked. Translation: In Tatarkhaniyyah, chapter of prohibition and permission: When a book is made a pillow, if the intention is preservation, it is not makruh, otherwise it is makruh. Explanation: Leaning on a book without a valid Shar'i need is disrespectful and makruh, and if out of fear of theft he places it under his head and leans and sleeps, it is not makruh because of 'al-umur bi maqasidiha'. A person with a satchel containing books of the traditions of the Prophet (peace be upon him) or books of Abu Hanifah or others, and he uses the satchel as a pillow: if he intends preservation, it is not disliked, as there is no abandonment of respect; if he does not intend preservation, it is disliked because it involves abandonment of respect. (al-Muhit al-Burhani vol. 6 p. 49) And if he plants in the mosque, then if he intends shade, it is not disliked, and if he intends another benefit, it is disliked. Translation: If he plants a tree in the mosque, then if he intends shade, it is not makruh; if he intends another benefit, it is makruh. Explanation: By mosque is meant the Shar'i mosque. If the purpose of planting is shade, it is permissible, no dislike; if there is another purpose, e.g., selling leaves or some other benefit, and due to this the mosque becomes narrow or rows are disrupted, it is not permissible. And if it is the annex of the mosque, then both cases are permissible, no dislike. And also from him: regarding one who plants for hire in the mosque: if he does that for shade, no problem; if he does that for selling leaves or for another benefit, it is disliked when it narrows the mosque for the people's prayer or causes disruption of rows. (al-Muhit al-Burhani vol. 2 p. 539) And writing the name of Allah the Exalted on the dirham: if it is with the intention of a marker, it is not disliked; otherwise it is disliked. And sitting on a saddlebag in which there is a mus-haf: if he intends preservation, it is not disliked; otherwise it is disliked.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the fifth major maxim of Hanafi fiqh: 'Al-umur bi maqasidiha' (Matters are judged by their aims). The author first presents a ruling from the Hidayah concerning a military situation where it is permissible to shoot at the enemy even if Muslim prisoners are present, because the intention is to repel general harm (daf' al-darar al-'amm). This example is not directly about intention but serves as a prelude to show that the rule applies broadly. The author then states that, fearing excessive length, he will supply only a selection of furu' (applications) for this maxim. The first furu' is from the chapter of luqtah (found property). The ruling depends entirely on the picker's intention: if he intends to return the item to its owner, picking it up is halal (permissible); if he intends to keep it for himself from the outset, he is a ghāsib (usurper) and sinful. The definition of luqtah follows: it is a lost item, and legally it is picking up a lost thing for preservation on behalf of another, not for ownership. The second furu' is from al-Tatarkhāniyyah regarding using a book as a pillow. If one intends preservation (e.g., to protect it from theft), it is not makruh; otherwise it is makruh because it shows disrespect. A similar case from al-Muhīt al-Burhānī concerns a satchel containing sacred books: same ruling based on intention. The third furu' is planting a tree in the mosque. If the intent is to provide shade for worshippers, it is not makruh; if the intent is any other benefit (e.g., selling leaves), then it is makruh because it may inconvenience or disrupt prayers. The fourth furu' is writing Allah's name on a coin: if intended as a marker (i.e., a distinguishing sign), it is not makruh; if not, it is makruh. The fifth furu' is sitting on a saddlebag containing a mus-haf: if the intention is preservation, it is not makruh; otherwise it is makruh. All these rulings are unified under the same principle: the legal classification of an action is determined by the underlying intention (niyyah).

Key Terms
اللُّقْطَة (al-luqtah): Lost property found on the ground; legally, picking up a lost item for the purpose of preserving it for its owner, not for ownership.
غَاصِب (ghāsib): One who takes another's property unlawfully with intention to possess it.
مَقَاصِد (maqāṣid): Intentions, aims, or purposes behind an action.
تَوَسَّدَ (tawassada): To use something as a pillow or cushion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi rulings presented, what is the ruling on picking up a lost item (luqtah) if the finder intends to return it to its owner?
A) It is forbidden (haram).
B) It is permissible (halal).
C) It is disliked (makruh).
D) It is obligatory (wajib).

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'Al-Umur bi Maqasidiha' establishes that intention is the decisive factor in determining the legal ruling of an action, with the exception that public necessity may override individual intention.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

The Tenfold Framework of Intention (Niyyah) in Hanafi Usul al-Ifta
Outline of ten sections on intention (niyyah) in Hanafi usul al-ifta.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to outline the ten sections of the discussion on intention (niyyah) and identify its core legal function in Hanafi usul al-ifta.

Core Idea
Intention (niyyah) is a condition for worship—its systematic study covers ten pillars, from reality to conditions.

This lesson introduces the ten-section framework that the Hanafi usul tradition uses to analyze intention (niyyah). As a key qa'ida, 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' governs much of fiqh. The author has listed the ten topics that will be elaborated in subsequent lessons. Understanding this roadmap is essential before diving into the details.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two underlying principles
Read the opening line: 'These two principles encompass the discussion on intention.' Though unnamed here, these are likely 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' and another core qa'ida. Recognize that the entire discussion is anchored in broader maxims.
The two principles are not detailed in this passage, but they frame the subsequent sections.
2
List the ten sections in order
Extract the ten topics from the Arabic text: from 'first on explaining its reality' to 'tenth on its conditions'. Write them down sequentially.
Memorize this list—it is the skeleton of the Hanafi theory of intention.
3
Group sections into thematic parts
Identify logical groupings: Sections 1-2 (definition and legislative purpose), 3-7 (application details: determination, quality, sincerity, combining, timing), 8-10 (continuity, locus, conditions).
This grouping helps in retrieval and application.
4
Infer the central question of each section
For each section, ask: What legal problem does this address? For example, Section 3 answers: Must the intended act be explicitly specified, or is a general intention sufficient?
This prepares you for deeper study of each topic.
5
Reflect on the framework's completeness
Consider whether any aspect of niyyah is missing. The ten sections cover essence, purpose, specificity, modality, sincerity, combination, timing, continuity, locus, and prerequisites—a comprehensive approach.
This completeness is characteristic of Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ إعْلَمُ: أَنَّ هَاتَيْنِ الْقَاعِدَتَيْنِ يَشْمَلُهُمَا الكَلَامُ عَلَى النِّيَّةِ، وَفِيْهَا مُبَاحِتُ الأَوَّلُ: فِي بَيَان حَقِيقَتِهَا الثَّانِي فِي بَيَانِ مَاشُرِعَتْ لأجله. ألثَّالِتُ: فِى بَيَانِ تَعْيِينِ الْمَنْوِي وَعَدْم تعينه الرَّابِعُ : فِي بَيَانِ التَّعَرُّض لِصِفَةِ المَنْوِى مِنَ الْفَرْضِيَّةِ وَالنَّفْلِيَّة والأداءِ وَالْقَضَاءِ . الخامس: فِي بَيَانِ الإِخْلَاصِ فِيْهَا السَّادِسُ : فِي بَيَانِ الْجَمْع بَيْنَ عِبَادَتَيْنِ بِنِيَّةٍ وَاحِدَةٍ. السَّابِعُ فِي بَيَان وَقْتِهَا . الثَّامِنُ : فِى بَيَان عَدَم إِشْتِرَاطِ إِسْتِمْرَارِهَا، وَفِيهِ حُكْمُهَا فِي كُلِّ رُكن مِنَ الْأَرْكَان. التَّاسِعُ : فِي مُحَلّهَا الْعَاشِرُ : فِي شُرُوطِهَا.
Then know that these two principles encompass the discussion on intention. And it has ten sections: first, on explaining its reality; second, on explaining why it was legislated; third, on explaining the determination of the intended and its non-determination; fourth, on explaining the engagement with the quality of the intended from obligation and supererogation, performance and makeup; fifth, on explaining sincerity in it; sixth, on explaining combining two acts of worship with one intention; seventh, on explaining its time; eighth, on explaining the non-requirement of its continuity, and in it is its ruling for every pillar of the pillars; ninth, on its place; tenth, on its conditions.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage serves as a table of contents for the upcoming detailed discussion on intention (niyyah). The author, having established the two foundational qawa'id (likely 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' and another), now outlines ten sections that will be covered. These sections systematically examine niyyah from its definition and legislative basis, to how specific intent is required, the distinction between obligatory and supererogatory actions, sincerity, combining multiple acts, timing, continuity (which is not a condition in Hanafi fiqh), and its locus and conditions. This structured approach reflects the rigorous methodology of the Hanafi usul al-ifta tradition, where theoretical principles are followed by detailed applications.

Key Terms
النِّيَّة (al-niyyah): The intention by which an act is directed toward a specific purpose, distinguishing it from idle action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Intention (niyyah) is a condition for worship, and its systematic study in Hanafi usul al-ifta covers ten distinct aspects.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
10 min
The Legal Definition of Niyyah and Its Ten Sections
Outlining ten discussions on niyyah and defining it linguistically and legally

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of niyyah, identify its ten sections, and explain the Hanafi principle that intention in abandonments only counts when abandonment becomes active restraint (kaff).

Core Idea
Niyyah is the heart's resolve to obey Allah; mere abandonment is not an act of worship unless it becomes active restraint.

This passage opens the discussion of niyyah (intention) under two overarching qawa'id. The author first outlines ten sections that will systematically cover all aspects of niyyah, then provides the linguistic and legal definitions, and finally clarifies an important principle: that intention does not apply to mere abandonment (tark) but only to positive acts, including restraint (kaff) which is considered an act. Understanding this is crucial for distinguishing between valid and invalid intentions in worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ten sections of niyyah
Read the passage and list the ten mabahith (discussions) on niyyah as enumerated by the author.
These sections cover reality, legislation, specification, attributes, sincerity, combination, time, continuity, locus, and conditions.
2
Extract the linguistic definition from al-Qamus
Find the exact Arabic text where niyyah is defined linguistically as 'qasd' (intention) and note the reference to al-Qamus.
Linguistically, niyyah and qasd are synonymous.
3
Extract the legal definition from al-Talwih
Locate the definition from al-Talwih: 'Qasd al-ta'ah wa al-taqarrub ila Allah ta'ala fi ijad al-fi'l'.
This definition restricts niyyah to acts of worship and seeking nearness to Allah.
4
Understand the objection and response on intention in abandonments
The author raises a possible objection: what about intention in leaving something (turuk)? He responds that mere abandonment is not an act of worship because non-existence is not within human power; but when abandonment becomes active restraint (kaff), it is a positive act and requires intention.
This is a key Hanafi principle: intention is only for positive acts.
5
Compare with al-Baydawi's definition
Read the definition from al-Qadi al-Baydawi: intention is the will directed towards the act seeking God's pleasure and fulfilling His command. Note its similarity to al-Talwih.
Al-Baydawi adds an explicit component of seeking God's pleasure (ibtigha' wajh Allah).

Then know that these two qawa'id encompass speech on niyyah, and it has sections: first: in explaining its reality; second: in explaining that for which it is legislated; third: in explaining the specification of the intended (manwi) and its non-specification; fourth: in explaining the engagement with the attribute of the intended from obligatory (fardiyya) and supererogatory (nafliyya) and performance (ada') and make-up (qada'); fifth: in explaining sincerity (ikhlas) in it; sixth: in explaining combining two acts of worship with one intention; seventh: in explaining its time; eighth: in explaining that its continuity is not a condition, and in it is its ruling in every pillar of the acts; ninth: in its place (mahall); tenth: in its conditions. Translation (Urdu): Then know that the discussion of these two qawa'id consists of niyyah, and it has several sections... (Urdu translation of the Arabic list). Explanation: The ten sections of niyyah: ... As for the first: it is in language 'qasd' (intention) as in al-Qamus: 'nawa al-shay'a yanwi niyyatan mushadhdhadatan wa tukhaffafu, fa qasadahu' – end. And in Shari'ah as in al-Talwih: 'Qasd al-ta'ah wa al-taqarrub ila Allah ta'ala fi ijad al-fi'l' – end. And the objection of niyyah in abandonments (al-turuk) does not apply to this definition, because as we have said, one does not seek closeness through abandonment, except when abandonment becomes restraint (kaff) and that is an action, and it is what is commanded in prohibitions, not abandonment in the sense of non-existence; because it is not within the ability of the servant, as in al-Tahrir. And al-Qadi al-Baydawi defined it legally as: 'The intention (irada) directed towards the act seeking the face of Allah and fulfilling His command,' and linguistically as: 'The inclination (inbi'ath) of the heart towards what it sees as conforming to a purpose of bringing benefit or warding off harm, present or future' – end. (Then Urdu translation of the above).
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage is a structured introduction to the topic of niyyah (intention) as it relates to the two foundational qawa'id (maxims) previously discussed. The author first lists ten sections (mabahith) that will cover: (1) the reality of niyyah, (2) its legislation, (3) specification of the intended act, (4) dealing with attributes like obligatory/voluntary, (5) sincerity, (6) combining acts, (7) its time, (8) continuity not being required, (9) its locus, and (10) its conditions. Then he begins the first section: the definition of niyyah. Linguistically, from al-Qamus, it means qasd (intention). Legally, according to al-Talwih, it is the intention of obedience and seeking closeness to Allah in performing an act. The author addresses an objection regarding intention in abandonments (e.g., intending to leave a sin). He explains that mere abandonment (tark) is not an act of worship and cannot be a means of drawing near to Allah unless the abandonment becomes an active restraint (kaff), which is a positive action. This is based on the principle that a person cannot be commanded to do something impossible, and non-existence is not within the servant's power. Al-Qadi al-Baydawi's definition is also provided, which aligns with the Talwih but adds clarity: it is the will directed towards the act seeking God's pleasure and complying with His command, with a linguistic note about the heart's inclination. This passage establishes that niyyah is a heart-based resolve, not a verbal pronouncement, and is essential for distinguishing worship from habit.

Key Terms
نیة (niyyah): Linguistically: qasd (intention). Legally (Talwih): intention of obedience and seeking closeness to Allah in performing an act. Also (Baydawi): will directed towards the act seeking God's pleasure.
قصد (qasd): Purpose or aim; the linguistic meaning of niyyah.
كف (kaff): Active restraint; an action of holding back, considered a positive act in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the definition in al-Talwih, what is niyyah in the Shari'ah?
A) Mere determination in the heart
B) Intention of obedience and seeking closeness to Allah in performing an act
C) Verbal declaration of intent
D) Avoiding harm without any specific purpose

Key Takeaway
Niyyah is the heart's resolve to obey Allah in performing an act of worship; it does not apply to mere abandonment unless that abandonment becomes active restraint (kaff).

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
8 min
Purpose of Niyyah: Distinguishing Ibadaat and Applications
Explains the two purposes of niyyah with examples and the exception of purely distinct acts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim "al-muqsad min al-niyyah tamyiz al-ibadat 'an al-adat" to identify when niyyah is required and when it is not, and construct a fatwa on a related case.

Core Idea
Niyyah separates worship from custom; purely distinct acts need no niyyah.

The Hanafi school emphasizes the pivotal role of niyyah (intention) in transforming ordinary actions into acts of worship. This lesson unpacks a key maxim from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair: the purpose of niyyah is to distinguish worship from customs and to differentiate among various forms of worship. Through practical examples and an important exception, you will learn how intent determines the fiqh ruling of many daily actions—and when niyyah is not required at all.

Guided Path
1
State the Maxim and Its Two Purposes
Read the opening of the passage: the maxim states two purposes of niyyah—tamyiz al-ibadat 'an al-adat (distinguishing worship from custom) and tamyiz ba'd al-ibadat 'an ba'd (distinguishing some acts of worship from others). Commit this to memory.
This maxim is a sub-maxim (dabt) under the major qawida 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'.
2
Work Through the Furuat (Applications)
The passage gives four main examples: refraining from eating (fasting vs. diet), sitting in the mosque (i'tikaf vs. rest), giving wealth (charity vs. gift), and slaughtering (udhiyah vs. food vs. honoring a ruler). For each, ask: what is the same physical act, and how does niyyah change its ruling?
Consider the detailed discussion on slaughtering: honoring vs. hospitality makes a difference.
3
Identify the Exception (Istithna)
The passage then states that acts which are exclusively worship (ma la yakunu illa 'ibadah) and not confused with other acts do not require niyyah. Examples: iman, qira'ah, adhkar, niyyah itself. Understand why no niyyah is needed—there is no possibility of confusion.
This is based on consensus (ijma') as reported by al-Ayni.
4
Apply the Maxim to a New Scenario
Choose a scenario not in the text, e.g., a person takes a walk in a garden. If he intends to reflect on Allah's creation, it becomes worship; if for exercise, it is custom. This reinforces the maxim's scope.

ترجمه: دوسری بحث اس چیز کے بیان میں جس کی وجہ سے وہ مشروع ہوئی فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ مقصود اس سے عبادات کو عادات سے ممتاز کرنا اور بعض عبادات کو بعض سے ممتاز کرنا ہے جیسا کہ نہا یہ اور فتح القدیر میں ہے جیسا کہ مفطرات سے رکھنا کبھی پر ہیز کے طور پر ہوتا ہے کبھی علا جا اور کبھی ضرورت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے۔
تشریح نیت کے متعلق دوسری بحث یہ ہے کہ نیت کے مشروعیت کے دو مقصد ہیں۔ (۱) عبادات کو عادات سے الگ کرنا ۔ (۲) بعض عبادات کو بعض عبادات سے الگ اور ممتاز کرنا۔ اول کی مثال جیسے کھانے پینے اور جماع وغیرہ سے رکنا کبھی پر ہیز اور علاج کے طور پر ہوتا ہے یا ضرورت نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور بھی روزہ رکھنے کی وجہ سے ہوتا ہے ان میں اول صورت کو عادت اور دوسری صورت کو عبادت سے تعبیر کرتے ہیں۔ وَالْجُلُوْسُ فِى الْمَسْجِدِ قَدْ يَكُونُ لِلْإِسْتِرَاحَةِ، وَقَدْ يَكُوْنُ قُرْبَةً كَزَكَاةٍ، أَوْصَدَقَةٍ وَالذَّبْحُ قَدْ يَكُونَ لِلأَكُل، فَيَكُونُ مُبَاحًا أَوْ مَنْدُوبًا، أَوْ لِلْاضْحِيَّةِ، فَيَكُوْنُ عِبَادَةً، أَوْ لِقُدُومٍ أَمِيْرٍ ، فَيَكُوْنُ حَرَامًا، أَوْ كُفْرًا عَلَى قَوْلٍ. ترجمہ: اور مسجد میں بیٹھنا بھی آرام کی نیت سے ہوتا ہے اور کبھی قربت کی غرض سے اور مال کا دینا کبھی ہبہ

۱۴۲
كے طور پر ہوتا ہے یا دنیوی غرض کی وجہ سے اور بھی بطور قربت کے ہوتا ہے جیسے زکوۃ اور صدقہ اور ذبیح بھی کھانے کے لئے ہوتا ہے تو مباح یا مستحب ہوگا یا قربانی کے لئے تو عبادت ہوگا یا کسی امیر کے آنے کی وجہ سے تو حرام ہوگا یا ایک قول کی بنا پر کفر ہوگا۔ تشریح مسجد میں بیٹھنا اگر استراحت کے لئے ہے تو یہ محض ایک عادت ہے اس پر ثواب نہیں لیکن اگر یہی شخص مسجد میں بیٹھتے وقت ثواب کی یا اعتکاف کی نیت کرلے تو عبادت بن جائے گا۔ مال ایک انسان دوسرے انسان کو دیتا ہے تو نیت ہبہ کی ہوتی ہے یا دنیوی غرض مثلا بیج وغیرہ کے طور پر ضرور ما دیتا ہے تو عادت ہے اور بھی صدقہ خیرات کی نیت سے دیتا ہے تو عبادت ہے اور اس صورت میں اجر و ثواب ملے گا، انسان جانور کبھی ضیافت کی نیت سے ذبح کرتا ہے تو مباح ہے اور اگر ولیمہ کے اندر ذبح کیا جائے تو مستحب ہے اور اگر قربانی کی نیت سے کیا جائے تو عبادت ہو جاتا ہے اور اس پر اجر و ثواب مرتب ہوتا ہے۔ اور اگر یہی جانور کسی امیر کی آمد کے موقع پر بغرض تعظیم ذبح کیا جائے تو پھر یہ جانور ما اہل بہ لغیر اللہ میں داخل ہو کر حرام ہو جائے گا اور اگر اس امیر کی اہمیت اس کی نظر میں اللہ سے بھی زیادہ ہے جس کی وجہ سے جانور ذبح کرایا ہے تو یہ صریح کفر ہے علی اختلاف الاقوال۔ واعلم ان المدار على القصد عند ابتداء الذبح فلا يلزم انه لو قدم الضيف غيرها ان لاتحل لانه حين الذبح لم يقصد تعظيمه بل اكرامه بالاكل منها وان قدم اليه غيرها ويظهر ذلك ايضاً فيما لو اضافه امير فذبح عند قدومه فان قصد التعظيم لاتحل وان اضافه بها وان قصد الاكرام تحل وان اطعمه غيرها (شامی زکریاج روص /۴۴۹)
ثُمَّ التَّقَرُّبُ إِلَى اللهِ تَعَالَى يَكُوْنُ بِالْفَرْضِ وَالنَّفْلِ وَالْوَاجِبِ فَشُرِعَتْ لِتَمْيِيزِ بَعْضِهَا عَنْ بَعْضِهَا فَيُفَرَّعُ عَلى ذلِكَ أَنَّ مَالَا يَكُوْنُ إِلَّا عِبَادَةٌ، وَلَا يَلْتَبِسُ بِغَيْرِهِ لَا تُشْتَرَطَ فِيْهِ كَالْإِيْمَانِ بِاللَّهِ تَعَالَى كَمَا قَدَّمْنَاهُ ، وَالْمَعْرِفَةِ، وَالْخَوْفِ، وَالرَّجَاءِ، وَالنِّيَّةِ، وَقِرَاءَةِ الْقُرْآنِ، وَالْأَذْكَارِ لِأَنَّهَا مُتَمَيَّزَةٌ لَا تَلْتَبِسُ بِغَيْرِهَا، وَمَا عَذَا الْإِيْمَانِ لَمْ أَرَاهُ صَرِيحًا وَلكِنَّهُ مُخَرَّجْ عَلَى الْإِيْمَانِ الْمُصَرَّح بِهِ، ثُمَّ رَأَيْتُ إِبْن وَهْبَانَ فِي شَرْحِ الْمَنْظُومَةِ قَالَ: إِنَّ مَالَا يَكُونُ إِلَّا عِبَادَةً لا يَحْتاجُ إلَى اليَّةِ، وَذَكَرَ أَيْضًا : أَنَّ اللَّيَّةَ لَا تَحْتَاجُ إِلَى نِيَّةٍ. وَنَقَلَ الْعَيْنِي فِي شَرْحِ الْبُخَارِي الْإِجَمَاعُ عَلَى أَنَّ التَّلَاوَةَ وَالْأَذْكَارَ وَالْآذَانَ لَا يَحْتَاجُ إِلَى النِّيَّةِ.
ترجمه: پھر تقرب الی اللہ فرض نفل اور واجب سے ہوتا ہے پس وہ مشروع کی گئی ہے بعض کو بعض جدا
Second discussion: concerning the purpose for which it (niyyah) was legislated. They said: its purpose is to distinguish acts of worship from customs and to distinguish some acts of worship from others, as in al-Nihayah and Fath al-Qadir. For example: refraining from invalidators of fasting; it may be for diet (himya), or treatment, or due to lack of need. Translation: The second discussion about the thing for which it was legislated: the jurists say that its purpose is to distinguish acts of worship from customs and to distinguish some acts of worship from others, as in Nihayah and Fath al-Qadir. For example: refraining from invalidators may be for diet, or treatment, or lack of need. Explanation: The second discussion about niyyah is that its legislation has two purposes: (1) To separate acts of worship from customs. (2) To separate some acts of worship from others. Example of the first: refraining from eating, drinking, and intercourse may be for diet and treatment or due to lack of need, and also due to fasting. The first is called custom and the second worship. And sitting in the mosque may be for rest, and it may be for closeness (qurbah). And giving wealth may be as a gift (hibah) or for a worldly purpose, and also as a charitable gift like zakat and sadaqah. And slaughtering may be for eating, so it is permissible or recommended; or for udhiyah, so it is worship; or for the arrival of an amir, so it is haram, or according to one opinion, kufr. Explanation: Sitting in the mosque: if for rest, it is a mere custom with no reward; but if the person intends reward or i'tikaf, it becomes worship. Giving wealth: if intended as a gift or worldly purpose (e.g., gift or loan), it is custom; if intended as charity, it is worship with reward. Slaughtering: if for hospitality, it is permissible; if for a walimah, recommended; if for udhiyah, worship with reward. If slaughtered for the arrival of an amir to honor him, it becomes haram as 'slaughtered for other than Allah', and if the amir's status in his view is greater than Allah's, it is explicit kufr, according to differences of opinion. Know that the basis is the intent at the beginning of slaughter; if the guest brings something else, it does not become unlawful because at the time of slaughter he did not intend to honor him but to honor him by eating from it, even if he brought something else. This also appears in the case where an amir is hosted and he slaughters upon his arrival: if he intends honor (ta'zim), it is not lawful even if he hosts him with it; if he intends hospitality (ikram), it is lawful even if he feeds him something else. (Shami, Zakariya, vol. 3, p. 449). Then, drawing close to Allah is by farḍ, nafl, and wajib, so it (niyyah) was legislated to distinguish some of them from others. On that basis, it is derived that whatever is only worship and is not confused with anything else, niyyah is not required in it, such as belief (iman) in Allah as we have mentioned, and ma'rifah (knowledge of Allah), khawf (fear), raja' (hope), niyyah itself, recitation of Quran, and adhkar (remembrances), because they are distinct and not confused with others. As for what is besides iman, I have not seen it explicitly, but it is derived on the basis of the explicitly mentioned iman. Then I saw Ibn Wahban in Sharh al-Manzumah say: indeed, whatever is only worship does not need niyyah. And he also mentioned that niyyah does not need a niyyah. Al-Ayni in Sharh al-Bukhari narrated consensus that recitation (tilawah), adhkar, and adhan do not need niyyah. Translation: Then drawing close to Allah is by farḍ, nafl, and wajib; thus it was legislated to distinguish some from others.
Source pages p. 141

Commentary
This passage is a qawida (maxim) with its furuat (applications). It states the two purposes of niyyah: (1) tamyiz al-ibadat 'an al-adat (distinguishing worship from custom), and (2) tamyiz ba'd al-ibadat 'an ba'd (distinguishing some acts of worship from others). The text provides multiple examples: refraining from eating (could be diet or fasting), sitting in a mosque (rest vs. i'tikaf), giving wealth (gift vs. charity), slaughtering (food vs. udhiyah vs. honoring a ruler). Each example shows that the same physical act becomes worship or custom based on niyyah. A detailed discussion follows on slaughtering, citing Shami, emphasizing that the decisive factor is the intent at the commencement of slaughter. If the intent was to honor (ta'zim) a ruler, it is haram; if to show hospitality (ikram), it is halal. Finally, the passage states a furu' derived from the maxim: acts that are purely worship and not confused with other acts do not require niyyah. Examples include iman, ma'rifah, khawf, raja', niyyah itself, qira'ah, adhkar, and adhan. This is based on consensus as reported by al-Ayni. This is a critical refinement: the requirement of niyyah is not universal; it applies only where confusion exists.

Key Terms
تمييز العبادات من العادات (tamyiz al-ibadat 'an al-adat): The function of niyyah to separate acts done with worship intent from those done out of habit or worldly purposes.
ما لا يكون إلا عبادة (ma la yakunu illa 'ibadah): An act that is inherently and exclusively worship, with no possibility of being a mere custom; these do not require niyyah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, which of the following acts does NOT require niyyah?
A) Fasting on the day of Ashura (intending to fast the whole day)
B) Reciting the Quran in prayer or at other times
C) Giving charity to a poor person with the intent to help
D) Sitting in the mosque for i'tikaf for ten days

Key Takeaway
Niyyah's primary purpose is to differentiate worship from custom; however, acts that are inherently distinct as worship (like Quran recitation) require no niyyah.

The Rule of Ta'yin: When Specification is Necessary in Worship
Explaining when specification of the intended worship is necessary

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'When time is a container for worship, specification is necessary' to distinguish between cases requiring ta'yin and those exempted, and construct a fatwa using this qawida.

Core Idea
Specification is necessary when time can hold multiple acts; otherwise not.

In this passage, the author presents a key Hanafi maxim concerning when specification (ta'yin) of the intended worship is required. The maxim states that if the time allotted for an act can also accommodate other similar acts, then you must specify which act you are performing. This principle is derived from the prophetic hadith 'Actions are by intentions' and is applied primarily to the five daily prayers, where the times overlap with possibilities for make‑up or voluntary prayers. However, the maxim includes two important exceptions: when the time is limited (mu'addi) such that only one act fits, or when the time is problematic (mushkil) and the specification becomes unclear. Understanding this rule is essential for a mufti to advise on the validity of intentions in various scenarios.

Guided Path
1
State the Maxim
Begin by memorizing the qawida: 'When the time is a container for the worship, specification is necessary.' Understand its scope: it applies mainly to salah but also to other flexible acts.
The maxim is a minor (sughra) universal rule within the Hanafi qawaid framework.
2
Identify the Three Time Scenarios
Recognize the three categories mentioned: zarf (container) – time remains after the act; mu'addi (limited) – time only suffices for one act; mushkil (problematic) – time is unclear. Specification is only required in the first.
These categories determine when ta'yin is wajib, mustahabb, or not needed.
3
Apply the Maxim to a Concrete Case
Work through the example in the text: the Zuhr prayer. If the time is still present and you intend 'Zuhr of today', it is valid even if time later exits. If you only intend 'Zuhr' and the time exits, it may not suffice.
The distinction hinges on linking the intention to a specific day or to the time slot.
4
Note the Exceptions (Istithna'at)
Identify the two exceptions: (1) when the time is limited (mu'addi) – no ambiguity; (2) when the time is problematic (mushkil) – the principle of certainty (al-yaqin la yazul bi al-shakk) applies.
These exceptions show the maxim is not absolute; it is restricted by other qawaid.
5
Connect to the Hadith and Usul
The maxim is based on the hadith 'Innama al-a'malu bi al-niyyat.' Understand how this hadith supports the need for ta'yin when actions are identical in form.
This is a dalil naqli (textual evidence) that the Hanafi school uses to establish the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما الثالث: في بيان تعيين المنوى وعدمه، الأصل عندنا أنَّ المنوى إما أن يكون من العبادات أولا، فإن كان عبادة، فإن كان وقتها ظرفًا للمنوى بمعنى أنه يسعه وغيره فلابد من التعيين كالصلاة كأن ينوى الظهر، فإن قرنه باليوم كظهر اليوم صح، وإن خرج الوقت أو بالوقت ولم يكن خرج الوقت، فإن خرج ونسبة لا يجزئه في الصحيح وفرض الوقت كظهر الوقت. ترجمه: تیسری بحث منوی کی تعیین اور عدم تعیین کے بیان میں ضابطہ ہمارے نزدیک یہ ہے کہ منوی نیت کی گئی یا تو عبادات کے قبیل سے ہو گی یا نہیں اگر عبادت ہے تو اس کا وقت ظرف ہو منوی کے لئے بمعنی کہ وہ اس کا اور اس کے علاوہ کی گنجائش رکھتا ہو تو تعیین ضروری ہے جیسے نماز اس طور پر نیت ظہر کرے پس اگر اس کو یوم کے ساتھ ملایا جیسے آج کی ظہر تو صحیح ہے اگر چہ وقت نکل جائے یا وقت کے ساتھ ملایا حال یہ کہ وقت نہ نکلنا ہو وقت نکل گیا اور وہ اسے بھول گیا تو صحیح قول کے بموجب اس کو کافی نہ ہوگی اور فرض وقت ظہر کے وقت کی ظہر ہے۔ تشریح: اس تیسری بحث میں مصنف فرما رہے ہیں کہ کونسی عبادات میں تعیین ضروری ہے اور کونسی میں نہیں پس جس عبادت کو آپ ادا کرنے جارہے ہیں اس کی تین صورتیں ہیں وقت اس عبادت کے لئے ظرف ہے یا معدی ہے یا مشکل ہے۔ ظرف کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ وہ وقت اس فرض کی ادائیگی کے بعد بھی باقی رہے اور اس جیسی رویہ عبادت بھی ادا کی جا سکے جیسے نماز کے اوقات نماز کے لئے ظرف ہیں۔ لہذا ایسی عبادات کی ادائیگی کے لئے تعیین ضروری ہے مثلا یہ کہئے کہ میں ظہر کی نماز پڑھ رہا ہوں یا عصر کی یا مغرب کی یا عشاء کی یا فجر کی کیونکہ نبی اکرم صلی اللہ علیہ وسلم نے ارشاد فرمایا " لكل امرئ مانوی " ہر آدمی کے لئے وہی ہے جس کی اس نے نیت کی اس سے مدنی ظاہر ہے کہ فرائض کی ادائیگی کے لئے تعیین ضروری ہے اس لئے کہ ظہر اور عصر مثالا صورت اور فعل کے اعتبار سے ایک ہیں، ان میں تمیز تعیین کے ذریعہ ہی ہو سکتی ہے۔
Third: On specifying the intended worship and not specifying. The principle with us is that the intended thing is either from worship or not. If it is worship, and its time is a container for the intended, meaning it accommodates it and other acts, then specification is necessary, like prayer: one must intend Zuhr. If he links it to the day, like 'Zuhr of today', it is valid even if the time exits. If he links it to the time and the time has not exited, but if it exits and he forgets, then according to the correct view it does not suffice him. And the obligatory time is like the time of Zuhr for Zuhr. Translation: Third discussion: On specifying and not specifying the intended. The rule with us is that the intended thing, which is intended, is either from the category of worship or not. If it is worship, and its time is a container for the intended, meaning it can accommodate it and other than it, then specification is necessary, like prayer: one should intend Zuhr. So if he couples it with the day, like 'Zuhr of today', it is valid even if the time exits. If he couples it with the time and the time has not exited, but then the time exits and he forgets, then according to the correct view it does not suffice him. And the obligatory time is like Zuhr for the time of Zuhr. Explanation: In this third discussion, the author states which acts require specification and which do not. The act to be performed has three possibilities: the time is a container (zarf) for that act, or it is limited (mu'addi), or problematic (mushkil). Container means the time remains after the act, accommodating another similar act, like prayer times. Therefore, for such acts, specification is necessary: e.g., one must say 'I am praying Zuhr' or 'Asr' etc., because the Prophet (peace be upon him) said, 'Every man will have what he intended.' Hence, specification is necessary for obligatory acts because Zuhr and Asr are identical in form and action; distinction is only possible through specification.
Source pages p. 144

Commentary
This passage presents a Hanafi rule regarding specification (ta'yin) in worship. When a time period can accommodate multiple acts of the same type (e.g., the Zuhr time can contain an obligatory Zuhr and also a makeup or voluntary prayer), the worshipper must specify which act he is performing. This is based on the hadith 'Actions are by intentions.' The text distinguishes three scenarios: the time is a container (zarf), limited (mu'addi), or problematic (mushkil). In the first case, specification is necessary. The author illustrates with the example of prayer: if one intends 'Zuhr of today' it is valid even if the time passes; but if one merely intends 'Zuhr' and the time expires, the prayer may not suffice. The commentary explains that for obligatory prayers, which are identical in form, specification is essential.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specifying the exact worship (e.g., which prayer) in the intention
ظرف (zarf): A time that accommodates the act and other similar acts
معدي (mu'addi): Limited time – only sufficient for one act, no room for another
مشكل (mushkil): Problematic time – uncertain or ambiguous

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is specification (ta'yin) required in worship according to this passage?
A) When the time is limited and cannot accommodate another act
B) When the time is a container that can hold multiple similar acts
C) When the act is purely custom with no worship
D) Always, without exception

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'When the time is a container for worship, specification is necessary' governs ta'yin in worship, with exceptions for limited and problematic times.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
