Time as Container vs. Standard for Intention
Explaining the rule of time as container vs. standard for intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida distinguishing 'container' (zarf) vs 'standard' (mi‘yār) time to determine whether specific intention (ta‘yīn) is required, and evaluate the dispute regarding Jumu‘ah as substitute.

Core Idea
If time can accommodate another similar act, specify intention; if not, any intention suffices.

This lesson unpacks a fundamental Hanafi principle that governs intention in worship: the distinction between time as a container (zarf) and time as a standard (mi‘yār). You will see how this simple binary determines whether you must specify which act you intend, and how it applies to prayer, fasting, Hajj, and the debated case of Friday prayer.

Guided Path
1
State the qawida and its two conditions
Read the Arabic qawida: 'If the time is a container that can accommodate another like it, determination (ta‘yīn) is a condition; if it is a standard that cannot accommodate another, determination is not a condition.' Identify the two types: zarf and mi‘yār.
Memorize the qawida text; it is a wusta rank maxim.
2
Identify the time type for a given act
For each act of worship (Zuhr prayer, Ramadan fast, Hajj), determine whether its time can accommodate another act of the same type. If yes (e.g., Zuhr time can hold a later Zuhr? Actually one Zuhr per day, but the principle considers the day as container for multiple prayers via relation to day), it is zarf; if no (e.g., a day of Ramadan cannot hold two fasts), it is mi‘yār.
For Zuhr, the time is considered zarf because one can relate the prayer to the specific day; the day can hold multiple prayers in theory.
3
Apply the rule
If the time is zarf, specific intention (ta‘yīn) is required: e.g., intending 'today's Zuhr'. If the time is mi‘yār, any intention suffices: e.g., intending nafl fast on a Ramadan day results in Ramadan fast.
The rule is reversed from common intuition: container requires specification, standard does not.
4
Handle mixed times (e.g., Hajj)
Hajj's time (months of Hajj) has both aspects: it can only accommodate one Hajj (mi‘yār), but time remains after performance (zarf). The rule: absolute intention suffices because the mi‘yār aspect overrides the zarf aspect in determining the requirement of ta‘yīn.
Mixed times follow the less restrictive ruling (mi‘yār side).
5
Analyze the Jumu‘ah dispute
Consider the disagreement among Hanafi imams: Is Jumu‘ah a substitute (badal) for Zuhr or an original obligation? According to the qawida, if Jumu‘ah time is zarf (can accommodate both Jumu‘ah and Zuhr? Actually the dispute is about whether intending Zuhr suffices for Jumu‘ah. The preferred view (asahh) allows it, treating Jumu‘ah as a substitute.
This is an intra-madhhab dispute with practical consequence: if one intends Zuhr on Friday, his prayer is valid according to Shaykhayn and the asahh view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
منا کوئی آدمی ظہر کی نماز پڑھ رہا ہے تو دن کی طرف نسبت کر دینا ہی کافی ہے کہ میں آج کی ظہر پڑھ رہا ہوں تو یہ نسبت اس کے لئے کافی ہو گی خواہ وہ وقت میں نماز ادا کرے یا وقت نکل جانے کے بعد لیکن اگر گذشته ایم میں سے کسی دن کی عصر کی نماز پڑھے اور ظہر الیوم کی نیت کرے تو اسے آج کی عصر کہنا درست نہ ہو گا اس لئے یہ نیت درست نہ ہوگی۔ اور اگر اس نے ظہر کی نسبت وقت کی طرف کی تو اگر وقت میں ہی نماز ادا کر لی تو نماز ہو جائے گی اور اگر وقت ظہر کی نیت تو کی لیکن ظہر کا وقت نکل چکا اور وہ اسے بھول گیا کہ وقت نکل چکا ہے تو پھر اس کی ظہر کی نماز صحیح نہ ہوگی۔ فرض الوقت: اگر کسی نے وقت ظہر کہا یا وقت فرض کہا تو دونوں کا ماحصل ایک ہی ہے لہذا وقت میں نماز ادا کر صحیح ہو جائے گا اور اگر وقت فعل عبادت کے لئے معیار ہے۔ معیار ہونے کا مطلب یہ ہے کہ فعل عبادت وقت کو گھیر لے اور اس عبادت کے بعد وقت باقی نہ بچے کہ اس جیسی دوسری عبادت ادا کر سکے تو اس میں تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے جیسے رمضان کا مہینہ رمضان کے روزوں کے لئے معیار ہے تو اس میں تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے لہذا رمضان میں نفلی روزہ کی نیت کر لے تو نفلی روزہ نہ ہوگا بلکہ رمضان ہی کا روزہ ہوگا۔ اور اگر فعل عبادت کے لئے وقت مشکل ہو یعنی پورے وقت میں ایک ہی عبادت ادا کی جائے لیکن فعلِ اد وقت کا احاطہ نہ کرے بلکہ فعل عبادت کی ادائیگی کے بعد وقت بچ جائے ، جیسے حج کا وقت حج کے لئے مشکل ہے۔ کیونکہ اشہر حج میں صرف ایک ہی حج ادا کر سکتا ہے زیادہ نہیں اس اعتبار سے معیار ہے اور حج ادا کرنے کے بعد بھی وقت بچا رہتا ہے اس اعتبار سے ظرف ہے تو چونکہ حج کے وقت میں دونوں جہتیں ہیں اس لئے حج کے وقت کو فعل حج کے لئے مشکل قرار دیا گیا ہے اور جب یہ وقت حج کے لئے معیار بھی ہے تو مطلق حج کی نیت سے حج ادا ہو جائے گا تعین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے اور حج کا وقت فعل حج کے لئے ظرف بھی ہے جس طرح نماز ادا کرنے کے بعد وقت بیچ جاتا ہے اسی طرح افعال حج کے بعد وقت بچ جاتا ہے۔
إِلَّا فِي الْجُمُعَةِ فَإِنَّهَا بَدَّلْ لَا أَصْل إِلَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ إِعْتِقَادُهُ أَنَّهَا فَرْضُ الْوَقْتِ، فَإِنَّ نَوَىٰ الظهر لَا غَيْرَ ، أَخْتلِف فِيهِ وَالأَصْحُ الجَوَاز. :ترجمه مگر جمعہ میں اس لئے کہ وہ بدل ہے اصل نہیں مگر یہ کہ اس کا اعتقاد ہو کہ وہی فرض وقت ہے پس اگر ظہر کی نیت کی نہ کہ اس کے علاوہ کی تو اس میں اختلاف ہے اور جواز اصح ہے۔
تشریح: جمعہ کے دن جمعہ اصل ہے یا بدل ہے؟ شیخین علیہم الرحمہ کے نزدیک جمعہ کے دن جمعہ بدل ہے اور ظیر اصل ہے البتہ جمعہ ادا کرنے کی وجہ سے ظہر ذمہ سے ساقط ہو جائے گی ، علامہ حصکفی اور علامہ ابن عابدین کی بھی سیکی رائے ہے، امام محمد کے نزدیک جمعہ کے روز جمعہ ہی اصل ہے البتہ ظہر کی ادائیگی سے جمعہ کو ساقط کیا جاسکتا ہے امام اقر کے نزدیک جمعہ ہی اصل ہے اور ظہر جمعہ کے فوت ہونے کی صورت میں بدل بن سکتا ہے بعض فقہاء کے نزدیک
ور ٹرک میں بہتہ جمعہ فرض ہے جس کو شروع کر دے وہی فرض ہے۔ علامہ حموی کا رجحان اس طرف ہے کہ جمعہ میں ہے اور خبر دی ہے۔ الا بھی المحمومة سے پہلے مصنف نے فرمایا تھا فرض الوقت اور وقت الظہر ایک ہی حکم میں ہے لیکن اگر کسی نے جوری که زمین فرغل وقت کمدی تو شیخین کے نزدیک جمعہ کے دن فرض الوقت کی نیت درست ہو جائے گی کیونکہ ان کے ازاد یک جمعہ کے دن جمعے کی نماز ہی اصل ہے اور ظہر جمعہ فوت ہونے کے بعد بدل بن سکتی ہے۔ هران موی ر اگر کسی نے جمعہ کی نماز ظہر کی نیت سے ادا کی تو شیخین کے نزدیک ادا ہو جائے گی کیونکہ ان کا کے ایک جمعہ کے دن ظہری اصل ہے اور اصل کی نیت سے بدل ادا ہو جاتا ہے البتہ امام زفر کے نزدیک جمعہ کے دن جلدی میں ہے بدل نہیں ہے اس لئے ظہر کی نیت سے جمعہ ادا نہ ہوگا کیونکہ بدل کی نیت سے اصل ادا نہیں ہوتا ہے۔ عد جنب کتاب علیہ الرحمہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اصبح یہ ہے کہ نماز جمعہ ظہر کی نیت سے بھی ادا کر لی تو نماز جمعہ صیح ہو جائے گی مفصل جمعہ کی نماز کو جمعہ کی ہی نیت سے ادا کرنا چاہئے۔
وَإِن كَانَ وَقْتُهَا مِعْيَاراً لَهَا بِمَعْنِى أَنَّهُ لَا يَسَعُ غَيْرَهَا كَالصَّوْمِ فِي يَوْمٍ رَمَضَانَ، فَإِنَّ التَّعْمِينَ لَيْسَ بِشَرْطٍ إِن كَانَ الصَّائِمُ صَحِيحاً مُقِيماً ، فَيَصِحُ بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ، وَنِيَّةِ النَّفْلِ وَوَاجِبِ آخر، لأنَّ التَّغيينَ فِى الْمُتَعيَّن لغو.
ترجمہ: اور اگر اس کا وقت اس کے لئے معیار ہو بائیں معنی کہ اس کے علاوہ کی گنجائش نہ رکھتا ہو جیسے رمضان کے دن میں روز ور رکھنا تو عین ضروری نہیں ہے، اگر روزہ رکھنے والا تندرست اور مقیم ہو ، تو مطلق نیست نفل کی نیت اور واجب آخر کی نیت سے روز ہ صحیح ہو جائے گا اس لئے کہ متعین میں تعیین لغو ہے۔
From: 'If a person is performing Zuhr prayer, then relating it to the day is sufficient...' To: 'Translation: And if its time is a standard for it, meaning it cannot accommodate another like it, such as fasting on a day of Ramadan, then determination is not a condition if the fasting person is healthy and resident; so it is valid with absolute intention, intention of supererogatory, and intention of another obligatory, because determination in the determinate is futile.'
Source pages p. 145

Commentary
This passage is a legal principle (qā‘idah) regarding the requirement of specific intention (ta‘yīn) in acts of worship. It distinguishes between two types of time: container (zarf) and standard (mi‘yār). If the time can accommodate another similar act (container), specific intention is needed; if it cannot (standard), any intention suffices. The author provides examples: Zuhr prayer (time is container, so one must specify which day's Zuhr), Ramadan fast (time is standard, so any intention suffices). For Hajj, the time has both aspects, so absolute intention suffices. The passage then discusses the Friday (Jumu‘ah) prayer: according to Shaykhayn (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), Jumu‘ah is a substitute (badal) for Zuhr, so one can intend Zuhr and it counts; Imam Muhammad says Jumu‘ah is the original; Imam Zufar maintains it is only Jumu‘ah, so intending Zuhr does not count. The preferred view (asahh) is that it is permissible. Finally, the Arabic quote and translation reiterate the rule for fasting.

Key Terms
مِعْيَار (mi‘yār): Time that can only accommodate one specific act of worship and no other of the same type.
ظَرْف (ẓarf): Time that can accommodate more than one act of the same type, thus requiring specific intention.
تَعْيِين (ta‘yīn): Specifying which particular act of worship one intends, e.g., 'Zuhr of today'.
بَدَل (badal): A substitute act of worship that takes the place of the original one, like Jumu‘ah for Zuhr.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A person fasts on a day of Ramadan with the intention of a nafl fast. According to the Hanafi principle, what is the ruling?
A) The fast is not valid because it must be specifically intended as Ramadan.
B) The fast is valid as a Ramadan fast because the day is a standard (mi‘yār) and any intention suffices.
C) The fast is valid only if he later changes his intention to Ramadan.
D) The fast is valid as a nafl fast only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi qawida on time as container vs. standard is a powerful tool: if time can accommodate another like it, specify; if not, any intention works.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
6 min
The Qawida: Specification (Ta'yin) Is Not Dropped by Narrow Time
Establishing the rule that specification of intention is required and not waived by narrow time.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qawida 'لا يسقط التعيين بضيق الوقت' to determine that specification of intention remains required even in constrained time, and distinguish the ruling for ada (action-based) vs. qada (verbal-based) specification.

Core Idea
Specification remains needed even when only one act fits because performing another act, though sinful, is still legally possible.

The Hanafi school rules that the obligation to specify which worship one intends is not dropped simply because time is too short for more than one act. This lesson unpacks the reasoning behind this qawida, showing how the mere possibility of performing a different act—even if forbidden—keeps the requirement alive. We'll explore its application in prayer timings, oath expiation, and the essential contrast between on-time and make-up acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the qawida and its plain meaning
Locate the maxim 'لا يسقط التعيين بضيق الوقت' and state its basic meaning: specification is not waived by narrowness of time.
This is a sub-maxim (dabt) restricting the broader principle that time is a vessel for worship.
2
Understand the rationale (ta'lil)
The text explains that even in a narrow time, one could theoretically perform a different prayer (e.g., a nafl), though it would be sinful. The existence of that option keeps specification necessary.
The key proof: 'لانه لو شرع فيه متنفلاً صح وان كان حراماً'
3
Apply the qawida to furuat
Work through the cases: (1) narrow time for Zuhr, (2) verbal specification of a time part, (3) verbal specification of expiation type. In all cases, specification is required until action.
The furuat are given in the source: verbal specification alone does not bind.
4
Identify the istithna' (exception)
For qada (make-up) acts, specification is still necessary but verbal specification alone suffices. This is because the time is no longer a vessel; the act must be designated by intention only.
The text states: 'وَأَمَّا فِي الْقَضَاءِ: فَلَابُدَّ مِنَ التَّعْيِينِ صَلَاةً، أَوْ صَوْماً، أَوْ حَجًّا'

Source Text

في هامش الحسامي ص (27) ولا يقع التعيين : نماز كا وقت نماز كے لئے ظرف ہے اس لئے اس ميں وقتیہ نماز كے علاوہ دوسري نمازيں بھي ادا كي جاسكتي ہيں اس لئے تعيين صلوۃ ضروري ہے ليكن اگر وقت تنگ ہو جائے مثلاً ظہر كي نماز كا وقت اتنا تنگ ہو گيا كہ اس ميں صرف ظہر كي نماز ہي پڑھي جاسكتي ہے تو اس ميں تعيين صلوۃ كي ضرورت باقي نہيں رہني چاہئے حالانكہ آپ ايسي صورت حال ميں بھي تعيين صلوٰۃ كو ضروري قرار ديتے ہيں نماز بھي پڑھي جاسكتي ہے (اگرچہ حرام ہے) تو تعيين صلوۃ كي ضرورت باقي رہي۔ ولابد من التعيين وقال الشامي تحته وفى الاشباه ولا يسقط التعيين بضيق الوقت لانه لو شرع فيه متنفلاً صح وان كان حراماً (شامي كراچي ج ۷اص /۴۱۸) وَلَا يَتَعَيَّنُ جُزْءٌ مِنْ أَجْزَاءِ الْوَقْتِ بِتَعْيِينِ الْعَبْدِ قَوْلًا وَإِنَّمَا يَتَعَيَّنُ بِفِعْلِهِ كَالْحَانِثِ فِي الْيَمِيْن لَا يَتَعَيَّنُ وَاحِدٌ مِّنْ خِصَالِ الْكَفَّارَةِ إِلَّا فِي ضِمْنِ فِعْلِهِ، هَذَا فِي الْآدَاءِ . ترجمہ: اور وقت کے اجزاء میں سے کوئی جز بندہ کے قول سے متعین کرنے سے متعین نہیں ہوتا اور صرف اس کے فعل سے متعین ہوتا ہے جیسے قسم میں حانث ہونے والا کفارہ کے انواع میں سے کوئی ایک متعین نہیں ہوتی مگر اس کے فعل کے ضمن میں ، یہ اداء میں ہے۔ تشریح : اگر کوئی وقت کو قول تعیین کرے اور عملاً تعیین نہ کرے تو اس کی اس تعیین کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا بلکہ فعلی تعین ضروری ہے جیسے کوئی شخص قسم میں حانث ہو گیا اور اس میں کفارہ کے طور پر تین چیزیں ہیں جس میں حانث ہونے والے کو اختیار ہے۔ (۱) دس مسکینوں کو کھانا کھلانا (۲) انہیں پوشاک پہنانا (۳) ایک غلام آزاد کرنا تو اب اگر کوئی زبانی طور پران میں سے ایک کی تعیین کر دیتا ہے تو اس کی اس قولی تعیین کا اعتبار نہ ہوگا جب تک وہ اپنے فعل سے تعین نہ کر دے یعنی ان تین میں سے ایک کو انجام نہ دیدے، یا جیسے کوئی آدمی زبان سے یہ طے کر دے کہ مجھے ظہر کی نماز تین بجے پڑھنی ہے تو صرف زبان ہلانے سے تعین نہ ہوگی جب تک کہ نماز شروع نہ کر دے لیکن یہ تفصیل اداء میں ہے اور اگر عبادات قضا ہوں تو ان میں تعیین قولاً ہی ضروری ہے۔ وَأَمَّا فِي الْقَضَاءِ: فَلَابُدَّ مِنَ التَّعْيِينِ صَلَاةً، أَوْ صَوْماً، أَوْ حَجًّا . ترجمہ : اور بہر حال قضا میں تو تعیین ضروری ہے خواہ نماز ہو یا روزہ یا حج ۔ تشریح : قضا خواہ نماز ہو یا روزہ یا حج ہر ایک میں تعیین ضروری ہے۔ علامہ حموی اس پر اعتراض کرتے ہیں کہ تعیین جیسے قضا میں ضروری ہے ایسے ہی ادا میں بھی تعیین ضروری ہے جیسا
In the margin of al-Hasami p.27: 'Specification does not occur: The time of prayer is a vessel for prayer, therefore other prayers besides the time-based prayer can also be performed in it, so specification of the prayer is necessary. But if the time becomes narrow, e.g., the time of Zuhr becomes so narrow that only the Zuhr prayer can be prayed, then specification should not remain necessary. However, you (the Hanafis) still consider specification necessary in such a situation. Why? The answer: The reason is that in a narrow time, although it is not permissible to pray another prayer besides the time-based prayer, if someone does start (a nafl), it is valid. Therefore, since other prayers can still be performed (even if prohibited), specification remains necessary.' And it is necessary to specify. And al-Shami said underneath: 'In al-Ashbah: Specification is not dropped due to narrowness of time, because if one starts a nafl prayer in it, it is valid though prohibited.' (Shami Karachi vol.7 p.418) And the text: 'And no part of the parts of time becomes specified by the servant's verbal specification; rather it becomes specified only by his action, like the one who breaks his oath does not specify one of the types of expiation except within his action. This is in performance (ada).' Translation: And no part of the parts of time becomes specified by the servant's verbal specification; rather it becomes specified only by his action, like the one who breaks an oath does not specify one of the types of expiation except within his action. This is in ada. Commentary: If someone verbally specifies a time but does not practically specify, then his verbal specification is not considered, rather practical specification is necessary. For example, if someone breaks an oath and has three options: feed ten poor, clothe them, or free a slave. If he verbally specifies one of them, it is not binding until he acts upon it. Or like someone says, 'I will pray Zuhr at three o'clock,' the mere utterance does not specify until he actually begins the prayer. But this detail is in ada. For qada (make-up) acts of worship, verbal specification alone is sufficient. And as for qada: specification is necessary, whether prayer, fasting, or Hajj. Translation: And in qada, specification is necessary, whether prayer, fasting, or Hajj. Commentary: In qada, whether prayer, fasting, or Hajj, specification is necessary. Allama al-Hamawi objects that just as specification is necessary in qada, so too it should be necessary in ada, as it is.
Source pages p. 150

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule that specification (ta'yin) of intention is not dropped even when the time for an obligatory prayer becomes very narrow. The margin note poses a challenge: if the time is so tight that only one prayer fits, why is specification still needed? The answer is that even in a narrow time, it is legally possible (though sinful) to start a nafl prayer; therefore, the possibility remains, so specification is required. The rule from al-Ashbah is cited: 'Specification is not dropped due to narrowness of time, because if one starts a nafl in it, it is valid though prohibited.' This demonstrates that the existence of the option (even if sinful) is the basis for requiring specification. The passage then derives a related principle: verbal specification alone does not cause a specific part of time (or type of expiation) to be fixed; it is only fixed by action. This is illustrated with the example of expiation for breaking an oath: one may verbally choose one type, but it is not binding until one actually performs that type. Similarly, for ada (on-time performance) of prayers, merely saying 'I will pray at 3' does not specify; actual commencement does. For qada (make-up), however, verbal specification alone is sufficient because the time is not a vessel for other acts. The passage notes an objection by Allama al-Hamawi that specification should be necessary in ada as well, but the Hanafi position maintains the distinction.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yīn): The specification of which particular worship (e.g., which prayer) one intends, or which specific action (e.g., which time slot) one is performing.
ضيق الوقت (ḍīq al-waqt): The constriction of the time window such that only one obligatory worship can physically fit.
اداء (adā'): Performance of an act of worship within its prescribed time.
قضاء (qaḍā'): Performance of an act of worship after its prescribed time has passed (make-up).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does specification remain necessary even when the time for a particular prayer is extremely short?
A) Because time is always a measure for salah.
B) Because it is legally possible to start a nafl prayer in that time, even if sinful.
C) Because the intention must be renewed every moment.
D) Because the time is considered purely ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
Specification of intention is not waived by time constraints; it remains mandatory because the option to perform a different act (even if impermissible) continues to exist.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

Tayammum: No Need to Specify Between Hadath and Janaba
Ruling on specification for tayammum regarding different states of impurity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that tayammum does not require specification of impurity type, and evaluate the counter-argument of al-Khassaf.

Core Idea
Tayammum is one purification for both minor and major impurity; intention distinguishes uses, not types.

Tayammum is a substitute for both wudu and ghusl when water is unavailable. A key question arises: must one specify which impurity he intends to remove? The Hanafi school holds that specification is not required, based on the nature of tayammum as a single purification method. This lesson examines the ruling, its proof, and a notable disagreement.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Identify the Hanafi position: tayammum does not require distinguishing between hadath (minor impurity) and janaba (major impurity).
This is the core ruling of the passage.
2
Identify the proof
The proof is that tayammum occurs in one manner for both impurities; it is a single species of purification.
The text says 'li-annahu yaqa'u lahumaa 'alaa sifatin waahidah'.
3
Understand the counter-argument
Al-Khassaf argued that specification is needed, analogizing to obligatory prayer where different intentions matter. The Hanafi response refutes this analogy because prayer has multiple species, unlike tayammum.
The analogy is rejected because tayammum is unitary.
4
Apply the rule
Conclude that any act requiring purity (prayer, touching Quran, etc.) is valid with tayammum, regardless of the original impurity or the specific intention of the performer.
The text gives the example of a junub intending wudu – it is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَقَالُوا : فِي التَّيَمُّمِ لَا يَجِبُ التَّمْيِيزِ بَيْنَ الْحَدَثِ وَالْجَنَابَةِ حَتَّى لَوْ تَيَمَّمَ الْجُنُبُ يُرِيدُ بِهِ الْوُضُوْءُ جَازَ خِلَافَاً لِلْخَصَّافِ لِكَوْنِهِ يَقَعُ لَهُمَا عَلَى صِفَةِ وَاحِدَةٍ، فَيُمَيَّزُ بِالنِّيَّةِ كَالصَّلَاةِ الْمَفْرُوضَةِ، قَالُوا: وَلَيْسَ بِصَحِيح؛ لأنَّ الحَاجَةَ إِلَيْهَا لِبَقَعَ طَهَارَةً، وَإِذَا وَقَعَ طَهَارَة جَازَ أَنْ يُؤدِّيَ بِهِ مَا شَاءَ لأَنَّ الشَّرُوْطَ يُرَاعِي وُجُوْدُهَا لَا غَيْرَ، أَلَا تَرَىٰ أَنَّهُ لَوْ تَيَمَّمَ الرَّجُلُ جَازَ لَهُ أَنْ يُصَلَّى بِهِ غَيْرَهُ.
And they said: Concerning tayammum, distinction between hadath (minor impurity) and janaba (major impurity) is not obligatory, so if a junub person performs tayammum intending wudu by it, it is permissible, contrary to al-Khassaf, because it occurs for both in the same manner, so it is distinguished by intention like the obligatory prayer. They said: And this is not correct, because the need for it is for purification, and when it occurs as purification, it becomes permissible to perform with it whatever he wishes, because the conditions are observed for their existence only. Do you not see that if a man performs tayammum, it is permissible for him to pray with it for another?
Source pages p. 154

Commentary
This passage discusses the rule regarding tayammum and whether one must specify between minor impurity (hadath) and major impurity (janaba) when performing it. The Hanafi position is that specification is not required because tayammum serves as a single type of purification for both. Even if a junub person intends wudu, it is valid because the essence of tayammum is purification, and once purification is achieved, one can perform any act requiring purity. Al-Khassaf disagreed, but his view is considered incorrect. The analogy with obligatory prayer is rejected because tayammum, unlike prayer, does not involve multiple species; it is a single purification method.

Key Terms
حدث (hadath): Minor impurity, e.g., after using the toilet or passing wind, requiring wudu.
جنابة (janaba): Major impurity requiring ghusl.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling if a person in major impurity (janaba) performs tayammum intending wudu?
A) Invalid because wrong intention.
B) Valid, and he may perform any act requiring purity.
C) Valid only for acts that require wudu, not ghusl.
D) Invalid unless he repeats with intention of janaba.

Key Takeaway
Tayammum is a single purification that does not require distinguishing between hadath and janaba; intention for purification suffices.

Principle: Specification is for Distinguishing Types
Statement of a qawida with definitions of jins and naw'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the qawida 'al-ta'yin li-tamyiz al-ajnas' and apply it to determine when specification of intention is required in worship.

Core Idea
Specification is needed only when an act falls under a broad type (jins) with different subtypes (naw').

The author sets down a key rule to guide when a worshipper must specify their intention (ta'yin) and when a general intention suffices. To apply this rule, you first need to understand the distinction between jins and naw' as used by Hanafi jurists. This lesson will anchor that distinction and the qawida itself.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the qawida text
Commit the Arabic wording 'التعيين لتمييز الأجناس' to memory. This is the central rule.
2
Understand jins and naw'
Jins is a universal category with varying rulings/purposes (e.g., 'human'). Naw' is a universal where all individuals share the same ruling (e.g., 'man'). Grasp the difference.
Hanafi jurists use these terms to decide if ta'yin is needed.
3
Apply the rule: jins with multiple naw' requires ta'yin
If an act belongs to a jins that has several distinct naw', you must specify which naw' you intend. Example: each fard prayer is a different jins (different cause), so specify 'Zuhr'.
4
Apply the rule: single naw' does not require ta'yin
If all instances within the jins have the same ruling and purpose, no specification is needed. Example: tayammum for hadath or janabah – both are the same jins and same naw', so simply intend tayammum.
This is the dabt (restriction) of the qawida.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ضابطة في هذا البحث: التعيين لتمييز الأجْنَاسِ.
ترجمہ: اس بحث کا ضابطہ کی تعیین اجناس میں تمیز کے لئے ہوتی ہے۔
تشریح : اس عبارت میں صاحب کتاب علیہ الرحمہ ایک ضابطہ بیان کرنے جارہے ہیں جس سے آپ کو یہ معلوم ہو جائے گا کہ کونسی عبادت میں تعیین کی نیت ضروری ہے اور کونسی میں نہیں ؟ اس سے پہلے کہ مقصد سے بحث کی جائے جنس اور نوع کی تعریف محفوظ کر لیجئے ۔ فقہاء کے نزدیک جنس ایک ایسی کلی ہے جو مقاصد و احکام کے اعتبار سے مختلف افراد پر بولی جاتی ہے جیسے انسان جبکہ نوع و کلی ہے جو احکام و مقاصد کے اعتبار سے ایسے افراد پر بولی جائے جو متفق ہوں جیسے "رجل"
A rule in this discussion: Specification is for distinguishing types. Translation: The rule of this discussion is that specification is for distinguishing types. Explanation: In this passage, the author, may Allah have mercy on him, is about to state a rule by which you will know in which act of worship the intention of specification is necessary and in which it is not. Before discussing the purpose, memorize the definition of jins and naw'. According to the jurists: Jins is a universal that applies to different individuals in terms of purposes and rulings, like 'human'. While Naw' is a universal that applies to individuals that agree in rulings and purposes, like 'man'.
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage introduces a foundational qawida (maxim) for understanding when specification (ta'yin) in intention is required: 'Specification is for distinguishing types.' The author explains that this rule determines which acts of worship need precise specification and which do not. To apply the rule correctly, one must understand the distinction between jins (type) and naw' (sub-type or species) as used by Hanafi jurists. Jins is a broader category that encompasses individuals differing in legal rulings and purposes, such as 'human' (which includes men, women, slaves, etc.). Naw' is a narrower category where individuals share the same rulings and purposes, like 'man' (where all individuals of that subgroup have identical legal treatment). In the context of intention, specification (e.g., saying 'I intend to pray Zuhr') is needed when the act belongs to a jins that contains multiple naw' with different rulings. If the act is within a single naw', specification may not be required. This qawida is essential for understanding the rules of niyyah in Hanafi fiqh, particularly for distinguishing between prayers of different types (e.g., fard vs. sunnah, or various fard prayers).

Key Terms
جِنْس (jins): A universal category that applies to different individuals that vary in legal rulings and purposes, e.g., 'human'.
نَوْع (naw'): A universal category where all individuals share the same legal rulings and purposes, e.g., 'man' (as a subgroup of human).
تَعْيِين (ta'yin): Specific mention or intention (e.g., 'I intend Zuhr prayer') to distinguish one type from another.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When is specification (ta'yin) in intention required according to the principle stated?
A) In all acts of worship without exception.
B) Only when the act is a condition (shart) for another act.
C) When the act belongs to a jins (type) that has multiple different naw' (sub-types).
D) Only in prayers that are fard.

Key Takeaway
Specification in intention is required only when the act belongs to a broad type (jins) that contains multiple subtypes (naw') with different rulings or purposes.

The Maxim of Specification (Ta'yin) for Distinguishing Genera
Explains the maxim of specification for distinguishing genera with furuat and a madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-ta'yin li tamyiz al-ajnas' to determine when intention of specification is required in acts of worship.

Core Idea
Specification in intention is only needed when acts belong to different genera; within the same genus, general intention suffices.

This lesson explores a key Hanafi legal maxim that governs the role of intention (niyyah) in acts of worship. Understanding when specification is required is essential for performing prayers, fasts, and other rituals correctly. The maxim is applied to concrete cases such as tayammum and the daily prayers, and an intra-Hanafi dispute with Imam al-Khassaf is analyzed.

Guided Path
1
Understand the maxim and its definitions
Learn the Arabic maxim 'التعيين لتمييز الأجناس' and the definitions of jins (genus) and naw' (species) according to the Hanafi jurists. Jins is a universal applying to different individuals in rulings; naw' is a universal applying to similar individuals.
Memorize: jins is broader than naw'.
2
Identify the criterion for difference of genus
The source states that difference of genus is known by difference of cause (sabab). If the cause of obligation differs, the acts are of different genera.
Dabt: ويعرف اختلاف الجنس باختلاف السبب
3
Apply the maxim to the tayammum case
Analyze why the Hanafi school holds that intention to distinguish between hadath and janabah is not required for tayammum. Contrast with the dissenting opinion of Imam al-Khassaf, who requires specification by analogy with prayer.
Tayammum is a condition (shart), not an independent worship.
4
Apply to prayers and fasts
See why each prayer (e.g., today's Zuhr vs yesterday's Zuhr) has a different cause (time), thus requiring specification. Conversely, the days of Ramadan share a single cause (shuhud al-shahr), so general intention to fast Ramadan is sufficient.
Exception: Ramadan fasts are unified by the month.
5
Internalize the exception and the ruling for fatwa
The relied-upon fatwa (wa 'alayhi al-fatwa) is that one may pray multiple obligatory prayers with a single tayammum. General intention for Ramadan fasts is sufficient; specification of each day is not needed.
Mufta bihi: no specification needed for tayammum or Ramadan fasts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: اور فقہاء نے تیمم کے سلسلہ میں فرمایا کہ حدث اور جنابت کے مابین تمیز ضروری نہیں ہے حتی کہ اگر کسی نے وضو کے ارادے سے تیمم کیا تو جائز ہے خصاف کا اختلاف ہے یتیم کے دونوں کے لئے ایک ہی طریقہ پر ہونے کی وجہ سے تو نیت کے ذریعہ تمیز کی جائے کی جیسے فرض نماز اور فقہاء نے کہا یہ بیج نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس کی ضرورت اس لئے ہے کہ طہارت ہو جائے اور جب طہارت ہو گئی تو اس سے ادا کرنا جائز ہے جو چاہے اس لئے کہ شرائط میں صرف ان کا حصول مقصود ہوتا ہے نہ کہ ان کا غیر ۔ کیا نہیں دیکھتے اگر عصر کے لئے تقسیم کیا تو اس کے علاوہ اس سے پڑھنا جائز ہے۔
تشریح تیم حدث اور جنابت دونوں کے لئے ہوتا ہے لیکن دونوں میں تمیز پیدا کرنے کے لئے نیت ضروری نہیں ہے ولا يجب التمييز بين الحدث والجنابة حتى لو تيمم الجنب يريدبه الوضوء جائز
وعليه الفتوى (بند بیج اس (۲۶)
جبکہ امام خصاف فرماتے ہیں کہ حدث اور جنابت دونوں کے لئے تیم ایک ہی طریقہ پر ہوتا ہے اس لئے دونوں میں تمیز کے لئے نیت ضروری ہے جیسے فرائض خمسہ ایک ہی انداز پر پڑھی جاتی ہیں لیکن تمیز کے لئے نیت ضروری ہوتی ہے۔ قتصاد فرماتے ہیں کہ تمیم کا مقصد طہارت ہے خواہ جنابت کا تختم ہو یا حدث کا لہذا اس سے نماز وغیرہ پڑھنا جائز ہے لہذا تیم کو نماز پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے اس لیئے کہ نماز عبادت مقصودہ میں سے ہے اور تیم شرائط میں سے لہذا شرط کا صرف وجود کافی ہوتا ہے نیت ضروری نہیں ہوتی اس لئے مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی نے عصر کی نماز کے لئے تیم کیا تو اس سے دوسری نماز بھی پڑھی جاسکتی ہے ویصلى الرجل بتيممه ماشاء من الصلواة من الفرائض والنوافل الفوائت مالم يحدث او تزول العلة او يجد الماء (تاتار خانیه ج ۱ ص۲۵۸) علامہ جموعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ کو یہاں ذکر کرنا بر محل نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ یہاں ان عبادات کا بیان ہے جو منوی ہیں ۔
ضابطة في هذا البحث: التعيين لتمييز الأجْنَاسِ.
ترجمہ: اس بحث کا ضابطہ کی تعیین اجناس میں تمیز کے لئے ہوتی ہے۔

تو وہ لغو ہوگا۔
فَنِيَّةُ التَّعْيِينِ فِي الْجِنسِ الْوَاحِدِ لَغَوُ لِعَلمٍ الْفَائِدَةِ والتصرف إِذَا لَمْ يُصَادِق مَحَلَّهُ كَانَ لِغَوا ترجمه : پس جنس واحد میں تعیین کی نیست لغو ہے فائدہ نہ ہونے کی وجہ سے اور تصرف جب اپنے کل میں نہ ہو تشریح جنس واحد میں نیت تعیین افو ہے تین نیت کا مقصد اجناس کے مابین تمیز پیدا کرتا ہوتا ہے بہت واحد ہونے کی صورت میں مفقود ہے جنس واحد میں نیت تعیین کا تصرف غیر حل تصرف ہے جو لغو اور بے فائدہ ہے اگر کوئی آج کا روزہ رکھ رہا ہے تو یہ کافی ہے کہ میں آج کا روزہ رکھ رہا ہوں، یہ ضروری نہیں کہ یہ بھی کہے کہ کل کا نہیں رکھ رہا ہوں ۔
وَيُعْرَفُ اخْتِلَافُ الْجِنْسِ بِاخْتِلَافِ السَّبَبِ.
:ترجمه اور اختلاف جنس کا پتہ اختلاف سبب سے ہوتا ہے۔
تشریح: اتحاد جنس اور اختلاف جنس کا پتہ اختلاف سب سے چلتا ہے اگر سب مختلف ہے تو اختلاف پر ہے اور اگر سبب متحد ہے تو اتحاد جنس ہے۔ وباختلاف السبب يختلف الواجب ( تاتارخانيج راص (۴۲۹) والصَّلوةَ كُلُّهَا مِنْ قَبْلِ المُخْتَلِفِ حَتَّى الظَّهْرَيْنِ مِنْ يَوْمَيْنِ أَوِ الْعَصْرَيْنِ مِنْ يَوْمَينِ بِخِلَافِ أَيَّامٍ رَمَضَانَ فَإِنَّهُ يَجْمَعُهَا شُهُوْدُ الشَّهْرِ .
ترجمہ: اور تمام نمازیں مختلف جنس کے قبیل سے ہیں حتی کہ دو دن کی دو ظہر کی نماز میں یا دوران کی عصر کے نمازیں بخلاف ایام رمضان کے اس لئے کہ شہود شہر ان کو جمع کر دیتا ہے۔
تشریح: جب یہ معلوم ہو گیا کہ اختلاف جنس کا مدار اختلاف سبب پر ہے تو تمام نمازیں مختلف الاجناس ہو۔ گی کیونکہ ان کے وجوب کا سبب مختلف ہے۔ لہذا ان میں سے جس وقت کی بھی فرض نماز ادا کریں گے اس وقت کہ اس دن کی تعیین ضروری ہوگی ، مثلاً آج کی ظہر اور کل گذشتہ کی ظہر یا آج کی عصر یا کل گذشتہ کی عصر کا سب وجوب
مختلف ہے تو ہر ایک کی ادائیگی کے لئے نیت تعیین ضروری ہے۔
فائدہ: رمضان کے سبب وجوب میں فقہاء کرام کا اختلاف ہے۔ (۱) رمضان کے روزے کا سبب دن ہے رات نہیں یہ قاضی ابوزید کا اختیار کردہ مسلک ہے اس اعتبار سے کہ دن کا جزء اول اس کے روزے کے وجوب کا سبب ہے۔ (۲) رمضان کے روزوں کا سبب مطابق شہور شہر ہے اس میں رات اور دن شامل ہیں یہ علامہ سرخی کا پسندیدہ قول ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے دونوں قولوں کے درمیان عدم منافاة کا قول نقل کرنے کے بعد اس طور پر جمع کیا ہے کہ رمضان
Translation: And the jurists said regarding tayammum that distinction between hadath and janabah is not required; even if someone intending wudu performs tayammum, it is permissible. There is a difference of opinion with Khassaf: because both are on the same manner, so distinction is made through intention, like obligatory prayers. The jurists said this is not valid because its need is only to achieve purity, and when purity is achieved, it is permissible to perform whatever one wishes from it, because in conditions only their attainment is intended, not their specific type. Do you not see that if one performed tayammum for Asr, it is permissible to pray other than it with that tayammum. Commentary: Tayammum is for both hadath and janabah, but intention to distinguish between them is not necessary. 'And it is not obligatory to distinguish between hadath and janabah, so even if a junub person performs tayammum intending wudu, it is valid, and this is the relied-upon fatwa.' While Imam Khassaf says that tayammum for hadath and janabah is on the same manner, so intention for distinction is necessary, like the five daily prayers are performed in the same manner but intention for distinction is necessary. The correct view is that the purpose of tayammum is purity, whether it is for janabah or hadath, so it is permissible to pray etc. with it. Therefore, analogy of tayammum to prayer is an analogy with a difference, because prayer is an intrinsic act of worship while tayammum is among the conditions. For a condition, mere existence suffices; intention is not necessary. Thus, the ruling is: if a person performs tayammum for Asr prayer, he can also pray other prayers with it. 'And a man may pray with his tayammum whatever he wishes of prayers, obligatory, voluntary, or missed, as long as he does not break wudu, or the excuse ceases, or he finds water.' (Tatar Khaniya vol.1 p.258). Allama Jamui says that mentioning this ruling here is not appropriate because here the discussion is about acts of worship that are intended. Rule in this research: Specification is for distinguishing between genera. Translation: The rule of this discussion is that specification is for distinguishing genera. Commentary: In this phrase, the author is going to state a rule by which you will know in which acts of worship intention of specification is necessary and in which not. Before discussing the purpose, memorize the definition of genus (jins) and species (naw'). According to the jurists, genus is a universal that applies to different individuals in terms of purposes and rulings, like 'human'. While species is a universal that applies to individuals that agree in terms of rulings and purposes, like 'man'. [Page 156] then it will be void. 'The intention of specification in one genus is void due to lack of benefit, and an action that does not correspond to its place is void.' Translation: So the intention of specification in one genus is void because there is no benefit. Commentary: In one genus, intention of specification is void. The purpose of intention is to create distinction between genera; it is absent when there is oneness. In one genus, the action of intention of specification is an invalid action, void and without benefit. If someone is fasting today, it is sufficient to say 'I am fasting today'; it is not necessary to say 'I am not fasting yesterday'. 'And difference of genus is known by difference of cause.' Translation: And difference of genus is known by difference of cause. Commentary: Unity of genus and difference of genus is known by difference of cause; if the cause is different, then there is difference; and if the cause is unified, then there is unity of genus. 'And by difference of cause, the obligatory differs.' (Tatar Khaniya p.429) 'And all prayers are of the genus of different types, even the two Zuhrs of two days or the two Asrs of two days, contrary to the days of Ramadan, because the witnessing of the month unites them.' Translation: And all prayers are of the different genus, even the two Zuhr prayers of two days or the two Asr prayers of two days, contrary to the days of Ramadan, because the witnessing of the month unites them. Commentary: When it is known that difference of genus depends on difference of cause, then all prayers are of different genera because their cause of obligation is different. Therefore, when performing any obligatory prayer of a particular time, specification of that time and day is necessary. For example, today's Zuhr and yesterday's Zuhr, or today's Asr and yesterday's Asr, their cause of obligation is different, so intention of specification is necessary for each. Benefit: There is disagreement among the jurists regarding the cause of obligation of Ramadan fasts. (1) The cause of Ramadan fasts is the day, not the night. This is the chosen view of Qadi Abu Zaid, on the basis that the first part of the day is the cause of its fast. (2) The cause of Ramadan fasts is the witnessing of the month, which includes night and day. This is the preferred view of Allama Sarakhsi. The author of Hidayah, after reporting that there is no contradiction between the two views, reconciled them in this way: Ramadan
Source pages p. 155

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a legal maxim (qa'idah) concerning the requirement of specification (ta'yin) in intention for acts of worship. The author begins with an application: the ruling on tayammum. The Hanafi position is that intention to distinguish between hadath and janabah is not required for validity of tayammum; if a junub person intends wudu, it is still valid. This is based on the principle that tayammum is a condition for worship, and conditions do not require specification—mere existence suffices. Imam Khassaf disagreed, arguing that since both are performed the same way, intention is needed to distinguish, like obligatory prayers. The passage refutes this using qiyas ma'a al-fariq: prayer is an independent act of worship (maqsudah), while tayammum is a condition; analogy between them is invalid. The relied-upon fatwa is that one may pray multiple prayers with one tayammum as long as purity is maintained. The author then states the central maxim: 'Specification is for distinguishing between genera.' This means that intention to specify the type of worship is only necessary when the acts belong to different genera (ajnas); if they are of one genus, specification is futile. The genus is defined as a universal applying to different individuals in terms of rulings and purposes (e.g., human), while species is a universal applying to similar individuals (e.g., man). Examples: When fasting on a specific day, it is enough to intend that day's fast; one need not negate other days. To determine whether acts are of different genera, one looks at their cause (sabab). If causes differ, the acts are of different genera and specification is required. All prayers (Zuhr, Asr, etc.) have different causes of obligation (the time), so each requires specification. Exception: Ramadan fasts—their cause is the witnessing of the month (shuhud al-shahr), which unites all days into one genus, so general intention to fast Ramadan suffices; specification of each day is not required. The passage ends with a note on scholarly disagreement about the precise cause of Ramadan fasts.

Key Terms
تعيين (ta'yin): Specification in intention; identifying the specific act of worship one is performing.
جنس (jins): A universal category that applies to different individuals in terms of rulings and purposes, e.g., 'human'.
نوع (naw'): A species; a universal applying to individuals that agree in rulings and purposes, e.g., 'man'.
سبب (sabab): The cause that triggers obligation of an act of worship (e.g., time for prayer, sighting of moon for Ramadan).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented, when is intention of specification (ta'yin) required in acts of worship?
A) Always required for all acts of worship.
B) Required only when the acts belong to different genera (different causes).
C) Required only for obligatory acts, not for voluntary.
D) Never required; general intention always suffices.

Key Takeaway
Specification in intention is only required when acts belong to different genera, determined by difference of cause; within the same genus, general intention suffices.

Intention Specification in Obligatory and Recommended Acts
Concluding rules on when intention specification is and is not required in worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-jins al-wahid la yahtaj ila ta'yin al-niyyah' to identify when intention specification is and is not required in acts of worship, and state the Hanafi ruling for at least three furuat.

Core Idea
Acts of the same genre require no intention specification — only different genres need distinct intentions.

You already know that intention (niyyah) is essential for all acts of worship. But how specific must that intention be? The Hanafi school has a clear rule: if the acts belong to the same type, a general intention suffices. This concise passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair gives you the key cases where specification is unnecessary, from witr to funeral prayer. Let's unpack the rule and its applications.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the maxim
State the Arabic maxim: 'al-jins al-wahid la yahtaj ila ta'yin al-niyyah'. Understand that it means 'A single genre does not require specification of intention'.
This is a sughra (minor) maxim in the Hanafi qawaid literature.
2
Identify the scope
The passage explicitly applies to fara'id and wajibat, including nadhr (vowed acts), witr, Eid prayer, two rak'ahs of tawaf, funeral prayer, and sajdat al-tilawah.
The rule covers both obligatory and supererogatory acts when they fall under one genre.
3
Apply the maxim to each furu'
For each case, confirm that a general intention is sufficient. For witr, intend 'witr' not 'wajib witr' due to disagreement. For funeral prayer, intend 'prayer for Allah and supplication for the deceased'. For sajdah, no need to specify which verse.
The common thread: all acts of the same type need only a generic intention.
4
Note the exception embedded in the rule
The rule is absolute for same-genre acts. The passage warns against over-specification in witr because of the ikhtilaf over its wujub. This illustrates the principle's application in nuanced contexts.
Specifying 'wajib' could cause confusion; thus a general 'witr' intention is safer.
5
Summarize the principle
The core takeaway: ta'yin (specification) is only needed to distinguish between different genres (ajnas). Within one jins, al-niyyah al-mutlaqah (general intention) is valid.
This principle eases the burden of worship for laypeople.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هذَا كُلَّهُ فِي الْفَرَائِضِ وَالْوَاجِبَاتِ كَالْمَنْدُوْرِ، وَالْوِتْرِ عَلَى قَوْلِ الإِمَامِ وَالْعِيْدِ عَلَى الصَّحِيح ، وَرَكْعَتَي الطَّوَافِ عَلَى الْمُخْتَارِ وَيَنْوِى الْوِتْرَ لَا الْوِتْرِ الْوَاجِبِ لِلإِخْتِلَافِ فيهِ، وَفِي صَلَاةِ الْجَنَازَةِ يَنْوِي الصَّلَاةَ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَالدُّعَاءَ لِلْمَيِّتِ، وَلَا يَلْزَمُهُ التَّعْيْنُ فِي السجودِ التَّلَاوَةِ لأى تِلَاوَةِ سَجَدَ لَهَا، كَمَا فِي الْقِنْيَةِ». ترجمہ: به یوری تفصیل فرائض اور واجبات کے بارے میں ہے جیسے منذ ور اور وتر امام صاحب کے قول پر در میون اور پسندیدہ قول کے مطابق اور طواف کی دورکعتیں مختار قول کے مطابق اور وتر کی نیت کرے نہ کہ واجب وتر میں اختلاف کی وجہ سے اور نمازہ جنازہ میں اللہ کے لئے نماز کی نیت کرے اور میت کے لئے دعا کی اور تلاوت سے کہوں میں تعیین ضروری نہیں ہے کہ کس تلاوت کا سجدہ کر رہا ہے جیسا کہ قضیہ میں ہے۔ تشریح : ماقبل کی تفصیل سے آپ کو یہ بات معلوم ہو چکی کہ جنس واحد میں تعیین نیت کی ضرورت نہیں البتہ مختلف وں کی تمیز کے لئے نیت کی تعیین ضروری ہے لیکن عبادت میں تعیین وعدم تعیین نیت کے بارے میں جو تفصیل گزری وہ خراش اور واجبات کے بارے میں ہے جیسے کسی نے نذر مانی کہ اگر میرا افلاں کام ہو گیا تو میں دو روزہ رکھوں اور وہ کام کی تو روزہ ایک ہی جنس ہے اس لئے کہ روزہ کا سبب ایک ہی ہے اگر چہ اس کے افراد الگ الگ ہیں لہذا یہاں پر تعیین کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔
All of this is concerning the obligatory acts (fara'id) and wajibat, such as al-nadhr (vowed), and witr according to the Imam's statement, and Eid according to the correct opinion, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf according to the chosen opinion. And he should intend witr, not the wajib witr due to difference of opinion about it. And in the funeral prayer, he should intend the prayer for Allah and the supplication for the deceased. And specification is not incumbent upon him in the prostration of recitation (sajdah tilawat) as to which recitation he prostrated for, as is in al-Qunyah. Translation: This entire detail is about fara'id and wajibat, like nadhr, and witr according to Imam Abu Hanifa's saying, and Eid according to the reliable opinion, and the two rak'ahs of tawaf according to the preferred opinion. And he should intend witr, not the wajib witr because of disagreement about its wujub. And in the funeral prayer, he should intend prayer for Allah and supplication for the deceased. And in the prostration of tilawah, specification is not necessary for which tilawah he is prostrating, as in al-Qunyah. Commentary: From the previous detail, you have learned that in a single genre (jins wahid), specification of intention is not required. However, for distinguishing between different genres, specification of intention is necessary. But the detail that has passed about intention and lack of intention in worship is about fara'id and wajibat. For example, someone made a vow (nadhr) that if such-and-such work is accomplished, I will fast two days. Then the work is done. Since fasting is a single genre, specification is not needed even if the instances are different.
Source pages p. 161

Commentary
This passage provides a summary of the principle that specification of intention (ta'yīn al-niyyah) is not required when the acts belong to the same genre (jins wāḥid). It applies to various obligatory and recommended acts: nadhr (vowed acts), witr prayer (according to Imam Abu Hanifa, witr is wajib but one should not specify 'wajib' due to disagreement), Eid prayer, the two rak'ahs of tawaf, funeral prayer, and sajdat al-tilawah. In each case, a general intention suffices. The commentary explains that the previous detailed discussion about intention was specifically about fara'id and wajibat, using the example of nadhr fasting: if one vows to fast two days for a specific reason, since all fasts are the same genre, one does not need to specify the exact occasion for which each fast is intended.

Key Terms
تعیین (ta'yīn): Specification of the particular act intended in intention
جنس واحد (jins wāḥid): Single genre or type of worship

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Eid prayer
B) Funeral prayer
C) Witr prayer
D) Two rak'ahs of tawaf

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, intention specification is only needed to distinguish between different genres of worship; within a single genre, a general intention is sufficient.

Intention in Acts of Means: The Ruling on Wudu and Ghusl
Ruling on intention in acts that are means and critique of phrasing in Kanz and Quduri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on intention in acts of means (wasail), apply it to wudu and ghusl, and identify the mufta bihi position in light of al-Zayla'i's objection.

Core Idea
For means like wudu, specifying intention for the act itself is not required—the intention for the end suffices.

This passage clarifies a key distinction in Hanafi usul: between primary acts of worship (ibadat maqsuda) which require specific intention, and means (wasail) such as wudu and ghusl, where the intention is directed towards the end purpose. However, the exact phrasing of this rule has been a matter of scholarly refinement. Al-Zayla'i and others objected to formulations that might imply one should intend wudu itself. This lesson unpacks the rule, the critique, and the preferred view for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Categories
Recognize the distinction between acts intended for themselves (ibadat maqsuda) and acts that are means to an end (wasail). For means, the intention does not need to specify the act itself.
Example: salah is ibadat maqsuda; wudu is wasail.
2
Note the Exception: Tayammum
Understand that tayammum is an exception—intention is required due to the Quranic verse (al-Ma'idah 5:6).
This exception is established by nass (text).
3
Examine the Objection by al-Zayla'i
Al-Zayla'i criticized the phrase 'wa niyyatuhu' in al-Kanz because it could be read as intending wudu itself, which is incorrect. The proper intention should be for the act that necessitates purification.
The pronoun in 'niyyatuhu' was debated: does it refer to wudu or the person?
4
Determine the Preferred Madhhab
The relied-upon view is to intend either the worship that requires purification (e.g., prayer) or the removal of ritual impurity (raf' al-hadath).
Some scholars, like Ibn al-Qayyim, reinterpreted the pronoun to refer to the person, not the act.
5
Recognize the Variant
Some Hanafi scholars (al-Ba'd) hold that merely intending purification (al-tahara) is sufficient. This is a weaker opinion.
The mufta bihi is the former view (intending prayer or removal of hadath).

وَأَمَّا إِذَا لَمْ يَكُنِ الْمَنْوِيُّ مِنَ الْعِبَادَاتِ الْمَقْصُوْدَةِ وَإِنَّمَاهُوَ مِنَ الْوَسَائِلِ كَالْوُضُوء وَالْغُسْلِ وَالتَّيَمُّمِ، قَالُوْا فِى الْوُضُوْءِ : لَا يَنْوِيْهِ، لِأَنَّهُ لَيْسَ بِعِبَادَةٍ. ترجمہ: اور بہر حال جب کہ وہ جس کی نیت کی جارہی ہے عبادات مقصورہ میں سے نہ ہو بلکہ وہ وسائل سے؟ جیسے وضو غسل اور تیم تو فقہا وضو کے بارے میں کہتے ہیں کہ وہ اس کی نیت نہ کرے اس لئے کہ وہ عبادت نہیں ہے۔ تشریح اگر منوی عبادات مقصورہ میں سے نہ ہو بلکہ اس کا تعلق وسائل سے ہو جیسے وضو اور غسل وغیر و توان میں تعیین نیت ضروری نہیں ہے، رہا مسئلہ تمیم کا تو اس میں نیت نص قرآنی کی وجہ سے ضروری ہے، البتہ حصول ثواب کے لئے عبادات غیر مقصودہ میں بھی نیت ضروری ہے۔ وَإعْتَرَضَ الشَّارِحُ الزيلعي على الكنر " فِي قَوْلِهِ : وَنِيَّتُهُ بِنَاءً عَلَى عَوْدِ الضَّمِيرِ إلى الْوُضُوءِ، وَكَذَا اعْتَرَضُوا عَلَى الْقُدُوْرِي فِي قَوْلِهِ : يَنوى الطَّهَارَةَ، وَالْمَذْهَبُ أَنْ يَتْرِى مالا يصح إلا بِالطَّهَارَةِ مِنَ الْعِبَادَةِ، أو رفع الحَدَثِ وَعِندَ الْبَعْضِ فِيَّة الطَّهَارَةِ تَكْفِي. ترجمہ: اور شارح زیلعی نے کنز پر اس کے قول و نیتہ پر اعتراض کیا ہے جو ضمیر کے وضو کی طرف لوٹے پرمبنی ہے اور ایسے ہی فقہاء نے قدوری پر اس کے قول مینوی الطہار پر اعتراض کیا ہے اور پسندیدہ مذہب یہ ہے کہ اس عبادت کی نیت کرے جو بدون طہارت صحیح نہیں ہوتی یا رفع حدث کی نیت کرے اور بعض کے نزدیک طہارت کی نیت کافی ہے۔ تشریح: صاحب کنز نے وضو کی سنت شمار کرتے ہوئ ونیہ کا لفظ استعمال کیا ہے جس میں امیر کا مرجب بندہ ہے اس پر علامہ زیلعی نے اعتراض کیا ہے کہ مصنف کی عبارت سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ تحصیل سنت کے لئے وفضولی نیت کافی ہے حالانکہ ایسا نہیں ہے بلکہ وضو میں تحصیل سنت کے لئے یا تو ایسی عبادت کی نیت ہو جو بغیر رفع حدث کے درست نہ ہو، یا اقامت صلاۃ کی نیت ہو۔ علامہ ابن قیم نے اس کا ایک جواب تو یہ دیا ہے کہ نیت میں ضمیر کا مرجع وضو نہیں ہے بلکہ متوضی ہے
And as for when the intended (manwi) is not from the primary acts of worship (ibadat maqsuda) but rather from the means (wasail), like wudu, ghusl, and tayammum, they said regarding wudu: do not intend it, because it is not worship. Translation: And if the intended object is not from the primary acts of worship but rather from means, like wudu, ghusl, and tayammum, then the fuqaha say regarding wudu: do not intend it, because it is not worship. Explanation: If the intended is not from the primary acts of worship but rather relates to means, then specifying intention is not necessary. As for tayammum, intention is necessary due to the explicit Quranic text. However, for reward, intention is necessary even in non-primary acts. And al-Zayla'i objected to al-Kanz in his statement: 'and his intention' (wa niyyatuhu), based on the pronoun referring to wudu. Likewise they objected to al-Quduri in his statement: 'he intends purification' (yanwi al-tahara). The preferred madhhab is that one intends the act of worship that is not valid without purification, or intends removal of hadath. According to some, the intention of purification suffices. Explanation: The author of al-Kanz counted wudu among sunan and used the word 'wa niyyatuhu' with the pronoun referring back to wudu. Al-Zayla'i objected that the author's expression suggests that intending wudu is sufficient for attaining the sunna, whereas it is not. Rather, for wudu, one should intend either an act of worship that is not valid without removal of hadath, or the performance of prayer. Ibn al-Qayyim gave one response: the pronoun in the intention does not refer to wudu but to the person performing wudu.
Source pages p. 180

Commentary
This passage distinguishes between two types of acts: 'ibadat maqsuda' (primary acts of worship intended for their own sake, like prayer and fasting) and 'wasail' (means, like wudu and ghusl). For means, specifying intention is not required; one simply intends the act that necessitates purification. However, tayammum is an exception because the Quran explicitly requires intention. The text also addresses a critique: al-Zayla'i and others object to the phrasing in Kanz al-Daqa'iq and al-Quduri, which seem to imply that the intention should be for wudu itself. The preferred view is that the intention should be for the act that requires purification (e.g., prayer) or for removing the state of ritual impurity (raf' al-hadath). Some scholars suffice with the intention of purification itself. The commentary concludes with a note that Ibn al-Qayyim suggested the pronoun in Kanz refers to the person performing wudu, not to wudu itself.

Key Terms
عبادات مقصودة (ibadat maqsuda): Acts of worship intended as ends in themselves, e.g., salah, fasting.
وسائل (wasail): Acts that are means to an end, like purification for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did al-Zayla'i object to the phrase 'wa niyyatuhu' in al-Kanz?
A) Because wudu is not a sunnah.
B) Because the pronoun suggests intending wudu itself is needed.
C) Because intention is not required in wudu at all.
D) Because the phrase is grammatically incorrect.

Key Takeaway
For acts that are means (wasail), the intention should be for the end purpose, not for the act itself, except where nass requires otherwise (tayammum).

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
12 min
Necessity of Intending Obligatory Nature in Acts of Worship
Qawida furuat on niyyat al-fardiyya in four ibadat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle on when intention of obligatoriness (niyyat al-fardiyya) is required in salah, sawm, zakat, and hajj, and identify the exceptions based on the clarity of the act's designation as obligatory.

Core Idea
The intention of 'fard' is not always required—when an act is clearly designated as obligatory, absolute intention suffices.

This lesson examines the Hanafi qawida 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' through the specific issue of whether one must explicitly intend an act as fard. Using the four pillars of Islam, Ibn Nujaym demonstrates how the requirement varies with the worshiper's knowledge and the act's inherent designation. A mufti must understand these nuances to correctly assess the validity of worship in complex real-life scenarios.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing qawida and its scope
Recognize that this entire discussion is an application of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) to the specific issue of niyyat al-fardiyya. The qawida is a major (kubra) principle that governs all acts of worship where intention determines category.
The qawida is universal but the furuat show its contextual variation.
2
Analyze the six categories of worshippers in salah
Work through each category: (1) knows obligation and intending specific prayer suffices; (2) knows obligation but not details — still valid; (3) intends fard but doesn't understand meaning — invalid; (4) knows some are fard but cannot distinguish — invalid; (5) believes all prayers are fard — valid; (6) completely ignorant of obligation — invalid.
The critical variable is the person's knowledge and understanding of 'obligatoriness'.
3
Apply the principle to sawm, zakat, and hajj
For sawm: Ramadan's clear designation exempts intention of fard. For zakat: multiple types of sadaqah require explicit intention. For hajj: hardships imply fard, but if one explicitly intends nafl, it counts as nafl.
Each case is determined by whether the act is unambiguously linked to obligation.
4
Identify the exception and its rationale
Ramadan fasting is the clearest exception: the month itself designates the fast as fard. Even if one intended a nafl fast on the night of doubt, it counts as Ramadan. This is based on the principle of designation (ta'yin) and ease (taysir).
This exception is operative even though the general rule requires specification for obligations.
5
Formulate the mufta bihi for each act
Summarize: Salah — valid if the worshiper understands obligation and intends the specific prayer, except when ignorant of the concept. Sawm — intention of fard not required. Zakat — required. Hajj — intention of fard not required unless one explicitly intends nafl.
These are the operative positions a mufti applies in fatwa.

پر بند و ثواب کا مستحق ہو اور ترک پر سزا کا مستحق نہ ہو ایسا شخص اگر صرف فجر ظہر وغیرہ کی نیت کرے تو بھی اس کی نماز درست ہے اس کے لئے یہ معین ضروری نہیں کہ فجر پڑھ رہا ہوں جو فرض ہے اس لئے کہ یہ شخص فرضیت کے معنی سے واقف ہے اسے یہ بھی معلوم ہے کہ فجر کی نماز فرض ہے تو اس کا فجر ظہر وغیرہ کی نیت کر لینا ایسا ہی ہے جیسے فرض کی نیت کر لی ہو۔ " (۲) جس کو اوپر کی باتوں کا علم تو ہو اور وہ فرض کے اندر فرض کی نیت بھی کرتا ہو لیکن فرض کے اندر کیا کیا چیزیں فرائض ہیں اور کیا سنن ہیں یہ نہ جانتا ہوتو بھی اس کے حق میں فرض کی نیت کافی ہوگی۔ (۳) تیسرے درجہ کا نمازی وہ ہے جو فرض کی نیت کرتا ہو اور اسے اس کے معنی کا علم نہ ہو تو اس صورت میں اس کے حق میں فرض کی نیت کافی نہ ہوگی۔ (۴) چوتھی قسم ان نمازیوں کی ہے جنہیں یہ تو علم ہو کہ لوگ جو نمازیں پڑھتے ہیں ان میں کچھ فرائض ہیں اور کچھ سنن ہیں، لہذا وہ بھی لوگوں کی طرح نماز پڑھ لیتا ہے مگر فرائض اور نوافل میں تمیز نہیں کر پاتا ہے تو اس صورت میں محض اتنی نیست اسے کافی نہ ہوگی کیونکہ فرض میں تعیین نیت شرط ہے۔ (۵) پانچویں قسم ان نمازیوں کی ہے جو تمام نمازوں کو فرض سمجھتے ہیں تو ان کی نماز جائز ہو جائے گی۔ (1) چھٹی قسم ان نمازیوں کی ہے جنہیں یہ معلوم نہ ہو کہ اللہ تعالی نے اپنے بندوں پر کچھ نماز میں فرض کی ہیں لیکن وہ ان نمازوں کو ان کے اوقات میں پڑھ لیتا ہے تو اس صورت میں بھی اس طرح نمازیں پڑھنا اس کے لئے درست نہ ہوگا۔
وَأَمَّا فِي الصَّوْمِ: فَقَدْ عَلِمْتَ الَّهُ يَصِحُ بِنِيَّةِ مُبَانِنَةٍ وَ بِمُطْلَقِ البَيِّةِ، فَلَا تُشْتَرَطُ لِقَوْمٍ رَمَضَانَ ادَاءً نِيَّةُ الفَرْضِيَّةِ، حَتَّى قَالُوا: لَوْ نَوَى لَيْلَةَ الشَّبِّ صَوْمَ آخِرِ شَعْبَانَ، ثُمَّ ظَهَرَ بَعْدَ الصَّوْمِ أنَّهُ اوّل رَمَضَانَ اجْزَاهُ.
:ترجمہ: اور بہر حال روزے میں تو آپ کو معلوم ہو گیا کہ وہ متضاد نیت سے اور مطبق نیت سے میچ ہو جاتاہے پس رمضان کے اداروزے کے لئے فرضیت کی نیت شرط نہیں ہے حتی کہ فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر لیلتہ الشک میں شعبان کے آخری روزے کی نیت کی پھر روزے کے بعد ظاہر ہوا کہ وہ یکم رمضان ہے تو اس کو کافی ہوگا ۔
تشریح: رمضان کا مہینہ رمضان کے روزوں کے لئے معیار ہے یہی وجہ ہے کہ رمضان کے اداء روزوں کے لئے فرضیت کی نیت شرط نہیں ہے کیونکہ من جانب اللہ رمضان کا مہینہ فرض روزوں ہی کے لئے متعین ہے لہذا اس کیمیا جو بھی روزہ ہوگا وہ فرض ہی ہو گا اسی وجہ سے کہا جاتا ہے کہ وہ متضادنیت اور مطلق نیت سے بھی صیح ہو جاتا ہے۔ ويصح اداءها بمطلق النية وهو ان يتعرض لذات الصوم دون الصفة (مجمع الانهرج، ص ١٣٢)

وَأَمَّا الزَّكَاةَ: فَخَشْتَرَطُ لَهَا بَيَّةُ الْفَرضية، لأن الصدقة متنوعة ولم أو حكم لية الزكاة المعجلة وَظَاهِرُ كَلامِهِمْ أَنَّهُ لابدَّ مِنْ نَة الفَرْضِ، لأنه تعجيل بعد أصل الوجوب، لأن نسبة هُوَ النصاب النامي، وقد وجد ، بخلاف الحول، فَإِنَّهُ شَرط لوجوب الأداء، بخلاف تعجيل الصَّلَاةِ عَلَى وَقْتها فإنَّهُ غَيْرُ جانز؛ لكون وقتها نسبياً للوجوب، وَشَرِّطاً لصحة الآداء. ترجمه اور بہر حال زکوۃ تو اس کے لئے فرضیت کی نیت شرط ہے اس لئے کہ صدقہ کی بہت سی اقسام ہیں اور ڈینگی زکوۃ کی نیت کا حکم میں نے نہیں دیکھا اور فقہاء کے ظاہر کام سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ فرض کی نیت ضروری ہے، اس لئے کہ وہ اصل وجوب کے بعد تجمیل ہے اس لئے کہ اس کا سبب وہ انساب نامی ہے اور وہ پایا گیا، بر خلاف تولان حول کے کیونکہ وہ وجوب اداء کے لئے شہروا ہے برخلاف نماز کے وقت سے پہلے پڑھنے کے کہ وہ جائز نہیں ہے، کیونکہ وہ و جوب کا سبب ہے اور ادائیگی کے صحیح ہونے کے لئے شرط ہے۔ تشریح زکوۃ کی ادائیگی کے لئے فرضیت کی نیت ضروری ہے لیکن ایک آدمی کے دوسرے آدمی کو مال دینے کے لئے مختلف وجوہات میں کوئی بطور میہ دیتا ہے کوئی بطور ہدیہ دیتا ہے کوئی ہوں ہی تبر عادید یتا ہے کوئی بطور ز کو تا دیتا ہے اس لئے تعین نیت بھی ضروری ہے تا کہ تمیز ہو سکے ڈیلیگی زکو دینے میں نیت فرضیت کیوں شرط ہے۔ علامہ ابن نجیم مصری اوپر کا مسئلہ ذکر کرنے کے بعد فرماتے ہیں کہ پیشگی زکوۃ دینے میں نیت فرض ہے یا نہیں؟ اس سلسلہ میں مجھے کوئی حکم صراحة تو نہیں ملا۔ البتہ اتنی بات سمجھ میں آتی ہے کہ زکوۃ کے اندر فقہاء نے دو چیزیں الگ الگ ذکر کی ہیں (۱) نفس وجوب زکا وہ اس کا سبب تو بقدر نصاب مال کا ہوتا ہے (۲) وجوب ادامز کو ہ تو پیکی زکوۃ دینے میں وجوب زکوۃ کا سبب تو ہے لیکن زکوة کا سبب نہیں ہے اس لئے پیشیکی زکوۃ دینے میں فرضیت کی نیت شرط ہے۔ ويجوز التعجيل لاكثر من سنة لوجود السبب كذا فى الهداية (هنديه ج ١ ، ص : ١٧٦ ) برخلاف نماز کے کہ وقت سے پہلے جائز نہیں ہے کیونکہ وقت نفسِ وجوب کا سبب ہے اور صحت ادا ئیگی کے لئے شرط ہے تو اس صورت میں مسبب کا سبب سے پہلے پایا جانا لا زم آئے گا جو درست نہیں۔
أما في الصلواة السبب مختلف وهو الوقت (تاتارخانیه ج ۱، ص ۴۲۹)
وَأَمَّا الْحَج فَقَدَّمْنَا أَنَّهُ يَصِحُ بِمُطْلَقِ النِّيَّةِ، وَلكِنْ عَلَلُوْهُ بِمَا يَقْتَضِي أَنَّهُ نَوَىٰ فِي نَفْسِ الْأمْرِ الْفَرْضِيَّةَ، قَالُوا : لأنَّهُ لَا يَتَحَمَّلُ الْمَشَاقَ الْكَثِيرَة إِلَّا لأجل الْفَرْضِ، فَاسْتَنْبَطَ مِنْهُ المُحَقِّقُ إبْنُ الْهُمَام أَنَّهُ لَوْ كَانَ الْوَاقِعُ مِنْهُ أَنَّهُ لَمْ يَنْوِ الْفَرْضَ لَمْ يَجُزُهُ؛ لِأَنَّ صَرْفَهُ إِلَى الْفَرْضِ حَمْلاً لَهُ عَلَيْهِ عَمَلاً بالظاهر ، وَهُوَ حَسَنٌ جِدًّا فَلَا بُدَّ فِيْهِ مِنْ نِيَّةِ الْفَرْضِ؛ لِأَنَّهُ لَوْ نَوَى النَّفْلَ فِيْهِ، وَعَلَيْهِ حَجَّةُ الإِسْلَامِ كَانَ نَفْلاً.
(1) A person who is deserving of reward for obedience and not deserving of punishment for omission, if he intends merely Fajr, Zuhr, etc., his prayer is valid. For him, it is not necessary to specify that he is praying Fajr which is obligatory, because this person understands the meaning of obligatoriness and knows that Fajr prayer is obligatory. So his intending Fajr, Zuhr, etc. is just like intending obligatory. (2) One who knows the above matters and also intends obligatory within obligatory, but does not know which things are obligatory and which are sunnah within the obligatory, for him the intention of obligatory is sufficient. (3) The third category of worshiper is one who intends obligatory but does not know its meaning; in that case, intention of obligatory is not sufficient for him. (4) The fourth category consists of those who know that among the prayers people perform, some are obligatory and some sunnah, so he also prays like people, but cannot distinguish between obligatory and supererogatory; in that case, mere intention is not sufficient for him because specification of intention is required for obligatory. (5) The fifth category consists of those who consider all prayers as obligatory; their prayer is valid. (6) The sixth category consists of those who do not know that Allah has made some prayers obligatory upon His servants, but he prays these prayers at their times; in that case, this way of praying is not valid for him.

As for fasting: you have known that it is valid with a contradictory intention (niyyah mubayanah) and with an absolute intention (mutlaq al-niyyah). So intention of obligatoriness is not required for performing the fast of Ramadan. Indeed, they said: If on the night of doubt (laylat al-shakk) one intends the last fast of Sha'ban, then after the fast it becomes clear that it was the first of Ramadan, it suffices him.
Translation: And in any case, regarding fasting, you have come to know that it is valid with contradictory intention and with absolute intention. So for the performance of Ramadan fast, intention of obligatoriness is not required. Indeed, the jurists say: If on the night of doubt one intended the last fast of Sha'ban, then after the fast it appeared that it was the first of Ramadan, it will suffice.
Explanation: The month of Ramadan is the criterion for the fasts of Ramadan. This is why intention of obligatoriness is not required for performing the fasts of Ramadan, because the month of Ramadan is designated by Allah solely for obligatory fasts. Hence, whatever fast occurs in it will be obligatory. For this reason it is said that it is valid with contradictory intention and with absolute intention. And its performance is valid with absolute intention, which is to refer to the essence of fasting without the attribute. (Majma' al-Anhur, p. 132)

As for zakat: intention of obligatoriness is required for it, because charity (sadaqah) is of various types. And I have not seen a ruling regarding the intention of advanced zakat (zakat mu'ajjalah). And the apparent meaning of their words is that the intention of obligatory is necessary, because it is ta'jil (prepayment) after the original obligation. Because its cause is the growing nisab, and it is found, unlike the passing of a year (hawl), for that is a condition for the obligation of performance. Unlike prepaying prayer before its time, for that is not permissible, because its time is a cause for obligation and a condition for the validity of performance.
Translation: And in any case, for zakat, intention of obligatoriness is required, because charity is of many types. And I have not seen the ruling on the intention of advanced zakat. And from the apparent words of the jurists, it is understood that the intention of obligatory is necessary, because it is prepayment after the original obligation, because its cause is the growing nisab, and it is found, unlike the year, for that is a condition for the obligation of performance. Unlike prepaying prayer before its time, which is not permissible, because the time is a cause for obligation and a condition for the validity of performance.
Explanation: For the performance of zakat, intention of obligatoriness is necessary. But when one person gives money to another, there are various reasons: some give as a gift, some as a present, some as charity, some as zakat. Therefore specification of intention is also necessary so that distinction can be made. Why is intention of obligatoriness required in giving zakat? Allamah Ibn Nujaym Egyptian, after mentioning the above issue, says: In giving zakat in advance, is the intention of obligatory required or not? In this regard, I have not found any explicit ruling. However, this much is understood: In zakat, the jurists have mentioned two things separately: (1) The essence of the obligation of zakat, its cause is possession of nisab wealth. (2) The obligation of performance. In advanced zakat, the cause of obligation of zakat is present, but the performance obligation is not. Therefore, in giving advanced zakat, intention of obligatoriness is required. And it is permissible to advance for more than a year because of the existence of the cause. Thus in Hidayah (Hindiyyah vol. 1, p. 176). Unlike prayer, which is not permissible before its time, because the time is the cause of the obligation itself and a condition for validity of performance. In that case, the effect would occur before the cause, which is not correct. As for prayer, the cause is different: time. (Tatarikhaniyyah vol. 1, p. 429)

As for hajj: we have already stated that it is valid with absolute intention, but they explained it in a way that implies that in reality he intended obligatoriness. They said: Because one does not undertake many hardships except for obligation. Hence, the muhaqqiq Ibn al-Humam deduced that if in reality he had not intended the obligatory, it would not be valid for him, because his action is attributed to obligatory, acting on the apparent (zahir), and that is very good. Therefore, intention of obligatory is necessary in it, because if he intended supererogatory (nafl) while the Hajjat al-Islam is due on him, it would be nafl.
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage from Sharh al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair discusses the application of the maxim 'al-umur bi maqasidiha' (matters are judged by intentions) specifically regarding the requirement of intending the obligatory nature (niyyat al-fardiyya) in acts of worship. The author, Ibn Nujaym, presents a detailed breakdown for prayer, fasting, zakat, and hajj, illustrating when such intention is necessary and when it is not.

The passage begins with six categories of worshippers in salah. The key distinction is whether the person understands the concept of obligatoriness. If he knows that Fajr is obligatory and intends Fajr, that suffices even without explicitly saying 'fard'. If he does not understand the concept, he must intend 'fard'. The fourth category, where the person knows some prayers are fard but cannot distinguish, is invalid because specification (ta'yin) is required. The fifth category, where one believes all prayers are fard, is valid due to his sincere belief. The sixth, ignorance of obligation, invalidates.

For fasting, the month of Ramadan itself designates the fast as obligatory. Therefore, intention of obligatoriness is not required. Even if one intends a nafl fast on the night of doubt and it turns out to be Ramadan, the fasting is valid because the essence of fasting in Ramadan is automatically obligatory. This is an exception to the general rule due to the clear designation of time.

Zakat requires explicit intention of obligatoriness because charitable giving can be for many reasons (gift, charity, zakat). Without specifying, one could be fulfilling a different type of sadaqah. Advanced zakat (given before the year completes) also requires this intention, as the cause (nisab) exists but the performance obligation is not yet due; thus ta'yin is necessary.

Hajj, like fasting, is valid with absolute intention (mutlaq niyyah) because the hardships undertaken imply one intends the obligatory Hajjat al-Islam. However, Ibn al-Humam qualifies that if one consciously intended nafl while the fard is due, it would be valid only as nafl—so he must actually intend fard. This nuance is important for fatwa: the default assumption is that a person performing hajj does so for obligation, but if evidence shows otherwise, it is not counted.

The underlying qawida is that when the act is unambiguously designated for obligation by Shari'ah (like Ramadan for fasting, or the overwhelming practice of hajj), the intention of the specific act suffices without stating obligatoriness. When multiple possible categories exist (like zakat), explicit intention of obligation is required.

Key Terms
نية الفرضية (niyyat al-fardiyya): The intention that an act is being performed as an obligatory duty (fard).
نية مطلقة (niyya mutlaqa): An absolute intention that specifies the essence of the act (e.g., 'fasting') without qualifying it as obligatory or voluntary.
نية متعبنة (niyya muta'ayyana): A specified intention (e.g., 'Fajr prayer') that suffices even without mentioning fard if the person understands it as fard.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification in this passage, what is the ruling for a person who prays all five daily prayers at their times but does not know that Allah has made any prayers obligatory?
A) His prayer is valid because he performed the prayers in their times.
B) His prayer is invalid because he lacks the intention of obligation.
C) His prayer is valid if he intended the specific prayer name (e.g., Fajr).
D) His prayer is valid because he prayed like the general public.

Key Takeaway
The need for explicit intention of fard depends on the clarity of the act's obligatory designation; in Ramadan and hajj, the default is obligation, so absolute intention suffices.
