The Ruling of Riya in Obligations and the Exception in Sacrifice
Explaining a legal maxim and its exception in sacrifice.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi maxim 'al-fara'id ma'a al-riya' sahihah' and identify the exception when the act is indivisible, using the sub-maxim 'al-i'raqatu la tatajazz'.

Core Idea
Obligatory acts with riya are valid, but indivisible acts like sacrifice require pure intention from all participants.

This passage presents a key Hanafi maxim: obligatory acts are valid and discharge the obligation even when performed with riya (showing off). However, there is a crucial exception in the chapter of sacrifice: when the act is physically indivisible—like the spilling of blood in sacrifice—any impure intention invalidates the whole. This lesson explores the rule, the exception, and the underlying rationale, helping you apply the maxim correctly in fatwa.

Guided Path
1
State the general maxim
Identify the rule that fara'id (obligatory acts) performed with riya are still valid and drop the obligation. This is from al-Bazzazi.
The maxim is a sughra (minor) qawida.
2
Identify the exception from the chapter of sacrifice
In Kitab al-Adhiya, for a shared badana (camel/cow), if even one partner intends mere meat or is a non-Muslim, the sacrifice is invalid for all.
The exception is restricted by the dabt 'ma waqa'a ala wajh la yatajazz''.
3
Analyze the rationale (illa)
The reason given is 'al-i'raqatu la tatajazz' (spilling blood is indivisible). The act is one unit; if part is not for qurba, the whole loses qurba status.
This is a qiyas jaliy: indivisibility of the act.
4
Apply the maxim and exception to the furuat
For a single person: if he intends both Allah and other, a fortiori it does not suffice and is haram. For obligatory acts like prayer: if riya is present, the prayer is still valid because the act is divisible into parts (intention can be mixed).
Contrast divisible vs. indivisible acts.
5
Extract the dabt (restrictive sub-maxim)
The general maxim is restricted by the sub-maxim: 'If an act is indivisible, corruption of intention in a part corrupts the whole.'
This dabt governs acts like slaughter, not habitual prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَ قَدْ أَفَادَ البَزَّازِي بِقَوْلِهِ فِي حَقِّ سُقُوطِ الْوَاجِبِ: إِنَّ الْفَرَائِضَ مَعَ الرِّيَاءِ صَحِيحَةٌ مُسْقِطَةٌ لِلْوَاجِبِ، وَلكِنْ ذَكَرُوْا فِي كِتَابِ الْأضْحِيَّةِ، بِأَنَّ الْبُدْنَةَ تُجْزِى عَنْ سَبْعَةٍ، إِنْ كَانَ الْكُلُّ مُرِيدِيْنَ الْقُرْبَةَ وَإِنِ اخْتَلَفَتْ جِهَاتُهَا مِنْ أَضْحِيَّةٍ وَ قِرَانِ وَ مُتْعَةٍ، قَالُوْا فَلَوْ كَانَ أَحَدُهُمْ مُرِيدًا لَحْماً لِأهْلِهِ، أَوْ كَانَ نَصْرَانِيًّا لَمْ يُجْزِ عَنْ وَاحِدٍ مِنْهُمْ، وَعَلَّلُوْا بِأَنَّ البعض إذا لَمْ يَقَعُ قُرْبَةً خَرَجَ الكُل عَن أن يكون قُرْبَةً لِأَنَّ الْإِرَاقَةَ لَا تَتَجَزَى، فَعَلَى هَذَا لَوْ ذَبَحَهَا أُضْحِيَّةٌ لِلَّهِ تَعَالَى، وَلِغَيْرِهِ لَا تُجْزِتُهُ بِالْأَوْلَى، وَ يَنْبَغِي أَنْ تَحْرُمَ.
And al-Bazzazi has informed by his statement regarding the dropping of obligation: Indeed the obligations with riya are valid, dropping the obligation. But they mentioned in the Book of Sacrifice that the badana suffices for seven, if all are intending closeness (to Allah) even if their directions differ, from sacrifice, qiran, and tamattu'. They said: So if one of them intends meat for his family, or is a Christian, it does not suffice for any of them. And they gave the reason that when some (portion) does not occur as closeness, the whole leaves being closeness because the spilling of blood is not divisible. So upon this, if he slaughtered it as a sacrifice for Allah and for other than Him, it does not suffice him a fortiori, and it is befitting that it be forbidden.
Source pages p. 198

Commentary
This passage presents a legal maxim from al-Bazzazi that obligatory acts (fara'id) performed with riya (showing off) are still valid and discharge the obligation. This is a general rule. However, the passage then introduces an exception from the chapter of sacrifice (udhiya). For a badana (camel or cow) shared by seven people, if all intend qurba (drawing near to Allah), it is valid even if their specific types differ (udhiya, qiran, tamattu'). But if even one person intends merely to get meat or is a non-Muslim, the sacrifice is invalid for all. The reason is that the act of spilling blood (i'raq al-dam) is indivisible; it either is wholly for Allah or not. Therefore, if one partner's intention is not for qurba, the entire act loses its qurbah character. The passage then applies this to a single owner: if he slaughters partly for Allah and partly for another, the sacrifice does not suffice and is likely forbidden. The apparent contradiction between the general rule (fara'id valid with riya) and this exception is resolved by noting that the exception is not due to riya but due to the absence of a condition for sacrifice (pure intention for qurba) and the indivisible nature of the act.

Key Terms
رياء (riya'): Performing an act of worship to be seen by others, not purely for Allah
الفرائض مع الرياء صحيحة (al-fara'id ma'a al-riya' sahihatun): The ruling that obligatory acts (fard) performed with riya are still valid and discharge the obligation
الإراقة لا تتجزأ (al-i'raqatu la tatajazz'): The spilling of blood (in sacrifice) is not divisible; the act is one unit

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if seven people share a badana for sacrifice and one of them intends merely to get meat for his family, what is the ruling?
A) The sacrifice is valid only for the six who intended qurba.
B) The sacrifice is invalid for all seven.
C) The sacrifice is valid for all, but the one with wrong intention sins.
D) The sacrifice is invalid only for the one with wrong intention.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim that obligatory acts with riya are valid is restricted by the dabt that indivisible acts require pure intention from all participants, as illustrated in the case of shared sacrifice.

Intentions in Jihad and Hajj: The Maxim Applied
Ruling on whether a merchant who joins jihad or hajj with trade intention deserves reward or share

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to distinguish when a secondary intention nullifies an act in jihad and hajj, using the Hanafi sub-maxim (dabt) on primary versus subordinate intentions.

Core Idea
Intention determines the ruling; secondary intentions may or may not harm depending on the act's nature.

This passage from the works of Al-Zayla‘i illustrates the famous legal maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' (actions are judged by intentions) across jihad and hajj. It demonstrates that the effect of a secondary worldly intention depends on the specific act: in some acts, like tawaf, any worldly intent invalidates; in others, like standing at ‘Arafah, the act remains valid. The key is the sub-rule (dabt): if the primary intention is the act of worship, a subordinate worldly purpose does not harm. Understand these distinctions now to avoid common mistakes when issuing fatwas on mixed intentions.

Guided Path
1
Recall the maxim and its sub-rule
Begin by stating the first major maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' and its Hanafi explanation: the ruling of an act is based on the intention. Then recall the relevant dabt: when intentions are mixed, the primary intention governs, and a secondary intention only causes harm if it overrides the primary.
This dabt is explicitly used in the passage to justify the merchant's entitlement when he fights.
2
Analyse the first application: the merchant in jihad
Identify the ruling: a merchant who joins solely for trade gets no share of spoils. But if he fights, his combat intention becomes primary, trade becomes subordinate, and the share is earned. Note the analogy with the pilgrim who trades on the way without losing reward.
The text says 'ka-al-hājj' (like the pilgrim) – a qiyas.
3
Examine the second set of applications: tawaf vs. wuquf
Contrast two cases: performing tawaf while seeking a debtor is invalid, but standing at ‘Arafah with the same intention is valid. The difference is explained by the nature of each act: tawaf is a pure act of worship requiring pure intention, while wuquf at ‘Arafah is a physical pillar that is not invalidated by a worldly side-intention.
The passage says 'al-farq ẓāhir' (the difference is apparent).
4
Derive the Hanafi sub-maxim (dabt)
From the examples, formulate the principle: for acts that are purely devotional (like tawaf), any worldly intention nullifies the act; for acts that combine physical presence and intention (like wuquf), a subordinate worldly intention does not invalidate, provided the primary worshipping intention is present.
The dabt can be expressed as: 'al-niyyah al-ūlā tuʿtabiru wa al-thānawiyyah lā taḍurru idhā lam tughlib'.
5
Apply the maxim to a novel case
Consider a case not in the text: a person performs ‘umrah but also plans to visit a friend in Mecca. The primary intention is ‘umrah; the visit is subordinate. According to the sub-rule, the ‘umrah is valid and reward is not diminished. This parallels the pilgrim trading on the way.
This shows the predictive power of the qā‘ida.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَصَرَّحُوْا فِي كِتَابِ السِّيرِ بِأنَّ السُّوقِى لَهُ سَهْم، لَهُ، لأَنَّهُ عِنْدَ الْمُجَاوَزَةِ لَمْ يَقْصُدْ إِلَّا التِّجَارَةَ، لَا إِعْزَازَ الدِّيْنِ وَ إِرْهَابَ الْعَدُوِّ ، فَإِنْ قَاتَلَ إِسْتَحَقَّهُ؛ لِأَنَّهُ ظَهَرَ بِالْمُقَاتَلَةِ أَنَّ قصْدَهُ القِتَالُ، وَالتِّجَارَةُ تَبْع فَلَا تَضُرُّهُ كَالحَاجَّ، إِذَا إِنَّجَرَ فِي طَرِيقِ الْحَجِّ لَا يَنْقُصُ أجْرُهُ، ذَكَرَهُ الزَّيْلَعِيُّ. وَظَاهِرُهُ أَنَّ الْحَاجَّ إِذَا خَرَجَ تَاجِرًا، فَلَا أَجْرَ لَهُ، وَصَرَّحُوْا بِأَنَّهُ لَوْطَافَ طَالِبًا غَرِيْمَهُ لَا يُجْزِتُهُ، وَلَوْ وَقَفَ بِعَرَفَةَ طَالِبًا غَرِيْمَهُ أَجْزَاهُ، وَالْفَرْقَ ظَاهِرٌ .
And they explicitly stated in the book of Siyar that the merchant (sūqī) has no share of spoils, because at the time of crossing the border he intended only trade, not the glorification of the religion nor intimidation of the enemy. But if he fights, he becomes entitled to it, because fighting shows that his intention is combat, and trade is subsidiary, so it does not harm him, like the pilgrim, if he trades on the way of hajj, his reward is not diminished. Al-Zayla‘i mentioned it. And its apparent meaning is that if the pilgrim sets out as a trader, he has no reward. And they explicitly stated that if one performs tawaf seeking his debtor, it is not valid, but if he stands at ‘Arafah seeking his debtor, it is valid. And the difference is apparent.
Source pages p. 201

Commentary
This passage presents a qawida with furuat (applications of the maxim 'acts are judged by intentions'). The main ruling: a merchant who joins a military expedition solely for trade gets no share of spoils. However, if he actually fights, his combat intention becomes primary, and trade is secondary, so he becomes entitled. Similarly, a pilgrim who trades on the way without it being his primary intention does not lose reward. But if one sets out primarily as a trader, he gets no hajj reward. Two further applications: tawaf (circumambulation) done with the worldly intention of seeking a debtor is invalid, but standing at ‘Arafah with the same worldly intention is valid. The difference: tawaf is a pure act of worship that requires exclusive intention, while wuquf at ‘Arafah is a physical presence that cannot be invalidated by a secondary worldly intention. This shows the nuanced application of the intention principle across different acts.

Key Terms
السوقي (al-sūqī): A merchant who joins a military expedition for purposes of trade, not combat.
السهم (al-sahm): The share of spoils (ghanimah) allocated to a participant in jihad.
الأمور بمقاصدها (al-umūr bi-maqāṣidihā): Acts are judged by their intentions; a major legal maxim.
الفرق ظاهر (al-farq ẓāhir): The difference is apparent; used by the author to indicate that the distinction between tawaf and wuquf is obvious once understood.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition does a merchant who joined an expedition become entitled to a share of spoils?
A) If he trades on the way
B) If he fights in battle
C) If he intends to glorify the religion from the start
D) If he stays for the entire duration

Key Takeaway
The maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' with its Hanafi sub-maxim (primary intention governs; secondary does not harm if subordinate) is applied differently to various acts, as seen in the contrasting rulings on tawaf and wuquf.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims

Intention in Jihad: The Merchant's Share in Booty
Expansion probe of the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' through two major furuat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' to determine entitlement to ghanimah and reward in hajj, and distinguish cases where intention is repurposed.

Core Idea
Intention governs entitlement in jihad booty and reward in hajj; incidental trade does not harm, but primary trade intention negates.

The Hanafi legal maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions' (الأمور بمقاصدها) is one of the five major universal principles of Islamic jurisprudence. This lesson explores its application through two classic furuat from Kitab al-Siyar and Kitab al-Hajj: the merchant accompanying mujahideen and the pilgrim trading during hajj. By examining these scenarios, you will see how intention determines legal consequences in both worldly and devotional acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the governing maxim
The entire passage revolves around the qa'ida kubra 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha'. Recognize that every furu' is a direct application of this maxim.
Maxim: Acts are judged by intentions.
2
Apply to the merchant in jihad
Analyze the merchant's intention at the point of crossing the border. If he intended only trade, he gets no share; if he later fights, his intention changes and he becomes entitled. Trace how the maxim determines the ruling.
Key: initial intention vs. actual fighting manifests new intention.
3
Apply to the pilgrim trading
For a hajj pilgrim, the primary intention is worship; incidental trade does not affect reward. However, if the primary intention was trade, reward is lost. Compare with the merchant case.
Contrast: primary vs. incidental intention.
4
Analyze the tawaf/wuquf distinction
The text adds a nuanced furu': tawaf performed with intention of searching for a debtor does not suffice, but wuquf at Arafat with the same intention does suffice. Understand why – tawaf is a pure worship that requires specific intent, while wuquf is a standing that is fulfilled regardless of incidental worldly purpose.
Distinction based on the nature of the act (mahd worship vs. broader rite).
5
Extract the principle for fatwa
Synthesize: the mufta bihi is that intention at the outset is decisive, but a change in intention through action (like fighting) overrides the original intent. This principle guides fatwa in similar cases.
Practical takeaway for ifta.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ترجمہ: اور فقہاء نے کتاب السیر میں وضاحت کی ہے کہ تاجر کے لئے کوئی حصہ نہیں ہے اس لئے کہ اس نے بجاتے وقت صرف تجارت کا ارادہ کیا ہے نہ کہ دین کی بلندی اور دشمن کو مرعوب کرنے کا پھر اگر و و قتال کرے تو وہ اس کا حق ہوگا اس لئے کہ تھمال سے ظاہر ہو گیا کہ اس کا اراد و قتال کا ہے اور تجارت ضمنا ہے جو اس کو مستمر نہیں ہے جیسے حج کرنے والا جنب جج کے راستہ میں تجارت کرے تو اس کا اجر کم نہ ہوگا زیلعی نے اس کو نہ کر کیا ہے، اور اس نیا ظاہر یہ ہے کہ حج کرنے والا بنب تجارت کی نیت سے نکلا تو اس کے لئے تو اب نہیں ہے اور فقہاء نے تصریح کی ہے کہ اگر وہ اپنے مقروض کو تلاش کرنے کی نیت سے طواف کرے تو اس کے لئے وہ کافی نہ ہوگا اور اگر اپنے مقریر کو تلاش کی نیت سے عرفہ میں مشہرا تو اس کو وہ کافی ہے اور فرق ظاہر ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ جنب مجاہدین کا شکر دار الاسلام سے دار الحرب جہاد کے لئے نکلا تب ان کے ساتھ کوئی شخص روز مرہ کی ضروریات لیکر پھیری لگانے کے لئے ان کے ساتھ ہو گیا تو جب مال غنیمت حاصل ہوگا وہ اس پھیری کی نیت سے مجاہدین کے ساتھ جانے والے کو بھی ملے گا یا نہیں اس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ اگر وہ جہاد میں شریک نہ ہوا تو اسے مال غنیمت میں سے کچھ حصہ نہ ملے گا، اس لئے کہ سرحد عبور کرتے وقت اس نے تجارت کا ارادہ کیا تھا۔ دین کی تقویت اور دشمن سے لڑنے اور ان کو بھگانے کا ارادہ نہیں تھا، اور اگر اس نے بالفعل جہاد میں شرکت کی تو سید ہاں غنیمت میں شریک ہو گا اس لئے کہ اس نے اگر چہ ابتداء مسفر تو بغرض تجارت کیا تھا لیکن بعد میں اس نے جہاد کی نیت کرلی اور اس نیت کا اختیار اس کے جہاد میں بالفعل شرکت کرنے سے ہو گیا۔ والأصل ان من دخل للقتال استحق السهم قاتل اولم يقاتل ومن دخل لغير القتال لم يستحق السهم الآن يقاتل (هند به ج ٢، ص ٢٠٨)
كالحاج إذا اتجر : اگر کوئی حاجی سفر حج کے لئے جاتا ہے اس کا مقصد حج ہی کا ہے لیکن راستہ میں ضمرہ تجارت بھی کر لیتا ہے تو اسے اس کی اجازت ہے اور اس سے اس کے اجر میں کوئی کمی نہیں آئے گی۔ لہذا اس کا ظاہری مفہوم یہ نکلتا ہے کہ اگر حاجی بھی تجارت کے مقصد سے حج کے لئے گیا تو اسے بھی اجر نہیں ملے گا۔ ويحترز من تجريد السفر من التجارة احسن ولو اتجر لا ينقض ثوابه كذا في البحر الرائق
هندیه ج ۱، ص : ۳۳۰)
Translation: And the jurists have explained in Kitab al-Siyar that the merchant has no share because at the time of departing he intended only trade, not the elevation of the religion and intimidating the enemy. Then if he fights, it will be his right because it becomes apparent from the actual fighting that his intention was fighting, and trade is incidental, which does not continue for him. Like the person performing Hajj who trades along the way—his reward will not decrease. Zayla'i has transmitted this, and from this it appears that if the pilgrim set out with the intention of trade, there is no reward for him. And the jurists have explicitly stated that if a person performs Tawaf with the intention of searching for his debtor, it will not suffice him, but if he performs Wuquf at Arafat with the intention of searching for his debtor, it is sufficient for him, and the difference is clear.
Explanation: The issue is that when a group of mujahideen set out from Dar al-Islam to Dar al-Harb for jihad, a person accompanied them carrying daily necessities to peddle. When booty is obtained, will that person who went with the intention of peddling also get a share? The detail is: if he did not participate in fighting, he gets no share of the booty, because at the time of crossing the border he intended trade, not strengthening the religion and fighting the enemy. But if he actually participated in jihad, then he will share in the booty, because although he initially set out for trade, later he formed the intention of jihad, and this intention became effective through his actual participation in jihad. The principle is: whoever enters for fighting deserves the share, whether he actually fought or not; whoever enters for other than fighting does not deserve the share unless he fights. (Hindiyya vol. 2, p. 208)
Like the hajj pilgrim if he trades: If a pilgrim goes for hajj with the sole intention of hajj but engages in incidental trade along the way, he is permitted to do so and his reward will not be diminished. Hence the apparent meaning is that if a pilgrim went with the intention of trade, he will not receive reward. And it is better to avoid making the journey solely for trade; if he trades, his reward is not nullified. So in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. (Hindiyya vol. 1, p. 330)
Source pages p. 202

Commentary
This passage is a qawida expansion illustrating the legal maxim 'Acts are judged by intentions' (الأمور بمقاصدها) through two furuat. The first furu' concerns a merchant accompanying mujahideen: his share in the ghanimah depends on his intention. If he crossed the border with only trade in mind, he gets nothing; but if he later fights, he becomes a mujahid and gets a share. The second furu' concerns a pilgrim who trades during hajj: since his primary intention is hajj, incidental trade does not harm his reward. However, if his primary intention was trade, the hajj reward is lost. The text also introduces a related principle about tawaf and wuquf, which is elaborated in the next lesson.

Key Terms
نیت (niyyah): Intention in the heart that determines the legal validity and reward of an act.
مال غنیمت (mal al-ghanimah): Booty taken from the enemy after battle, distributed according to Shariah rules.
طواف (tawaf): Circumambulation of the Kaaba, a pillar of Hajj and Umrah.
وقوف عرفہ (wuquf al-Arafah): Standing at Arafat on the 9th of Dhul Hijjah, the essential pillar of Hajj.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, under what condition does a merchant accompanying mujahideen get a share of the ghanimah?
A) If he accompanies them with any intention
B) If he fights or always intended to fight
C) If he trades during the journey
D) If he crosses the border with trade intention but later fights

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi maxim 'al-umur bi-maqasidiha' governs entitlement in ghanimah and reward in hajj: primary intention determines the ruling, and actions can override initial intention.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
10 min
Worldly Motive in Fard Acts and Hiring for Worship
Testing a Shafi'i branch against Hanafi principles and discussing ijarah on worship

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qawida that riya does not affect the obligation-fulfillment of fard acts, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on ijarah for acts of worship.

Core Idea
Riya does not invalidate fard, but fard cannot be hired; later Hanafis permit ijarah on worship by necessity.

This passage reports a Shafi'i case about praying Zuhr for a promised dinar, which the author confirms aligns with Hanafi principles. The case triggers two key Hanafi discussions: the effect of riya on fard acts and the permissibility of ijarah for worship. The passage then traces the evolution of the Hanafi position on ijarah for worship from early invalidity to later permissibility, and touches on sincerity in freeing slaves.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Shafi'i case and its ruling
Read the reported case: a person is promised a dinar to pray Zuhr, prays with that intention. The ruling: the prayer is valid (suffices), but no dinar is deserved. Note that the author hasn't seen this in Hanafi texts but says it follows Hanafi principles.
The case is from al-Nawawi.
2
Analyze the validity: apply the qawida on riya
The prayer's validity is justified by the qawida: 'Riya does not enter into the fara'id regarding the dropping of the obligation.' Even with a worldly motive, the fard act fulfills the obligation.
This qawida is a wusta (intermediate) dabt (restricting) principle.
3
Explain no wage due: fard outside ijarah
No dinar is deserved because performing fard acts cannot be the subject of a hire contract. Analogous to a father hiring his son for obligatory service – no wage.
This leads to the broader issue of ijarah on worship.
4
Examine the early Hanafi position on ijarah on worship
Early Hanafis (mutqaddimun) gave fatwa that hiring for acts of worship (imamate, adhan, teaching Quran/fiqh) is invalid. Worship cannot be hired.
This is the original ruling.
5
Note the later Hanafi change
Later Hanafis (mutakhkhirun) permitted ijarah on worship due to necessity (to preserve religious knowledge). This is the mufta bihi (relied-upon) opinion today.
The shift is based on istihsan and 'alayhi al-fatwa.
6
Reflect on the note about freeing a slave
The author adds that if one frees a slave with intention for a specific person, it is permissible. Allamah Hamawi questions its relevance but confirms that sincerity is not a condition for validity here.
This reinforces that riya does not invalidate fard-like acts.

وَرَأَيْتُ فَرْعًا فِي بَعْضِ كُتُبِ الشَّافِعِيَّةِ، حَكَاهُ النَّوَوِيُّ فِيْمَنْ قَالَ لَهُ إِنْسَانٌ: صَلِّ الظُّهْرَ وَلَكَ دِيْنَارٌ، فَصَلَّى بِهَذِهِ النِّيَّةِ ، أَنَّهُ تُجْزِتُهُ صَلَاتُهُ، وَلَا يَسْتَحِقُ الدِّيْنَارَ ، إِنْتَهَى، وَلَمْ أَرَ مِثْلَهُ لأصْحَابِنَا، وَيَنْبَغِي عَلى قَوَاعِدِنَا أَنْ يَكُونَ كَذلِكَ ، أمَّا الاجْزَاءُ فَلِمَا قَدَّمْنَا أَنَّ الرِّيَاءَ لَا يَدْخُلُ الْفَرَائِضَ فِي حَقَّ سُقُوْطِ الْوَاجِبِ، وَ أَمَّا عَدَمُ إِسْتِحْقَاقِ الدِّيْنَارِ فَلَانَّ أَدَاءَ الْفَرَائِضِ لَا يَدْخُلُ تَحْتَ عَقْدِ الْإِجَارَةِ، الاتَرى إِلى قَوْلِهِمْ: لَوِ اسْتَاجَرَ الْأَبُ إِبْنَهُ لِلْخِدْمَةِ، لَا أَجْوَلَهُ، ذَكَرَهُ فِي الْبَزَّازِيَّةِ؛ لأنَّ الْخِدْمَةَ عَلَيْهِ وَاجِبَةٌ ، بَلْ أفتى الْمُتَقَدِّمُوْنَ بِأَنَّ الْعِبَادَاتِ لَا تَصِحُ الإجَارَةُ عَلَيْهَا كَالْإِمَامَةِ وَ الْآذَانِ وَ تَعْلِيمِ الْقُرْآنِ وَالْفِقْهِ، وَلَكِنَّ الْمُعْتَمَدَ مَا أَفْتَى بِهِ الْمُتَأَخِّرُوْنَ مِنَ الْجَوَازِ وَقَدَّمْنَاهُ أَنَّهُ إِذَا نَوَى الْإِعْتَاقَ لِرَجُلٍ، كَانَ مُبَاحًا. ترجمہ: اور میں نے شوافع کی بعض کتابوں میں ایک جزئیہ دیکھا جس کو نووی نے نقل کیا ہے اس شخص کے بارے میں جس سے کسی انسان نے کہا ظہر کی نماز پڑھ اور مجھکو ایک دینار ملے گا اس نے اس نیت سے نماز پڑھی تو اس کو نماز کافی ہے اور وہ دینار کا محق نہیں ہوگا، نووی کا کلام پورا ہوا۔ اور اس جیسی بات میں نے اپنے اصحاب کے یہاں نہیں دیکھی اور ہمارے قواعد کے مطابق ایسا ہی مناسب ہے، بہر حال درست ہوجانا اس کی وجہ وہی ہے جو ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ سقوط واجب کے حق میں ریاء فرائض میں داخل نہیں ہوتی اور بہر حال دینار کا مستحق نہ ہونا تو اس لئے ہے کہ فرائض کی ادائیگی عقد اجارہ کے تحت نہیں آتی کیا آپ ے تہار کا قول نہیں دیکھا کہ اگر باپ نے اپنے بیٹے کو خدمت کے لئے کرایہ پرلیا تو اس کے لئے اجرت نہیں اس کو بزاز یہ میں ذکر کیا ہے اس لیئے اس پر خدمت واجب ہے بلکہ متقدمین نے فتویٰ دیا ہے کہ عبادات پر اجارہ درست نہیں ہے جیسے امامت ، اذ ان تعلیم قرآن اور فقہ لیکن قول معتمد وہ ہے جس پر متاخرین نے فتوی دیا ہے یعنی جواز اور کا ہم بیان کر چکے ہیں کہ جب اس نے کسی آدمی کے لئے آزاد کرنے کی نیت کر لی تو وہ مباح ہے۔ تشریح شوافع کی بعض کتب میں یہ جزئیہ ذکر کیا گیا ہے کہ ایک شخص نے کسی دوسرے سے کہا تو ظہر کی نماز پڑھ تجھکو ایک دینار ملے گا اس نے اس نیت سے نماز پڑھی تو اس کی نماز درست ہو جائے گی البتہ وہ دینارکا مشتق ہوگا ، صاحب کتاب کہتے ہیں کہ اس طرح کا جزئیہ اگر چہ ہمارے اصحاب کی کتابوں میں مجھے نہیں ملالہ تہ قواعدکی روشنی میں ہمارے یہاں بھی یہی حکم معلوم ہوتا ہے۔ نماز کا درست ہونا تو اس لئے ہے کہ واجب کے سقوط میں ریاء کو فرائض میں دخل نہیں اور دینار کا مستحق اس لئے نہیں ہوگا کہ یہ اجارہ علی الطاعات کی قبیل سے ہے اور اجارہ علی الطاعات محقد مین کے نزدیک جائز ہی نہیں، جیسے اگر کوئی باپ اپنے بیٹے کو خدمت کے لئے کرائے پر لے تو بیٹے کے لئے کوئی اجرت نہیں ہوگی اس لئے کہ باپ کی خدمت بیٹے پر واجب ہے یہ مسئلہ بزاز یہ میں بھی مذکور ہے اس لئے کہ اجرت غیر واجب عمل پر ملتی ہے اور باپ کی خدمت بیٹے پر واجب ہی ہے۔ عبادات پر اجرت لینے کا مسئلہ عبادات پر اجرت لینے کا مسئلہ در اصل اس بات پر منی ہے کہ طاعات پر اجارہ درست ہے یا نہیں اس کے بارے میں حقد مین احناف کی رائے تو یہ ہے کہ عبادات جیسے امامت، اذ ان تعلیم قرآن اور فقہ و غیر و یا اجارہ درست نہیں ہے۔ وفي الاصل لايجوز الاستئجار على الطاعات كتعليم القرآن والفقه والاذان والتذكير والتدريس والحج والعمرة ولا يجب الاجر كذا في الخلاصة. لیکن بعد کے متاخرین احناف نے ضرور دین کی حفاظت کے پیش نظر امامت ، اذ ان تعلیم قرآن اور فضا غیرہ پر اجارہ کو درست قرار دیا ہے۔ ص:۵۵) و مشائخ بلخ جوزوا الاستجارة على تعليم القرآن (هندیه ج ۴، ص: ۵۵) قال في الهندية و بعض مشائخنا رحمهم الله تعلى استحسنوا الاستئجارة على تعليم القرآن اليوم لظهور التواني في الامور الدينية ففي الامتناع تضييع حفظ القرآن وعليه الفتوى. (شایج میں ) وقدمنا انه اذا نوى الاعتاق : اگر کسی نے غلام آزاد کیا اور غلام آزاد کرتے وقت کسی آدمی کے لئے آزاد کرنے کی نیت تھی تو ایسا کرنا مباح ہوگا، علامہ حموی فرماتے ہیں کہ بات عبادت میں اخلاص کی چل رہی تھی اور اعتباق عبادت نہیں، لہذا ظاہر اس مسئلہ کو یہاں ذکر کرنے کی کوئی وجہ معلوم نہیں ہوتی ، بہر حال اگر اعتاق میں اخلاص نہ ہو تو اعتماق باطل نہیں ہو گا۔
And I saw a branch in some books of the Shafi'is, narrated by al-Nawawi, concerning a person who was told by someone: Pray Zuhr and you will get a dinar. He prayed with this intention, that his prayer is valid and he does not deserve the dinar. End. I have not seen the like from our companions, and it should be according to our principles as well. As for the validity, it is because we have mentioned that riya does not enter into the fara'id concerning the dropping of the obligation. And as for not deserving the dinar, it is because performing fara'id does not come under a contract of hire. Do you not see their statement: If a father hires his son for service, he does not get wages? It is mentioned in al-Bazzaziyyah, because service is obligatory upon him. Rather, the early scholars gave fatwa that hiring for acts of worship is not valid, like imamate, adhan, teaching Quran and fiqh. But the relied-upon opinion is what the later scholars gave fatwa of permissibility. And we have mentioned that if he intends freeing (a slave) for a man, it is permissible. Translation: ... Explanation: In some books of the Shafi'is, this branch is mentioned... ... And we have mentioned that if he intends freeing... Allamah Hamawi says: The discussion was about sincerity in worship, and freeing a slave is not worship, so there is no reason to mention this issue here. Nevertheless, if freeing lacks sincerity, it is not invalid.
Source pages p. 203

Commentary
This lengthy passage discusses a specific legal case reported from Imam al-Nawawi: a person is promised a dinar if he prays Zuhr, and he prays with that intention. The ruling is that the prayer is valid (valid enough to fulfill the obligation), but he does not deserve the dinar. The author of the current book (likely Ibn Nujaym or similar) says he has not seen this case in Hanafi texts, but based on Hanafi principles, it should be the same. The validity is justified by the principle that riya (showing off) does not affect the validity of fard acts regarding the dropping of the obligation; i.e., even if one has a worldly motive, the obligation is still fulfilled. The non-entitlement to the dinar is because performing fard acts cannot be the subject of a hire contract (ijarah). This is further illustrated by the case of a father hiring his son for service: no wages are due because the son is already obligated to serve his father. The passage then discusses the broader issue of hiring for acts of worship (ijarah 'ala al-ta'at). The early Hanafi scholars held such contracts invalid, as worship cannot be hired. However, later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) permitted hiring for acts like teaching Quran, adhan, and imamate to preserve religion, given the weakness of religious commitment. The author then mentions freeing a slave (i'taq) and notes that if one frees a slave with the intention of doing it for a specific person, it is permissible. Allamah Hamawi critiques this inclusion, noting that freeing a slave is not an act of worship (in the context of sincerity) and that the discussion was about sincerity in worship. Nevertheless, he confirms that even if sincerity is lacking in freeing a slave, the act is still valid.

Key Terms
الرياء (al-riya): Showing off or having a worldly motive in worship.
الإجارة على الطاعات (al-ijāra ʿalā al-ṭāʿāt): Hiring for acts of worship such as leading prayer, teaching Quran.
الاعتاق (al-iʿtāq): Freeing a slave.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why does the person not deserve the dinar even though his prayer is valid?
A) Because the dinar was promised by a non-Muslim
B) Because performing fard acts cannot be the subject of a hire contract
C) Because the prayer was invalid due to riya
D) Because the promise was verbal and not written

Key Takeaway
Worldly motive does not invalidate fard acts, but fard acts cannot be hired; later Hanafi fatwa permits ijarah on worship by necessity.

Al-Qawaid al-Kubra — The Five Major Maxims
intermediate
12 min
The Qa'ida of Combining Two Acts of Worship: Wasa'il vs Maqasid
Detailed exposition of combining two acts of worship in intention, with furu'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the qa'ida 'al-jam' bayna ibadatayn' to classify new furu' cases as wasa'il or maqasid and state the ruling with reference to Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Core Idea
Means combine freely; ends combine only with details — a single act can serve two worship purposes only under specific conditions.

When a Muslim performs an act of worship, the intention (niyyah) determines its validity and reward. But what if one act is intended for two worship purposes? This lesson unpacks the Hanafi maxim that distinguishes between means (wasa'il) – acts that facilitate worship – and ends (maqasid) – worship itself. The maxim is a practical tool for a mufti to rule on cases like combining ghusl for Friday and janabah, or combining qada and kaffarah in fasting. The source passage from al-Ashbah wa al-Nazair presents the rule and its furu' with an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
1. Classify the act as wasa'il or maqasid
Determine whether the acts being combined are means (e.g., ghusl for purification) or ends (e.g., prayer, fasting, zakat). The ruling hinges on this classification.
Wasa'il are not intrinsically worship; maqasid are inherently acts of worship.
2
2. If wasa'il: both valid
If the combination involves means only, or a means and an end, the act fulfills all intentions. Example: ghusl on Friday for sunnah and janabah removal – both valid.
3
3. If maqasid: subclassify further
Identify whether the intended acts are both fard, both nafl, or one of each. Then check if it is in prayer or other acts (like fasting, expiation, zakat).
Prayer has its own strict rule.
4
4. Apply the specific rulings
Two obligatory prayers: both invalid by consensus. Other cases: e.g., qada+kaffarah in fasting: Abu Hanifa says it counts for qada; Muhammad says nafl. Two kaffarah: Abu Hanifa gives choice, Muhammad says nafl. Zakat+kaffarah: specific assignments as per the text.
The text lists multiple scenarios; memorize the pattern.
5
5. Determine the mufta bihi
In fatwa, Abu Hanifa's position is often preferred for leniency, but caution may lead to following Imam Muhammad. State the operative ruling for each scenario.
The fatwa hierarchy: Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon unless a later master overrules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
السَّادِسُ فِي بَيَانِ الْجَمْعِ بَيْنَ عِبَادَتَيْنِ: وَ حَاصِلُهُ: إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُونَ فِي الْوَسَائِلِ، أَوْ فِي الْمَقَاصِدِ، فَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْوَسَائِلِ، فَا لَكُلٌّ صَحِيحٌ، قَالُوْ لَوِ اغْتَسَلَ الْجُنُبُ يَوْمَا الْجُمُعَةِ لِلْجُمُعَةِ، وَلِرَفْعِ الْجَنَابَةِ ارْتَفَعَتْ جَنَابَتُهُ، وَحَصَلَ لَهُ ثَوَابُ غُسْلِ الْجُمُعَةِ.
مقاصد میں پس اگر وسائل میں ہو تو سب صحیح ہے فقہاء فرماتے ہیں، کہ اگر جنبی نے جمعہ کے دن جمعہ کے لئے اور رفیع ترجمه: چھٹی بحث دو عبادتوں کو جمع کرنے کے بیان میں، جس کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ یا تو یہ وسائل میں ہو گا ؟ جنابت کے لئے غسل کیا تو اس کی جنابت مرتفع ہو گئی اور اس کو جمعہ کے دن کے غسل کا ثواب مل گیا۔ تشریح چھٹی بحث کا ماحصل یہ ہے کہ دو عبادتوں کو ایک ہی نیست میں جمع کیا جا سکتا ہے یا نہیں ، صاحب کتاب فرماتے ہیں کہ جمع بین العباد تین کی نیت وسائل یعنی عبادات غیر مقصودہ میں ہوگی یا مقاصد یعنی عبادات مقصور میں اگر اول ہے یعنی وسائل میں دو عبادتوں کو ایک نیت میں جمع کیا ہے تو درست ہے جیسا کہ فقہاء فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی شخص نے جمعہ کے روز ایک ہی غسل کیا اس سے غسل جمعہ کی سنیت اور رفع جنابت دونوں کی نیت کرلی تو وہ ایک ہی غسل دونوں کے لئے کافی ہوگا۔ وَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الْمَقَاصِدِ فَإِمَّا أَنْ يَنْوِىَ فَرْضَيْنِ أَوْ نَفْلَيْنِ أَوْ فَرْضًا وَنَفْلًا، أَمَّا الْأَوَّلُ فَلَا يَخْلُوْا إِمَّا أَنْ يَكُوْنَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ، أَوْ فِي غَيْرِهَا فَإِنْ كَانَ فِي الصَّلَاةِ لَمْ تَصِحْ وَاحِدَةٌ مِنْهُمَاء قَالَ فِي السِّرَاجِ الْوَهَّاجِ لَوْنَوَى صَلَا تَيْ فَرْضِ كَالظَّهْرِ وَالْعَصْرِ لَمْ تَصِحًا إِتِّفَافًا وَلَوْ نَوى فِي الصَّوْمِ الْقَضَاء وَالْكَفَّارَةَ ، كَانَ عَنِ الْقَضَاءِ، وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ: يَكُوْنُ تَطُوْعًا وَإِنْ نَوَى كَفَّارَةَ الظُّهَارِ وَكَفَّارَةَ الْيَمِيْنِ يَجْعَلُهُ لِايْهِمَا شَاءَ وَقَالَ مُحَمَّدٌ : يَكُوْنُ تَطُوعًا، وَلَوْنَوَى الزَّكَاةَ وَكَفَارَةَ الظَّهَارِ جَعَلَهُ عَنْ أَيَّهِمَا شَاءَ، وَلَوْنَوَى الزَّكَاةَ وَكَفَارَةَ الْيَمِيْنِ، فَهُوَ عَنِ الزَّكَاةِ وَلَوْنَوَى مَكْتُوبَةً وَصَلَاةَ جَنَازَةٍ فَهِيَ عَنِ الْمَكْتُوْبَةِ. ترجمہ: اور اگر یہ مقاصد میں ہوتو یا تو وہ دو فرضوں کی نیت کر لے گا یا دونوں کی یا ایک فرض اور ایک کل کی رہی پہلی صورت تو وہ یا تو وہ نماز میں ہوگی یا اس کے علاوہ میں اگر وہ نماز میں ہو تو ان میں سے ایک بھی بھیجنی ہوگئی السراج الوہاج میں کہا ہے کہ اگر کسی نے دو فرض نمازوں کی نیت کی مثلا مظہر اور عصر کی تو بالاتفاق دونوں میچ ہیں اور اگر روزہ میں قضاء اور کفارہ کی نیت کی تو وہ قضاء کی طرف سے ہوگی اور امام محمد فر ماتے ہیں کہ وہ نفلی ہوگا اور اگر کفارہ ظہار اور کفارہ یمین کی نیت کی تو اسے جس کی طرف سے چاہے بنا دے۔ اور امام محمد فر ماتے ہیں کہ وہ نفل ہو گا۔ اور اگر ز کوۃ اور کفارہ ظہار کی نیت کی تو ان میں سے جس کے لئے چاہے بنادے، اور اگرز کو اور کفارہ مین کی نیت کی تو وہ زکوۃ کی طرف سے ہوگی اور اگر فرض نماز اور نماز جنازہ کی نیت کی تو وہ فرض کی طرف سے ہوگی۔
The sixth: On explaining the combining of two acts of worship. Its summary: either it is in the means (wasa'il) or in the ends (maqasid). If it is in the means, both are valid. They said: If a junub (impure) person bathes on Friday for Friday (the sunnah ghusl) and to remove janabah, his janabah is removed and he obtains the reward of the Friday bath. (Then Urdu translation and commentary). And if it is in the ends, then either he intends two obligatory (fard) acts, or two supererogatory (nafl), or one obligatory and one supererogatory. As for the first: it is either in prayer or in other than prayer. If in prayer, neither is valid. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If one intends two obligatory prayers like Zuhr and Asr, they are invalid by consensus. And if one intends in fasting both qada (make-up) and kaffarah (expiation), it is for the qada, and Muhammad said: it becomes supererogatory. And if one intends kaffarah of zihar and kaffarah of oath, he may apply it to whichever he wishes, and Muhammad said: it becomes supererogatory. And if one intends zakat and kaffarah of zihar, he may apply it to whichever he wishes. And if one intends zakat and kaffarah of oath, it is for zakat. And if one intends an obligatory prayer and funeral prayer, it is for the obligatory prayer.
Source pages p. 206

Commentary
This is the sixth discussion in the book, dealing with the ruling on combining two acts of worship in a single intention. The key maxim is: if the combination is in the 'means' (wasa'il) – acts that are not intrinsically worship but are means to worship – then both are valid. The example given: a person in a state of janabah performs ghusl on Friday with the intention of both Friday ghusl (sunnah) and removing janabah (obligatory). Both intentions are fulfilled: janabah is removed and reward for Friday ghusl is obtained. This is because the ghusl itself is a single act that serves both purposes.

If the combination is in the 'ends' (maqasid) – acts that are themselves worship – then the ruling depends on the type of acts: (a) Two obligatory prayers: cannot be combined; both are invalid by consensus. (b) Two obligatory fasts: if one intends both qada and kaffarah, the default view (Imam Abu Hanifa) is that it counts for qada, and Imam Muhammad says it becomes voluntary. (c) Two kaffarahs (e.g., zihar and oath): the person can decide which one it fulfills; Muhammad says it becomes voluntary. (d) Zakat and kaffarah of zihar: can decide; zakat and kaffarah of oath: it is for zakat. (e) Obligatory prayer and funeral prayer: it is for the obligatory prayer.

The general principle: if both are obligatory and from the same category (e.g., two prayers), they cannot be combined; if from different categories, the stronger one takes precedence or the person has a choice. Imam Muhammad often holds that a single act cannot fulfill two obligatory duties, so it becomes nafl.

Key Terms
الوَسَائِل (al-wasa'il): Acts that are means to an end; not intrinsically worship but they facilitate worship (e.g., ghusl for purification).
المَقَاصِد (al-maqasid): Acts that are ends in themselves, i.e., intrinsically acts of worship (e.g., prayer, fasting, zakat).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling if a person intends in one fast both qada (make-up of a missed Ramadan fast) and kaffarah (expiation for breaking a fast)?
A) The fast counts for both qada and kaffarah.
B) The fast counts for qada (Abu Hanifa); Muhammad says it becomes nafl.
C) The fast counts for kaffarah only.
D) The fast is invalid because two obligations cannot be combined.

Key Takeaway
The qawida distinguishes means (wasa'il) – which combine validly – from ends (maqasid) – which require specific rules; the mufti must apply the exact furu' and note intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.
